Praelections upon the Sacred and holy Revelation of S. John, written in latin
by William Fulke Doctor of Divinity, and translated into English by George
Gyffard:

JOAN. 21. verse. 24. This is the Disciple which bears witness of these
things, and which wrote these things, and we know that his testimony is
true.

Revel. 22. us. 8. I am John which saw and heard these things.

Imprinted at London, by Thomas Purfoote, at the sign of the Lucrece.

Anno. 1573.

TO THE RIGHT HOnorable and noble Lord Ambrose Dudley, Earl of VVarwike,
Baron Lisle, general of the Q. Majesty's Ordinance, and Knight of the most
noble order of the Garter.
THE life of man (right Honorable) is said of the holy man Job to be a
continual warfare on earth: whereby it is evident, that so long as we remain
in the tabernacle of this flesh, we are even in the midst of this difficulte
and daungerouse fight, compassed in on every side with huge Armies of feyrce
and cruel enemies, and also subject at every moment to the furiouse assaults
and invasions of strong and subtle adversaries. As the holy Aposte S. Paul
witnesses Ephesians. 6. That we wrestle not against flesh and blood, but
against principalities, against powers, and against the worldly governors,
the Princes of the darckenesse of this world, against spiritual wickednesses
which are in the high places. Being therefore so weak and feeble of our
selves, that we are altogether unable to resist or to stand in battaill, and
encounter with so mighty stout Champions as these, namely that old serpent
with all the whole rablement of the hellishe Army, which by long practice are
so expert, that there subtlety is more to be feared then there power: the
holy ghost warns all those that will be the true soldiers of Christ, to put
on all the armor of God* as to have there loins gyrded about with verity,
having on the breast plate of righteousness, and to have there feet shood with
the preparation to the Gospel of peace, to take the shield of faith, and the
sword of the Spirit, the helmet of Salvation. All which spiritual weapons,
the Lord does minister unto us by his holy word. And our savior Christ as a
most mighty Captain, by his example has taught all his soldiers how they
shall use the same to the vanquishinge of Satan. But the malice of the devil
wrought so effectuously in the corrupt nature of man: that by the means of his
general Vicar Antichrist, for a long space of time, he had almost quite
banished these spiritual weapons and Christian armor, and brought in a great
number of his own framing, which are so far vnfite or unable to repel the
violence of his fyerie darts, that of themselves they give deadly wounds unto
all those that put or repose any confidence in them. For of them selves
(whatsoever they seem to be) they are nothing else to the souls of men, but
deadly poison. And yet notwithstanding, the blindness of the world through
the just judgment of God: For the contempt of his holy word, was such, that
being made druncke^ with the abominatio^s of Antichrist, it ra^ne a whoring
after strange Gods, and in such filthy manner, that fully it has been
verified in the^ which the Lord does grievously complain of by his Prophet
saying, my people have committed two evils: they have forsaken me the fou^tayn
of living waters to dig to the^ selves pits eue^ broken pits, that can hold
no waters, yea this madness proc^aded so far and the corruptions of Antichrist
were so depely roted in the hearts of men, that even unto this day, although
the LORD in great mercy by placinge a noble and virtuous Prince to reign
over us, which has set up and maintained his holy word, has outwardlye
banished them, they remain still in the minds of the people: but whereto may
this be imputed, that in all places almost of this Realm, the greater part
bear more favor to the monstruouse proceadinges of the man of sin, then to
the pure Gospel of Jesus Christ but that they are kept in such ignorance and
blindness, that they have not tasted of the power of Gods word. For this has
always been and is the crafty pollecie of the Devil, when as he can not
whollye stop the course of the Gospel, yet that he may make it the less
fruitful, to endeavor by all means possible even to entangle the ministers
thereof in the vain pleasures of this world, with covetousness and ambition,
that thereby they may become more studiouse, to set forth there own glory,
then to advance the glory of Christ, more careful to erect and garnishe there
own bowers, then to build up the house of the Lord. The miserable experience
of our time is an evident proof hereof. For out of what other founteyne have
all the mischeifes of latter time flowed, in this our Realm of England? But
that the carelesnes in feedinge the Lords flock has been so great, that in
most places eather raueninge wolves, or else such lewd unskillful blind
guides as are not able to govern them selves, instead of true pastors are made
governors in the church, and have the rule over the flock of Christ, so that
it is no great marvel, that the people in some places of this realm, for
want of good instruction not knowinge there duty to God set themselves in
armor to rebel against the minister of God, there Sovereign Prince. Thus
Antichrist by means of ignorance the mother of deuilishe devotion, seducinge
the people into sundry errors does mayntaine his bloudye kingedome. For if
his subtle practices were disclosed, and his abominations made manifest, there
is no doubt but that the greatest part of those that have there minds still
bewiched with the enchauntementes of that whore, would even looth and detest
her filthiness and hate here with a deadly hatred. Now seeinge that the Lord
has always had such a provident and fatherly care oue^ his Church, that he
would have nothing hid from his elect which should tend to there eternal
health and salvation, but even long before by sendinge his Angel, revealed
to his servant John what subtiltye and cruel tirannye, the devil by the
ministry of Antichriste would practice against the saints the true
servants of Christ. I think the Church should suffer great iniurye, if it
should want or be deprived of the use of those treasu^es which are contained
in this prophecye, which are so manifold and so great (as the godly and
diligent reader shall find) that I am far unable to speak any thing, which
may set forth the excellency and worthiness of the same. Which all men must
needs confess, seeing the holy ghost pronounces them to be blessed, which
here and keep the sayings of the prophecy of this book: especially living in
these daungerouse and troublesome times, wherein the Romish monster, inspired
with a deuilishe spirit, fearinge the utter subversion and overthrow of his
kingdom rages so vehemently, that he uses all kind of falsehood and subtle
dealinge, yea Barbarouse, and monstrouse tyranny, and all to establishe and
maintain his own pride and usurped authority, he has oftentimes such
success in warring against the true professors of the Gospel, that he has
victory and sleaeth there bodies, and that in such terrible manner, that it
might seem to be a Just quarill which he mainteyneth, except the Lord had
here revealed to his servant John, that he should thus for a time prevail:
and that in the end he will revenge the blood of his Saints. Again here is
fully answered that deuilish and blind objection of the Papists, which so
sore troubles the consciences of the ignorante: namelye that the Church of
Rome having continued so many hundred years, and been so general, and has
had from time to time a succession of Bysshoppes, and always remained visible
in the eyes of the world, can not be but the true Church. On the other side,
they say that this Church of ours was not any where to be found within an
hundred or two hundred years paste, and therefore can not be the true
Catholic Church of Christ. But let the diligent reader Judge, of these
things when he has perused this book: for herein he shall find even painted
out before his eyes, the form and shape both of the true Church, and also of
the false, which is the Synagoge of Satan. I might stand to reckon up a great
number of the like commodities, wherewith this prophecy is full, but then I
^houlde be over tediouse: and I wish rather that the diligente Reader should
gather them him self, which shall not be heard for him to do: seeinge the
aucthour thereof, as it does evidently appear applied him self to write
briefelye and plainly, not troubling the Reader with any long circumstances,
nor yet wading curiously in searching out darcke mysteries, but with modesty,
comparing and alludinge to other places of the scriptures. Whereby those
things that seemed most darcke and difficulte to be understood, are made plain
and easy. Thus when I had finissed my labor in translating this book, I was
bold to dedicate the same unto your honor, with diverse and sundry causes and
respects being moved thereto. As considering the great benevolence and good
will, which ye have toward the Aucthour hereof, and to all other that are
godly learned: adjoining thereto especially the fervent zeal and love toward
the Gospel, which God has wrought and planted in your heart: with the hatred
of Papistrie and all other deuilissh doctrine and errors, which by any ways
or means anoy the Church of Christ. These are not the gifts of nature, or of
flesh and blood, but of the spirit of God, given for the mainteyning of his
glory here in earth, and for the succouring of his pore afflicted Church,
especially in those which for the same end and purpose, he has placed in high
calling and authority: whose greateste honor and chiefest dignity does
consiste in this, that they are made the nourcing fathers and nourcing mothers
of Gods people. The Lord which has begun and wroughte these his graciouse
gifts in you, continue and increase the same daily more and more, bless ye
with all spiritual blessings, give unto ye long life with increase of Godly
honor, to the advancement of his glory, the commodity of his Church, and
your everlasting comfort and salvation in Christ our savior and redeamer.
Amen.

FINIS.
1573. Your Lordshippes humble Orator George Gyffard.

COMMENTARIES OF William Fulke upon the holy and sacred Revelation of Saint
John.
BEfore that saint John does enter into the full and just narration of the
prophetical visions, he thought good, to place some things before as in yt
way of a preface, which should make to the commendation of his doctrine, and
get authority to his writing.

Verse. 1. The revelation of Jesus Christ.

THis first verse conteyneth the title of the book, that it is ye revelation
of Jesus Christ, which God gave unto him, to this end that he might show his
servants those things which should shortly after come to pass. It is
usual among all the Prophets, least they should be thought to spread abroad
among the commun people the devises of there own brain, to ascite God as the
aucthor of there doctrine, of which sort are these, The word of the Lord, The
burden of the word of the lord. etc. The self same does saint John, in
saying the revelation of Jesus Christ: saving this that they do simply allege
god as their only aucthor, but this Apostle shows Jesus Christ to have
delivered those things unto him, which he himself received of the father. And
truly Saint John nourished up in the clear light of the Gospel, does speak
much more plainly and sensibly unto us, the^ the Prophets which were brought
up under the shadows of Moses law. For although Christ, which is the eternal
wisdom of his father, had always this prerogative, to deliver forth the
heavenly oracles, by whose benefit we ought to knowledge our selves to have
received, whatsoever good gifts God has at any time bestowed upon his Church:
yet notwithstanding it was not so manifest to the fathers in time past under
the law, as after yt the sone of God took our flesh, and manifested him self
to be beholden of us under ye clear light of ye Gospel, ye vail being taken
away. Rightly therefore says John, the revelation of Jesus Christ, whereby he
does not only sever, and distinguish this heavenly doctrine from all devises
of men, but also extolleth the great and most excellent dignity of our
savior Jesus Christ, to whom he does attribute this divine revelation: which
is all one, as if he should say our flesh to be lifted up and exalted to so
great honor that it should eue^ be made partaker of gods mysteries, which
ought not to seem straung, when as Christ placed at the right hand of god, in
his fathers steed does govern the Church and moreover the whole world.

WHich God gave unto him that he might show to his servants. etc. The
wonderful goodness of God does here shine forth unto us, that he does
vouchsafe to revels to his Church such great mysteries and secrets of things
to come, neither does he suffer his servants to be ignorant of any thing,
which is any way profitable for them to know.

Here therefore God is appointed and declared to be the aucthor of this
doctrine, Jesus Christ by whose means so great a treasure is come unto us, to
be the mediator, for truly in him which is our head, God does also embrace us
which are his body, so that we refuse not to be his servant, most ready to
receive and obey all his commandments. Moreover S. John means not by these
words, those secrets only, to be known of our savior Christ, which are
declared in this book (for seeing that he is the wisdom of God no part of the
divine counsel can be hid from him) but he understands that Christ in the
person of the mediator, has received this revelation of the father, that he
might communicate the same to his Church. For it is not to be doubted, but that
God revealed also many things by visions to other Apostles and holy men,
which should make either to their confirmation and strengthninge, or else to the
admonicion of the Church then present. But he would have this revelation only
committed to writing for ye use of the whole Church. For like as before the
coming of Christ, when doctrine and teaching was more dark and obscure, the
Church stood in need of many revelations, so after ye light of the gospel is
sprung up, and has dispersed and driven away all clouds and darkness, we
ought to hold our selves content with very few extraordinary visions. This
one therefore, but yet a most excellent revelation the holy ghost thought
sufficient for the Church, that he might admonish it of the perils and dangers
which it should pass through. And this is it that John says, that God gave
this revelation to Christ that he might declare it to his servant ( Those
things that should shortly come to pass.) Although the execution and
fulfilling of many things which are fore told of in this book, should be
differred unto a long time after, yet he means that even then the utility
and profit of this prophecy was to take place, when as by and by after,
horrible persecutions should be stirred up against the Church by the Roman
Emperors, and even a little before were begun to be stirred up by Nero and
Domitian ( And sending his angel) He teaches by whose ministry this
revelation was brought unto him, that is by an Angel being sent of Christ who
partly by word and partly by signs showed all these things unto him. And
this is no small commendation of this doctrine that Christ sent it from heaven
by an angel. That he calls him self the servant of Christ, it is the same
that the other Apostles do, as Paul, Peter, James and Jude, he means that
he is a servant of Christ, peculierly ordained to the ministry of the Gospel.

Verse. 2. Who bare record of the word of God and of the testimony of Jesus
Christ, and of all things that he saw.

HE procures authority to this prophecy, by the person of him self,
because that like as God has ordained and appointed him to be a preacher of
his gospel, so he has faithfully discharged the duty and office committed
unto him: for these two things are required in a teacher, first to be lawfully
called, least any other should rashly intrude, and thrust in him self, besides
him which is called of the lord, and secondlye to be faithful, that he may
sincerely, diligently and truly execute those matters which are committed unto
him. The Apostle therefore does signify that his faithfulness is already
sufficiently known and approved to the Churches, because it is he which
always here to fore With great faithfulness and constancy, has testified
and professed the word of God and the gospel of Jesus Christ, whereby they
may less doubt but that he will now also deliver and bring a perfect, sound,
and uncorrupted prophetical vision, sent down to him from heaven. So he
says in the end of the gospel which he writ. The same disciple is he which
testifies of these things, and wrote these things, and we know that his
testimonye is true.

Verse. 3. Happy is he that reads, and happy are they that hear the words of
this prophecy and keep those things which are written therein for the time is
at hand.

HE commends this doctrine by the great profit and commodity that it
brings, that it does not for a short time delight those that are studiouse in
the same, with a vain, colored and painted eloquence of words, according to
the manner of profane writings, but it makes the^ altogether happy and
blessed for evermore. Which thing although it may well and truly be spoken of
all the whole sacred scripture and of every book of the same, yet it is
evident that S. John speaks here only of his own prophecy. For that he
says the time is at hand, he admonishes the faithful, if they will take
any fruit thereof, that they ought to give them selves diligently to the
meditation and study of this prophecy, least the perils and dangers now
presently hanging over there heads, they living securely and carelessly, should
oppress the^ unawares. But rather being instructed in the doctrine of this
prophecy, they may be able to stand strongly against all the violent, force,
fraud, and deceit of the adversary. And here is the singular love of God and
of our savior Christ toward his Church commended unto us, over which he has
so provident a care, that the faithful may not only be admonished of the
dangers and evils hanging over there heads, but also yt way and means may be
showed, by which they may not only eschew the evils, but also put them selves
in possession of true and perfect blessedness. If they will diligently
exercise themselves in meditating upon this prophecy, and in keeping and
observing those things that are written and contained in the same, whereby it
shall come to pass, that they may be prepared to receive and resist all the
assaults of Satan, and may quietly triumph and have the victory, even in the
midst of the daungerous^ waves and flouddes of mischief and iniquite.

Verse. 4. John to the seven Churches which are in Asia.

Saint John warned by the holy ghost writes to seven of the most famous
Churches of Asia the lesser, to whose keeping he was commanded to commit the
great treasure of this prophecy, that by there faithful ministry it might be
preserved and kept, and spread over the whole world.

Grace and peace. etc.

ACcording to the custom and manner of the other Apostles, he wishes unto
them grace and peace: Grace that is the free favor of god, that he would
vouchsafe to embrace them with his so tender love and compassion, from whence
flows and springs this peace, that is the happy and prosperouse success of
all things, which god is accustomed to grant to those, whom he does
acknowledge for his children.

From him which is, and which was, and which is to come.

HE craves and desires this grace and peace of him which only can give the
same, that is of the eternal god, which in all ages does remain the self
same and like him self, with who^ (as says saint James) there is no mutatio^ or
change, neither any shadow of alteration, which as he is now, and always
has been, so shall he for ever and ever continue a patron and mighty defender
of his Church.

And from the seven spirits which are before his throne.

IT is the office and work of the holy ghost to seal and confirm grace and
peace in the hearts of the faithful, no marvel it is therefore, though he
desire the same from the holy spirit to be given unto the Churches. But this
does trouble some men, that for one spirit, he says seven spirits, for
howsoever the gifts be diverse, yet one spirit works all in all. 1. Corin.
12. But we must understand yt the Apostle speaks here according to the vision
showed unto him, which he expresses in the fourth chapter and first verse,
where there do appear seven lamps of fire burning before the throne which are
the seven spirits of God, which does no more take away the unity of the holy
ghost, then those fiery tounges, which sat upon every one of the Apostles, in
the second of the Acts. That he places seven spirits before the throne, he
signifies that those heavenly gifts, which are the effects and workinges of
the holy ghost, do descend unto us from no other then from the most high
father of light which is the aucthor and giver of all good things.

Verse. 5. And from Jesus Christ, which is a faithful witness and first
begotten of the dead and prince of the kings of the earth.

Seeing there is but one only mediator between God and man, even Jesus Christ
which alone has pacified his fathers wrath toward us: not without great
cause S. John desires and craves grace and peace at his hands, which has
brought us again into the favor of God, and by his death has established
true and perfect peace, betwixt God and mankind. In that the Apostle in this
place does so beautify and adorn our savior Christ, with diverse excellent
comme^dations of dignity and praise, he does it to this end that the greater
reverence, and aucthorite might be given to this revelation which he received
of Christ. First therefore he calls him a faithful witness, that is one
that testifies the truth, which has been accoustomed to deliver nothing to
his church but that which he has drawn out from the sacred and holy bosom of
his Father: whereupon he him self says, my doctrine is not mine but his that
sent me. He therefore which does deminish the faithfulness and truth of this
his testimony, does accuse the truth it self of untruth and lying, nether
shall his so great blasphemy against the sone of God escape unpunished. To
this end also he is called ye first begotten of the dead, and prince of the
kings of the earth: whereby his most high and souerayngne authority and
power, which he has both over the quick and the dead is approved, as he which
ouercomming death and triumphing over all his enemies, has obtained the chief
Empire and government both in heaven and earth. To whom now being risen and
returned from death, and exalted into the height of glory and majesty, if we
do not give due credit and reverence, we are altogether unworthy to enjoy
any benefit of his death and passion, or upon whom he should bestow and
impart any spark of his glory. Unto him which. etc. when he falls into
mention of the benefits of Christ he cannot withould himself, from celebrating
his grace with worthy praise and commendations, which we know Saint Paul
does almost always, as often as he was drawn into the consideration of the
same grace. And truly we are more then blockish, if at the remembrance of so
great benefits, we be not wholly turned in to thanckes giving and celebrating
of his divine glory. He does also admonish us, that even the only remembrance
of the benefits of Christ ought to suffice among all godly men, that the
authority of this doctrine should be sacred and holy.

Verse. 6. Which loved us and washed us from our sins in his blood, and made
us Kings and priests to god, even his father to him be glory and dominion for
evermore. Amen.

HE appoints the love of Christ to be the beginning of one redemption, which
for this cause is after a meruailouse sort commended unto us, that when we were
his enemies he refused not to wash away all the filthy spots of our sins
even with his own precious blood, and to bring us again into the favor of
God his father, and not this only, but also of wretched miserable, and abject,
bondslaues of Satan, of profane and vnpure contemners of God, by his benefit
he has exalted and lifted us up to a kingly honor and dignity, and preistly
holiness. Seeing he has made us partakers and heyers of his kingdom, and has
consecrated us preistes to offer spiritual sacrifices to god, to him worthelye
be all praise glory and dominion for evermore. Amen. But here the papists
have to consider, which study by all means to deminishe and make light the
benefit of the death of Christ, whereas the Apostell does attribute all yt
may be thereto, as remission of sins, kingly and preistly honor wherewith
Christians are exalted, he acknowlegeth to be received only by Christ.

Verse. 7. Behold he comes with clouds and every eye shall se him yea even they
which have pierced him through, and all kindreds of the earth shall wail
before him. Even so. Amen.

HE proceeds forward in the same argument, that he might get credit to his
prophecy, shewinge that none can falsely and without danger, despise this
doctrine, seeing yt came from him which shall come to judge the quick and the
dead, and shall take vengeance upon the wicked despisers of god. In that he
says he shall come in the clouds, he sets forth the glory of his cominge,
as well to terrefy and beat down the hautye stomachs of the wicked, as to
the lyftinge up of the minds of the godly into the hope of blessed
redemption, as in the. 24. of Math. And every eye shall se him. etc. No man can
fly from his presence, for even the wicked will they nill they shall be brought
into the presence of there judge, and those that would most of all withdraw
and hide themselves, yea they which pierced him, and handled him most
despitefully, shall even against there wills be drawn forth into his
presence. Furthermore all the kindreds of the earth which do so scornfully and
proudly reject and despise all his government, shall then but all to late, with
great sorrow acknowledge, how unhappily they conspired together to reject and
cast of his yoke, whose judgment they are compelled to receive and enter into
vnwillinglye.

Even so Amen. He confirms the former sentence with a double affirmation in
Greake and Hebrew, that he may commend the certeinte of the same. For there is
nothing more easy to profane persons then to deride our hope that we have of
the second coming of Christ and to delight and sport the^ selves, the mean
whiles in their delicate pleasures. But at length they shall prove by
experience to there great hurt, that this promise is not in vain. When as all
the tribes of the earth in desperate manner shall bewail them selves over him.
S. John does also express with how fervent prayers, all the godly ought to
desire the coming of that day, when as all the wicked being thrown down,
Christ shall have his perfect glory.

Verse. 8. I am alpha and Omega, that is the beginning and the ending says the
Lord, which is, and which was and which is to come, the almighty I say.

LAstelye he beautifieth and sets forth the excellency and worthiness of
this prophecy, in this, that it is his which is the beginning, and the end,
eternal and almighty, whom also (that the authority may be the greater)
he brings in speaking in his own person I am the Alpha and Omega, alpha in
the Grecians proverb, which is also in use among latin writers, signifies the
first* and by the same reason Omega signifies the last. The beginning and the
end, of whom all creatures took there beginning, which unless they should be
kept from destruction by his secreat virtue and power, they would every moment
vanish away and consume to nothing, which thing although it should come to
pass, yet no part of his divine majesty should be thereby deminished. For
howsoever all creatures be subject to alteration and change, God alone is free
from all unstableness. It remains therefore if we will be happy and blessed,
yt we cleave wholly to him, because yt about him we shall find nothing but
corruption and destruction. Which is. That is eternal, unchangeable, and the
self same throughout all ages, ( And which is to come) he shows yt he does
not speak of the incomprehensible essence of God, of which the sophisters do
folishly and childishly babble many things, otherwise he should say, And he
which shall be. But when he affirms that he will come, he signifies unto us,
that hereafter he will make manifest his glory even unto men, as well for the
comfort and consolation of his Church, as for the destruction and overthrow of
the wicked. For the lord is said to come, either to defend the faithful, or
else to revenge him self upon the wicked. Almighty we ought not here to dreme of
any idle power which does nothing, but to understand it of such a might as
governs all things with his only will, disposes all things by providence,
and by force and strength brings all things to pas. The meaning is, that
Christ (which is alpha and omega, the beginning and the end, eternal and
unchangeable) is the aucthor of this prophecy, that the faithful may receive
it with reverence, the wicked and ungodly can not despise the same without
there deserved punishment.

Verse. 9. I. John which am also your brother, and companion in tribulation and
in the kingdom and patience which is in Jesus Christ.

NOw he enterith into the narration of the first vision, describing the time,
and place and manner of the same. But it is offensive to some, that he so often
mentions his own name, as though it were not needful for him that declares
so wonderful visions, often to put the faithful in mind, who he is which
writes them, least that they should suspect those things to be but devises of
man's brain, when as they were testified of him whose calling and faith were
sufficiently known to the Church. Which self same thing we know, to be done
often time of the other Prophets, but especially of Daniell which does more
oftener repete his own name then this S. John. Howbeit the great modesty of
ye apostle here apeareth, that when as in many degrees he excelled other, yet
he makes himself equal with the rest, calling himself a brother, and a
partaker of the commune grace of the saints. Far otherwise is it with the
Roman Bishop which even in every trifling question but does nothing else but
ratle out ye popely dignity of the sea Apostolic, and the excellency of his
own holiness. But these three things are to be noted, in which Saint John
says he is a companion, that is in the kingdom, in affliction, and in the
patience of Jesus Christ. He chalingeth therefore unto himself a portion in
afflictions, because it is almost impossible, that any should profess Christ
syncerely, but that Satan will seek to lay manifold troubles upon them: how
much more then if he preach the Gospel: but it is a gloriouse thing to
suffer for Christ. S. John does therefore comfort the godly, that they are not
chastised with any other of Gods scorges, then he him self, whom they knew
to be most tenderly beloved of God. But this is more, that he adds, in the
kingdom, for if we be made like unto Christ in sufferinges, we shall also be
made partakers of his glory: according to that which Paul says, if we
suffer together with him we shall also raygne together with him.

And moreover he sets forth the qualite of Christ's kingedome in this life
to be such, yt although we seem daily to be overwhelmed with adversities and
troubles, yet the majesty of this his kingdom getting the victory, triumphs
over all afflictions. And thirdly that he adioyneth, in patience, he teacech
that troubles and afflicttons do no otherwise profit us to the attayning of
this kingdom, then if we bear them patiently for christ's glory and the
spreading abroad of his gospel In the mean while let us not pas over this,
that he calls it the patience of Christ, which none can have but by his
benefit, that they may be able with a quiet and pacified, yea a merry and
ioyefull mind to bear the cross laid upon there shoulders.

I was in an I Will called Patmos. etc. Now he shows the place, that is a little,
desert, barrain and unpleasant island of the sea Aegium, which is called
Patmos, into which he was banished by the tyrant Domitian, as all histories
agree with one consent.

For the word of God and for the testimony of Jesus. etc. He shows that
the preachinge of the word of God and the Gospel of Jesus, was the cause of
this his banishment, not that he would willingly seek any solitary place their
to dwell in, as now of later time the Monks, the Heremites Anachorts and other
solicarie persons have used to do, for who^ it had been more meter, if they had
been able, or if it had been lawful for them, to have given there diligent
attendance in declaring Gods word and preaching Christ's Gospel, in the
greatest and most famous cities, if they would truly have immitated S. John.

Verse. 10. I was ravished in the spirit on the Lords day. etc.

Now he declares the time when this vision was showed unto him, yt is upon ye
day of the Lord or sunday, which day was kept holy in the assembleies of the
Christians, and S. Paul calls it the first day after the Sabbath. At which
time, I doubt not but that Saint John, even in that great deserte, although he
were absent in body, yet was present in spirit, with the Churches: and with
his godly prayers and meditations, did commend them to the custody and
defense of Christ. That he says he was in the spirit, I understand that he
was ravished from himself, and that his bodily senses in the mean time
rested, that his mind might be more free in beholding those things which the
Lord showed unto him. Here we are taught that the baseness or deformity of
any place, can not let but that the godly mind, may be drawn up into the
secrets of the heavenly glory. John receives visions in the I Will of Patmos,
Peter in the roufe of a tanners house, and afterward also in prison: and Paul
in a torn ship, for to such things, neither does the excellency of the
place any thing availl, nether the unworthiness thereof any thing hinder.

And I heard behind me a great voice as it were of a trumpet saying. etc.
That suddenly he heard a great voice, even as it were of a loud sounding
trumpet, the lord would have him first stricken down and amassed with the
strangeness and greatness of the thing it self, that he might be the more
attentively prepared, to receive those things which by and by after, were
revealed unto him. To the same end also. I refer this, that he heard the
voice behind his back. For those things are more sudden and more unawares,
which come upon us behind our backs, then those which come before our faces.

Verse. 11 I am Alpha and Omega, the first and the last.

LEast that S. John should stand in doubt whether this vision were delivered
unto him by divine inspiration or no, Christ testifies with plain and clear
voice, that he is eternal God, the first and the last, according to with
sense, the lord in the 41. and 44. Chap. of Esaias calls him self the first
and the last.

That which thou see, write in a book, and send it unto the seven Churches
which are in Asia, etc. That he might not think that he was made partaker of
this divine revelation only for his own sake, (as saint Paul which was taken
up even into the third heaven and heard things which it was not lawful to
utter) but that he might make it commen to ye whole Church, he is commanded
to gather together in a book those things which he saw, and to send it to the
seven Churches of Asia, both that they might be keepers of this prophetical
book, and also that they might witness to the whole world, that it was
written by the ministry of that same Apostle, of whose faith and plain dealing
they had sufficient proof.

Verse. 12. And I turned back to see the voice that spoke with me, and when I
was turned I saw seven golden candelstickes.

WHen as he saw nothing before him, and yet was commanded to write those
things which he saw, he turned back that he might see him which uttered this
voice, which seemed also to talk with him even as familierly as with one whom
he knew. And when he was turned, he saw seven golden candelstickes, which
because Christ himself afterward expounds to be seven Churches, we need
not any longer rest in them. The like is showed to Zachary in the 4. Chapt. of
his prophecy, excepting this, that Zachary saw but one for the whole Church,
and John did see seven for many particular churches, which were as parts and
members of the whole. But how the sign does represent the thing signified, we
will afterward declare.

Verse. 13. And in the midst of the candelstickes one like unto the son of
man.

IT is not greatly material whether we understand, that S. John did know the
outward form and shape of our savior Christ in the Angel which he had seen,
or whether yt speaking simply according to ye manner of the old Prophets, he
means that he appeared having taken upon him yt form and shape of a man, so
that we hold this for certentie, that he represented the person and figure of
Christ, which manifested him self to be seen. For he is always co^uersant in
the midst of his church and does govern it with his spirit, and has a
continual care over the same. In vain therefore we seek Christ any other
where, then in the church, in vain also do we seek a Church founded upon any
other then Christ. What can the Roman bishops here answer, which boast them
selves to be Christ's vicares as though he were absent, whom nevertheless
John saw in the midst of the ca^delsticks, because he is always present
with his Church, and chalengeth the whole government thereof to him self
alone.

Clothed with a garment down to the feet. etc. Because this kind of garment
was such as pertayned to the priests, I do not mislike that some do
interpret it to signify in this place, the pureness and innocence of the
priesthode of Christ: although in my judgment it is more simple to say, that
it declares a certain rare dignity, and reverend majesty of the person
that wears it.

And gyrded about the papps with a golden gyrdle. The priests were also girded
about with a gyrdle yt they might ye more spedely execute there office, for a
large garment hanging louse about one, is a let or hinderaunce to those which
should spedely finishe any work they go about. Christ therefore is gyrded
about with a goulde^ gyrdel that we should not think he s^andeth in the
midst of the candelstickes like a dead Image, or as an idle loker on, but as
one that is girded up, and so most redely prepared to execute those necessary
business, which do apperteyne unto him in the government of the Church. Which
readiness truly is more preciouse then any gold, and is such an ornament to
his office and function, that not unworthily, it might well be signified unto
us by a golden gyrdle. But in that he has his breast gyrded about and not his
loins, some think it to be done for this cause, that he has no need, as
mortal wreches have, to repress with gyrding about, praue and wicked
affections from which he was free, but his breast only replenishede with
wisdom, and love toward his servant is gyrded about with a golden
gyrdell, to signify his great diligence.

Verse. 14. His head and his hear were white as wolle, and as snow.

BY this shining brightness of his head and his hear, it is necessary that we
understand his wonderful glory and dignitye, which far surmounteth the
condition of men, which nevertheless shines in the manhood of Christ. A show
whereof he gave, when he was tra^sfigured in the mount, when his garments
shined whiter then any snow.

And his eyes were as a flame of fiere, etc. Some do refer this to
wrathfulnesse and anger, wherewith he is incensed and styrred up against his
enemies. But I think rather yt they signify the exceeding quickenes and
sharpenes of his sight, wherewith even as fiere he perceth through all things,
so yt nothing can be hid from his presence, no not the secrets and hid
corners of y^ heart. In vain therefore do hypocrites hope that they can keep
them sel^es close from his sight, whose fierye eyes do pearce through eue^
unto all the depest secrets. And such an head yt behooves ye church dispersed
over the face of the whole world to have, which being furnished with fiery eyes,
may look round about into all parts of the same, and find out the subtle and
pryuie practices and deceiptes of Satan, and when they are found out can
auoyed them.

Verse. 15. And his feet were like unto fine brass as though they burned in a
furnace.

THis similitude does express the constancy and vnweryed study and diligence
of Christ in cherishing and helping his Church, when with these feet he
walks continually in the midst of the candelstickes. There is also noted
unto us, the beauty and perfection of his ways, because he has feet of
metal tried and polished with fire.

And his voice was as the sound of many waters. First he compared his voice
to a trompet, now to the noise of many waters, and afterward also he will
compare it to thonder, and not without Just cause, which sounded through the
whole world in spreading abroad of the Gospel. Which that we may pass over
other things, is of such virtue and force, that the dead shall hear it out of
there graves. Whereby the shamful insensible blockishnesse of those me^ is the
more to be abhorred, whose ears being daily stricken with the sound thereof,
do either scarcelye at the length hear but a little, or else are altogether
deaf.

Verse. 16. And he had in his right hand seven stars.

THE stars he himself does interpret to be Aungells, yt is pastors of the
Churches, which otherwise are subject to innumerable perils and dangers, but
that the Lord holds them in his right hand, least that they should fall, and
with great care he defends those, to whom he has committed the charge over
his Church. Here the true pastors are admonished, that they ought not to leave
of from doing there duty, for any labors, crosses, or afflictions, for
howsoever Satan and his ministers shall raise up false accusations against
them, and threaten imprisonments, torments and death also it self, yet they
ought manfully to contemn all these, because he himself has a care over there
health and safegarde, out of whose hand, no force or power is able to draw
them.

And out of his mouth went a sharp two edged sword. It is very usual in
the scriptures to compare the word of God unto a two edged sword which s.
Paul calls the sword of the spirit. With this sword the faithful are armed
against all the violence, crafts and subtiltye of the devil, the mighty
force whereof the Apostell does notably describe in the 4. Chapter to ye
Hebrews. With the same Christ fyghteth against his enemies. And we may not
take this sword any where else, then proceeding out of his mouth, for what soever
came not forth of the holy mouth of Christ, is not in any wise to be taken for
ye word of God.

And his face shone even as the sun in his strength. etc. The same that the
Su^ne is to ye whole world, even the same is Christ to his church, which being
but only one, and placed in heaven, yet nevertheless, with his shining
brightness he lighteneth ye whole church being a stranger upon earth, for truly
he is ye sun of righteousness, which so soon as he shines in the consciences
of the godly, straighte way drives away all the darkness of the devil, and
fills the mind with most joyful light, whose brightness to cover with the
clouds of darkness the devil laboreth all in vain, which is so far of,
that they should be to able obscure and darken his clear countenance, that
they being dispersed and driven away, his glory does appear out of them far
more clear and bright.

Verse. 17. And when I saw him I fell at his feet even as dead.

Man's infirmity can not bear the beholdinge of Gods glory, but straight
way it falls down. No marvel it is therefore though S. John beholding
Christ in such brightenes, fell down as it were dead before his feet. For
which cause his word is more to be reverenced, where with he allureth us so
gently and familierly to come unto him, which if he should show forth but even
the least shadow of his heavenly glory, we should not be able to abide it, but
should fall down upon the earth as dead.

Then he laid his right hand upon me saying. etc. The Lord lifts up his
servant that lay prostrate upon the earth wc his touching and with his voice.
For after that God has humbled us to his obedience he comfort us again by
his mercy. We are here taught that we shall lie dead at the beholdinge of the
heuenlye glory, except Christ reach forth his hand unto us, and with his
comfortable voice take from us our fear.

Fear not I am the first and the last. etc. He shows that they need not to
fear, to whom Christ which is the first and the last does vouchsafe to be
merciful.

I live and was dead. etc. And which lives for this end yt he may for ever
save those that come unto god by him. From whom it is so far of that death
should take away his life, that contrariewise being conqueror of death he has
attained eternal life. This particle Ame^ is added for the greater
confirmation.

I have the keys of hell and of death. etc. He says that he has obtained the
high government and empire over eternal death, that he might declare unto us,
that they need not to be afraid of death or hell: whom Christ has taken into
his custody and keeping: on the contrary part, that they shall be adjudged to
eternal punnishments which become enemies to him, which has the keys of hell
and death.

Verse. 19. Write therefore the things which thou have seen and the things
which are, and the things which shall be fulfilled hereafter.

HE commands that he should diligently commit to writing the visions showed
unto him: of which he declares some of them to be descriptions of things
even then present, as those which did peculierly pertayne to those seven
Churches: and some of them to express the state and condition of the church
even unto the worlds end.

Verse. 20. And the mystery of the seven stars which thou saw in my right
hand and the seven golden candelsticks. The seven stars are the angels of the
Churches and the seven candelstickes which thou saw are seven Churches. etc.

CHrist is the best interpreter of all mysteries, he expounds therefore the
mystery of the seven stars and of the seven canstelstickes teachinge that by
the stars is signified the Ministers of the Churches, which ought to shine
before the Churches in ye light of heavenly doctrine, and as stars to take
all their light from the sun which is Christ. By the golden candelstickes is
meant the churches which God has chosen, to sustain the light of his gospel
in the midst of ye darkness of this world, as in an other place the Church is
called the pillar of truth. The candelsticks are of gold, that we may know
in what price they are with God. Moreover here, we learn that without the
Churches which are the candelstickes to bear the light, we shall find
nothing in this world but horrible darkness. Let us beseech Christ therefore,
that he will for ever keep this light among us, and that he will draw us out
of the darkness of this world and bring us to the light of his heavenly
glory, to whom be all praise and honor for ever and ever. Amen.

The second Chapter.
Verse. 1. Unto the Angel of the Church of Ephesus write. etc.

THat the Churches might understand how proffitable this prophecy should be to
the ages following, and therefore they might receive it more reverently, and
keep it more religiouslye, and spread it abroad more diligently: the lord
would instruct them by some experience in them selves. The Church of Ephesus was
as it were the mother city of all Asia. Not that it had any authority over
the rest (for there was no difference perceived to be among the golden
Candelstickes) but yt it was gathered together in the most famous city and
therefore ought chiefly to give forth her light by example of doctrine and
manners. And he writes to the Angels of the Churches that is to the Ministers
and Pastors, not that those admonitions were necessary to them only but
because that, from them whether it be good or evil that proceaded, it flowed
into the whole body of the Church whereof they had the government, like as
also in the Church whatsoever things were well or evil, they ought to be
imputed either to there diligence or negligence.

These things says he that holds the seven stars in his right hand, and
walks in the midst of the seven golden Candelstickes.

THat the pastors of the Church might know how greatly they ought to esteem
these admonitions, Christ foretells yt they all proceeded from him, which a
little before was perfectly described in the vision. As touching the pastor of
Ephesus, he writes, that it is the commandment of him that holds the seven
stars. etc. That is, which by his ayed and succor does defend as well the
Churches them selves, as there pastors, and by his provident care, does keep
them in safetye, that he may acknowledge it to be his benefit, that being free
from so many evils, and adorned and decked with so many virtues, he should be
praised of Christ.

Verse. 2. I know thy works, and thy labor, and patience.

BEcause nothing is more easy to hipocrites then to boast of faith which
outwardly does not appear by any works, or else does glory in works that are
only colored and deceyrable, he forwarneth all me^, that whatsoever faith
they boast themselves, in outward profession to have, that he thoroughly sees
and knows what there works are (. And thy labor) It seems that the
diligent care of this pastor in governing the Church was very great, that the
Lord does count it worthy of such praise. And truly this diligence is most
necessary for the minister which has the care of the Lords flock committed
unto him, to which also he ought to join patience, because it can not be, that
any can be able to execute diligently the office committed unto him, but that
Satan will devise, and stere up diverse persecutions and troubles against him,
which that he may bear with a strong and stable mind, he has need to be
armed with patience.

And thou can not forbear them which are evil, and have examined them which
say they are Apostels and are not, and have found them liers. etc. He does also
commend the zeal of this pastore, in driuinge Wicked men out of the church,
and such as would not be brought to a better mind, and not only those which
showed them selves openly to be such, but even those also, which showed them
selves under the honorable name of Apostels, when as in the mean time they
were grievous plagues to the churches, of which sort are said to be, Nicholas,
Ebion, Cherinthus, Marcion, Manicheus, which striued and labored with there
new opinions, to defyle the puretie of the gospel, whose subtilties and
deceiptes by his diligence, and wisdom being found out, he perceived, and when
they were perceived he strongly resisted them.

Verse. 3. And thou have suffered and have patience and for my names sake have
labored and have not faynted.

Although he could not bear there wickedness, yet he was constrained to suffer
the troubles and persecutions which they stirred up against him. Which because
he bare pacie^tly, he declared that he did not boast of patience, but that he
had patience in deed. Lastly that he would willingly sustain so great labor
for Christ's names sake, and yt he never fainted as over come with any griefs,
it is sufficient proof, that he was the servant of Christ, and not of his
own belly, a pastor of the church, and not an heyering.

Verse. 4. Nevertheless I have somewhat against thee because thou have left thy
first charity.

THere is nothing thoroughly perfect in this corrupt nature of man. For he which
a little before seemed to want nothing that should make to the praise and
commendation of a good pastor, is now accused, that he has left his former
love. For when as we ought to profit and go forward daily in the study of
godliness, and charity toward our neighbors, he went not forward, but into yt
which was worse. For he had cast of much of his former burninge zeal,
which nevertheless, he ought daily more and more to have increased. But it
may be demanded how his zeal should first be commended, and his vnweried
exercise of labouringe. It may be answered, that his zeal was eue^ then also
worthy commendation, although it were much more fervent before, and it may come
to pass, yt one may he endued with a heroical spirit against the ungodly, and
yet not love his brethren as he ought to do, for these two I join together,
piety toward God and love toward our brethren, because nether of them is
without the other.

Verse. 5. Remember therefore from whence thou art fallen and repent and do the
first works, or else I will come against thee shortly and will remove thy
candelsticke out of his place except thou Amend.

THE disease being found out and showed, although never so secreat, he
counsels and persuades to lay to it ye medicine of repentance, which that
it may be healthful, he commands him two things. First to way and consider
from how exelle^t godliness he is cast down, out of what blessed state and
condition he is fallen, and whether at length (except he take heed in time) of
necessity he must fall, which suffers love by little and little to die in him
self. The other is that he slatter not him self, like as hipocrites do in
this dangerous estate, nether seek colors or clokes to hide and excuse his
fault, but without delay recover his former love, and do his former works,
which things if he neglect, he shall shortly prove, how dangerous a thing
it is, to despise the frendely admonitions of Christ, when as his candelsticke
being removed out of his place, he may look for nothing but horrible
darkness yea more then the darkness of Egypt, to come upon him. This place
does admonish us how sharply God will punish the neglecte of profiting and
goinge forward in godliness. But it seems contrary to all reason, that for one
man's offense, ye whole church should be punished with so extreme and deadly a
punnishment, but we ought to remember that this evil flowing out of the
pastor him self, did run over the whole Church. For such as the ministers
of the Church are such also we see the people for the most part to be.

Verse. 6. But this thou have that thou hate the works of the Nycholaites
which I also have. ^c.

HE means him to have deserved, that even out of hand he should execute
sharp punishment upon him, but that he might not think his former virtues to
be defrauded of there just reward, he shows that there is a time of
repentance granted, specially for this cause, that he fully hated the
doctrine and works of the Nicholaites which the Lord also pronou^ceth to be
worthy of his hatred. Whith works if we may believe ancient writings, were
wicked and foul pollutions and defilinges of Matrimony, and prostitutiones of
there wives, which they would have in common among them and afte^warde Christ
callethe it fornication, and eatinge of things offered to Idols. But the
papists shall here unfitly move any question as concerning the deserts of
works.

When as also the Lord does seem often to give some reward to the works of the
wicked, which have but an outward show of goodness as the feigned repentance of
Achabe, which he does for this cause that he may show how greatly those which
are good works in deed do please him, much more the virtues of the godly ought
to be accepted of him which is ye aucthor of all goodness, not that they
deserve any such thing, seeing they be imperfect, but because through his
fatherly favor, they are taken in good part.

Verse. 7. He that has ears to hear, let him hear what the spirit says to
the Churches. etc.

LEast any should think these things to be spoken only to the pastors of the
Churches, the holy ghost speaks generaly to all, as many as have there ears
opened to hear what the spirit says, not only to the Aungells, but also to
the Churches them selves. Whereby we do well understand, that these
admonitio^s are not private to some particular persons, but common to all. For
those that shall sin after the the same manner, shall be rewarded with the like
punishment, like as also the same rewards are appointed to those that covet to
follow the same virtues which are here commended.

To him that over comes I will give to eat of the tree of life which is in
the midst of the paradise of God. etc. He teaches that the godly have a
great strife, with this world and with the devil, but all labors are to be
set light by, in consideration of the inestimable greatness of the reward. To
the conquerers therefore in this battaill, the Lord which is our governor in
the same, will grant them to eat of the fruit of the tree of eternal life,
which is in the midst of the heavenly paradise, from the use whereof we know
that our first parents for there sin were justly excluded. Here we are
taught that it is Christ, that opens the paradise unto us which was shute,
which freely gives unto us eternal life, whereof the tree of life was a
sacrament, and yet, not unto such as are slothful and idle, but to those that
fight valiantly against the enemies, and in the end by his virtue and power
overcome the^. We are here also put in mind, what a prouocatio^ to stir us up
to contend, the greatness of the reward set forth to those that overcome, ought
to be, when as we daily see the greatest labors to be borne for the obteyning
of the smallest benefits of this corruptible life.

Verse. 6. And unto the Angel of the Church of the Smyrnians write, these
things says he which is the first and the last which was dead and is alive.
etc.

SMyrna was ye chefest city of Ionia, therefore he was comanded to send the
second epistle to the Bishop of the same, this bishop as it seems was a right
faithful Christian, when as the Lord counted nothing in him worthy
reprehension, not that he was without sin, but that as much as man's
weakness could, he was free from heynouse offenses, and a faithful
administratour of the office and charge committed unto him. Which was down so
much the more, because the Lord had exercised him with continual temptations.
For we se that idleness bredeth carelesnes and securite. He had need therefore
of great consolation, because he was oppressed with many adversities. Christ
therefore uses such a kind of preface, which should be most fit to confirm
and strengthen him, that he is the first and the last, that is eternal God,
therefore though he should suffer the most grieuouse affliction of all, which
is death it self, yet Christ which has overcome death, and hell, lives for
ever, not for him self but for us.

Verse. 9. I know thy works and tribulation and poverty, but thou art rich.
etc.

THat his works are allowed of Christ, it ought to be as much as all
rewards, and a most notable comfort, for God can never forsake, those whose
works he testifies do please him. But he proceadeth foreward, and first he
says that he does know his affliction and poverty. The Devil can lay nothing
upon the godly, rashly or without the determinat counsel of God the lord
knows both. The weight of afflictions and the strength of his servants,
wherefore he will not suffer them to be tempted above that they are able to
bear, but he will show a way out, even of the midst of the maze of
temptations. He is not ignorant how heavy a burden poverty is, but yet he
says that this pastor is rich because he had an incorruptible treasure laid
up in heaven. The riches of this world are thorns, by which the immortal
seed is choked, therefore we ought not to be grieved for the want of them.
And it is very like that by these two things, that is by affliction and
poverty, he was holden in his office, least he should wax wanton, or be taken
in the deceitfulnes of the world.

And I know the blasphemy of those that call them selves Jews and are not
but are the synagoge of Satan. etc. Thirdly he adds the sclaunder wherewith
the wicked did assail him, which falselye called them selves Jews, that is the
Church of God when as there wickedness did bewray them, not to be the holy sede
of Abraham, but ye profane synagog of satan, and as it is said in the history
of Sufanna, ye seed of Chanaan and not of Judah. Truly a noble mind and a clear
conscience of all evils bears this cauilinge slaunderings most greuouslye,
but this ought to suffice the godly that Christ pronounces them blessed, which
for his cause have all poisoned tounges armed against the^. And here he
admonishes that this blasphemy is not spronge up from good men, but it was
raised by wicked hypocrites, whose abominations were detested and abhorred of
all the godly. This place does teach, that it is profitable to the godly
pastors of the church, to be tried by afflictions, by pouertye, and sometime
also by infamy and sclaunderinge, raised up by the subtiltye of Satan and his
ministers, by which there faith, constancy, patience, and innocencye, is
better proved and tried, then if they should live in happy estate all there
life long not oppressed with any adversities.

Verse. 10. Fear none of those things that thou shall suffer, be hold it
shall come to pas that the devil shall cast some of you into prison that ye
may be tried.

AFter that he has testified that he knows his labors, least that he might
think any thing to come upon him by chance or at the will and pleasure of the
adversaries, that he might perceive he was strengthened by the aied of god,
that hitherto he did not faint in the troublesome waves of afflictions: he does
instruct and arm him against the storms following against the most bitter
hatred of Satan, which he should shortly tai^ of by experience. For the mad
rage of the devil should proceed so far, that he would cast certain of his
flock into prison, for the testimony of the gospel, but he shows that the
divine providence of god would so moderate this his furious rage, that this
tribulation should not bring destruction to the children of god which Satan
sought to bring to pas, but a trial which is profitable for them. Here we se
by whose leadinge the enemies of the Church rage in cruelty against the
faithful, that is by the inspiration of the Devil, which has the
governance of all there works, and also works in them. We are put in mind
with what kind of weapons and armoure we ought to be furnished against this
spiritual adversary, that is with spiritual armor.

And ye shall have tribulation ten days. etc. The number of ten in the
scriptures, according to the phrase of the Hebrew tongue, is the number of
fullness or perfection. As in Genes. 31. Number. 14. Job. 29 He declares
therefore unto them, that so long as they remain in this world, they must not
hope to have an end of there afflictions. Nevertheless he mitigateth the
grief of the continaunce thereof, in that he notes that time, by days and
not by years, as if he should say, for a few days, whiles ye live in this
world ye shallbe subject to troubles and afflictions, which being finished ye
shall inioye eternal blessedness in heaven.

Be faithful unto death and I will give the a crown of life. etc. We see now
what shield he counsels us to hold out against all these weapons, that is
faith, which he commands us to keep constant, and stable even unto death
that it may be adorned with the crown of immortality, He teaches that
afflictions are not to be suffered heauiely or sorowfully, throughout the short
course of this life, when as they are to be rewarded with perpetual felicite,
and that death is manfully to be suffered for Christ, which eternal life shall
recompense, reproach and ignominye is not to be feared, which does bring us to
the crown of glory.

Verse. 11. Let him that has an ear hear what the spirit says to the
Churches he that ouercometh shall not be hurt of the second death. etc.

Again the holy ghost does witness that this is a voice which all the godly
should diligently way and consider: He that overcomes shall not be hurt of
the second death, that is he shall be delivered from everlasting damnation.
The first death is of the body only, the second both of body and soul. A
wonderful comfort that they which be tormented with sundry kinds of
afflictions in this world, after death has finished this wretched life, shall
live for ever in most blessed estate, and voyed of all fear of death. For this
mortal life is eue^ for this cause miserable, yt it is in fear of death
always hanging over it, not only of the body but much more of the soul,
except in those in which by ye death of Christ, the stinge of death being
broken, they are called to the hope of blessed, and immortal life.

Verse. 12. And to the Angel of the Church which is at Pergamus write, this
says he which has the sharp sword with two edges.

PErgamus was the chief city of Phrygia, to whose bishop the third epistle
is sent, with this preface, yt it was sent from him, which has the two edged
sword, whose doctrine can suffer no mingling of profane opinions, but cutteth
of all perverse doctrines from the Church, as perniciouse plagues to the same.

Verse. 13. I know thy works. etc.

FIrst Christ does knowledge, and confess that he does allow, whatsoever
things are well done of him, and yet this does not hinder, that he should
less freely show, what soever he notes in him worthy reprehension.

And where thou dwell, even where Satan's throne is and thou kepest my name.
etc. How much more grieuouse the perils were which compassed him in on every
side, so much more commendable was his faith and the invincible constancy of
his mind. He dwelled wheare the throne of Satan was, that is, where all
godliness was trodden down, and ungodliness bare all the swaye. Where as Satan
sitting as it were in the stately seat of his kingdom ruled all things
according to his own pleasure. In that place, as it was necessary that all
wickedness should abou^d, so likewise the greatest cruelty and tyranny. It was
an argument of a couragiouse and heroical spirit, and a plain proof of
divine constancy, in so great dangers, to hold a free and sound confession
of the faieth.

And have not denied my faith even in those days when Antipas my faithful
martyr was slain among you where Satan dwells. etc. He testifies that the
constancy of this confession of his faith, was not broken by any denial, no
not even then when persecution did most of all rage against the church, that
is, even at that time when as the faithful martyr of Christ Antypas was
cruelly murdered, with those which being led and governed by Satan like
ravening wolves do cruelly rage against the flock of Christ. This place does
teach that whersoeuer c^uelty and tyranny does rage against the children of
God, there is neither the seat of Christ nor of the Apostels, but of Satan, as
it is in the Church of Rome. Moreover that denial of faith, although it be in
extreme dangers, is not permitted to christians, as the false Nychodemits
mainteyne. And lastly what honorable mention Christ makes of his martyr
which was slain, that we should not doubt how precious the death of them is
to the Lord, to whom it is granted, by there death to glorify God.

Verse. 15. But I have a few things against thee.

CHrist does not keep close that which was wanting in him that is to say the
zeal which he had commended in the pastor of Ephesus, that he could not suffer
the wicked, and specially the Nicholaites whose doctrine also the lord
testifies that he hates, this pastor of Pergamus did not so manfully and
stoutlye resist such kind of persons.

Because thou have there, them that maintain the doctrine of Balaa^, which
taught Balac to put a stumbling block before the children of Israel, that they
should eat of things sacrifised to Idols and commit fornication. etc. That
he might make those men more to to be abhorred he compares there doctrine,
with the doctrine of the old false Prophet Balaam which for rewards sake,
taught and instructed Balac, with what engines the health and safeguard of the
Israelites might he overthrown, that is, that by the whorishe women of the
Madianites they might be enticed to fornication and idolatrye, which came so
to pas, as we read in Numery 14 and 25. and the Nicholaites did teach ye same
things, that is to have wives in common and without any difference to eat
those things that were offered to Idols, whereby it is gathered, that as they
were given to foul pleasures of the flesh, so also couetously minded, which
for filthy ^ukers sake taught those things yt were not mete. The pastors are
here admonished that they ought not to wincke at the aucthors and teachers of
errors, and false doctrine no not even then, when as persecution is most
cruel and bitter, for it is great danger, tha^ the poison should spread
further abroad, and devour the whole and sincere sheep of Christ.

Verse. 16. But be converted, or else I will come unto the shortly and will fight
against them with the swoorde of my mouth. etc.

WE must needs confess that he had heynousely sinned, that he should be called
to repentance, and that under this condition, that except he should spedely
return in to the right way, the Lord himself will fight against them, and
^lea them with the sword of his mouth. For this is the force and strength of
his word, that those which it does not bring to a better mind it makes
subject to eternal curse. But here the question may be asked, what this did
pertayne to the pastor of Pergamus which was of a right judgment in the faith,
if the Lord justly punish the Nicholaites being heretics. I answer that the
Lord comprehends him in the number of the same persons, so long as he shall
not leave of to communicate with them in there sins, by favoring, and
wickinge at the same. For he will require there blood at his hands, if he
shall be negligent in doing his office, either in correcting, or driving them out
of the Church.

Verse. 17. He that has an ear to hear let him hear what the spirit says
to the Churches. etc.

HE does always repeat this, that we may know, that it is the purpose of the
holy ghost to set forth this doctrine not for one man or one Church only
but generallye for all men.

To him that overcomes I will give to eat manna that is hid and will give
him a white stone, and in the stone a new name written, which no man knows
saving he that receives it. etc. Like as he threteneth punishment to the
dispisers of his word, so also he promises reward to the faithful that shall
overcome all temptations: that being made partakers of the heavenly table,
they shall be satisfied with angels bread. Not with that manna which there
fathers did eat forty years in the wilderness and yet are dead, but with
that living bread which came down from heaven, and gives eternal life to as
many as shall eat it. Of which the former manna was but a figure and shadow.
And he seems to allude to that manna which was hid in the arc, which being
kept by the commandment of God, remained many hundred years uncorrupted, when
as that notwithstanding which the Israelites did eat, being kept but unto the
next day would putt^^ye and slincke. A white stone, in election of officers
did assign him, which should be made a magistrate. By this white stone thefore
the Lord does signifye, what great honor he will be stowe upon him, which
shall overcome the vain enticementes of this world. By the name written in
it, which none does understand, but he which receaueth the stone, I understand
that by the earnest of the spirit shall be sealed in his heart, the full
assurance of eternal life, of which every one is privy to him self alone.
He does promise therefore, not only of the hiden manna plenty and fullness,
but also everlasting tranquillity of mind, through the feling of Gods mercy.
The new name signifies the grace of regeneration, that a new name may agree to
a new man. Woe be to our cowardlye sluggishnes, if pleasing our selves in the
vain pleasurs of this world we either despise or little esteem so ample
rewards, and like to the Israelites, desire flesh to be given us insteede of
manna, and being called to the dignity of the children of God, we had rather
serve in Egipte, in most miserable bondage.

Verse. 18. And unto the Angel of the Church of the Thyatirian^, write this
says the son of God, which has his eyes like unto a flame of fire, and his
feet are like fine brass. etc.

HE is commanded to write the fourth epistle to ye pastor of the Church which
is at Thyatira a city of Lydia. He makes this preface that the son of God
is the aucthor of this Epistle, from whose fiery eyes no spotte or blemish of
the Church can be hid, whose feet being like fine brass, do signify the
perfection of his ways, neither do they admit any forged myxtures.

Verse. 19. I know thy works and thy charity, and service, and faith, and thy
patience. etc.

THere are many virtues commended in him, but yet not without some spotte of
negligence. Very properly and fitly he joins service to charity, and
patience to faith. For if we love our brethren with unfeigned love, we shall not
be grieved to do the duetyes of charity toward them. And if we have a lively
faith in God, we will for his glories sake, suffer patiently all the calamities
which he shall lay upon us.

And thy works. etc. which sprung and flowed out of these virtues, faith in
God and love toward our neighbors. It was not a bare and empty name of
faith and charity, but he was endued with true faith which works by charity.

And the last are more then the first. etc. This does almost excede the other
praises, and commendations, that he had not left his former love, as the
pastor of Ephesus had, but the study of godliness did increase in him daily
more and more. Which thing although it be straightly required of all men, yet we
find but few which do not the contrary, that is that either they profit not
in godliness at all, or else are changed into worse. We must therefore have great
care to imitate and follow this Church and the pastor of the same, that we may
do our endeavor, that the procedinges may not only be agreeable to the
beginninges, but also excel the same.

Verse. 20. Notwithstanding I have a few things against the, that thou
sufferrest that woman Iezabell which calls her self a prophetuse to teach
and to deceive my servants, to make them commit fornication and to eat
meat offered to Idols. etc.

THis pastor is reproved, for his neclect of ecclesiastical displine, that
he did not put to silence, those prattling women which taught wicked things.
Whereby we gather, that it is the office of the minister, to repress the
insolent pride of those which arrogantly take upon them the office of teachinge
not being called thereto by the Church, much more it perteyneth to them, to
repress false Prophets, which set forth there perverse opinions. Like as this
minister is here first reprehended, that he suffered a woman, whether she were
but one, or whether they were more, to teach, which is not agreeable to the
comlines of ecclesiastical discipline: and after, that he did bear with her
teaching so wicked things. And he calls her Iezabell because that according
to the example of the wicked wife of Achab, she deceived the people and seduced
them into errors. Which although she pretended to have a spirit of prophecy
in here impieties, yet she is known by this, that she feigned new revelations,
to establish the damned doctrine of the Nicholaites. For she taught with these
Nicholaites, these things, to commit fornication and to eat meat offered
to Idols. This was no small necligence of the pastor, that he suffered the
servants of God, the sheep of Christ, by his carelesnes to fall hedlonge into
so deape a dongeon of errors. We may note here the craftiues of satan, which
that he may make his false stuff sailable among men, invented new
revelations contrary to the word of God. So Simon shows of on Selen,
Apelles of Philemena, Montanus of Prisca and Maximilla, the Papists have there
Brigites, and in our age also they suborne certain prophesing wenches, as now
of late in Kent a certain nun named Elizabeth Barton, all of them that they
may defile the pure doctrine of the Gospel, set forth in the holy writings of
the Apostles with new and vnpure opinions, under the show of heavenly
revelations. Such pestilent sores as these are diligently to be eschewed.

Verse. 21. And I gave her space to repent of her fornication and she repented
not. etc.

IT is meruail that the most mighty God would not straitway strike down with
thunder these great blasphemies and the Aucthores of the same, so sone as they
were brought forth, but his gentleness is wonderful, by which he grants a
time of repentance even to such persons, which when they shall despise, as it
is said this arrogante woman did. He reco^penseth his slackenes, with
increasing the punnishement.

Verse. 22. Behold I will cast her into a bed, and them that commit
fornication with her into great affliction except they repent them of there
works. etc.

HE threteneth not her only, but those also which willingly apply there
corrupt ears to hear her adulterate doctrine, that except they repent in
time they shall be taught by most sharp punishments, that it is no light
matter or such as shall escape unpunished, to defile the heavenly doctrine with
these deuilish devises. By the bed he himself expounds to be mente great
affliction, and the Metaphor does fitly agree, for as adulterers have beds
serving for there filthy plesures, which they esteem as the greatest delights,
so the Lord will cast the^ into a bed of the greatest miseries, out of which
they can not rise without extreme and final destruction.

Verse. 23. And I will kill her children with death, and all the Churches shall
know that I am he which search the remes and heart and I will give to every
one of you according to his works. etc.

THe disciples of the prophets are called there sons. This woman therefore
which chalinged to her self the name of prophetisse had her disciples which
are here called her children. These the Lord does adiudge to death, and
pronou^ceth that he will punish them most sharply and extremely. That it may
be made manifest to all Churches, that no hipocrisy can deceive Christ, which
perceth even unto the deep and secret thoughts of the reins and heart. All men
peradventure will acknowledge this in voice and words, but yet many do so
favor and flatter them selves in gross disimulation that they hope that they
can auoyed Gods judgment, and therefore to themselves, they let lose the
bridle to all ungodliness. But when god shall perform, yt which he has
promised, that he will render to every man according to his works, then they
shall perceive how horrible a thing it is to reject the grace offered unto
the^ and to continue in there accustomed crooked path of wickedness obstinatly
unto the end. But of the deserts of good works here can nothing be gathered,
for this far differs, that God will give to every man according to his
works, from this that the papists defend, that God does respect the merits
of works in justifying a man.

Verse. 24. And unto you I say the rest of them of Thyatyra as many as have no
this learning neither have known the depenes of Satan as they term it I will
put upon you none other burden.

IT appears that there were many in this Church which did not only not
favor this wicked and deuilishe doctrine but also by all means did oppugn
and resist the same. Those Christ does not charg in the same fault with the
rest, but does only exhort them, that they suffer not the simplicite of there
faith to be corrupted with any fained inventions of new revelations, howsoever
the aucthors of the same boast nothing else but the deep mysteries of God,
which nevertheless rather deserve to be called the secrets of Satan. Except
peradventure they them selves called the secreates of there knowledge the
depthes of satan, as the words pretend, which comes all to one end. Truly
