the majesty of God is here described compassed about with an innumerable
army of blessed spirits, which are all most redely prepared to obey him, these
also do rejoice with the Church for the grace of Christ, whom they extol with
worthy praise.

Verse. 12. Saying with a loud voice the lamb is worthy which was killed to
receive power and riches, and wisdom, and strength, and honor, and glory,
and praise etc.

THousand thousands of blessed spirits do witness with a loud voice, that
Christ which by his death redeamed mankind from destruction, is most worthy
all the praise of power, riches, wisdom, strength, honor, glory, and
blessing. Would God all those which profess yt they seek the glory of
Christ, would retain this Aungelicall confession, to ascribe all laud,
honor, dignity and thanks giving, to him alone, which by his death has
bewtified the power, riches, and wisdom of God above all the capacity of men
and Angels. The Angels therefore could satisfy them selves with no
multitude or deaping together of words, that they might worthily extol his
glory.

Verse. 13. And all the creatures which are in heaven, and on the earth, under
the earth and in the sea, and all that are in them heard I saying, praise and
honor and glory and power be unto him that sits upon the throne and unto
the lamb for euermor. etc.

THis may worthiely be called a catholic confession, which all the creatures
which are within the compass of heaven do make, that to God only and to
Christ all blessing, honor, power, is dew for ever and ever. Moreover when the
same things are attributed to Christ together with him that sits on the
throne, who sees not yt they acknowledge Christ to be eternal god? that he
names creatures under the earth, he means not souls in Purgatory, neither
the deuill^ of hell, but it is added for amplification and enlarging the
matter, like as he numbreth all the creatures as it were by there kinds, as
before in the third verse, likewise in these words (and all things which are
in them) when as he had rehearsed before all things in heaven and earth and in
the sea. But in that the dumb creatures do also sound forth the praises of
God, with what ardent zeal ought men endued with reason apply them selves to
set forth the glory of God.

Verse. 14. And the 4. beast said Amen, and the 24. elders fell down and
worshipped him that lives for evermore. etc.

TO this godly and holy song, the 4. beasts which are Cherubine and Seraphin
appointed of God for the preservation of his creatures, do sing Amen. The 24.
elders which are the company of the faithful, falling prostrate, do worship
him which lives for ever and ever, with all submission of mind giving to God
only by Christ all glory, honor and thankesgeuing, for the health and
salvation purchased unto them.

The syxte Chapter.
THe six first seals of the book being opened by the la^be, so many secret
mysteries of Gods will a^e revealed to the Church, the victory of the Gospel,
murder, famine, pestilence, ye complaints and consolation of the martyrs, and
lastly an earthquake, which should shake the whole world.

Verse. 1. And I saw when the lamb had opened one of the seals and I heard one
of the beasts say as it were thunder come and see.

Whatsoever God has decreed with him self, concerning the ordering and
disposing of things in the world and principally in the Church, the same is
far removed from the knowledge of men, except the lamb which is the son of
God, vouchsafe to open the same unto us, which does not only reveal the
secreates of things to come, but also he shows unto us the invisible God
himself, John the 1. chap. After therefore that ye lamb, to whom this office
does only belong as we have learned in the former chap had opened one of the
seals s. John heard a voice uttered by one of the 4. beasts, as the voice of
thunder which gives him leave to behold, this voice although it were uttered
up one of the 4. beasts, yet it is known to be the voice of God him self,
whose servant only ye Angel was for it is not lawful to any creature to
give leave of him self either to approach near or to behold any thing in
the divine mysteries of God: it was like thunder that it might wake and sterre
up al his senses to attentatio^ and diligent consideration, for we ought to
shake of the drowsenes fyxed in man's nature if we will come (...) to the
beholdinge of Gods mysteries.

Verse. 2. Therefore I behold and lot there was a white horse and he that sat
on him had a bow, and a crown was given unto him, and he went forth
conqueringe that he might overcome. etc.

THe openinge of this first seal, to the comfort of the godly describes
under the figure of a white horse, and of him that sat upon him, the victory
of the Gospel spread over the whole world. For the white horse signifies
the ministry of the gospel, over which Christ has the ruling even as one
that sits upon an horse, by whose ayed, the heavenly doctrine is carried
with wonderful swiftnes over the face of the whole earth, so that wtin few
years after ye ascension of Christ, ye base and contible co^pan^ of the
Aposteles, spread abroad ye doctrine of ye gospel into all regions of the
world. The whitenes of the horse describes the ministry of the gospel to be
most beautiful, such as it is in it self not such as it seems unto the
world, for beutifull are the feet of them yt bring the glad tidinges of peace
of them that declare good things. Joyful and happy therefore is ye coming of
this horse chiefly when he bears such a one upon his back. For by him that
sits upon the horse, we must understand Christ him self, or else the
doctrine of the gospel, which should be spread into al parts of ye world, by
the ministry of the word. He is armed with a bow, which showteth far, and
perceth deep. that he might signify that his force should with swift course
he sent forth into the uttermost borders of the earth, and enter eve unto the
depest secreates of the heart. Lastly he has a crown given unto him, which
is a sign and token of the kingdom and victory which he shall get in the
world, in spite of Satan ^ all his ministers. Because the full time was come
in which he that sat upon the horse should show forth his strength, in
delivering the Church out of the ^awes of satan, he sets forward and
whether soever he goes, he gets the victory, neither is he sent forth of
God to any other end, then that he might get a noble victory over Gods
ennemies. This truly ought to be a comfort, and as a spur to the ministers
of the gospel, that they should not fainct under there burden, neither by
cowardlynes leave there camp, if they were persuaded, that the doctrine which
they preach, shall suerly get the victory, in spite of the devil and all other
ennemies. For in vain does all the wickedness of the world labor to hinder
his course, or to overcome him, whom God him self has purposely sent forth
already crowned, not to a doubtful battle, but to a certain victory. And
this figure does represent the primitive Church, a that first age, in which
the white horse clear from all spots of perverse and wicked opinions, carried
ye doctrine of y^ Gospel through the whole world.

Verse. 3. And when he had opened the second seal I heard the second beast
saying come and see. etc.

LEast we might suppose that all things should joyfully go forward
according to these happy beginninges, the opening of the second seal does
show, that the doctrine of the gospel should be received with the wicked
hatred and malice of satan and the world. Touching that he is called to behold
by the voice of the second beast, we may learn to use our selves soberlye
and modestly in searchinge out the mysteries of God, that we covet not to know
more, then the Lord does vouchsafe to reuele unto us. Moreover that he might
more diligently consider all ye several of this vision, it behooves that to
every one he should be styrred up with a new call, for such is the weakness
of our nature that except we be very often provoked to meditate and consider
those things which God has reveled unto us, nothing is more ready then that
the same should fall ^ slip out of our minds.

Verse. 4. And there went out another horse that was red, and power was given
him that sat there on, to take peace from the earth, and that they should kill
on another, and there was given him a great sword.

IT is certainly sure that the gospel of it self is the doctrine of peace,
not only between God and men, but also to men among them selves. For what
other thing does the gospel teach then that we should rest by true faieth in
God our father, which is reveled unto us by the death of Christ, and that we
should embrace righteousness and peace with men which are our brethren. But it
comes to pas by ye wickedness of men and ye craft of satan, that when this
holsom and peaceable doctrine is rejected, men do cruelly rage among them
selves, with murdering and slaughters, and god him self sends tumults and
vprores of war, that he may take vengeance upon the wicked despicers of his
word, which is here plainly expressed under the figure of the red horse, and
satan sittinge upon him. For the red horse does signify the cruel and
bloody purpose of Satan, by which he strives even at once utterly to root
out all the professors of the gospel, except his cruelty should be bridled
by the unchangeable decree and purpose of God. Hereof it comes to pas, that
the gospel being once preached, there arise horrible commotions, slaughters,
and tumults. But Gods divine providence does so moderate all these things,
that by these temptations he truth his children, he suffers his adversaries
to flea and murder one another. And this is it which John says that power
was given to this rider, to take peace from the earth, that me^ might rage and
war cruel among them selves with killing and murdering and for a token of the
same power, he received a great sword. This is that sword, which Christ
affirms he came into the world to send. This worthy to be noted yt the devil
him self although he burn with cruel hatred against the godly, yet he can
work nothing against them, but so much as there merciful father does grant.
Also for the revenge of the death of the godly, yt the lord does turn the
sword of the enemies through there own bowels. For we scarce read at any
time, yt cruelty was used against the godly, but yt there blood was revenged,
is greater bloodshed of the persecutours. And this seems to be the figure of
the Church, which Satan assalted with open violence under the Roman
emperors, even to the time of Constantine the great, for in that space Satan
wrought innumerable slaughters of ye holy martyrs under Domitiane, ^ra^ane
Antoninus, Decius, Dioclesian, Maxentius, Licin^^s, and other cruel tyrants.
But god thoroughly revenged there death, when infinity thousands of them which
became ministers of Satan's madness in persecuting the Church were daily
consumed, either by foreign wars, or civil seditio^s, and the Emperors also
themselves, proconsuls, and governors of provinces, by poisoning, by treasons,
by tumults, and often times murdering them selves, did bear the due punishment
of there cruelty. And yet his course was not hindered, nor his victory
disgraced, which sitting upon the white horse went forth that he might co^quer
and overcome. But rather among these bloody swords, and sore wou^des, his
victory appeared much more gloriouse.

Verse. 5 And when he opened the third se^le I heard the third beast saying come
and see, then I beheld and ^o a black horse and he that sat on him had
balaunces in his hand.

HE had need of a new admonisher that he might diligently print in his mind
the mystery of the third seal. And it was on this sort, when men waxed werie
of heavenly food, God sends hunger and famine among them, that they may
suffer there deserved punishments for despicing his gospel. There appears
therefore a black horse, carrying the sorrow and grie^e of famine into the
world, yt they which will not acknowledge ye happy victory of him yt sat upon
the white horse going before, should he miserably afflicted of the sturdy and
cruel sitter upon the black horse. This horsema^ carries a paier of bala^ce yt
he may beliuer to me^ for there sustena^ce bred and water by weight, by which
we read that the scarcite of things, and famine is signified, as in Leuit. 26.
Ezekiel 4. and ^. When the Lord threateneth that ten women shall bake together
in one oven, and shall deliver forth bread by weight, and the Lord does
denounce by ye Prophet, that the Israelites shall take for there sustenaunce
bread and water, by weight and measure. But here he foretells not so much
the scarcity of corn and victualles, as that woeful scarcity and hunger of
the word of God, which Amos says shall come upon the world for the contempt
of the same.

Verse. 6. And I heard a voice in the midst of the 4. beasts say: A measure
of wheat for a penie, and three measures of barley for a penny, and oyel and wine
hurt thou not. etc.

LEast he should think this famine to be the most bitterest of all the
plagues, he hears an oracle out of the midst of the 4. beasts, that this
punishment shallbe tolerable, as that which should not bring utter
destruction. For he proclaymeth one measure called Chenix of wheat for a
penye, and three of the same measures of barley for a penny, and that there shall
be no scarcity of wine and oyel. Chenix was a measure of wheat and barley, so
much as should suffice a servant, for one days sustenaunce. The old
interpretor does translate it two pownde, Budeus four pound, Pollux writes
that it weieth but three pound. Ezechiel in Chap. 4. does allow for the
sustenaunce of one man for a day twenty sycles, that is one pound of bread,
and the sixth part of a hin of water. And the Roman penny comed under Domitia^
was almost as much as 7. of our pence. And at that time they did work for a
penie a day. When as therefore every days labor should be spent for there
breadcorne of wheat* he signifies that the scarcity should be great, but yet
such as might be borne, seeing there should be greater plenty of barley, and no
scarcetie of wine and oil. And this figure seems to represent the state of
the Church, after it had taken root in the world, but chiefly after the
peace granted thereto by constantine when as besides the horrible herisyes
which did openly defyle and corrupt the doctrine of Christ, many other
traditions of men and unprofitable ceremonies crepte in, by which a great
famine of sincere and pure doctrine which is the spiritual meat of the soul,
was brought into the Church, and yet not so great, but that there was
sufficient of necessary food, to the keeping of eternal life. For although
they suffered the penury of pure wheate^ bread, yet there was barley bread,
which they might use although not for so pure nurishment, yet for necessary
food. Notwithstanding in the mean time, there wanted not matter of spiritual
joy and gladness, (which is figured by the wine and oyel) to the godly,
which holding the only foundation of there faith, which is Christ, have
obtained remission of sins, peace and quietness of conscience, through the
benefit of the same Christ.

Verse. 7. And when he had opened the fourth seal I heard the voice of the
fourth beast say come and see. etc.

THe fourth seal being opened, he is admonished by the voice of the fourth
beast to come nerer and to behold the thing more certenlie and throughlye.

Verse. 8. And I looked and behold a pale horse and his name that sat on him was
death, and hell followed after him, and power was given unto him over the
fourth part of the earth, to kill with sword, and with hunger and with death,
and with the beasts of the earth. etc.

THis pale horse which carries death upon his back. signifies the plague and
other pestilent dyseases, which by the just judgment of God do slay men for
the contempt of the Gospel. And after death follows hell, that it should
not be thought to be a pestilence of the bodies only, but that with eternal
death of the soul and torments of hell do follow after. And truly hell
always follows the death of the body, except in those only, to whom the
stinge of death is broken, and the victory of hell spoiled and taken away, by
the death of Christ. And least it might be thought, that pestilence only
should devour the reprobate, he hereth that there was power given unto him, to
destroy the third part of men with sword, famine, pestilence, and teeth of
wild beasts. with these 4. kinds of punishments God being angry, does
strike, as Moses witnesses in the 26. chap. of Leuit. Whereby we gather that
the condition and state of those times shall be very miserable, this terrible
thretening shall be fulfilled. Such as those times were when the empire of Rome
was spoiled and wasted fair and wide by the Goths, Hunnes, Vandalles, and
other barbarouse nations. For histories do testify, that there were never
more manifest examples of Gods vengeance, then in those miserable times, when
all places were filled with murderings, burninges, famishment, pestilence, and
beasilye cruelties of barbarouse people. What meruail, if then the pure
doctrine of Christ almost driven out, and condemned in many places were sylent,
whereas before it flourished wonderfully, if heresies, perverse, and wicked
opinions, and traditions of men did then receive so great strength? when by the
just judgment of God the minds of men must be bewitched with lies and
falsehood, for neclecting the truth: if the Church smitten and shaven with the
persecutions of pagans and heretics was greatly deminished and brought into
a straight and narow Rome? But against all these calamities and miseries the
minds of the faithful ought to have been armed, that they should not faint
in such sturdie storms of temptations, but hold and keep an undefiled and
constante profession of there faith even to the end.

Verse. 9. And when he had opened the fyft seal, I saw under the altar the
souls of them that were killed for the word of god and for the testimony
which they maynteyned. etc.

THe opening of the fifte seal declares the state of the faithful after they
are departed this life. For when as they being oppressed with infinite
calamities, were all the day long as sheep appointed to the slaughter, this
doubt might rise in the minds of the godly, what good or evil may come to
them after death? when all there life they are entreated after a wretched
manner, and afterward by the Barbarouse cruelty of there enemies they are
diliuered up and put to most bitter death. Christ takes away this scruple or
doubt, when as he shows, that those which were slain for the word of God,
and the testimony of the Gospel, which they always boldly and frelye
professed, do after this wretched life, inioye blessed tranquillity in heaven
and do look and wait for just revenge upon there wicked enemies. And the
souls of those that were departed out of this life are placed under the altar,
that is, they rest under ye defense of Christ, which is made to god, for them,
the priest, altar and sacrifice, and they them selves also are offered up in
earth by martyrdom for a sacrifice of acceptable and sweet smell. Ve^e fitly
therefore rest is assigned unto them in heaven under ^he altar. But as
concerning the place in which the spirits and souls of the saints are
placed, none other thing is here sign^^^ed by the altar then that which in the
16. Chap. of ^. Luke, is men^ by the bosom of Abraham, and in the 23. Chapter
by paradise.

Verse. 10. And they cried with a loud voice saying how long tariest thou Lord
holy and true to judge and avenge our blood on them that devil on the earth.
etc.

THe blessed spirits wish and desire that the glory of God may be extolled
above all things, they are here therefore brought in by a figure called
prosopopeia taking it grievously that the judgment of God was so long
deferred: that vengeance was not yet taken upon the bloody enemies of Christ
and his Church. But it is not so much here expressed in what kind of affection
they are endued, as it is described, what there persecutoures have deserves.
That we should not either imagine those to be lost which give there lives for
the glory of Christ, or think that the wicked shall always preuail in there
wickedness. They cry with a loud voice, that they seem to be touched with an
earnest desire of revenge. How long o Lord. etc. They do not expostulate or
quarrel with God, as though he were unjust unto them, in that he deferred
there revenge in long, but according to the manner of the godly they pour
forth there complaints into his bosom. For when they call him holy and true,
they signifye that he neither can nor will suffer any thing, which is not in
all points agreeable to his righteousness and truth. For it is not agreeable
to the justice of God, that he should always suffer the injuries done to the
godly to be unrevenged and it is contrary to the truth of his word, that
wicked men should escape unpunished, of whom he has promised so often that he
will take due punishemente upon them for there wicked and heynouse offenses.

Verse. 11. And long white garments were given to every one of them.

WHite garments are signs of dignity, wherewithe Christ extolleth the souls
of them, which have not refused valiantly to suffer death for the testimony
of his Gospel. For although they do not as yet inioye the full and perfect
joy of happiness (such as shall be given them after the restoring of both body
and soul) yet they live and reign with there head Christ in heaven, inioying
happy and blessed tranquillity, but yet so that they carefully under hope, do
wait for the restoring of the bodies, and the time of the last judgment. And
this dignity comes unto them only by Christ, as we shall hear in ye next
chapter following, of those that have washed there garments in the blood of
the lamb.

And it was said unto them that they should rest for a little season until
the number of there fellows and brethren and of them that should be killed as
they were, were fulfilled. etc. They are commanded to rest in this quietness,
and to bear patiently for a little time the deferring of the last judgment,
that the whole number of them whom God has likewise ordained to the glory of
martyredome, should obtain with them the same palm and praise of victory.
Whereby it is euidente, that although almost infinite thousand martyrs
which suffered under those ten famous persecutions, that yet there
remainethe a great number of the godly, which are reserved and kept and shall
suffer the like things, in the openinge of the sixth and seventh seals.
Moreover the time is called short, although it last many hundred years after,
because the Lord has appointed the end and terms of the same, which if we
have respect to the everlasting comfort and consolation, ought to seem very
short. For what equallity or proportion is there of that which has an end,
with that which is infinite? Neither are our sufferinges to be esteemed if they
be compared to the glory that shall follow. Moreover we understand by this
place yt can none promote or prefer them selves to the glory of martyredome,
but he which is appointed and ordained of God for the same work. Lastly we are
sufficiently instructed by this vision, yt the souls of those that are
departed do not sleep without any sense or felinge of happiness, when with a
loud voice they desire revenge they praise and magnifye God, are clothed in
white garments are commanded to wait and abide for the victory of there
fellows and brethren.

Verse. 12. And I beheld when he opened the sixth zeal and lo there was a
great earth quake, and the sun was black as sackecloth made of hear, and
the moon waxed even as blood. etc.

THe openinge of the sixte zeal sets forth a terrible earth quake and also
diverse wonderouse things of heaven. Christ prophesied in the 24. chap. of
Matthew, that there shall be famine, and pestilence and great earthquakes in many
places al which things, as also they are foretold to come by this vision, so
if they be understood without figure, as Christ himself testifies, they are
only the beginniges and as it were the foretellinges of sorrows, and truly
there cronicles are full of many great earthquakes in diverse and sundry nations
and cuntries, which as Il grant that they were signs of euilles should
follow, so I doubt not but that by the earthquake here are forshewed great
alterations and chaunges of empire and religion, which should follow almost
through the whole world. such as were when the wicked pestilence of mahomet
prevailed in the world through the sarasines, and suddenly spread over the whole
empire of the cast and at length the turks succedinge oppressed ye greatest
part of the west also. Then truly Christ the son of righteousness suffered
a great eclipse, when the pure doctrine of the gospel was darkened almost to
all which seemed to be like sackeclothe of hear to them, whose eyes the
brightness of this world had so tied and bound that they were blind even in
the clear and broad daily light. For Christ himself suffered not any part of
his own glory to be deminished: which was even then also the light of the
world and the son of righteousness, to the faithful although they were very
few, but that he seemed to be so to the wicked multitude, when as most sharp and
cruel persecution raging, very few durst truly and boldly profess him. The
moon that is the church which boroweth here light of the sun, that is of
Christ, is not only (the sun being darkened) deprived of her light, but
also through the horrible slaughters and calamities is all over covered with
bloudye colloure.

Verse. 13. And the stars of heaven fell unto the earth even as a fygge tree
casts of her untimely fygges when she is shaken of a mighty wind. etc.

THe doctors and teachers, which in the sincere doctrine of ye Gospel seemed to
shine as the stars in heaven, and other professors also, now overcome with
calamities, and oppressed with miseries, do fall down to earthly things:
they forsake Christ and his Church and embrace this present world. And least
they may seem to be few which shall do this, he shows that there shall be
innumerable, which no otherwise the^ untimely fygges do fall from the fygge
tree when it is shaken of a vehement and mighty wind, even so together and as
it were with one violent motion, many, and at length almost all, shall fall from
the confession of the heavenly doctrine to the dross and corruption of this
world.

Verse. 14. And heaven departed a way as a scrole when it is rolled together and
all mountains and Islles were moved out of there places. etc.

THe doctrine of ye gospel being taken from among the^ which was wont to open
heaven, the very sight also of the heaven it self is taken from the eyes of
men. The similitude of the scrole rolled together does express the sudden
taking away of the same. The mountains also and the Isles which were wont to
be refuges and places of safeguard in such calamities, are not free them selves
from the same terrible motions, so that there apeareth no comfort at all to
wretched and miserable men either in heaven or in earth.

Verse. 15. And the kings of the earth and the great men and the rich men, and
the chief Captains, and the mighty men, and every bond men and every free
man, hid them selves in dens and in rocks of the hills. etc.

THese proud despisers of the wholesome doctrine, which giving them selves to
riote, and vain pleasures, have neclected the true worship of God, whether
they be kings, or wether they be great men, rich men, or chief captains,
potentates or mighty men, with all there train, both free and bound, shall
now bear the punishmente of there impiety, when as for fear of the evils
hanginge over them, they shall fearfully hide them selves in the dens and
holes of the mountains.

Verse. 16. And they said to the hills and rocks fall on us and hide us from
the presence of him that sits on the throne and from the wrath of the lamb.
etc.

NOw they which hitherto have carelessly despised God, being pricked with the
furies of there own conscience, do at length acknowledge these calamities to
be sent upon them from God being angry. They do not so much fly death, which
they desire to be upon them for ever, but the sight of him that sits upon
the throne, and the wrath of the lamb, which is judge both of the living and
dead: what the^ are the torments of hell when the horror and fear of
judgment is so great? and we may note that the wrath of the lamb which is so
gentle to his friends, is terrible to his enemies, although in time past he
offered up him self to the Jews to be slain.

Verse. 17. For the great day of his wrath is come and who can endure it. etc.

NOw they confess that the time is come in which they shall be punished for
there wickedness, and that it cannot be avoided, but that they must needs
feel the severity and sharpness of the la^be which no mortal creature is
able to bear. Let us therefore kiss the son while he offreth himself unto
us easy to be pleased, that being free from these evils, we may live
blessedly with him for ever.

The seventh Chapter.
THe blessed rest of the souls departed out of the body, is described before
in the openinge of the fyfte seal, that is the state of the triumphante
Church in heaven, now is seemed convenient, that it should be declared in this
Chapter, which does perteyne to the opening of the sixte se^le, what should
be, the state and condition of the Church militante in earth. For the same
being preserved and kept out of the greatest affliction of all which heretofore
has happened and signed with the seal of the living God delivered out of the
calamities and miseries of this life, at length is taken up with those that
went before into the same degree and state of blessedness.

Verse. 1. And after that. etc.

AFter this terrible earthquake, which altogether draw away slothfulness and
dilicacie from the wicked Princes of the world and all the champeons of Satan's
guard which being greatly amazed with terror of wind, they rather wished any
kind of death then that they would be drawn to the tribunal seat of the
angry Judge: Ihon might meruail what should become of the Church of Christ.
He is admonished therefore by this vision, that not one of the whole number of
the faithful whom God has predestinate to eternal life can be brought from
the constant confession of the true faith either by the cruel torments of the
persecutours or by the subtle and privy deceites of heritiques, and false
deceyuers, although never so great storms of persecutions fall upon them.

I saw four Aungells stand on the four corners of the earth holding the
four winds of the earth, that the voices should not blow on the earth never
on the sea neither on any tree. etc. It pertayneth not greatly to us to know
wether they were good or evil Augels, for God as it seems god unto him self
executes his judgments both by good and evil Angels. For a^ evil Angel
brought in the plague in the time of king David. A good Angel also
ouerthrewe the army Sennacheri^ with a mighty great slaughter. Although I do
incline to the Judgment of those which contend that evil Angels are
understood in this place. Howesoeuer it be, it is thought good to the just
judgment of God, to take away almost altogether out of the world, the free
preachinge of the gospel, which before sownded in the whole earth. And the
metaphore of the wind, does very fitly agree: for the word being taken away
the force of the holy ghost, which shows him self forth in the preachinge
of the gospel, is restrained and holden back, that he should not blow upon
the earth nor upon the sea, neither upon any tree. For that which wholesome and
seasonable winds are to the world, the same is the holy ghost, to the
Church. The mystery of the word therefore being taken out of the world, the
Church must needs suffer a sore decay and deminishinge. And here no doubt is
signified the greateste defection and departing almost of the whole world, from
the pure doctrine of the gospel, such as happened in those miserable times,
when the pestilente doctrine of Mahomete invaded all Asia and Africa, the
popish dross daily received great increase in Europe. And it is very like,
that here is noted that general Apostasy, which Saint Paul foresaw
should go before the reuealinge of Antichrist 2. Thessal. 2. chap. which is
plainly described in the openinge of the seventh seal.

Verse. 2. And I saw an other angel ascend from the rising of the sun
which had y^ seal of the living God, and he cried with a loud voice to y^ 4
angels, to whom power was given to hurt the earth and the sea. etc.

I agree with them which understand Christ to be signified by this angel, to
whom those things, which are showed to John in y^ vision, concerning this
angel, do properly belong. And it is so usual in the scriptures, that the
angels do bear or represent the person of there lord and head Christ, that I
will not tarry in it. But as concerning this present place, y^ which is here
spoken, does truly agree to our savior Christ, that he ascended from the
rising of the sun, who Zachary in his song almost with the same words
magnifieth rising and springing from an high. For he is the sun of
righteousness, before whose risinge as well in the greater world as in the less
which is man, nothing is found but most thick darckenes. He is said in this
place to have ascended from the rising of the sun, that by his brightines he
might bring some comfort and consolation, to the godly, for we herd before yt
the sun was darkened in the world, as though it had put on a sack clothe of
hear. But that is applied to the sight of the wicked and of hipocrites, for
Christ ascending from the rising of the sun to the Church his spouse, does
illuminate the same with the most pleasant and brighte beams of his gloriouse
light. Furthermore Christ has yt holy seal of the living God, that is the
everliving, and from whom all life does flow, which seals with the holy
spirit all those whom the heavenly father the founteyne of life, has elected
and chosen to eternal salvation, and who^ he has redeamed by his death, and
restored, by his resurrection into newnes of life. Lastly with great
authority he restrains the force of the 4. Angels, to whom it was
granted that they might hurt the earth and the sea, that they should not touch
any thing at all until he had placed the servant of God in safety. This
place does most clearly show, that God does never so grieuouslye show forth his
wrath against the world; that he should cast away the ear he has over his
Children.

Verse. 3. Hurt ye not the earth, neither the sea, neither the trees, until we
have sealed the servants of our God in there forehedes. etc.

HE commands them that they hurt not the earth, nor the sea, nor the trees,
before that he shall by the setting on of his seal destinguish and sever the
servants of God, from the wicked and hypocritical. Here the punishments of
the ungodly are deferred. while there is provision made for the elect. The
flood came not before Noah with his family had entered into the arcke. And the
Angels witness that they can do nothing to y^ city of the Sodomits, except
Lot were first brought forth into safety. The angel spared the first borne of
ye Egyptians so long, until the posts of the Israelites were sprinkled with
the blood of the paschal lamb, a little before night. And there is the like
thing in the 9. Chapter of Ezekiell whereas the six armed men were sent forth
to destroy the city of Jerusalem, they are commanded to follow the man
clothed with the linen garment, having the inckehorne of a scribe at his
gyrdle, who^e God sent before to set a mark in ye forehead of those, which did
morn for all the abominatio^s which were committed in the city. Those whom
this first did not mark, he committethe to the other to be slain. But they
are signed in this place, not that they should be kept free from pestilence or
murder, but that being delivered from eternal death, they might be knit and
joined to God and Christ there deliverer. And there are none signed besides the
servants of God. And this is also moreover to be noted, that they receive the
print of the seal in there foreheads, to this end, yt as they are the
servants of God, so they may also be known of all men to be such, neither
that they should be ashamed, wheresoever need shall require, to confess whose
doctrine and religion they profess. And although they are signed in there
hearts by the holy ghost, yet the print and figure of the same seal apearethe
in there foreheades, when as with the heart we believe to righteousness, and with
the mouth we confess unto salvation.

Verse. 4. And I herd the number of them that were sealed, and there were sealed
and hundred and four and forty thousand of all the tribes of the Children of
Israel. etc.

THe number of the elect is certain to God, so that one of them can not
perish whom Christ has taken under his protection, for this foundation of
God shall always stand immovable, having this seal: the Lord knows who
be his: and let him depart away from unrighteousness, whosoever names the
name of the Lord. The number truly of the elect is great, and greater then men
would think. The elect in deed are not many if we compare them with the
infinite mylions of the reprobate, but when a man would think that there
remain very few and almost no true worshippers of GOD at all, yet Christ
has his Church. There were seven Thousand that is many thousands of the
Israelites, (when as Elias believed he was alone) which had never departed
from God to the wicked worshipping of Baale. And when we might think the
nation of the Jews almost taken out of the world, by the horrible persecutions
and calamities, which chanced after the opening of the four seals: S. John
hears an hundred and four and forty thousand of those that were signed of
all the tribes of Israel. This number is composed of twelve thousand, twelve
times repeated, the number of twelve signifies yt gathering together out of
yt miseable dispersio^, into one body of Christ and his Church which was
founded in 12. patriarchs, and afterward being foully dispersed, was gathered
together by ye 12. Apostels, which were the preachers of Christ. And Christ
would signify the same thing by the seue^ty and two Disciples sent forth
throughoute the whole region, when this number of so many elders instituted by
Moses, was counted famous among them, and it might plainlye enoughe admonish
the Jews, that the Messiah was come, which would gather together again into one
body, the wa^dering and straying Jews and the Israelits dispersed over the
whole world. We are caught here, that there remains a body of ye Church, to
God, although the members be separated one from another with never so long
distance of place, so that they hold the holy bond of unity in Christ there
head. For wheresoever the dead carcas is, thither will the Eagles be gathered.
Matthew 24.

Verse. 5.6.7.8. Of the tribe of Judah were sealed twelve thousand, of the tribe
of Ruben were sealed twelve thousand. etc.

HE counts it not enough to rehearse the whole number of those that were
sealed, except he should also number out of every particular tribe, twelve
thousand of those that were signed. Which thing he does for this cause,
least any thing of the promises of God, which yet remained most famous and
clear, concerning the restoring of the commune wealth of Israel, might
seem to fail. Not that it is necessary that an equal number should to be
taken out of every tribe, but because the number of twelve, notes perfection,
and it shewethe that the number of the elect is determinate with GOD,
likewise as the multitude of Soldiers is known to there Captain, which that
he may know the certain number of them the better and that order may be kept,
deuideth and distributeth his whole army into ensigns or standerdes, which
Christ does here. Otherwise there is no difference or prerogative of tribes in
the first election. For the order of the ensigns is otherwise distributed
here, then of Moses in the 2. Chapter of the book of Numbers although the
privilege of Judah kept, for the mystery of our redeamer and head, for Christ
came of the Jews. But it causes some to marvel, why the tribe of Dan should
be altogether omitted and left out of this rehersall. The ancient writers
supposed by the Prophecy of Iacobe that Antichrist should he borne of that
tribe, and therefore it was not to be reckoned among the elect tribes, which is
to weak and vain, and it brought forth mo^strouse fables concerning
Antichrist, when as the words of Iacobe sound no such matter Gene. 49. But
only, that like as serpents do set upon men unawares, so the nature of this
tribe should be such that by subtilties and deceytes it should overcome the
enemies. The simplest and plainest cause, why one tribe was omitted, is this,
that there might be place for the tribe of Leuy, which was not to be left out
of that rehersall, for the notable Mystery therein contained, For when as it
had no inheritance in Canaan the land of promise (because the lord was there
portion) now the priesthood being translated to Christ, the holy ghost would
plainly express, that the tribe of Leui also is admitted to the partaking of
the heavenly inheritance, although that among the rest it had no part in the
earthly omision, but of so great a number of Jews which are here rehearsed we
may gather that mystery which Paul touches in the 11. Chap. to the Romans That
blindness is partly happened unto the Jews until the fullness of the
gentiles become in and then all Israel shall be saved.

Verse. 9. And after this I beheld, and so a great multitude which no man could
number, of all nations, kindered, people, and tongues. etc.

IN the first place are numbered those that were signed of Israel which is the
first begotten of God, and after follow the gentiles in there order, which as
the Jews are above them in dignity of time, so likewise they are above them
in multitude and number. A great multitude, (says he) which no man could
number, but yet not of an uncertain number but which is known to God, and
can not be comprehended of men, out of all nations, kindredes, people and
tongues, God is no acceptor of persons but of every nation those that love
him, and work righteousenes, are accepted of him. For in Christ Jesus there is
neither Jew, nor gentile, Scithian or Barbarian, but those whom God has
chosen he has called, who^e he has called he has sanctified, whom he has
sanctified, he has glorified. We se here what a wounderfull great company
of the faithful, by the meruailouse counsel and providence of God besides all
hope of man, is escaped out of so great waves of persecutions. And where as we
thought the Church to be almost destroyed, yet great remnantes of the same to
be preserved by the help of God. We may learn hear that the Church is not
to be sought with the bodily eyes, neither the multitude thereof to be
measured by the Judgment of the senses. For if the Church should always
flourish in the eyes of men, there had been no need that the minds of the
godly should be confirmed by this vision, against that temptation by which
the whole Church should seem to be utterly overthrown, when all things
apeared full of slaughters, herisies falshoodes, defectio^s, that sound rock,
which is promised shall stand against hell gates* which was no where seen with
man's eyes.

Standing before the throne and before the lamb. etc. They which before were
aliants and strangers from y^ Church to whom there was no access open to
God, now are citisius thereof, and the sons of God through the lamb, which
takethe away not the sins of the Jews only, but of the whole world, so
that they may bouldly stand in the presence of God and of Christ, when as the
wicked desired nothing more then to be hid from the presence of him that sat
upon the throne, and from the wrath of the lamb, as we heard in the Chapter
going before.

Clothed with long white robes and palms in there hands. etc. There aparell
and decking eis here described, yt they are clothed in long white garments,
which are tokens of dignity and innocence that they bear palms in there
hands they testify and declare that they are conquerers of the world the
^leshe, and the devil, but because he speaks more at large hereafter of
there happiness, less shall here suffice.

Verse. 10. And they cried with a loud voice saying salvation comes of our
God that sits upon the throne and of the lamb. etc.

THere thanke^ullnesse is declared by the loudnes of there voice, that they
cried out with loud voice, giving worthy honor to God. But this is chiefly
to be observed, that there is one voice of all those that be saved, that they
refer all there salvation that they have received, wholly to God and Christ.
Salvation (say they) to him that sits upon the throne of our God and to the
lamb. These do attribute no part of there salvation to there own deserts,
no part to works of superarogation, no part to creatures although never so
holy, but they ascribe all the glory of the same being restored in God and
Christ, this is the Catholic doctrine of y^ Church, howsoever the Roman
Antichrist condemns it of heresye y^ cause not heard, and persecuteth the
professores of the same with fire and sword, and exquisite torments both by
sea and land.

Verse. 11. And all the Angels stood round about the throne and about the
elders and the 4. beasts, and they fell before the throne on there faces, and
worshipped God saying, Amen. etc

ALthough the whole root of the papists abhor and detest this doctrine as
heretical and Scismaticall, yet it has for defenders even infinite
thousands of Angels, which about the throne of the elders and the four
beasts, do diligently wait upon the will and pleasure of God, as we have
learned in the 5. chap. these do allow with there consent, the triumpha^t song
of the blessed spirits. For after they have yielded reverence to God, with due
submission, which they are wont before they dare bring forth any thing into
his presence, first they testify there godliness in the approving and alowinge
the former song, saying Amen. Afterward that they may satisfye there own
zeal, they expound the same sentence with many mo words.

Verse. 12. Praise and glory and wisdom and thanks, and honor and power and
might, be unto our God for ever more. Amen.

TO this end belongs this heaping together of words that they may testify
ye by all means they ascribe all glory to God alone. Therefore they express
the same thing with mo words all those are, praise and thanks giving, honor
and glory, power and strength. For we can never attribute to much to God in
praises. And by this note or marcke we may descerne the true doctrine of God
from that which is counterfere and forged, for that doctrine which fears to
give to much to god, as the popish doctrine does, is altogether false and
knows not the infinite Majesty of God. For the papists do fly and eschew
this confession, that they should ascribe all laud, glory, and praise, to God,
least nothing should be left which they might attribute to S. Images, to there
works and other there profane toys and trifles.

Verse. 13. And one of the elders spoke saying unto me, what are these that are
arased in long white robes? and whence came they?

Saint Ihon does meruail secretly with him self at the usiber and gloriouse
beauty of those, which after the sealeo^ Israelites ^ame forth before y^
throne. Yet he durst not ask who they were modestly waiting whether that
should be revealed unto him or not, by the permission of God. One of the elders
therefore makes answer not to the question but to ye doubt of Ihon
familierly talking with him, and asking him, whether he knew well what they
were, which were araied in long white garments and from whence they came.

Verse. 14. And I said unto him Lord thou know according to. etc.

IHon makes answer according to his simplicity, honorably (as the manner is
of speaking to a noble personage) calling the elder Lord that he is ignorant,
but yet hops that he shall be instructed of him concerning the condition of
them, who^ he believes to know the same.

And he said unto me these are they which came out of great tribulation. etc.
This elder declares first what they are and afterward whence they came. These
are (says he) those which by the benefit of God are delivered out of that
horrible affliction which before was described should come* and now being free
from all there labors, they are received unto blessed rest until the day of
resurrection, truly this seems wonderful and strange, that out of so great an
earthquake which did shake all parts of the world, such a number could be
saved, but that we may confess the meruailouse counsel of God to be far
above the capacity of our wit.

And have enla^ged there long robes and have made there long robes white in the
blood of the lamb. etc. He sets forth two notes of dignity to be
considered in there garments, the breath and the color, they ought to
acknowledge, to have received both of them by the benefit of Christ. Large
garments are the appareill of noble personages and mighty men. This largenes
they go in the blood of Christ, which hanged naked upon the Cross that he
might bewtifully cloth us. And they borrowed there white color, (which is as we
said before a token of dignity and innocence) of the red blood of the lamb
which though it always continue red, and as it were even new (...) has this
meruailouse quality, that in washing (...), it tourneth the purple color of
garments, in^o the whitenes of snow or wolle, according to that in the 1.
Chapter of Iesay if your sins shall be as red as scarlet they shall be made as
white as wolle, lastly we must note that all this whitenes is placed in there
garments and not in there bodies, that we may acknowledge that they do not
shine in there own righteousness, but that there uncleanness is covered with the
innocence of Christ, even as with a large garment.

Verse. 15. And therefore they are before the throne of God. etc.

NOt because they trust to there own merits, but because being covered with
the righteousness of Christ they are beautiful to behold, they dare come forth
in to the presence of the throne of the immortal and everliving God. Truly
the dignity of this garment is meruailouse, because they do were it although
they be privy of there own infirmity, yet they are not afraid to come into
the presence of ye most just judge.

And they serve him day and night in his temple. etc. God does accept free
service which are clothed with the innocence of Christ, without which ornament
the service of none can please him, but he will expel them out of his
familye as vagabondes, and runnagates, which do thrust any service upon him
which they would have to be accepted at his hands without Christ. But now
there obedience is acceptable unto him, so that they serve him in his temple as
holy preistes day and night, that is for ever, that they apply them selves to
his holy worship as though they had never been profane. We may learn here
by what means we may offer up in the Church reasonable service accepted of
God, yt is if unclothed of filthy garments of our flesh and having put on the
righteousness of Christ, we come forth into his presence.

And he that sits on the throne will dwell among them. etc. It is not only
accepted of God which his faithful servant do, but he takes upon him the
office of a merciful and liberal lord, when he on the other side becomes
there patron and defendoure, and as the hen covers her chickens, so God will
keep his servant free from the invasions of all evils.

Verse. 16. And they shall hunger no more neither thirst any more neither shall
the sun light on them neither any heat. etc.

ALthough so long as they followed the warfare of Christ in earth, often times
they suffered hunger, often thirst, and parthinge heat of the sun and other
such kind of adversities, now being made free and losed from the bond of
warfare, they feel no more such calamities neither any discommoditye at all
and of ye place some do not amiss that the fire of purgatory is here utterly
quenched, when as this Angel pronounces, that ye godly shall feel no kind of
burninge heat after this life.

Verse. 17. For the lamb which is in the midst of the throne shall feed them
and shall lead the^ unto the lively fountains of waters and god shall wipe
away all tears from there eyes. etc.

THis is a reueng of the cause, because the lamb which has redeemed them
sittinge in the midst of the throne equal to God his Father, has taken the
care and charge of them, and and shall lead them to the perpetual fountains
of living waters which being satisfied, they shall not thirst for ever, and
God himself also will wipe away all tears from there eyes, when from
hencforth there shall be no cause of sorrow and mourning offered unto them, but
they shall have the fruition of perpetual joy world without end. Amen.

The eight Chapter.
THere remains behind as yet the openinge of the seventh seal which being
opened there, are more greiuous calamities, then as yet have been hard of to be
sent forth into the world. When as the kings most terrible or rather the
tyranny of antichriste is described.

Afterward his ruin is fore told and lastly the signs of Christ coming to
judgment do appear.

Verse. 1. And when he had opened the seventh seal, there was silence in
heaven about the space of half an hour, and I saw the seven Aungells standing
before God, and to them were given seven trumpets. etc.

BEcause the greatest matter that ever hapened, and most worthy due
consideration, were made manifest in the openinge of y^ seventh seal, his mind
was to be prepared to ye diligent making of ye same, with a rare and
unaccustomed manner. There is silence therefore made in heaven as it were for ye
space of half an ower in with space whilst all things were silent, the
Apostell should sterre up his mind to the diligent consideringe, what
misterye should be revealed to the Church in the opening of the seventh seal,
which he now saw opened. Moreover when as his mind was holden in suspense half
an hour in ye waiting for of those things which should follow, he could not
but diligently print in his mind the things which so desirousely he had
waited for to know. But this silence may be also referred to the deliberation
of God, for Princes and wise men are accustomed when as they will decree or
pronounce any thing, concerning great matters and weighty affairs, to have
some silence in the mean time that they may not seem to have done it, but
with great deliberation not that the counsels of God are prolonged with
doubtful consultatio^s according to the manner of the counsels of men, but
because he would prepare our minds to the diligent consideration of his works
an^ words, by such signs as it were by aides: if therefore we will
understand those things which are revealed in the opening of this seal, let
us bring minds altogether, void of worldly troubles, and casting of the cares
of all other things for a time, let us give our attendance only to this, that
we may diligently receive those things which the holy ghost has spoken. I know
that this silence is diversely and far otherwise expounded of others, and some
do fly to vain and unprofitable speculations: But this interpretation which
I have brought, as it is the playnest, so it seemed most convenient and fit to
the purpose.

Verse. 2. And I saw seven Aungells which stood before God and to them were
given seven trumpets. etc.

ALl this preparation is set forth to express the greatness of the thing,
first there came forth seven Angels into the presence of god, they stand a
certain while as it were waiting what service god would command the^,
afterward there are delivered into there hands seven trumpetes, yet they do
not straitway sound the same, but they wait for the will of God in all
things. All these do after a sort prouosticate and foretell the heuinesse of
Gods judgments which should shortly after be made manifest. But the number
seven, of the Angels, as otherwhere so also hear, does represent the whole
fellowship of them, which are all continually most redely prepared, to the
obedience of god, although as it seems good to his infinite wisdom, he
apointeth now these, now those to the executing of diverse businesses. But here
the Angels are appointed to be tru^petters, which is because they are ordained
to publish ye judgments of god in the world. For as it is the manner of
kings and Emperors and always has been, to publish to the people there
decrees, especially perteyninge to wars, with the sound of a trompet: so God
has described under a like figure the judgments which he has prepared
against his enemies and despisers of his Gospel, when they are to be made
manifest in there times. And the seven trumpetes, do signifye all the
reuelatio^s of Gods judgments, like as the number of seven is universal, and
signifies fullness in the writings of the prophets. When as therefore seven
Angels go forth with so many trumpets, there is meant, that all the kinds of
punishments, which were included in the seven seals, are to be repeated in
this last seal. No meruail therefore, if our minds with so great preparation,
be stirred up to diligent marking. Moreover if we shall gather the duty of
the doctors and teachers of the Church, by the Angels that sound the trumpets,
we shall not do contrary to reason. And the analogy leads us to the same,
when as there office also is to be declarer of gods judgments. For god has not
been accustomed to send famous plagues into the world, but first me^ were
admonished of the same by prophets and teachers, that all pretense and cloak
of ignorance might be taken from the wicked and if any be curable, they might
repent from there errors, by which being seduced they wandered out of the way,
and so escape the evils hanging over them.

Verse. 3. And an other Angel came and stood before the altar having a
Golden censer. etc.

THis Angel does represent Christ, which is not an Angel by nature, but by
office, and Malachie the prophet calls him the Angel of the covenant. For
when as ye most dangerouse persecution of all, was at hand, under the tyranny
of Antichrist, which is revealed in the opening of the seventh seal^ Christ
comes forth into the presence of God, being the head and preserver of his
Church, as one that would defend the same, against the dangers which were at
hand. Whereby both the greatness of the perilles is expressed, as though now
necessity required that the present help of Christ should be with them, and
as it were to provide them in doubtefull matters: and also the singular love of
Christ toward his, and the especial care he has over them, which when
troubles aproche near, is ready prepared and present to defend the^ before
god, and by continual intercessions to commend the cause of the Church to his
fatherly mercy. And Christ is here brought in exercising the office of an
high priest, (which he has without succession) when as he is placed at the
altar. Whereby he can save for ever those that come unto God through him,
living always for this end, that he may make intercession for them. Hebrews
chap. 7. Which is notablye described under this figure. For he stands at the
altar, not that he may again offer up sacrifice propitiatory, because there is
no oblation for the forgiveness of sin without the shedding of blood. For
this sacrifice being once finished, by which eternal redemption is obtained,
we need not to have it repeated. But when as he is entered into the holy of
holiest that is into heaven, he offerethe up incense in the presence of God,
which are the prayers of the saints upon the golden altar of the incense.
For this figure does allude to the custom of the priests of the old law,
which daily entering into the sanctuary, did offer up incense upon the golden
altar of incense. Exodus 30. Which now the vailes and separations being taken
away and the priesthood translated to Christ only, is removed into the holy
of holiest into which Christ him self has once ascended.

And much odoures was given unto him. etc. The continual prayers of the godly
which they offer up to god through Christ, are odoures or incense, as in the 5.
chap. Verse. 8. And he says much, because when affliction does provoke, the
study of praying is more fervent in the faithful, which when matters are
quiet and pacified, is relented. And this is that pure incense which Malachie
in the 1. Chap. of his prophecy, foretold should be offered up through the
whole earth even from the sun rising to the setting thereof.

That he should offer with the prayers of all saints upon the golden altar
which is before the throne. etc. To this end much incense, (which are the
prayers of the saints) is offered to Christ, yt he might give an incense of
the^ upon ye golden altar which is before the throne. That is, yt by his
intercession which is the mediator and advocate of the Church, the prayers of
the saints might deserve to be herd of the majesty of God. This place
teaches very plainly, that we need none other mediatoures of intercession
with God, then this one Angel, which is Christ, for he alone offers up to God
ye prayers of all saints, and promises that his father shall perform unto
us, whatsoever we shall ask in his name. Moreover when as none either Angel or
Saint, can chaleng this priestly office of Christ without great sacrilege: it
follows y^ no Angel or Saint (this one Aungel of ye covenant being
excepted) can offer up incense upon the golden altar which is before the
throne of God.

Verse. 4. And the smoke of the odours with the prayers of the Saints, went up
before God out of the Angels hand. etc.

THe effect of this oblation is declared, that the prayers of the Saints
being offered as incense by Christ, are a sacrifice of sweet smell in the
presence of God. When as therefore prayers are directed to God with lively and
fervent faith in Christ, they can not but be heard for Christ's sake, which
makes them acceptable to God.

Verse. 5. And the Angel took the censer and filled it with fire of the Altar
and cast it into the earth. etc.

CHrist promises that his father will give the holy spirit to those yt ask
it importunatly, which when he also proceeds from the son, after great
perfume stirred up with prayers of the saints, is sent down into the earth, in
the shape and likeness of fire taken from the heavenly altar, whose fiery force,
or if any thing be more pearsinge then fire, is perceived in the Preachinge
of the word, in constancy of faith, in invincible patience, and other
Heavenly gifts of his. And the great abundance of the same spirit is
signified by the fillinge of the censer for in Isay chap. 6. one of the
Seraphins taking a burning cole with the tongues touched therewith the lips
of ye prophet, that the unworthiness of his sins being taken away, he
might be meet to declare the message of God. But here the great golden
censer, in which the prayers of the saints are offered, is filled with fire,
and is cast into the Church, wandering as a stranger in earth, according to
that saying of Christ I came to send fire into the earth. Luke 12.

And there were voices and thunderinges, and lightnings and earthquake. etc.
The holy ghost can not be in the world but that he will rebuke the same of
sin, of righteousness, and of Judgment, and then do those tumults arise,
that heaven and earth seem to be mingled together, but in the mean time it is
well provided for the Church, that against the most grieuouse persecutions of
Antichrist hanging over her, she being strengthened with Gods ayed, shall not
be overwhelmed with any raging tempests of adversity.

Verse. 6. And the seven Angels having the seven trumpetes prepared them selves
to blow the trumpetes. etc.

AFter that provision was made for the safegarde of the Church, least it
should faint under so great a burden of evils, the seven Angels do
straitway prepare themselves to sound there trumpets, whereby we may easelye
gather, that they were stayed before, so long as Christ made intercession for
the safety of the Church, and with his gifts might arm the faithful to
bear all adversities whatsoever. Which thing although he do continually, yet
it was enough that it should be showed once in a vision.

Verse. 7. So the first Angel blew the trumpet, and there was hayle and fire
mingled with blood, and they were cast into the earth, and the third part of
trees was burnt, and all green grass was burnte. etc.

WHen as every one of Gods Judgments is revealed, an Angel blowing a
trumpete goes before, and after follows the visione which opens the whole
matter. The sounding therefore of the trumpete is a sign that God will open
some thing which ought to be received of men with due reverence and
attention. And he notes by these figures the procedinges and increase of the
tyranny of Antichrist, which by the just judgment of God he shall obtain
through^ the whole world. As S. Paul writes in the 2. to the Thessal. 2. Chap.
That they which received not the love of the truth, that they might be saved,
should be deceived with lies that they might be damned. The like Allegories he
uses in the opening of the seals and will use in the powringe out of the
vials Chap. 16. When he understands that the sentence of God does perteyn to
the whole body of Antichrist and every part thereof: he reckeneth up
therefore the earth, the plants, the sea, the fluds, the heaven, the air, and
all things that are therein, that nothing may seem to remain whole or
untouched. These things therefore I have forewarned, that we should not to
curiously seek subtle and curiouse expositio^s in every word, when we
understand that it is the manner of the prophet, and also often used in this
vision, when as he will describe any general calamity, to rehearse all the
parts of the world after this manner. There followed (says he) after the
sounding of the trumpet of the first Angel, hail, which when it uses to
beat down the fruits of the trees, and the corn of ye earth, is wont to
bring in great famine and scarcity of corn and victuals. But here fails not
only hail, but also flames of fire together therewith, and the blood mingled
with the some makes the plague more horrible. For if the hail leave any thing
not ^ast down, the fire consumes it, or else the blood corrupts and rotteth
it, whereupon he says, yt the third part of the trees and every green
herb was burned. It is declared in the sixte Chap. In the opening of the sixte
seal, yt there was given power to death to sley the fourth part of men, with
sword, with, famine, with pestilence, and with wild Beasts: But here at the
sowndinge of the Trumpettes, it is foreshewed that the third part shall be
afflicted. And there is signified only the dearthe of victuals, as that
Chenix of wheat should be sold for a penny, but here is described a
meruailouse great scarcity, when as every green herb is burnt up. Whereby it
is gathered that these calamities should be greater then those, for the third
part is greater then the fourth part, and the scarcity of victuals is more
grieuouse the^ the dearnes of ye same. Except perhaps he alludeth to the third
part of the world, because in Europe which is esteemed to be the third part of
the world, the tyranny of Antichrist chiefly rages, the want of true and
sincere doctrine, which through the traditions of me^, and unprofitable
ceremonies, although not altogether wicked in the first institution, by long
continaunce of time was brought into the Church, whiles that the greater part
of men was bent to defend the ordinances of the elders, rather then to keep the
commaundeme^ts of Christ him self. Here upon it was necessary that a most
greuouse famine should be brought into the Church. For ye souls of men except
they be daily fedd and nourished with the iewce of Gods word, wax dry and
wither even like unto those herbs upon which blasting wind has blown, or
whith to much parching heat has burned up. We may also in this place not
vnfitlye understand, diverse other plagues coming all together, as by the hail
famine, by the fire pestilence, by the blood war, as histories do testifye,
that all these evils did vehemently rage in the world, in the beginning of the
Roman tyranny. But when as the two latter do immediately follow again, the
former interpretation likes me best: in the mean time I deny not but that the
godly ought to be admonished by those bodily calamities, of what sort that
kingdom of Antichrist should be, which with such unlucky signs and tokens
begone to be spread abroad.

Verse. 8. And the second Angel blew: and as it were a great mountain burning
with fire was cast into the sea and the third part of the sea turned to
blood. etc.

AT the sounding of the second trumpet which admonished that the second
judgment of God should be made manifest, there seemed to fall into the sea as
it were a meruailouse great mountain burning with fire. A horrible sight no
doubt and full of terror, and truly there neded such a wonderful sign to
the describing of the kingdom of Antichrist, which follows immediately after
the want of spiritual food. For this great mounteyne does signifye the
kingdom of Antichrist, as it is usual in the prophets that kingdoms, and
commune wealths are signified by mountains, as in Isay and Daniele. By the
sea which is a gathering together of many waters, the holy ghost understands
in this book, the infinite multitude of people divided into diverse nations,
kindreds and tongues. This whole mountain burns with devouring fire, what
soever shall come next to hand, for like as fire corrupts and consumes into
ashes the matter which is put unto it, even so the pestilent moren of
Antichrist does eat up, raven, and devour all things. And although it be
cast into the sea, yet it is not quenched, but turns the third part of the
sea into boiling blood. And this plague is sent into the world of God in his
wrath, because it would not esteem the most fruitful mount Sion that is the
kingdom of Christ. Therefore the world is compelled to bear the most sharp
and bitter tyranny of Antichrist, which had refused to bear the most sweet
and pleasant yoke of Christ.

Verse. 9. And the third part of the creatures which were in the sea died the
living things I mean, and the third part of ships were destroyed.

WHen as the world stobornly refused eternal life offered by Christ, it can
not fly the most bitter death which by ye kingdom of Antichrist is brought
upon very many. And here may be observed the quantity, quality, and effect,
of the Antichristian kingdom. The quantity is noted, in that it is compared
to a very great mountain, which is so much the worse, as it is spread the
brother, as when the papists do brag and boast that the borders of there
dominion are stretched forth unto the ends of the world, and of the firmament.
The quality is described that like deuouringe fire it burns, destroys, and
wastes all things, although those brawling hyerelings cry out never so loud,
that without this mountain there is no salvation. The effect is declared, in
that it turns the third part of the sea into blood. And how much blood he
has shed by diverse kinds of torments, and especially by fire (yt we may
omit the times that are past) our age that we now live in does see, and our
own eyes do daily testify the same unto us. Moreover we will not declare
what wars, and how cruel he has stirred up in the ages past. But in our
age, what tumults he has raised up in France, in Germany, in Spain, and in
Flanders, who is there through out all Europe which knows not? and in England,
what he has practiced and wroughte even this present year that we write these
things, I would to God it were as ready to be avoided, as it is easy to
remember it. That rightly he may be said to have destroyed the third part
of them that dwell in the sea, and the third part of ships by which we may
understand towns or cities. But at length this fiery mountain shall be cast
into the fiery lake. Which all godly hearts do wish to be done most spedely.

Verse. 10. Then the third Angel blew, and there fell a great star from
heaven burning as it were a tortch and it fell into the third part of Rivers
and into fountaynes of waters. etc.

THe third Angel sownding his trumpet, the Prince and head of this fiery
mountain fell from heaven in the likeness of a great star burning as a
torch. In time past the bishop of Rome shined in the heaven, bewtifull to
behold with the beams of heavenly doctrine, but after that he had by little
and little degenerate into a strange and usurped government (of which defection
the ancient writers co^playned more then a thousand years ago) he begun to
fall from heaven toward the earth, till at the length, for the establishing of
his pride and tirannie, he poisoned and infected all the puere doctrine with
his own inventions, and so in the end he fell into the third part of the
rivers and fountaynes.

Verse. 11. And the name of the star is called wormwood therefore the third
part of the water was turned into wormwood and many men died of the waters
because they were made bitter. etc.

THis Star takes his name of the effect, because with so great bitterness of
his poiso^, he infecteth the pleasant springes of pure doctrine, that he
makethe the waters into which he shall fall deadlye poison, so that as many
as shall drink thereof except a spedy remedy against poison be taken should
perish with everlasting death. And the waters are called bitter which this
star does poison. Not according to the sense and judgment of the flesh, to
which they seem to have the taste rather of honey then of wormwood. But to the
spirit of god, which searches all things by his sharp judgment, this
bitterness is found out. Which all the godly do easily acknowledge, which are
drawn from the pestilente drinkinge of this doctrine, that there is no taste of
heavenly and spiritual swetenes in popery, but a mere bucherie of conscience,
and all things most bitter, when any of them is but a little stirred up and
wakened out of the sleep of security (in which the most part of them are
drowned) and pricked with the sense and feling of there sins. We may learn
hear, that no drop of this bitter water, that is of the papisticall doctrine,
is to be mingled with the pure Gospel of Christ, least that it should taste of
this pestiserouse and poisonfull bitterness.

Verse. 12. And the fourth Angel blew the trumpet, and the third part of the
sun was smitten, and the third part of the moon, and the third part of the
stars, so that the third part of them was darckened, and the day was
smitten that the third part of it could not shine, and the night likewise. etc.

WHen as sound doctrine was corrupted with the pestilence devises and
inventions of men, what could remayn sound in the Church? The third part of
the sun, the moon, and the stars was smitten with thick mist and
darckenes, to those especially which dwell in this third part, in which ye
kingdom of Antichrist bare all the swaye. Hereof by the just iudgmente of God,
ye foul ignorance, even as it were a darcke cloud was sent into ye eyes of
those, which were willingly blind in ye light of knowledge and understanding.
Hereof the third part of the day loses the light* the sun being darckened,
the night also is darckened likewise in the third part, the moon and the
stars losing there light, so yt there appears no sparcke of the light to
expel and drive away the darckenes. And to be short, a most thick cloud of
ignorance which took away a great part of the heavenly light, covered the
world. And one we m^ruaill if the papists glory and boast that ignorance is
the mother of there religion? seeing that this darckenesse went before that
great and horrible defection which is afterward declared.

Verse. 13. And I beheld and herd an Angel flying through the midst of
heaven, saying with a loud voice, woe, woe, woe, to the inhabiters of the earth
because of the sounds to come of ye trumpets of the three Angels which were yet
to blow. etc.

ALthough assuredly the judgments of God are horrible, which were hitherto
revealed with the sound of the four trumpetes, yet there remain much more
greater and greuouser behind. Which undoubtedly are so terrible, that is
behooves us to be stirred up with a new admonition to the diligent
consideration of the same, Saint John therefore saw a certain Angel flying
in the midst of heaven, that he might as well be herd of the heaven, as of the
earth, whom he herd with a loud voice cryinge woe three times, to the
inhabitants of the earth, for the severe sharpenes of those judgments
which were yet to be revealed at ye sou^ding of the other three tru^pets. Here
except we weere as dull as stones, the weight of Gods judgments would drive
away all drowsinesse from us, and stir us up to the reverent receyuinge of
the same, that being delivered out of so miserable calamities, we may serve
him for ever.

The nyenth Chapter.
THere is described in this Chapter, the horrible confusion of the kingdom of
Antichrist, which was established partly by fraud and de^cite, and partly by
violence, until it came to the highest, and then should be discovered by the
restoring of the Gospel, and at length utterly abolished by the coming of
Christ.

Verse. 1. And the first Angel blew and I saw the star which fell from
heaven unto the earth. etc.

WHen as the participle is of the time past, (...) and not (...) I understand
that it was the same star which had fallen before into the rivers and
founteynes. which had the name of wormwood given it, which we said before
does signify the head of this Church, which is the bishop of Rome. And if
any man contend that it were not the same in number, yet I hold that it was the
same in office, for although there have been many popes in number, yet they all
make but one head of Antichrist, which has rule over the mo^strouse body of
the Roman Church. Therefore albeit the Roman prelate shined in time paste in
the heaven even as a star in the hand of the Lord, yet now being cast down
to the earth he has lost all his shininge beauty. It is ridiculouse
therefore that the pope does brag of the dignity of his seat, to be such as
it was acknowledged to have been of the old fathers in there time: and that he
makes mention of the virtues of his predecessors, which were martyrs of ye
primitive Church, all which do pertayne no more to him which is cast out of
the heavenly seat unto the earth, then if the devil should boast of his
principality which in time past he had among the Angels, out of which he has
long time been expelled.

And to him was given the key of the botto^lesse pit. etc. The pope which is
Antichrist boasts of the keys of ye kingdom of heaven in time past committed
to Peter, and with great sacrilege he snacheth and chalengeth them to him
self only, when as they pertayne and are common to all the ministers of Gods
word. But in very deed saint Ihon plainly declares what kind of key is
given unto him, that is the keye of the bottomless pit of hell. That as power to
open the heaven is given to the godly teachers of the Church, so to Antichrist
and his ministers, there is granted powers to open the pit of hell, We may
note here, that the power of the adversary, obteyneth rule in the world, not by
chance or against the will of Christ, but by his will and pleasure, to take
horrible and dreadful vengeance upon the profane contemners of his word.

Verse. 2. And he opened the botomles pit, and there arose the smoke of the pit
as the smoke of a great furnace. etc.

ANtichrist does not slackly and slowly use the key committed unto him, but the
same being received, he straytwaye opens the bottomless pit, which before
was shut up and locked. This place does teach, yt so long as the pure doctrine
of the gospel does flourish and take force, hell is shut, but after the same
