has been silent, or infected and darckened with the profane inventions of men
(as we have showed in the chapter goinge before) the most deep pit of hell is
opened, out of which all kind of evil does breath forth. We see therefore,
that not with out just cause the Angel thundered out woes to the inhabitants
of the earth, when as the pit of hell should be opened to there utter
destruction.

And the sun and the air were darckened by reason of the smoke of the pit.
etc. The pit of hell being opened, two most cursed and abominable evils ascend
out of it, ignorance and error. For by the smoke which darckeneth the air and
the sun, I understand ignorance: by the army of the locusts, the teachers
and defenders of errors. For that ignorance which before was spread only
over the third part of heaven, now the smoke ascends out of the pit of hell,
the miste does darken the whole Sun and the air. And truly how gross and
shameful the ignorance of the former ages has been no man can be ignorant,
which has tasted and known the barbarousenes of those times, by there
writings.

Verse. 3. And there came out of the smoke locustes upon the earth. etc.

THey say that locustes are bred of corrupt smoke, which if we receive for
truth, it is found out, that ignorance is the mother of errors. Howsoever it
be, that the locusts go forth of the smoke, it is manifest that the masters
and teachers of errors took occasion by the ignorance of the people, to
spread a broad there deuilish doctrine and wicked opinions. And like as the
swarms of locustes very often infeste and punish whole regions, even so the
whole routes of these, do infecte, corrupt, and devour all things. It is
very like that by the locustes is signified all the rableme^t of Romish mass
priests, Monckes, and especially of begging friars.

And unto them was given power as the scorpions of the earth have power. etc.
Heretics and mainteyners of wicked opinions can not sow and spread abroad
there poison, but so far as power is granted unto them, which is upon those
that perish. And this power of theirs, which they have to hurt is compared to
the venimouse poison of Scorpions, which though it be of it self but a very
little vermin, yet it has power enough to kill a man. They prick and sling
also secretly like scorpions, for they wind in them selves by privy deceits,
until they shall give a deadlye stroke. To these the Popish clergy is like
in all things, but specially the begging friars, which through a colored show
and visore of humility, do seem little, yet secretly they thrust in the
poisoned stings of there abominable errors, and so they sley men.

Verse. 4. And it was commanded them that they should not hurt the grass of
the earth: neither any green thing, neither any tree; but only those men
which had not the scale in there foreheades.

WE herd before, that the four Aungells were forbidden and stayed that they
should, neither hurt the earth, the sea, nor the treese, before the servants
of God were sealed in there foreheades, so likewise these locustes are
forbidden to hurt the grass, nor the green herbs, nor the trees, but only
those men which were not signed with the seal of god in there foreheades.
Whereby we are admonished, that neither the illusions of Satan nor the subtle
sleyghtes of Antichrist have any force to seduce the elect, which like green
plants being watered with the dew of the heavenly doctrine, are preserved from
the locustes which burn up all things, Psalm. 1. There are rehearsed diverse
kinds of plants, as grass, herbs, and trees that we may know, that all and
every one of the elect are drawn out and delivered from this plague: in which
although God work diversely, as in diverse kinds of plants, yet there is one
only foundation, that God knows who are his.

Verse. 5. And to them was commanded, that they should not kill them but that
they should be vexed five mounthes, and that their poison should be as the pain
that comes of a scorpion when he has strong a man.

Pliny in the 28. Chapter of the eleventh book of the natural history
writes, that the pestilence of the venim of scorpions is importunate, but that
with greater punishment, they sley with slow and lingering death, in three days
space. Not without great cause therefore, the perverse doctrine of the Popes
guard, is compared to the stinging of scorpions, which does not by and by sley
men by violent death, but tormenteth them a certain space with cruel torments,
and at length takes away eternal life. Of such sort are the persuasions of
the merits of works, of satisfactions and the peynes of Purgatory, and of
other such like trumporie, wherewith these locusts torment the miserable
consciences, and which alone were heed in pulpits, in lectures, and in there
shifts. When as in the mean while there was no mention, concerning the merits
of Christ free justification by faith, eternal election, and other points of
wholesome doctrine which are taught in so many places of yt holy scripture. There
is limited unto them a certain space of time in which there is, power to hurt,
granted the^, for five mounths, which is added for the comfort of the godly.
that they may not fear that this plague shall always increase, but the force
thereof shall be broken, before half a years space be finished. But if we will
more narowly interpret this place, this infection shall abound in five hundred
years, but in the sixth age, which goes before ye latter end of ye world, it
shall decay, which we see has come to pas in our age yt almost every where ye
popish clergy is conte^ned, yea even with ye very papists, and at length
without doubt it shall be utterly confounded and brought to nothing.

Verse. 6. Therefore in those days shall men seek death, and shall not find
it, and shall desire to die, and death shall fly from them. etc.

WHen as we heard before that those scorpions do sley with slow death, it is
no meruaill if those yt be stricken of them and tormented with cruel
torments, desire to dye sooner then it is granted to them by the strength of
the poison. By which sentence is expressed the greatness of the torments, by
which the papists do sley the miserable consciences of me^, with there
poisoned opinions, as it were with the singes of scorpions: which when as they
altogether lead from Christ in whom alone all consolation of the godly mind
does consiste: there remains nothing unto them besides the fear of hell
fire, and desperation full of horror.

Verse. 7. And the form of the locustes was like unto horses prep^red to
battle, and on there heads were as it were crowns, like unto gold. etc.

Hitherto he has spoken of there poisoned strength and ^orce, now yt we may
know them the better, he notably painteth the^ forth in their colors. The
form (says he) of there bodies is like to horses prepared to battle, whereby
ye manners of the popish clergy are clearly described, y^ like horses they tune
with swifte course through all things, and are always most ready to
battailles and strifes, if any man say against them by any manner of means.
They have crowns upon there heads, as it were of gold, because all of them,
although they be most obiecte verletes, do challenge unto them selves a certain
kinglye dignity, and they would be had in price and estimation, neither would
they be subject to the civil magistrate, when as notwithstanding they are but
vile locusts, which are noble neither by any virtue, learning or godliness,
and proffitable for nothing but to hurt. Yet at the will and pleasure of these
men all things were governed in time p^st, when as the world honored them as
kings, and kings them selves feared them, as those whith by shrifte and
confession knew all there secreates.

And there faces were as it had been the faces of men etc. They are not
terrible to behold, but lock inside and smoth with the countenaunces of men,
and allure men into there own destruction, for they are meruailouse great
flatterers, which for there lucre and bellies sake, and that they may win
the favor of mighty men, are not ashamed most filthily to flatter.

Verse. 8. And they had hear as the hear of women. etc.

THe delicate wantonness and unbridled lust of monckes and other of ye popish
clergy is noted, which can be contained to no bounds of shamefastnes or laws
of nature, but that it will break them all. Afterward there more then womanly
attire is reproved, and other whorish tricks, by which they would draw men to
there dishonest love. For the world was never so blind that it would greatly
esteem them, but that they bewitched the minds of men with there whorish
inticementes as it were with charmed drinckes of love.

And there teeth were as the teeth of Lions. etc. Although they look smothly
with gentle and womanly contenaunce, yet they have teethe like mermaydes. Which
for there hardness and ravening are compared to the teeth of lions. For
witnesses hereof let be the towns, howses, fields and Lordships, and moreover
whatsoever the world has which is gainful, and serving to pleasure, all which
these locustes have ground with there teeth, to serve for their meat. And to
co^clud there is nothing more rauenouse then they, which although they be very
small in body, yet with the hardness of there teeth, they devour whatsoever
comes next to their hand. In our country of England, they did posses the
half almost, of all lands, and when it was ordained by the law, that there
should no more lands of inheritance be delivered into there hands, without
the licens of y^ Prince, the popish clergy cast there lionish teeth upon there
own possessions. And the Monckes as the greatest Cormarantes drew all the
fattest benefices unto them selves, the hurt of woose devouring griedinesse,
the Church feels unto this day, being deprived of good pastores for lack of
living.

Verse. 9. And they had habbergions like to habbergions of Iron. etc.

THey are defended with so great favor and succor, as well of Princes, both
ecclesiastical, and civil, that they seem to have breasts so hard that no
weapon can pearce through them, and they dare boldly provoke all men to
battle.

And the sound of there wings was like the sound of charets when many horses
run unto battle. etc. Although they have the face of a man, yet they utter
not a man's voice, but like locustes who^e they chiefly resemble, they make a
horrible noise with there wings, even like the sound of chariots, which with
many horses are drawn into ye battle. For they bellowe in there temples, with
a terrible sound, crying out but without understanding. Sometime they utter
great soundes in pulpets, but with out all reason, that worthily they may be
said not to speak with the mouths of men, but to make a terrible noise with
there wings.

Verse. 10. And they had tails like unto scorpions, and there were stings in
there tails, and there power was to hurt men five months. etc.

BEfore he compared there pestilent power of hurtinge to scorpions, but now
when he does diligently recite all the parts of them, he shows that the
locustes are armed also to the tails of scorpions, whereby they closely send
forth there secreat poison, and suddenly when thou art not aware they thrust in
there venomed stinges. Afterward he repeateth that power is granted them to
hurt for shorter time then they them selves would wish, for they shall not
infest or hurt the world about five months.

Verse. 11. And they have a king over them which is the angel of the
bottomless pit, whose name in hebrew is Abaddo and in greek he is named
Apollyon. etc.

THat we may understand under what king this huge army of locustes does
war, he says that the Angel of the bottomless pit is there king, which
is satan him self, and the pope is his vicare, whose name is given him in
hebrewe and in greek of the great desire and study he has to destroy, for he
is called in hebrew Abaddon, and in greek Apollyon, which word in english
signifies a destroyer:

Verse. 12. Our woe is past, and behold two woes com after this etc.

S. John shows that this pestilence of the locustes is ye first of those three
horrible judgments of god, which ye angel said to remain, and it is in deed
a terrible judgment of God that he suffers so vile vermin by there venemouse
and poisoned subtilties, to rule me^ as they list, even to there eternal
destruction and yet there follow two heuier judgments of God the^ this.

Verse. 13. Then the sixth angel blew the trumpet, and I heard a voice from ye
four horns of the golden altar with is before God, etc.

HOw much more grievous dangers were at hand, so much more greater attention,
it was convenient should be moved, that ye faithful being admonished, might
arm and prepare the^ selves against most bitter temptations, when ye sixte
angel therefore sou^ded ye trumpet which did foretell ye most bitter and sharp
persecution of al which should come before ye end and co^sumatio^ of the
world, John herd a voice from the four horns of ye golden altar which is
before God. We spoke before of the golden altar which signifies Christ, which
is offered up to God for a sweet smelling sacrifice, the force and effect of
which sacrifice, because it remains for ever, an altar is always placed in
the presence of God. And the voice is uttered from the four horns of the
altar, that is from the highest part of the altar, that it might be known to
be the voice of Christ which governs the altar.

Verse. 14. Saying to the sixte Angel which had the trumpet, loose the four
Angels, which are bound in the great river Euphrates. etc.

THat voice sounds to the sixte Angel which had sounded the trumpet, that
like as he had been a messenger to declare so great a plague, so he should be a
minister of the furtheraunce of the same. Loose says he the four Angels
which are bound in the great river Euphrates. The four Angels signify yt
whole power of the devil, which he utters in Antichrist and his tyranny,
which should be spread into the four quarters of the world. Which nevertheless
has hither to been restrained, that it should not brust forth into extreme
cruelty, but now the bridle is losed to the same for a certain time. A place
no doubt, full of exceeding great consolation, by which we are taught, that
Christ which is our patron and defendour, holds the devils bound both
hand and foot, that they can not hurt the Church or move persecution, but upon
his sufferrance. But it seems obscure and dark, that he says yt these
wicked Angels are bound at the fludde Euphrates, of which there are sundry
interpretations. But I whileste I wey all things, think that the place is
assigned somewhat darckely, which shall be afterward described more pleynlye,
out of which this pestilence is powered in to the whole world. For Euphrates
being taken without figure, is a river flowing round about Babylon, by which is
meant Rome by a metapher in this book as shall be showed more plainly afterward.
This sense therefore I gather, that there was at Rome, which is the seat of
Antichriste a great desire of wastinge and destroyinge the Church with fire
and sword, neither were subtilties wanting, by which they might attempt there
cursed work: and more over that there were prepared all instruments of war.
But that this made rage was restrained and bridled from heaven, by Christ, that
it should not show forth it self to the world, before the time appointed of
God.

Verse. 15. And the four Angels were losed which were prepared at an hour, at
a day, and at a mounth, and at a year. etc.

CHrist commands when they are losed, whatsoever therefore the Angels that
were losed do, so far forth as they execute the just judgment of God, is to
be ascribed to Christ. They are said to be prepared, at an hour, at a day.
etc. Whereby is expressed not only the promptnes of there mind, by which they
are inclined to hurt, but much rather ye certain time and even the very
momentes thereof determined of God, in which they may rage after this manner.
And he notes a very short space to be granted unto them, that he calls
it an hour, a day, a month and a year at the most.

To sley the third part of men. etc. Before, at the sounding the trumpet of
the fyfte Angel, the locustes with there king Abaddon, by privy practices
and subtle deceites, slew a great part of men with the venim of there
poisoned doctrine, by torments that endured long: but now with open violence
and cruelty, to the wasting and destroying of mankind, these wicked and
malignante spirits are sent forth with fire and sword to slay the third part
of men. But how far they were from necligence in exercising this power
committed unto the^ and what slaughters they have made, all Europe oppressed
with the tyranny of the Bishop of Rome, has felt to much in these latter
times, and as yet is compelled to feel. And we know this tragedy was taken in
hand and begone by the ayed and help of these wicked Angels, and as yet is
continued by the same, although we now hope that the matter draws near to an
end.

Verse. 16. And the number of horsemen of war were twenty thousand times ten
thousand. For I herd the number of them. etc.

NOw he teaches with what means and instruments these destroyinge Angels
are furnished, and also with what preparation to battaill, that they may make
such a slaughter of men in the world. Verily that the whole army is all of
horsemen, whereby the strength and ^orce of the preparation is signified to be
the greater: That is to say, by so much as an host of horsemen is more
terrible, and more violent in war, then an host of fotemen. Lastly comes
the number of there army, which is almost infinite, twenty thousand times ten
thousand which number S. Ihon plainly expresses that he herd because it
seems incredible, that such an army could be gathered out of the whole world,
but by this huge army are signifiede, not the host of one age, but of many.
And this is ye multitude of the Church of Rome, which is so often boasted of,
which multitude is manifest to be mustred into battle against Christ and
his church. But this great army shall easily be driven back and discomfited by
him, which losed out of prison and sent forth. these Angels, which are the
leaders of it, which he can call back again into prison, when it pleasethe
him, and that we trust he will do now shortly after Antichrist has been so
long revealed.

Verse. 17. Thus I saw the horses in a vision and them that sat on them, having
fyery habergions, and of hyacinth and of brymstone. etc.

Saint Ihon proceadeth in describinge the furniture of the horsemen such as
they were showed to him in ye vision. And the whole description of them is full
of horror and fear. For lest they might be thought to be natural horses, or
the horsemen after the common sort, he declarethe, that there was a far
other form and shape both of the horses and also of the^ that sat upon them
showed unto him in a vision. For the horsemen had fiery habbergions, and of
hyacinth and of brymestone, by which is meant that there breasts were so armed
and fortifyed, against all violent force of weapons, yt they need not to fear
any thing at all, yea whether soever they ^ourned the^ selves, they might show
forth before them nothing else, but fire smooke and brimstone, for so I
interpret the hyacinth or yelow color, for that which follows in the next
clause. For as the horsemen which ride on barded horses, are wont to were
colors or signs in there breasts or there shield which might make the^
terrible to there enemies, so these soldiers of Antichrist showing forth in
there breast flammie, smoky, and brimstone like colors they plainly make
manifest to all me^, what they thretten to the world in every deed fire and
flame, that is extreme destruction.

And the heads of the horses were as the heads of lions and out of there
mouths went forth fire and smoke and brimstone. etc. The form of the horses
was monstrouse and horrible, as which besides the swiftnes of horses, had also
y^ heads and strength of lions, and yt which is above yt fearcenes of lions,
which tear only with there teeth and claws, out of there mouth says S.
John, went fire and smoke and brimstone, and under these figures is described,
yt mo^strouse and barbarous tyranny of Antichrist, which with open violence
defends the cursed seat of his pride, and cruelty warreth against all those,
which shall but move a finger against his presumtuouse arrogance.

Verse. 18. Of these three was the third part of men killed, that is of the fire
of the smoke and of the brimstone, which came out of there mouths. etc.

HE signifies that they shall be destroyed with most certain and present death,
which by any means oppose themselves to his tyranny. For the fire spedely
deuoureth, the smoke strangleth, and choketh, ye brimston both miserably
torment those yt it burns neither can it be quenched if it shall once burn.
Such shall be the rage and cruelty of antichrist, yt he is not wont to wou^d with
ye sword but utterly to consume with fire, to blind y^ eyes with smooke, to take
away ye spirit, and to burn cruelly with fiery flaming brimstone, and with these
three evils he slew ye third part of men, by his warriors, horsemen of
brimston, and lions like horses, that is by y^ princes which are subject unto
him, and the furious common people which like horses carry upon them ye bondage
and slavery of Antichrist and at the will and pleasure of there Lords, do fill
all things with smoke brimston and fyery flames.

Verse. 19. For there power is in there mouths and in there tails: for there
tails were like unto serpents, and had heads wherewith they hurt. etc.

ALthough certain copies have not these words (and in there tails (yet they
seem to me by other examplars in which they are found, yt they should be added,
or at the least understood: For ye sense is this, that this army does hurt
there adversaries with manifest violence, and as it were with open war, and yet
not inexpert or wanting fraud and deceipte, which was not perceived in ye
locusts, which seduced only by subtilty and craft. But these out of their
bloody and cruel mouths breath out, smoke, fire, and brimstone. But yet they
want not their enginnes and snares, because they have tails also like
serpe^ts, which tails also have heads, which after ye manner of serpe^ts,
privily byte, those which are uncircumspect, yet they hurt more with there heads
then with there tails, with violence the^ with deceit, because many do know
there subtilties, but they cannot bear there cruelty, therefore either they are
like wretches slain, or else revolt as cowards.

Verse. 20. And the remnant of the men which were not killed by these plagues
repented not of the works of there hands, that they should not worship devils
and Idols of gold and of silver, and of brass, and of stone and of wood with
neither ca^ see, neither hear nor go. etc.

HE teaches that ye world being corrected with these plagues yet would not be
brought to a better mind, for those yt remained vnkilled by these calamities,
were stricken with no repentance, for there heynouse offenses that they might
depart from there wicked works. They fained some sorrow peradventure so long
as evil oppressed them on every side, but it was mere hypocrisy which they
boasted. For so soon as the affliction ceased, they returned to there kind,
and gave them selves wholly to there accustomed impieties. They honored devils,
they worshipped idols, made of all kind of matter and substance, and although
they were blind, deaf and could not move themselves, yet they sought and
hoped for health of them. And it is worthy to be noted, that the Apostle
rehearses all kind of matter or substance whereof idols were made: both that
he might show the vanity of men that they would seek divine nature in
every creature, rather then in God, and also that he might declare that no
kind of Idols are to be esteemed.

Verse. 21. Also they repented not of there murder, and of there ^orcerye
neither of there fornication, nor of there theft, etc.

THey can not keep the commandments of the second table, which dishonor
God after such a sort, as S. Paul says to the Romans 1. Chapter, therefore
he reprehendeth not only there Idolatry, but also there murderers,
sorceries, theftes, and other such like abominable wickedness. And we see by
this prophecy that men took never the more heed for the plagues wherewith God
afflicted the world chiefelye for the tyranny of Antichrist, which although
many of the Papists them selves detest and abhor, yet they forsake not his
Idolatrouse religion, neither depart from there wicked ways.

The tenth Chapter.
THere is described in this chap. What comfort the Church shall have in so
great afflictions, when as Christ is brought in as patron and defendoure of
the same, which with the word of salvation, and his secreat virtue and power
will preserve the same safe and sound against all the violent assaults of
satan.

Verse. 1. And I saw another mighty Angel come down from heaven. etc.

IT behooved that the minds of the faithful, should be armed with some notable
consolation against so sharp and bitter temptations least they should be
altogether discoraged. For how could the feeble and weak multitude of the elect
be able to suffer and endure so sturdy force as hard as the Adamant, of these
horsemen, except they were furnished from heaven with such rare and singular
virtue, of the holy ghost? Christ therefore comes forth even in due time, in
the shape and form of an Angel as he does often in this prophecy, because
he does faithfully execute the will of his heavenly father in protecting and
defending the Church, and he is described to be a far other person from those
former seven Aungells, which sounded the trumpetes, as to be such an one as is
armed not so much for the taking vengeance upon the wicked as appointed for the
health and safegarde of the Church. For his wonderful and mighty power is set
forth, that the faithful might not doubt to rest quietly and safely under the
protection of him which is endued with invincible strength to break and
overthrow all the violent force of the adversaries. He descended from heaven,
that he might succoure the Church warringe in earth, and eue^ now presently
beginning to fainte under yt burden. For as often as we be oppressed with
evils, heaven seems to be shut unto us, and through the weakness of man's
nature we fear least the great distance of place should separate us from the
defense of Christ. Now therefore Christ descended from heaven, yt he might
bring present ayed to the afflicted and almost desperate estate of the Church.
For he has promised yt he will be with us even to the end of the world. And
although he ascended into heaven, yt he might fill all things with his majesty,
yet nothing lets, but that he may be said to descend unto the earth to ayed
and succor the godly in there afflictions. So Isay 64. desires that the Lord
would break the heavens and come down into ye earth, the same does David often
in y^ psalms: whereby we plainly gather, that the desce^ding of Christ into
the earth does minister matter of true and sound comfort to the faithful. For
God never forsakethe, nor leaves destitute his Children whom he has once
taken under his tuition.

Clothed with a cloud. etc. He descended unto the Earth clothed with a cloud,
that is full of majesty, for a cloud does often times in the scripture
represent to men a manifest sign and token of Gods divine majesty, so that
sometime it is called the garments, sometime the chariote or horse of God. And
at length our savior will come in the clouds with wonderful beauty and
glory, to judge both ye quick and the dead, that the faithful may learn
boldly to contemn all the glitteringe show of gorgiouse apparel, as of
purple robes scepters, and other princily ornaments, so often as it is bosted
of to obscure and darken the glory of Christ. For there is no such glory in
the robes of any prince, as there is in Christ clothed with a bright cloud.

And the rainebow upon his head. etc. He wears a notable ornament upon his
head, not a crown of goulde, not a miter garnished and set with the finest
preciouse stones, but ye rainbow, which is the old sacrament of the mercy of
God toward mankind, whereby not only the meruailouse greatness of him is
declared, whose head is seen compassed with ye rainbow, but also his infinite
clemency and gentleness, which being begun to be made manifest toward men
from ye creation of the world continues throughout al ages like it self. And
hereupon he bears that ancient token and sign of the covenant yt was made
with the whole world, that we should not think that the whole church which is
upon earth, shall be overwhelmed together with the storms and waves of cares,
griefs, and calamities, as often as we se the heaven wax dark and black with
thick mistye clouds of miseries.

And his face was as the sun. That which the sun is to the world, the same
is Christ to his church, which restores to the same the acceptable and
glorious bewty of his light, when the storms and tempests of adversities are
driven away. Therefore in so great darkness of the tyranny of Antichrist,
verily Christ the son of ryghteousnes arises in dew time to the faith full,
which being refreshed with the most pleasant bewty of his countenance, may
well hope yt the end of miseries which they wished is come. For by his virtue
and power that brymston-lyke smoke which is cast out of the mouth of the
monstrouse beasts is scattered and vanishes away, that it can not chooke the
remnants of the Church, as it does the other worldly men.

And his feet were like pillars of fire. etc. From the head even to the feet,
Christ is described to be endued with invincible power and strength. For he
has feet as it were pillars of fire, by which he will tread down and bring to
nothing all the violence of yt adversaries. For he must sit so long at ye
right hand of God until all his enemies be made his footestole. Therefore
there remains a terrible end for the wicked, because they shall be sla^ped to
poulder with the fiery and pillerlike feet of Christ. What can Abaddon the
king of locusts do against this Angel, what can the twenty thousand times
ten thousand horsemen do? what can those terrible horses do, which having heads
like lions do breath out of there mouths fire, smoke, and brymstone? what can
the fiery, smokie and brymston like habbergions of ye horsemen do? only the
feet of the Angel which are like pillars of fire, shall easily tread down
and overthrow all these preparatio^s and furniture.

Verse. 1. And he had, in his hand a little book open. etc.

THis book is an other (as I judge) from that we had before sealed with seven
seals which contained the secreat judgments of God, y^ were to be revealed by
Christ. But this book seems to conteyne, those great consolations which are
rehearsed every where in the scriptures as often as mention is made of God
reconciled to us by Christ, or yt I may speak more briefly, the promises of
the Gospel, with which it behooves the minds of the godly to be sustained and
holden up, yt they may not faint, when they are oppressed with evils, but may
lift up themselves to the hope, of eternal blessedness. And they are said to
be comprehended in a small book, because they do not lead us about by long and
doubtful circumstances, but brings us directly to the throne of grace by one
only mediator Christ. They are written in a book, yt they may remain
throughoute all ages, otherwise it should suffice to have preached and uttered
the^ only to ye men of one age. This little book is opened, because the
doctrine of the gospel is offered to all, though it be received, but of a few:
Therefore all excuse of ignorance is taken away, seeing that the book is showed
open unto us. Moreover the faithful have in a readiness wherewt they may
comfort one another, when no man forbids to draw out of this open book, yt
which may serve for there purpose. And Christ only reaches forth unto us
these co^solations, so that worthily the Angel is said to hold the book in
his hand, which afterward he delivered to Ihon which required it, to be eaten.

And he put his right foot upon the sea and his left ^oote upon the earth.
etc. His meruailouse greatness is noted in that with the one foot he trod upon
the sea and with the other upon the land. And also the largeness of his
kingdom is signified, that he possesses all things both by sea, and by land.
And treads upon both the same elements even as lord and ruler both of sea and
land. And I think this is not to be passed by, that he put his right foot
(upon which we stand more strongly) upon the sea, and his left foot he set on
the earth, for the waters are even as stable and firm rocks to his feet,
that the raging waves of the sea can not ouerwhelme and ^rowne them. There is
no cause therefore that we should fear, least any force of this deuilish army
should prevail against him.

Verse. 3. And he cried with a loud voice, as when a lion roreth. etc.

HE which seemed a long time to be dumb, and as a Lion to sleap in his den,
whiles the tyranny of Antichrist raged against the Church: Now having spied a
co^uenien^ time to revenge the cause of the faithful, suddenly this Lion of
the tribe of Judah, as it were raised from sleap, roreth with a terrible voice
against his enemies, and threatens that he will pluck the pray even out of
there Jaws. And the similitude of a lion roaring is fitly placed, whose voice
does strike a fear and terror into all the wild beasts. So when Christ
shall once thunder after a terrible manner with his mighty word, all the pride
of Antichrist must needs tremble and quake. Although I do not think that he
used an inarticulate voice, or y^ he filled the apee with a rude cry without
understanding, but that he thretned horrible vengeance to the wicked, with an
imperiouse and angry voice.

And when he had cried seven thunders uttered there voices. etc. It appears
that Christ with his loud cry called forth the seven thunders, that they
might make known to Ihon the severity and sharpenes of his judgment against
the wicked, for as soon as he had cried with a loud voice the seven thunders
uttered there voices. By the seven thunders I understand, all kind of most
greuouse judgments, which God shall thunder against the wicked contemners of
his divine Majesty, which are foretold that they are prepared, by seven
thunderinge, rather then speakinge Angels, least when we measure the
invincible power of the army of Antichrist with fleshly eyes, we should think
that God were scarce able, to cast them down out of so high dignity and
power and that he wants ways and means whereby he may succor the most
miserable state and condition of his Church.

Verse. 4. And when the seven thunders had spoken there voices I was about to
write, but I heard a voice from heaven saying unto me, scale up those things
which the seven thunders have spoken, and write them not. etc.

BEcause Ihon believed that those things which the seven thunders had uttered,
should be profitable to the Church, he would have committed the same to
writing, and set it forth with the rest as a part of this prophecy. But he
herd a voice from heaven forbidding that he should write the same, but that he
should shut up and seal them, as sacred and holy mysteries which it was not
lawful for men to know. For God would not have all things which he has
decreed to be known before they come to pas. So he commanded Daniele to seal
up certain things that they might not be spread among the people. Chap. 12.
And Paul was taken up into the third heaven and herd things which it was not
lawful to utter. But some will say, wherefore then spoke the seven thunders
the things which no man is granted to hear? I Answer, that they spoke when
Ihon herd them, that both his faith by the knowledge of the same, and also our
faith by his testimony might be confirmed, when as we know that God has
prepared all his judgments, wherewith he will strike and punish the wicked,
although it pertayne not to us to know, what time, by what means, and by what
minister he will e^ecute the same.

Verse. 5. And tho Angel which I saw stand upon the sea, and upon the earth.
etc.

AFter that the voices of the seven thunders were sealed, which the holy
ghost forbade to be uttered abroad: that most mighty Angel which stood
upon the earth and the sea (least any thing should be wanting to the godly
which might make to there full and perfect consolation) confirmed with a
solemn oath that there calamity should shortly be finished. For it has great
force to persuade to patience, if the faithful know, that the hope of there
deliverance shall not long be differred. Howsoever therefore God would have
very many of his counsels kept close from men, yet he suffered this to be made
manifest: and that the rewards prepared for his soldiers should not long be
kept back. But it is profitable more diligently to consider the form of the
words.

Lift up his hand to heaven. etc. It is certain, that in as much as
pertayneth to the form of the vision, he alludeth to those things which are
written in the 12. Chapter of Daniel: although for an other end, for there the
Angel lifting up hoth his hands to heaven swear, that after a time, two
times, and half a time, the persecution of the Church should be ended, but
here the Angel affirms that there shall be no delay or tarying at al, after
the soundinge of the trumpet of the seuenthe Angel. And in that he swereth
with his hand stretched forth to heaven, he observes the solemn cerimonie,
which the old fathers used in swering, whereby they signified that they called
the God of heaven to witness, and also to revenge if they had failed and broken
there oath. So Abraham in the 14. Genes. made answer to the king of Sodoma,
when he was earnestly requested to retain the pray and spoil of the slaughter
of the kings, I have lift up my hand (says he) to God the possessour of
heaven and earth. etc.

Verse. 6. And swear by him which lives for ever more. etc.

THis is a circumlocutio^ of the mighty god, which lives for evermore, by
which kind of speech he is separated, not only from dead idols, but also from
tyrants which are mortal, which would be worshipped them selves as gods, of
which sort were Caligula, Nero, and Domitian. To whom also this does
properly perteyne, because that by himself he lives eternallye, and is the
aucthor of that life, which is in all other things according as S. Paul
says in the 17. of the Acts in him we live, move and have our being. And it
ought not to trouble us, that this Angel which bears the person of
Christ, flies to the aucthority of God in swearing, when as he is God
himself, seeing Christ himself does the same thing very often in ye person of
the mediator. But rather the holy ghost would admonished S. John that this
decree concerning the consumation of the world and the last judgment,
proceeded not from any creature, but even from God himself. For we see how
carelessly the world does deride those things which are spoken in ye holy
scripturs concerning ye dissolutio^ of this frame of ye world, and the
faithful are sometime a sleep, when they give the^ selves to much to pleasurs,
so that they forget ye last judgment whom it behooves to be wakned with this
sacred oath of as Christ it were with a loud cryinge voice, that they may more
diligently meditate of those things which perteine to ye receiuinge of our
redemer from heaven.

Which created heaven and the things that are therein, and the earth and the
things that are therein and the sea and the things that are therein. etc. The
next thing yt is ascribed to God, is that he is ye creator of al things, and
that he lives not blessed to himself alone as yt Epicures do dream, but
governs all things which he has, created either in heaven or earth by his
divine will and providence. For it is against all reason when we shall ascribe
ye creation of all things to God, yt we would take from him all rule and
government over ye same. For it is necessary yt every work serve to y^ will
and pleasure of the workman. Moreover he does here solemnlye, and as it were
with expressed words, as the custom is in matters of great weight, number up
all kinds of creatures, taking the division of places wherein they be. Which
is done to amplify the matter, for though it be the very same as if he should
say (he that has created all things) yet we are more drawn into admiration
of so great power, wisdom, and goodness, when we here recited the heaven and
all creatures which are therein, whether we understand the Angelical powers,
or the stars, when we consider the earth and the infinite kinds of living
creatures pla^ts, stones, and metals, which are in the same, when we behold
more diligently the great huge sea, and the innumerable forms and shapes of
living things which are ingendered in the same. And that he mentions these
three places only, he does it according to the usual manner of the holy
scriptures, because these three commonly are most in sight to the common sort,
and the holy ghost by his infinite mercy does abase him self to the capacity
of the rude and ignorant people. Although to say the truth, all creatures are
contained in these three places. For nothing is engendered in the element of
fire, and the scripture co^prehendeth the higher regions of the air in which
the meteores are made, under the name of heaven, so that they are also called
the fowls of heaven which fly in the lowest part of this air which
compasses us about.

That time should be no more. etc. The greek word (...) signifies the long
delay of time. Whereupon it is said that (...) does signify to delay, or be
slack. For he does not understand, as certain do to subtlety gather. yt the
moving of the higheste sphere of the heaven called Primum mobile, by which we
measure time, shall then cease, but that from thence forth there shall be no
stop, nor stay to defer out redemption, nor no delay to take vengeance upon
ye ungodly and reprobate: for they shall not then mock the judgment of God,
as they now carelessly deride that, which is foreshewed concerning his
severity and sharpenes.

Verse. 7. But in ye days of y^ voice of ye 7. Angel when he shall begin to blow

HE shows how long the day of the last judgment shall be proroged, even until
the time in which the seventh aungel by the sound of his trumpete shall give
manifest signs of the resurrection, and judgment. Those things therefore
which remain to be made manifest in the soundinge of the trumpet of the sixte
Angel, are without all doubt to be referred to the last age of the world,
which if we diligently consider, do clearly express and point out the state
and condition of this our age, as we shall declare more at large in the
Chapter following.

Even the mystery of God shall be finished. etc. The secreate counsel of God
which is furthest removed from the wisdom of the world, against which Satan
with all ye wickedness of the world opposes and sets him self, shall at
lentgh obtain an end. The gloriouse and perpetual redemption of the whole
Church through Christ. And the everlasting destruction of Antichrist, with his
whole body: In either part ye unspeakable glory, and wonderful magnificence
of God shall be seen. Which things if they be not now seen of the wise men of
this world, we are admonished that it is, the mystery of god, which is
reuerentlye received of the simple and sincere faith of the godly, but is
proudly rejected of the swollen and puffed up knowledge of the ungodly, but in
his due time it shall be revealed to the whole world, to the wicked for there
reproach and condemnation, to the godly for there glory and endless
consolation.

As he declared to his servant the prophets. etc. The holy ghost did not
here first begin to admonish men of the judgment of God to come, but in
time past in all ages he did the same by his servant the prophets. For we
cannot rightlye understand God, except we acknowledge him to be a rewarder of
the good, and a taker of vengeance upon the wicked, as the Apostell witnesses
in the 11. chapter to the Hebrews, And this is also to be noted, that he uses
the word (of declaring the gospel) when he speaks of yt terrible judgment of
god, for that day is even the perfect finishing and fulfillinge of the gospel,
in which the Lord shall perform what soever he has promised. So Christ
preaches to his Apostels saying when ye see all these things come to pas,
lift up your heads for your redemption draws nere. And truly in that this
second coming of Christ seems terrible unto us, it is for this cause that
either we abound in sins and iniquities, in which alas, we do to securelye
sauoure and flatter our selves, or else that we are weak in faith which we
ought to pray continually that God will increase in us.

Verse. 8. And the voice which I, herd from heaven spoke unto me again, and
said, go and take the little book whith is open in the hand of the Angel,
which stands upon the sea and upon the earth. etc.

NOw the heavenly voice does teach to what end Christ held open the book of
the promises of the Gospel. Verily that when it was delivered by him to the
ministers of the Church in the person of Ihon, and received of them, yea
thoroughly digested in there breasts, it might afterward he spread abroad to
the consolation and comfort of the whole Church. (And the voice which I herd
etc.) the same heavenly voice which commands to keep close the secreate
mysteries of the seven thunders, commands him to take the little book of the
Evangelical truth, which is open in the hand of the Angel. Let us
diligently therefore look upon this book, which is committed unto us by the
commandment of the holy ghost, but let us not curiously search after those
things which the same spirit would have to be kept secreat. Moreover we may
note, that the doctors, and teachers of the Church are commanded (under the
person of Ihon) to require the doctrine of the Gospel at ye hands of Christ,
which they are bound to deliver forth pure unto the Church, even as they have
received it. Therefore the heavenly voice expresses by name, from the hand of
which Angel he ought to receive the same, not of eneey one, but of his verily
which stands upon the sea, and upon the land, whom S. John knew well
enough to represent our Lord Christ. For if an angel from heaven shall bring
any other Gospel, let that Angel be accursed. Galath. 1. Chap.

Verse. 9. And I went unto the Angel, and said to him give me the little
book, and he said unto me take it and eat it, and it shall make thy belly
bitter, but it shall be in thy mouth as sweet as honye. etc.

Saint Ihon does obey the holy ghost (and as this thing was done in a vision)
he goes to the Angel assigned him by the heavenly voice, and as he was
commanded he required the book of him. And the Angel does not only
deliver to him the little book, but also commands Ihon to eat up the same.
Afterward he shows the force and working of the same, saying that in taste it
would be as sweet as honye, but it would fill his belly with bitter juice and
such as could not be kept in.

Verse. 10. Then I took the little book out of the Angels hand and eat it up,
and it was in my mouth as sweet as honey, but as soon as I had eaten it, my
bellye was bitter. etc.

IHon shows that he gredely devoured the book, which he received according
to the commandment of the Angel, and that he found it to be so in very
deed, which he had heard before concerning the force and working of the same.
For as long as it was showed in his mouth, he seemed to be replenished with
the most pleasant sweetness of honye, but after it had descended into his
stomach and intrailes, he felt more then the bitterness of galle. And this
place alludeth to those things which are written in the third chap. of
Ezechiell, for there the prophet being commanded to eat up the book which
contained even the severity and sharpenes of Gods vengeance. yet felt the
sweet taste of honey in eating the same, how much more did S. Ihon eating a
book full of consolations, perceive an heavenly taste? but yt so sweet meat
does make the belly bitter, it is for this cause, that he should not think
that he had ^ate it up for him self alone, which was to be belched up again
for the medicine of many. For both ye Angel does plainly show this thing in
the next verse folowinge, and also the holy ghost does other where, use this
same figure of the bellye being made bitter. As in the 4. Chapter of Ierem. the
Prophet complayneth that he felt the greuouse torments of his bellye that was
made bitter because he had herd the sound of the trumpet, and the voice of
him that cried alarm. And in the 32. Chapter of Job. Elihu bosteth that his
belly is full of the holy ghost like to the vessele of the vintuer which would
burst except it be opened.

Verse. 11. And he said unto me thou must prophecy again among the people
and nations, and tongues and to many kings. etc.

HE teaches that so great treasure of the heavenly doctrine was not committed
to Ihon for him self alone, but that it was for this cause laid up in his
custody, that as often as need should require, it might be brought forth for
the use of the whole Church. And after he declares how largely yt fruit and
commodity of the same does extend, when as the utility and proffite thereof
must be spread abroad, among nations and people, and tongues, and also many
kings. And there is described in this vision by a notable figure, a true
pastor of ye Church and faithful minister, whom first of all it is meet to
be raised up by the holy Ghost to so high an office, and calling, and the
same spirit leadinge him, to receive and take desirousely the book of the
heavenly doctrine offered and reached forth to him of Christ, and when it is
received, to lodge it in the inward bowelse of his breast, and last of all when
it is well degested, to bring it forth to the proffite and commodity of many,
and to stir up Princes together with the people to the obedience of the same.

The eleventh Chapter
Saint John goes forward in this chapter in describinge those things which
remain to be uttered in the sowndinge of the trumpet of the sixth Angel, and
in the end of this chap. verse. 15. he describes the trumpet of the seventh
Angel which is a messenger of the resurrection and last judgment.

Verse. 1. There was given me a reed like to a rod. etc.

NOw it is declared under this figure, to what end the Apostle is commanded
to utter forth the little book of the heavenly word, (which he had eaten) in
prophesiyng diligently. Verily because ye Christ will yet always byld up his
Church yt it should not utterly be destroyed, although it be greiuously
oppressed with the tyranny of Antichrist, threatninge present destruction and
utter cuine. But chiefly he signifies that ye ruin of the same shall be
repaired toward the end of the world, eue^ as this figure perteyneth to the
trumpet of the sixth Angel. For the measuringe is referred to ye byldinge, like
as in other places of the holy scriptures, Ezechiell 40. Zachar. 1^ there is
the like metaphor.

And the Angel stood by, saying arise and meat the temple of God and the
alter and the^ that worship therein. etc. Although in certain copies these
words (and the Angel stood by) are not found yet I doubt not but John
understands that this was the speech of that noble Angel Christ which he
had described in the chapter going before. For Christ is the master bylter of
his Church. Under whom all the ministers of the word labor in preaching
and spreadinge abroad of the gospel to the bylding up of the same holy
temple. Therefore Christ commands to measure the temple of God, the alter
and those that worship in the temple: By which sign he teaches that he will
have a care, that the whole church, which is signified by the temple, that the
true worship of God which is figured by the alter, and that all the parts and
members of the Church, which are shadowed by those which worship in the
temple, shall for ever be builded up and preserved in safety the which would
all suddenly vanishe away, except by his ayed and defense, and by the ministry
of the word, they should be propped up, even as it were with pillars.

Verse. 2. But the court which is with out the temple cast out and meat it no^
for it is given unto the gentiles. etc.

Saying the readinge of this place is doubtefull in the greek books, for when
some have (without) and some (with in) we can a poynct nothing for certeynty,
but that having respect to the form of the old temple of the Jews, which
was divided into three parts, I rather incline to that readinge, which has
(without) for there was no inner court that I know, but the holy and the holy
of holiest. Although I leave it indifferente whether way it is to be red. Yet
this is certain yt by this court, whether we read the (inner) or the (utter) is
signified the fellowship and congregation of hypocrites, which though they
proudly boast them selves in the glorious title of the Church, yet they are not
comprehended in the bosom of the true Church. But rather as bastardes and
degenerate children, they are refused, cast out and banished, and no other wise
then the temple of the Jews, by the Roman gentiles is destroyed in such sort
yt not on stone is left upon an other: So these when they are banished and cut
of from ye people of God, shall be gathered and joined to the profane gentiles,
of whose number they are. Therefore least that S. John might think that Christ
comprehended under the name of the temple and those that worship there in, all,
as many as beast in an outward s^ew and vision of Christ and the Church, he
slatlye forbids him to account that utter court, that is, heritiques and
schismatiques, and all the other rablement of the sect of Antichrist, among
those whom the Lord will receive to be builded up into an holy temple, whereof
he himself is ye corner stone, he pulls away yt visor therefore from ye faces
of the papists and other heritiques which have nothing else in there mouths but
the Church, the Church, when he commands the^ to be cast forth, as those
that are neclected and despised.

And the holy city they shall tread under foot two and fortye months. etc.
The wicked and profane gentiles shall tread under foot, that is shall
greiuously oppress, persecute, and afflict the Church of God, for the full
space of two and forty months, that is for that time which Christ does
grant unto Antichrist to rage in cruelty against the godly. Some do count the
number of months, from the first persecutions of ye christians by the Roman
emperoures, even till the time of the emperor Constantine which granted
peace, unto the churches. But let them which maintain that opinion see how
certain it is. But to me it seems more plain that under numbers the certain
fixed, and determinate time of the persecution of antichrist is assigned,
which he cannot pas, although he fret sum and rage never so much. For the
Lord has counted the same time by months days, and hours. The reason of
the numbers seems to be of this sort, this time which sometime is called two
and forty months, sometime a thousand two hundredth and sixty days, sometime
a time two times and half a time, makes in all, three years and an half,
that is ye one half of a prophetical week, which time also is called three
days and an half. And this place alludeth to the weeks of years in the 9.
Chapter of Daniell. Whereupon we gather to the great consolation of the Church,
that a short time is appointed to Antichrist to wast the same, which is also
showed twice afterward in the 12. chap. and in the 20. y^ a short space of
time is permitted to the devil that he may s^riue with all his force to beat
down the Church, this interpretation as most simple and plain pleases me
best, those that seek more subtiler may follow there own judgment.

Verse. 3. But I will give power unto my two witnesses and they shall prophesy a
thousand two hundredth and threscore days. etc.

AFter that the Lord, in the figure going before of measuring the temple, has
promised that he will build up his church now he shows by whose industry
and labor he will perform the same verelye with the ministry of his word
and by those ministers, which he will always raise up to him self for this
work, yea even in the midst of the storms of persecutions. He promises
therefore that he will raise up to him self two witnesses at the least, which
the law requires for the confirmation of every cause, even then when as the
greatest multitude made droncke with the doting vaniti^s of Antichrist, would
refuse sound doctrine. They commonly interpret the two witnesses to be
Heuoch, and Helias, when as we may rather by those things which follow in the
sixte Verse gather that it is Moses and Helias. But it is absurd and against
all reason to restrain to certain persons those things, which are spoken of
all the Ministers of the word, which Christ has promised that he will appoint
even in that perilouse, and daungerouse time, which are called two, not for the
certain number, but for the fewness sake. And yet he promises that he will
furnish these with meet and agreeable virtues, and gifts of grace, so that by
the space of a thousand two hundred and sixty days, they shall valiantlye.
and boldlye execute the office and duty of prophets, in teaching, reproving
and comforting. That is for the space of 24. mo^ethes, whiles the holy city is
trodden down of the gentiles. He count^^h the same time also by days, that we
might not think that the Church should be deprived and want her teachers,
even the smalest space of time. For although to Antichrist and his blind
proctors, and adherentes the doctrine of the Gos^^ll seemed to be buried, yet
the Church had always a^ the (...) witnesses of Christ. Of which although ye
names of every one* by reason of the injury of ye time, have not come unto us,
yet hystories do sufficien^ly witness that there have alw^ies (...) some, as
in England, Wickli^^e, in Italy, Marcellius of (...), in France the pore people
of ^ionse, in Bo^mia Ihon Huss^, and Hierom of Phrage and in other places
diverse others.

Clothed in s^ckcloth etc. Persuading men by all means to repentance from
Idolatry and other works of darkness: moreover Christ does take to this so
honorable an office of being his witnesses, not golden popes, not purple
Carbinals nor yet mytred bishops, but base men of the abject people, clothed in
sackclothe whose dignity is to be esteemed not by there apparail, which is very
course, but by the office which is committed unto them.

Verse. 4. These are 2. olyue trees and 2. candelsticks before the god of ye
earth.

Because the world does scornefully receive those, which are sent of the Lord
except being adorned with outward pomp and glory, they may draw men's eyes upon
them, therefore Christ shows in how great price and estimation they are with
him. They are says he 2. olyue trees always fresh flourishing and green,
such as David glories yt he will be after he has eschewed ye false accusation
of Doeg, and always dropping down^ the oil of wholesome doctrine upon the
Church, they are says he, two candelstickes susteyning and holding up the
light of the Gospel in this darcke world, of what sort soever they seem to be
earthly men, they are of this sort to God and the Lord of the earth and the
whole world. The ministers of the Church may here be admonished of what sort
they ought to be if they will be allowed of Christ as his witnesses.

Verse. 5. And if any man will hurt them, fire proceaded out of their mouths
and deuoureth there enemies: for if any man would hurt them thus must he be
killed. etc.

THat the world might not escape unpunished in despisinge there simplicity, the
lord pronounces that there word against the reprobate shall be like fire, which
may burn them to ashes, and deliver them to be burned with infernal flames.
For it is the savor of death unto death to those yt perish. In vain therefore
does the pope commit the bodies of the Saints to be burned with corporal
flames, seeing that he himself shall be much more grievously tormented for ever,
with there fiery spirit. This place does teach with what earnest zeal the
godly preachers ought to burn with all against the wicked enemies of the
Church of Christ, and not to fear there cruelty, seying they have in a
readiness the vengeance that is to be taken against all ungodliness.

Verse. 6. These have power to shut the heaven, yt it rain not in the days of
there prophesiynge, and have power over waters to turn them into blood, and to
smite the earth with all manner of plagues, as often as they will. etc.

IT is no doubt but that he alludeth to ye history of Elias which fore told of
the three years brought in the days of Achab. 1 kings. 17. chap. like as
also in the other part of ye verse. to Moses which stroke the land of Egipte with
diverse and sundry plagues, as we may read in ye. 7.8.9.10. chap. of Exodus By
which (...) he signifies, yt his witnesses shall be endewed with the zeal of
Moses and Elias, whose contempt the lord will revenge with most grievous
punishments, as Egypt felt, as Israel felt, which escaped not unpunished for
despising Moses and Elias: and the popish Church daily feleth, the wrath and
vengeance of God denounced by these witnesses, to fall upon them armed with many
and sondrye plagues, and at length shall feel utter destruction. Furthermore,
to the great consolation of his Church and establishinge the authority of his
witnesses, Christ compares the^ to the most clear lights of the old Church,
that ye congregation of ye faithful may believe, yt Moses and Elias, are as it
were returned from death and come unto them, for the singular gifts of mind
and spiritual graces of ye holy ghost which God has bestowed upon ye same his
witnesses. Hereof it is yt we so highly honor ye wonderful virtues of Luther
and Calvin and others, that we think them to be inferior to none which have
lived since ye Apostels time, God grant that we may be thankful for so good
gifts and that we may use them well.

Verse. 7 And when they have finished there testimony. etc,

THe devil can do nothing, Antichrist can do nothing against the witnesses of
God, so long as they have not finished there testimony, that is not before
they shall have run the course prefi^ed them of God and shall fulfill the
office and duty committed unto them. They need not therefore fear the madness
of ye persecutors, but boldly to give testimony to christ and his gospel, so
long as it seems good to ye Lord, and at length when they have discharged
there duty to permit themselves to his will and pleasure.

The beasts that comes out of the bottomeles pit shall make war against
them, and shall overcome them and kill them. etc. The cruel and unreasonable
beast Antichrist, which shall come forth of hell to establishe the kingedome of
the devil which is inferiore to them in spiritual battle, yet their
superiore in carnal war, shall oppress, overcome, and slay the holy
Martyrs of God.

Verse. 8. And there* corpses shall lie in the streates of the great city. etc.

ANtichrist puffed up with so great a victory, shall triumph over their dead
bodies with barbarous cruelty, the streates of the great city shall be
scattered with there slain members. Every where through out the whole
dominion of Antichrist, how wide and large so ever it be, shall be seen, the
dead bodies of the saints, which thing how true it is, the history of the
former times and experience of our own age, does sufficiently, teach.

Which spiritually is called Sodom and Egipte where our Lord also was
crucified. etc. He shows which is that great city, the sea of Antichrist,
which falsely bosteth her self to be the holy city Jerusalem, that is the
Church of god, when as yet for there cursed wickedness and filthy abomination it
rather deserves to be called Sodom, and for the persecution and bondage which
it lays upon ye saints, to be named Egypt, neither does it resemble
Jerusalem in any thing, except in cruelty against the godly which as it killed
all ye prophets, so likewise it slew christ himself the head of ye Church with a
shameful death. And here he does plainly even as it were poynct at the sea
of Rome with the singer, when as he calls it the great city in which our
Lord was crucified. For Jerusalem of the Jews, deserved not by any reason to
be called the great city, much less when John received this vision, when as
it was utterly raised of the Romans and made even with the ground. But
saying that the holy ghost does after ward manifestlye by the great city
interpret Rome, it is certain yt the same city is also understood in this
place. And it fitly agrees, that the Roman tyranny is called the great
city, not only because the city of Rome is the head of the whole Romayne
Empire, but because the city it self is increased unto such meruailouse
greatness, that it became a Monarchia, which was not in the other three
Monarchies, the beginning whereof were taken of kings, and not of any city.
And it is not amiss to say, that Christ was crucified at Rome, seeing he was
condemned to death of the Romayne presidente as the enemy of Caesar, the
Emperor of Rome, he was delivered up and slain by that kind of death, which
was established by the laws of the Romans Ihon Chapter. 19.

Verse. 9. And they of the people and kindereds and tongues and gentiles shall
see there corpses three days and an half, and shall not suffer there
carcaseis to be put in graves. etc.

THere shall be no nation subject to the tyranny of Rome, which shall not see
the slaughter of the holy witnesses of Christ, the space of three days and an
half, that is for half a week. For they shall not long feed there ferce
eyes with this cruel sight, but God even in the midst of ye heat will break
the persecution, but yet in tho mean time so long as they have power, they
will persecute the godly with such hatred, that they will also show there
cruelty over the very dead bodies, and shall not suffer them to be buried,
but will show them open to all men, as it were signs, and tokens of there
victory.

Verse. 10. And they that dwell upon the earth, shall rejoice over them, and be
glad and shall send gifts, one to an other, for these two Prophets vexed them
that dwelt upon the earth. etc.

THe wicked inhabitants of the earth reioysed with themselves and were
joyful for the destruction of the prophets. For those two prophets although
they were but few in number, yet they grievously tormented all the wicked
inhabitants of the earth, whiles they thundered ye thretning of gods word
against their ungodliness. The wicked therefore do testify by this joy, with how
great pricks of conscience they were tormented, when as there sins and
offenses were reproved, and corrected of the godly pastors and teachers. For
such is the force of gods word, that it tormenteth even the contemners of the
same, with due deserved punishments.

Verse. 11. But after three days and an half. etc.

THE wicked shall not always triumph over the martirs of Christ which they
have cruelly slain, but they shall perish themselves, sooner the^ they
suppose. For all power shall be taken from Antichrist, which he has over ye
Saints, which although his flatterers and peuish adherentes do boast, shall be
eternal, yet Christ measures it here by the space of three days and an
half. Which verelye pertayneth both to the beatinge down the pride of the
wicked, when as they hear that there kingdom shall endure, but a few days,
and also to the comforting of the afflicted servants of Christ, and to teach
and instruct them to patience, when as they understand that in short space of
time the tyranny of Antichrist shall be taken from among them.

The spirit of life which came from God entered into the^ and they stood up
upon there feet. etc. According to the manner of the prophets he uses the
time paste for the time to come, and the meaning is, that we should not think
that they are utterly lost and destroyed, which Antichrist by a diuilishe
cruelty has slain and taken away, they which seemed to lie as dead, for the
space of three days and an half, at length when the power of there
adversaries is taken away, and God giving them a new life, and standing
vprighte upon there feet, shall prove and show that they were not dead, but
that they slept only for a certain time. Which thing shall clearlye be
seen in the resurrection of the just, although this place may well and fitly
be understood of a new raising up of ministers, which ye Lord will place in yt
rooms of those which are crowned with martyrdom, but chiefly in the end of
the world after that the man of sin is revealed, which we see is come to pas
in this our age.

And great fear came upon them which saw them. etc. The wicked must needs
be stryken with an horrible tear and terror, when as they shall see them
restored again to life whom they slew, where upon they certeynly understand
that they warred against God. For when as preciouse and dear in the sight of
the Lord is the death of his saints. Psalm 116. They can not but be
grieuousely tormented with fear of gods vengeance, which they perceive that
they have provoked against them selves with blind madness and rage.

Verse. 12. And they herd a great voice from heaven saying unto them come up
hither. etc.

WHiles fear and terror of eternal damnation, with the greatest horror of
wicked conscience does occupy and posses there adversaries, they are called up
to heavenly joys, with a sweet voice and full of consolation. This reward is
laid up for the faithful martyrs of Christ, that out of prison, torments,
and death it self, being raised up to a blessed life, they shall receive a
crown of glory in the kingdom of heaven, with him, whom they have witnessed
in earth. This hope nourishes there minds in the greatest torments, least
they should fainte for any pains or punishments of the body, which fight
against the wicked and have eternal happiness for there reward.

And they ascended up to heaven in a cloud. etc. Like as Christ our head
ascended in a cloud, and we also shall be taken up in the clouds to meet
Christ as the Apostle witnesses, so those two prophets the witnesses of God
are says to ascend up into heaven.

And there enemies saw the^ etc. Like as they shall see Christ which perced him
thorough, even so shall they see his members the holy martyrs lifted up to
heavenly joy, which despised, afflicted, and slew them in earth, when as
they them selves being thrust into the dongeon of hell, shall be tormented for
ever not only with there own evils, but also with the blessed estate of there
adversaries. So the rich Glutton saw Lazarus in the bosom of Abraham, whom
he despised as a most vile creature whiles he was living, neither cared he to
feed him at the least with the cromes yt fell from his table. Luke. 16.

Verse. 13. And in that hour there was a great earthquake. etc.

WHen as the ripe and full time shall come in which God will take vengeance
upon Antichrist and his folowers, men's matters shall be shaken with a mighty
great motion, all things shall be moved, with wars, with treasons, and with
seditions, neither shall Antichrist any longer inioye his kingdom peacibly
which being sore troubled with this horrible commotion as it were shaken with
an earthquake, shall shortly after fall to utter ruin. We may suppose that
this earthquake has happened in our age, for we have partly before our eyes,
and partly we bear in fresh memory, with what motions through the cause of
religion, all christendom is shaken. And the other things which follow in
this verse, are plainly seen in this our time. And the tenth part of the city
fell. etc. There is no man which knows not, how great a deminishing and decay
of it self the Church of Rome has suffered, from which very many nations
have utterly departed, and forsaken it. And also superstition it self has
failed in the tenth part among the papists, and they them selves are
constrained to leave and forsake many of there toys and trifles, and to
confess certain errors with which in time past they bound very straightly
the faith of the people.

And in the earthquake there were slain the names of 7. thousand men. etc. To
a great multitude of men, this earthquake shall not only be troublesome, but
also mortal, by the violent force whereof seven thousand men shall be destroyed:
concerning the numbers, of ten, and seven, we have often said before that they
are referred to fulness and perfection. As this number of 7. thousand
comprehends all those, who^ God has appointed and ordained to punishment in
this grieuouse co^motio^ of the world. For as many as are not humbled with the
scorges of God and called to repentance, those being hardened in there
ungodliness shall at length bear the deserved punishments of there heynouse
offenses.

And the remnants were afraied and gave glory to the god of heaven. etc. God
has always his remnantes, which according to election being drawn out of the
greatest flames, are preserved and kept to the glory of his name. The rest
thereof being tamed with the rods of God, and taught by the fall and ruin of
the other, are instructed to repentance, and being stricken with an earnest
fear of god forsaking the filthy worshipping of Idols, will apply them selves
to yield up due glory to the God of heaven. We see very many such in our age,
which being werie of the errors of Antichrist, do acknowledge the true
religion of Christ, and magnifye the God of heaven with ye other godly
worshippers. Here we ought to reverence the counsels of god, which are far
above ye capacity of our reason, when as the third part of me^ was slain by
the army of ye horsemen as we read, in the 9. chap. none repented, but here
when the 7. thousand are destroyed, ye rest return to a better mind.

Verse. 14. The second woe is past and behold the third woe will come anon.

THe second woe of those three, which were foretold to pertayne to the trumpet
of the three last Angels, when as the 6. trumpet has received an end, the
holy ghost shows that the last woe shall shortly come, which is eternal woe,
to all the reprobate, which shall be published by ye trumpet of yt 7. Angel.
Therefore if we se all things fulfilled which pertayne to the 6. trumpet, ye
next thing is that we shortly after wait for to hear the sound of the last
trumpet in the coming of Christ.

Verse. 15. And the seventh Angel blew the trumpet and there were great voices
in heaven. etc.

CHrist affirmed with an oath in the tenth chapter. That the trumpet of the 7.
Angel should be last, under which ye mystery of God should be finished, as he
has declared to his servant ye prophets. Therefore when the sound of this
trumpet was herd, Thou shows yt the praises of God, and of his Christ were
song with meruailouse joy of the heavenly spirits.

Saying the kingdoms of this world are our Lords and his Christ's. etc. The
heavenly spirits be joyful with God, now when Antichrist and his patron the
devil, which exerciced tyranny in the world, be vanquished, all the kingdoms
of the world are become gods and his Christ's to whom they properly pertayne*

And he shall reign for evermore. etc. They do not acknowledge an earthly and
transitory kingdom of God, but an eternal Dominion, which indureth
throughout all ages. But it may be demanded whether God does not now also
reign and always has reigned in the whole world? verily the chief
government has always been Gods, and all things are ruled at his will and
pleasure. But now Satan, and Antichrist by his permission and sufferance
obtain principality over the darckenes of this world, whose power in the
day of the last judgment shall be utterly abolished. Therefore God shall then
reign with his Christ, when no adversaries shall molest or trouble the
happiness of his Church. And in this song we may behold the right holy and
godly nature of the heavenly spirits, that they do not so much rejoice for
there own eternal blessedness, as that they triumph for the magnifyinge of
gods glory, of which (if we will be like unto them) it becomes us to be more
careful then of our own salvation. More over this place is of force to
overthrow the error of the Chi^iastes, which shut up the kingdom of Christ in
the space of a thousand years, when as that voice does clearly confess that
he shall reign for ever and ever.

Verse. 16. Then the 24. elders which sat before God on there seats fell upon
there faces and worshipped God. etc.

THe reverend company of the 24. elders, which being placed in seats
before the throne of god do represente the whole fellowship of gods elect, do
not omit there duty, but falling prostrate before the throne, they humbly
worship god with all earnest affection of mind.

Verse. 17. Saying we give the thanks o Lord. etc.

THose also do meruailously rejoice, that all the enemies of god being
overthrown, he has his sound and perfect glory: And thry sing a long of
thankesgeuing saying. We give thee thanks o Lord. Because he has now showed
himself to be a revenger of his own glory, as though they had received some
notable and singular benefit, they agree that praise and thanks are to be
ascribed to god. And not without just cause, for nothing ought to be so dear
to the sons of God, which love him with there whole heart, as the glory of
there heavenly father, if neclecting all other things they would diligently
seek, they should both show them selves to be indeed begotten of God, and
also they should the best provide for there own health yea eternal
blessednesses.

Lord God almighty, which art and which was, and which are to come. etc. We
have spoken at large before in the first and fourth Chap. of these speeches, by
which they attribute all Dominion power and eternity to God.

For thou have received thy great might and have obtained thy kingdom. etc.
The heavenly spirits do praise God, that now at length when all his enemies
are vanquished he has received the sovereign rule and government which was
always due unto him, and also has happily begun that most peaceable
kingdom against which none of all the adversaries dare oppose and set them
selves. For so long as the devil and Antichrist exercised tyranny in the
world, they seemed to reign alone in ye earth, and they chiefly labored in
this one thing, that the kingdom of Christ might not stand, but after yt god
has now openly exercised and declared his great power which before lay hid,
when satan is subdued and yt kingdom of Antichrist abolished, ye glory of god
shall alone excel, and shine over all his creatures.

Verse. 18. And the gentiles were angry. etc.

IN my judgment they allude to the beginning of y^ 99. psalm. The lord shall
reign although ye people be angry. That is in spite of all the profane
enemies, thou only do obtain the empire and Dominion. For the wicked
gentiles following ye camp of Satan have set the^ selves against the kingdom
of Christ as much as they could, but David himself foresaw as we read in the 2.
Psalm, that all there enterprises should he in vain.

And thy wrath is come and the time of the dead, that they should be judged,
and that thou should give reward to thy servants the prophets and to the
saints, and to them that fear thy name, to small and to great. etc. Nether
to the wrath of the wicked gentiles, heretics, Turks, hypocrites has raged
against thee, and the members of thy body, and now on the other side the time
of thy wrath is come, that thou may destroy all thine enemies: For now is
that day come which is terrible to the wicked, in which the dead being raised
to life, may feel the severity and sharpness of thy judgment: in which
also a reward not due or deserved, but promised freely may be given to thy
servants. Not only to those which thou have raised up to the government of
thy Church, whom thou have endued with the spirit of prophecy, but also to
all the rest of the saints, which worship the in true faith, and reverence
thy name, as well to the small as to the great.

And should destroy them, that destroy the earth. etc.
