THey pronounce with one word that the horrible and manifold wickedness of
the reprobate shall be punished with grieuouse torments and pains: and
together therewith they show, how equal and just it is, that God should for
ever destroy those, which studied nothing else, but to destroy ye whole world
with there wickedness.

Verse. 19. And the temple of God was open in heaven, and there was scene in his
temple the arcke of his couenannt, and there followed lightninges and voices,
and thunderinges, and earthquake, and much hayle. etc.

SOme do join this verse with the Chapter following, that it might be the
beginning of the next vision, but it seems to me to be the conclusion and
shutting up of this vision. So that Ihon does teach that after the praises of
God were song of the heavenly company, the execution of his judgment, which
they so often published abroad, should follow. Verily when as the temple was
open in heaven into which the true worshippers of God were received, and the
arcke of covenant openly showed, that is Christ, by whose mediation they
should be received, for the rest, it should straitwaye lighten. thunder, and
hayle from heaven upon: the reprobate and all the army of Satan, by which
terrors the wicked being driven to madness, should be thrust down to the
everlasting pains of hell. And he does briefly comprehend in this place the
form and manner of the last judgment, which he would afterward in the end
of this Prophecy, prosecute more at large.

The twelfte Chapter.
THis third vision conteyneth the ix. Chapters following, in which the madness
of the Devil and Antichrist against the Church is described, in other figures
then before, yet the same Church by the defense of Christ does stand and endure
safe against all the inuasio^s of the enemies. And the malignant Church which
seduceth the greatest part of the world into error is painted out in her
lively colors, then follow the punishments, which go before her fall, at
length follows here extreme ruin, which shall never be restored or repaired
again, after this follows the condemnation of the devil and Antichrist, and
the eternal felicity of the Church after the resurrection, all these things
are described more clearly, and more at large then in the former vision, and
the self same thing is expounded by sundry visions, that the truth thereof
might be more certain and that it might be printed more depelye in our minds,
which the prophets also do use often times. And in this 12. Chapter the
Church is brought in, suffering persecution of the Prince of darkness, which is
the head of all her enemies: and her state and condition is described of what
sort it should be from the first preaching of the Gospel even to the end of
the world.

Verse. 1. And there appeared a great wonder in heaven. etc.

GReat and meruailouse things were to be showed by a great and wonderful
sign, for it is above the capacity of our wit, how the Church, which is
described under the figure of a woman weak, unapt to war, and unarmed,
could any while stand in safety, against so sturdy and armed enemies. But
she appears in heaven that her birth and country might be signified, for
here in earth she is but a pilgrim and stranger.

A woman clothed with the sun. etc. The spouse of Christ is showed under the
form and shape of a woman, which of her self is weak and without force and
strength, but yet sufficiently furnished against all enemies, with the virtue
and strength of her spouse Christ. She is seen clothed with the sun, all
whose gloriouse apparaill is Christ the sun of righteousness, which
spreads the beams of his light upon the whole Church.

And the moon under her feet, etc. She treads under her feet all temporal
and transitory things, which although they seem to show forth there
brightness as the light of the moon, yet they are in no price or estimation
with the Curche, in which the gloriouse light of the sun being always
present, does darken all the beams of those things.

And upon her head a crown of twelve stars. etc. She has her head crowned
with twelve most bright shinning stars eue^ as it were with a beautiful
crown, not made of gold or earthly preciouse stones, but of stars, that is
of heavenly matter, which is the doctrine of the twelve Apostles which they
being lightened of the only son the fountain of Gods wisdom, have
preached, and after committed the same to writing. But if any object, that not
all the writings of the Apostles are extant, neither that they were all
Apostles, which writ Gospels, the answer is in a redines, because that
doctrine, which was delivered by a few writers, was nevertheless the doctrine
of all the twelve Apostles, verily even ye same which being received from
Christ they preached in the whole world. we showed before, yt in the number of
twelve is signified, ye unity of the Church gathered out of a miserable
dispersion, to which end Christ chose twelve Apostels, according to the
number of so many tribes of Israel, and afterward he sent ye same to ye
gentiles which he would have to be gathered into one body of Israel.

Verse. 2. And she was with child and cried travailing in birth and pained,
ready to be delivered. etc.

ALthough she was barren of her self, yet fruitful by he spouse, and now
even nighe to her travail, she is payned with great pensiuenes and carefulnes
that she might bring forth that which she has conceived by the seed of
Gods word. And this is a true and lively description of the true Church.

Verse. 3. And there appeared another wonder in heaven. etc.

AFter the Church described by a notable and clear figure, follows a full
description of a foul and cruel monster which is enemy of the same. And so
like as ye figure of the woman before painted out, was a wonderful sign, so
likewise the form and shape of her enemy seemed to John a thing worthy great
admiration, which was showed by and by after the most pleasant vision of the
woman. And it is so much more meruailouse that so horrible a monster appears
no where else but in Heaven. But we se in th^s figure, how far of it is from
the condition of the Church, to want an enemy, whose assaults and invasions
she is compelled to suffer, even in heaven. And we may chiefly here
acknowledge the malice of ye devil, which persecuteth ye Church even unto the
heavens, not countinge it not enough to vex the same with grievous torments in
earth, unless he may strive if he could so pluck down her eternal
salvation, which is in heaven. Let us not therefore make any covenant of since
with this enemy, for he seeks by all means nothing else but our utter
destruction.

Behold a great red Dragon. etc. He uses an aduerbe of shewinge for to sheere
up greater attention. For the thing is worthy to be diligently noted and
considered, this terrible Dragon is that old serpent which seduced ye first
woman to the destruction of the whole world, now laboreth diligently, not only
by subtilty as in time past, but also by force and cruelty to bring into
destruction, this woman restored to her old and also a far better s^ate and
condition by Christ. And seeing all kind of serpe^ts are both terrible and
hateful to us, ye great dragon cannot but raise up great terrore of himself,
and also no less hatred to all those which have a care to eschew his poisoned
and venim b^ringes Add moreover unto these, that shining in his fyery colloure
he thretnith nothing else to all those, which he shall enticelinglye draw into
his net, but mad fury and rage of destroyinge, and the studiouse care and
desire of sheading blood.

Having seven heads and ten horns, and upon his heads seven crowns. etc. He
is not simple in subtilty or a poisonful spirit of one mouth, but a deformed
monster with seven heads he testifies by the number of ye same heads that he
inuenteth and deuiseth all kinds of crafts and subtilties, like as being
armed with seven horns he boasts yt he wears crowns upon every one of
his heads, it shows his innumerable victories by which he has subdued to
his obedienc all the whole world.

Verse. 4. And his tail drew the third part of the stars of heaven and cast
them to the earth. etc.

IT may also be here gathered what strength he had in his horns, and his
heads, seeing that by casting his tail only, yt is the lust of earthly
things yt he drew the third part of the stars to the earth that is many of
the teachers which for a time seemed to shine as stars in heaven, which being
addict to the study of earthly pleasures, have utterly lost all there heavenly
brightness, by which wicked act he takes greater courage, and hope yt he can
more easily overthrow also the whole church. Moreover it is hear showed how
great the unmeasurable hugenes of that monstrouse body is, whose meruailouse
long tail would suffice to cast down the third part of the stars. Such
and so great is the enemy of the Church.

And the Dragon stood before the woman, which was ready to be delivered to
devour her children, when she had brought it forth. etc. It is shadowed under
this figure with how great madness the devil would rage against the Church. The
Dragon waits upon the woman, which is in trauaill that he might devour the
infant so soon as it should be horn. How diligently Satan labored even in
the first beginning of the Church to destroy her tender babe, and first issue
that there might no posterity of the same remain in the world, we know by
histories. What left he undone by his ministers the Jews, the pries^es, and
the Pharisees, that the doctrine of Christ might not be spread abroad in the
world, but might be utterly extinguished with the Apostles them selves. With
what violent rage did he stir up Nero and other bloody Emperors that they
might utterly subvert the whole Church, by murdering infinite numbers of her
children, the faithful confessors and martires of Christ. The devil therefore
would have destroyed the infant of the Church, even in the very birth
thereof, if the success had been agreeable to his will and careful trauaill.

Verse. 5. And she brought forth a male Child. etc.

THe Dragons hope deceyueth him, for although he had assayed every way, yt he
might destroy the fruit and offspring of the Church even in the very birth,
yet the Church brought forth a male child strong and lively, which in s^ite of
Satan should receive the inheritance of rule, and Dominion appointed and
ordained for him of God the father.

Which should rule all nations with a rod of Iron. etc This prophecy is of
Christ in the 2. psalm. Therefore Christ is formed in the hearts o^ yt
faithful by the ministry of the Gospel as Paul witnesses to the Galath. 4.
chap. And Christ does compel all nations to his obedience although they
obstinately resist, breaking them with a rod of Iron. And the members of Christ
which are the faithful through him are made partakers of the same kingdom.
The devil lies craftilye in waise for these that he might devour them, so
soon as they he brought forth into the light of yt Gospel. But he does not
obtain his desire, for howsoever he shall conspire with the whole army of hell
to bring them to destruction, yet the lord will not give the^ for a pray unto
his teeth. It follows therefore.

And her son was taken up to God and to his throne. etc. Under the protection
and defense of God, he is in safety, so that he whom the Dragon desired to be
drowned in the bottomeles pit of hell, is taken up to god, and to the throne of
his majesty, and drawn out of the Jaws of the devil. For Christ whom the
devil wished so much to be destroyed, fitteth at the right hand of the divine
glory, to the which dignity also of heavenly glory, by his benefit are
exalted, as many as are made the Children of God and of the Church by faith.
In vain therefore Satan seeks there destruction, whom God has drawn up to
him self, and has so received them to the throne of his glory. How greedely
the devil assayed to blotte out the name of Christianity in the first
spreading abroad of the same, we have before touched, but what proffited he in
the end in bestowing so great labor? For how much more his ministers raged in
there madness with sword and fire, and all kind of torments against, the child
of the Church, that they might destroy him yet being but an infant and not
able to make battle, so much the more godliness increased exceadingly, and the
Church daily received such increasings, as were not to be ashamed of. And
Christ whose glory the Devil so greatly envied, sitting in the throne of gods
majesty defends yt godly from heaven, takes vengeance upon his enemies,
and bestows all kind of good gifts upon his Church. We need not fear
therefore, least that the whole Church should ever be subject to the tirannie
of the Dragon.

Verse. 6. And yt woman fled into wilderness where she has a place prepared of
god, yt they should feed her there, a 1000.200. and threscore days.

AFter that he had declared how yt the son of the woman was taken up into a
place of safety, now he teaches how provision is made also for ye woman her
self. God could at his will bind and restrain the devil that he should not
hurt the Church at all. But this is the most wise dispensation of his holy
will, that when she has been proved, and tried by sundry afflictions in the
world, he will at length, take her to himself into heaven: yet in the mean
time he does not fail her even in the most desperate matters, but sends
ayed from heaven in due season. Therefore he opens a way for the woman to
fly, that the might for a time eschew the violence of ye Dragon. Christ him
self also permitted this manner of auoydinge haunger to his apostels Matthew the
10. But when and who ought to sly when persecution approchethe it is not so
easy to express in words, as that the holy^ ghost shall inwardly instruct
every one when time shall be. But that we should not think, that the woman
should perish in the desert, where there is the scarsity of all things. S.
John does express, that there was also in the desert a seat prepared for her
of God, whereas she might safely for a time appoincted by God, breath and
refreshe her self from ye persecution of the Dragon. And least we might
suppose that she should in the mean time want any thing, he shows that she
shall be nourished and fed there for a thousand two hundredth and sixty days,
that is, by the space of two and forty months, which make three years and an
half, which short time, when as it is the half of a prophetical week, is
said to be granted to satan and Antichrist, that they cannot any longer
oppress or afflict the Church. Moreover this place does plainly show, that
the church shall not always be visible to the world, which thing the papists
do urge most of all, for if it should be always in the fight of all men, how
may she be said to fly into ye wilderness? Yea it is certain by this place,
that the Church of Rome is not signified by this woman, which was never
banished and driven into the wilderness, from ye eyes of men. And lastly we are
here also taught that we must answer to our adversaries which ask us where
our Church was before these two or three hundred years. Verily if we know yt
the true worship of God, was to be found in no region of Europe or Asia, it is
enough that it was in ye desert, that is in places not commonly known, that it
lay hid by the decree of god, even unto the time by him appointed. For ye
number of ye elect, which is ye church shall never fail but God does preserve
and keep to himself 7. thousand men, which have neither bowed the knee to
Baal nor kissed his Image with the mouth, and that, when as Elias believed that
he remained alone in the people of Israel. How much more is it like that
there remained many elect of God, throughoute the large regions of Asia, and
Europe, and also some parts of Africa, in which the name of Christ is spoken
of, which although they were unknown to Antichrist and his adherentes, yet
they offered and yielded to god his due honor? The papists therefore to there
own hurt do boast of there visible Church, and rashly do condemn ours,
because it was some time invisible to the Romanistes. For in this it is more
like to this true Church, that it sometime lay hid: and there synagoge
always visible, does sufficiently bewray it self not to be this woman, which
fled into the desert.

Verse. 7.8. And there was a battle in heaven, Michaell and his Angels fought
against the Dragon, and the Dragon and his Angels fought, but they prevailed
not, neither was there place any more found in heaven. etc.

THe first attempt or enterprise of Satan was most daungerouse, namely that he
might steal away, and devour the infant of the Church, so soon as it were
borne, and that he might deprive the Church for ever, of her eternal happenes.
But Christ the defendour of his spouse sets himself against the wicked
enterprises and practices of the Devil, and so the scarce battle arose in
heaven, whilst Satan studieth utterly to destroy the Church, and Christ to
save, and defend the same for ever. Therefore I expound this battelle, which
was toughte in heaven, of the study and enterprise of the Devil, whereby he
chiefly labors with all diligence to assalte ye eternal salvation of the
Church, which is founded in Christ, and his madness and impude^cie is noted,
that he dare fight with God him self. (Michaell and his Angels) Michaell that
great prince of the army of God does signify Christ, which is the general
c^ntayne of our oste, which thing is also taught in the 9.10, and 12. chap. of
Daniell, That he joins to him self the Aungells, it does not argue that
there is weakness or want of stre^ght in him, but he does it to increase our
confidence and trust. For the Dragon mustreth his army on every side of the
Angels of darkness, and puts forth all his strength to oppress Christ. But
what was the end of the battle? They prevailed not neither was there place
found any more in heaven. The terrible Dragon guarded with the infinite
thousands of his soldiers can do nothing against Christ, which defends the
health of his Church. Satan therefore being overcome with all his whole
army, is compelled to leave of the battle, and not that only, but also
being deprived of all hope of renuinge the war, he with all his soldiers is
cast down unto ye earth. Now therefore is the salvation of the elect certain,
when as the devil himself having assaied and proved all his strength to
break and overthrow the same, being put to shameful slighte, is overthrown
by the virtue and power of the most mighty Michaell.

Verse. 9. And the great Dragon that old serpent called the devil and Satan
was cast out, which deceives all the world, and he was cast into the earth
and his Angels were cast out with him. etc.

AFter that he had said that he was driven out of Heaven that his place
could there no longer be found, neither could he frustrate, or make void the
everlasting salvation of the Church, he shows whither he was thruste out
into Banishement with his whole army, that is to say into tho earth, that he
might exercise his mad rage only upon the reprobate, and that he might
afflicte the Church with temporal evils only, and yet that he might not
obtain that he would: that is, that through the terror, and fearce of
torments, he might drive her out of the earth. Moreover we must observe
with what sundry names and titles the holy ghost sets him out, that all his
malice and subtle deceytes might be perceived. First he is called, that
great Dragon, which is described before in the third Verse of this Chapter.
Secondly, that old serpent which seduced our first parents to disobedience,
now so much more subtle, as he is more ancient by long use and experience.
Thirdly he is called in greek even as it were by his propre name, Diabolos,
which in english is devil, yt is a false accuser, which with false crimes, and
secreat accusations never ceased to accuse the godly before the Lord God, that
if he could by any means, he might bring them into Gods hatred. Fourthly he
is called in Hebrew Satan, that is an adversary, the sworn enemy of Christ
and all godly men, at whose hands we ought to look for nothing, but enmity,
whom, it behooves us chiefly both to hate and take heed of. Fyftlye he is
called the deceyuer of the whole world, of whom how great the deceites are,
and with what diligent care of us to be eschewed, we may know sufficiently
even by this place, yt he has seduced the whole world, that is the greatest
part of the world, into errors, and false worshipping of God, whereby we
understand, that, that is not the very catholic Church in deed, which
boasts in the greatest multitude of men, neither therefore to be called
catholic or universal, because all give there consent into the same, seeing
the Devil here deceyueth the whole world: but that which all ye godly do
acknowledge for there mother, although the reprobate in respect of number, by
infinite parts do excede them.

Verse. 10. And I herd a loud voice saying etc.

AFter so gloriouse a victory over Satan and his army, the heavenly spirits
do sing a triumphant song to God and his Christ. By which we are taught that
the glory of god is always to be celebrated of us in the Church for so
unspeakable a benefit. That he says a loud voice, he shows both the
multitude and also the fervent zeal of the singers, for we ought all earnestly
to brust forth to the singing and celebrating of gods praises.

In heaven now is salvation, and strength, and the kingdom of our God, and
the power of his Christ. etc. There is uttered in this song, what fruit and
commodity there is of so notable a victory. For in saying that there is
salvation in heaven, they understand that the everlasting health of ye Church
does now remain unshaken after yt the devil which assayed to oppress the
same with war, is vanquisshed and cast down prostrate unto the earth. The
virtue and power of god has showed forth it self, to beat down the
violence of Satan. And now the kingdom of God over the saints, which the
proud Dragon desired, remains inviolate, when the Dragon is thrust out. And
especially the dignity of Christ does excel over all the power of the
adversary, by whose government the battaill is fought, and likewise by his
invincible virtue and power all the whole army with there captain are
overthrown.

Because the accuser of our brethren is cast down, which accused them before
our God day and night. etc. He which weried continually the ears of god with
daily false accusations laid to the charge of the godly, that he might spoil
the^ of eternal bliss, and as if they were guilty of eternal death might
make them bond slaves to the torments of hell. But god will now no longer
abide to hear any accusatio^s against his saints, which are washed with the
blood of his son. Who shall say any thing to the charge of gods chosen: it
is god which justifies, who is he that shall condemn? Romans 8.

Verse. 11. And they overcame him by the blood of the lamb and by the word of
his testimony: and they loved not there lives unto the death. etc.

Wonderful is the clemency of Christ that he takes his saints into the
praise of this victory, but yet in such sort as redou^deth to his own
glory. The heavenly spiritess therefore rejoice with the faithful for there
victory, but yet obtained not by there own blood, but by the blood of Christ,
although they them selves also powered forth there lives in battaill. And this
Aungelicall song does clearly reach with what armor and weapons the
faithful may overcome the devil, that is with the shield of faith, which is
in the blood of the la^be, which offered up him self a sacrifice for there
sins, and with the sword of Gods word and the confession of the name of
Christ, which they were never ashamed of before me^, although for witnessing
the same they should suffer most bitter death. After the same manner ought all
the godly to be prepared to whom the glory of God and his Gospel is
preciouse, that they may not love there lives unto death, as often as necessity
of confessing his name does require ye same. And although the danger of death
be absent, yet the same affection ought always to be with us, that we may not
love our lives even to the death, in comparison of holding the incomparable
treasure of the truth of Gods gospel.

Verse. 12. Therefore rejoice ye heavens and ye that dwell in them. etc.

A benefit is bestowed upon those in vain, whereof they that are partakers,
have no fruition in the same. And often times it comes to pas through our
perverse crokednesse, that being adorned with great benefits of God, we feel
no fruit of the same. Therefore they exhorted the heaven, and all the heavenly
spirits that they would be touched with the most joyful sense and fealinge
of so great a good, and for the same would rejoice with joy unspeakable, that
to Christ, glory, and to the Church, eternal salvation, is obtained by this
so gloriouse a victory.

Woe be to the Inhabitants of the earth and the sea, for the Devil is come
down unto you, which has great wrath knowing that he has but a short time.
etc. They do not so much curse the wicked, as that they express there most
grieuouse dangers, to the seducing of whom, the devil descended into the earth
full of fury and wrath. (Of the earth and ye sea) according to the literal
sense is understood the inhabitants of the main land, and Islandes, but
figu^atiuely he understands all the reprobate, which are so much addicted to
earthly and fraill pleasures, that they never look up into heaven, to make
whom blind and that worthily, the Devil descended, not more moved by his
own fury, then sent down by the judgment of god. Whose madness, they show,
should be so much the more fearce and cruel, because he knew for certentie
that a very short time was granted him to stir up his tragedies in. He will
therefore pretermite nothing in the mean time, whereby he may draw a large
and fat pray into his nets. What does he therefore.

Verse. 13. And when the Dragon saw that he was cast unto the earth, he
persecuted the woman which had brought forth the man child. etc.

WHen he saw that he was driven out of heaven, that he could not by charging
and false accusing hinder the eternal salvation of the church, perceyuinge
the same to be yet warring in earth, he raises up horrible persecutions
against her by his ministers the tyrants. And when as he could not devour the
child which the woman brought forth, for which he had long time lien
subtillye in wait, he persecuteth the woman which brought forth, with beastly
cruelty. Being overcome of the head, he sets upon the body. We may note
here the deuilishe cruelty of some men, which if they can not bring the
greatest hurtes upon the godly, as death it self, that they do not leave of to
hurt by such means as they be able, they violently spoil them of there
goods, they d^fame them with reproaches and sclaunders, and hate also even
there friends, for there sakes.

Verse. 14. But to the woman were given two wings of a great Eagle.

BEfore he said that the woman being delivered of her child fled into ye
wilderness: now he shows by what means she could eschew or fly the
marvelous swiftnes of the dragon in pursuinge. Two wings, says he were
given unto her, with which she be came swifter then the devil, and he adds
moreover (of a great Egle that we should understand, that the woman might
safely trust unto them. By the wings we may acknowledge the sundry and
vnaccustomable ways and means of flying which the Lord opens to the Church
as often as he has decreed to deliver the same by slight from the hands of
tyrants.

That she might fly into the wilderness, into her place where she is nourished
for a time, times, and half a time, from the presence of the serpent. etc. We
have spoken before in the 6. verse, of the flight into the desert, and of the
wonderful providence of God, which even in the scarcity and want of all
things provides not only lodging but also meat for nourishment. And the
space which is here darckly called, a time, times, and half a time, I
enterprete to be ye same, which he said a thousand two hundredth and sixty
days, that is, three years and an half, so that one time may agree to a
year, two times, to two years, and half a time, to half a year, for in
Daniell to whom he alludeth, times are read in the duall number, that they
might signify two times. And these appellatio^s of time, seem to be applied to
the sense and affection of ye Church which was banished. For she thinks the
time of her calamity long, and afterward follow two times, which increase the
weariness, but at length the half time, when as the matters seem almost
desperate, does manifestly show that according to the promise of our savior,
the days of affliction are shortened.

Verse. 15. And the serpent cast out of his mouth water after the woman as it
had been a river, because she should have been caught of the sloude. etc.

THe devil being vanquished an hundredth times yet repareth the battaill
again, and though violence have small success, yet he absteyneth not from
crafts and subtilties. He follows the woman therefore flying into the
wilderness, who^ he cannot catch and tear with his teeth, with reproaches,
lies, and sclaunders framed by heritiques, and hypocrites, whereby if he could
he coueteth to bring her into an evil report. And we see what a great s^oude
of lies and reproaches he has cast after her by the Arrians, Pelagians,
Papists, and other such like hypocrites, by which he studied, and also now
studieth to draw her in to the hatred of Princes, mighty men, and moreover of
all those which gave any credit unto them. But Satan shall never have
success or prevail by his subtilties, for it follows.

Verse. 16. But ye earth help the woman, and the earth opened her mouth and
swalowed up ye river which the dragon cast out of his mouth. etc.

HE which delivered his Church from the greatest violence. and cruelty of the
enemies, will not suffer her to be taken with the subtle sleyghtes of Satan,
but the earth shall rather open her mouth as it did in time past to swalow up
the whole faction of Cho^e, Dathan, and Abyrame, then that at the will and
pleasure of the Devil a hear should fall from her head. And we see that all
the devises of heretics against the Catholic Church, by which the dragon
hoped that the woman should be destroyed, have vanished away, as though they
were droncke up of the earth, and yet the Church her self, now at length
drawn out of secreat places, stands immouable, and shall stand for ever,
even unto the end of the world, We may here note that the heaven the earth,
and all things, which are in them, do help the godly, as often as the Lord
will deliver them out of the hands of the enemies. And also that we be not to
much moved and troubled, for the reproaches and sclau^ders of the enemies of the
Church, heritiques and hypocrites, (which are the instruments of the devil) by
which they endeavor, even like a most swift flood to draw her, and her members
into hatred and envy. For all there lies shall shortly be swalowed up by ye
earth, and there deuilish enterprises shall be brought to naught.

Verse. 17. Then the Dragon was wroth with the woman: and went and made wary
with the remnant of her seed, which keep the commaundeme^ts of god, and have
the testimony of Jesus Christ.

THe devil having set upon her so often with so great violence, and being so
often so shamefully repelled, it is no marvel though he be driven into
wrath and fury, yet notwithstanding he leauethe not of from his purpose,
which he took in hand. But although he can not oppress the whole Church
with the sundry sleyghtes which he has invented, yet he persecuteth every one
of her members with a meruailouse study and care of destroyinge. He make the
war therefore with the remnante of her seed, wheresoever they be dispersed
through the whole Earth, and he never leauethe of, to assault them partly by
force, and partly by deceites, whom we ought to resist strong in faith,
putting on the whole armor of God which the Apostle describes in the 6. Chap.
to the Ephe. And in that he calls the sons of ye Church the seed of the
woman, he alludeth to that, which the Lord pronounced of the seed of the
woman, which should break the serpents head, that we should not fear the
invasion of him, whose head being broken by Christ, is delivered also unto us,
which are the seed of the woman, to be trodden upon. Furthermore he briefly
expresses, whom he nu^breth among the lawful sons of the Church, that is
they which kept the commandments of God, and also do openly confess the
faith of Christ, which they embrace.

Verse. 18. And I stood on the sea sand. etc.

THis verse pertayneth to the vision of the Chapter following, Ihon therefore
thought in a vision that he stood upon the shoore, that he might behold the
beast ascendinge out of the sea.

The thirtenth Chapter.
WHen as he had showed that the devil the chief enemy of the Church
attempteth all things for the destruction of the same, now he shows in this
chapter, what principal instruments he would use, in oppugning the salvation
of the same, verily even the Romayne Empire that is Antichrist and his most
cruel ministers.

Verse. 1. And I saw a beast rise out of the sea etc.

ANtichrist is compared to a most cruel beast, because he persecuteth the
Church without all reason, or any sense or felinge of humanity. Moreover he is
not called (...), but (...) that is a certain wild and cruel beast. For of
the brute beasts, some although they want reason, yet they are gentle and
hurtlesse, but Antichrist is a beast of untamed wildenes, void of all show of
gentleness. For no otherwise then a wild beast through hunger rampeth upon the
pray offered him, does Antichrist rage upon the Church. But he is also said
to ascend out of the sea, that in the very birth or first springing up he
might show of what sort his rule and Dominion should be, that is troublesome,
and tempestuouse, diverse and inconstant. And histories do testify out of how
great waves of battaill, and tumultes the Romayne Empire has risen.

Having seven heads and ten horns, and upon his horns were ten crowns and
upon his head, the name of blasphemy. etc. By the number of heads, and
horns this monster bewrays him self of what father he was begotten, verelye
of the great Dragon, whose natural properties he thoroughly resembles. For
although the Monarchy of the Romans was ordained by God, even as all power
is of God, yet in as much as it abounded in trandes, tyranny cruelty and
lust, and that it persecuted the Church of Christ, it was of the devil, but
chiefly when all the power thereof was translated to the Pope, which is
chiefly figured under this beast, without all doubt it is to be acknowledged
to be the very natural son of Satan, but when as other notes also of him,
by the number of his heads and horns are propounded of the Angel in the 17.
Chapter, we will not touch them before we come to that place. That he wears
then crowns in his horns, when as the Dragon had but seven on his heads, it
seems to be referred to that, that the ten horns do signifye kings, which in
the beginning were consuls only and presidentes of provinces, but when as this
beast shall the second time rise up they shall together with the beast in one
hour receive kingly power, of which there follows more in the 17. Chap. And
he bears in his heads the name of blasphemy, when he calls himself the
head of the universal Church For although in his decrees, and other writings
approved of him, horrible blasphemies may be found, in which he is called some
time neither God, nor man, but as it were a neuter between both, sometime he is
called Christ, sometime our Lord God, and sometime God above all gods, yet he
bears that name openly in his head to be seen of all men, whereby he
boasts himself to be Christ's vicare as though he were absent, and plucketh
to him self alone, the knowledge of all causes, and he boasts that he can
not err in any thing. The like blasphemies uttered his predecessors,
Caligula, Nero, Domitian, Diocletian, which commanded that they them selves
should be worshipped as Gods, and that temples should be buylte and altars
consecrated to there godhead. But none more impudently then the Romayne
Bishops, for all men did mark and deride the folly and madness of the emperors,
although they flattered them most filthily,, but almost all have in good
earnest acknowledged the divinity of the pope, and have asked that of him,
which is the property of God alone to grant, as remission of sins and other
such like.

Verse. 1. And this beast which I saw was like a cat of the mountain, and his
feet were as the feet of a bear, and his mouth as the mouth of a Lion. etc.

BY this description it is more clearer then the light it self, that the
Romayne Empire is assigned, which did conteyne in it the power of the other
throe kingdoms, which are described by the sumulitudes of a Lion, a Bear and
a Catte of the mountain, Daniell chapter 7. But the fourth monarchy that is
of the Romans, composed of the pride, raueninge, and cruelty of all the rest,
was unlike to all the other. He has therefore a body like to a catte of the
mountain, which signified Ale^ander the great, which was most swifte to
follow after the pray, he has the feet of a Bear, by which he is equal in
ravening with the Meades, and Persians, but he had ye mouth of a Lion, by
which he exceadeth in hautinesse and pride the Assirians and Chaldeans and he
exceadeth in cruelty the fearcenesse of all beasts.

And the Dragon gave him his power and his throne, and great authority. etc.
He receives not only the power to hurt, and persecute of the Devil, but
also he occupies his seat in earth, that the power of Satan is manifest to
be seen in nothing more then in his Vicare Antichrist, and this is that sea
of Antichrist, and authority of the Pope, of which they boast so much of,
that is to say, the throne of the Devil and power received at his hand. But
it may be demanded how the Devil could give power, or empire, seeinge all
powers are of him, which also bestows them upon the wicked and Tyrants. But
in the tyrannical power two things are to be considered, the one is the
ordinance of GOD, which disposes all Kingdoms at his will, and to whom he
will. And the other is, there frauds, there treasons, and cruelties, by which
they aspire to the government, which things are of the Devil. The devil
therefore granted power and authority to Antichrist, in as much as by his
provocation, by all wickedness and impiety they atteyne that tyranny, which
occupy that seat.

Verse. 3. And I saw one of his heads as it were wounded to death but his
deadlye wound was healed, and all the world wondered and followed the beast. etc.

ALmost all interpretours do grant that a great deminishing of the power of
Antichrist is signified by this head that was wounded, but when it was wounded
they agreed not. For some do suppose that it wounded at the time when as that
Ihon Husse, and Hierome of Phrage in disclosinge the subtilties of ANTICHRIST,
separated a great part of the Kingedome of Bohemia, from the authority of
that sea. Other do expound it of Julius Caesar, others of Nero being slain.
Others do refer it to the City of Rome taken, burned and spoiled by the
Goths. But to me, which by the Beast, do understand not the lawful
administration of the Empire, but the tyrannical power in persecutinge the
Church, that he seems then to have been wounded unto death when as
constantine the great after that Marentius, and Lic^nius the last persecutinge
tyrants of the heathenishe emperors were slain, in granting peace to the
Church, smote that most cruel and monstrouse head of Antichrist with a deadely
wound. But shortly after that wound was healed by the wicked emperors
Constantius and Iulianus, valence, and others of whom some being heritiques
and Iulianus a forsaker of the faith, persecuted the right Church until at
length the bloudye tyrante Phocas, and murderer of his Lord and Master
Mauritius, resigned the Antichristians Kingdom to Boniface the Pope, in whom
and his successors plainly revived ye head of deuilishe tyranny which was
almost cut of by Constantine. Yet in the mean I acknowledge ye the horrible
destruction, and calamities of men by battle, which were brought to the
lawful Empire of the Romans by the barbarouse people, the Goths, Vandales,
and Saracenes, opened and prepared a way to the rule of the Roman, bishop.
And this also is manifest by the writing and monumentes of the learned, yt the
byshoppricke of Rome, from syluester unto sabinianus being increased in
riches, and that through the favor of the Emperors, it did little and little
degenerate into foreign rule and government, until at length it ascended to
the very poynct and top of Antichristian Aucthority. Where upon to the great
wonder of the world his Kingdom was established, lyfted, and exaulted so high
out of so obscure and dark beginnings.

Verse. 4. And they worshipped the Dragon which gave power to the beast, and
they worshipped the beast saying, who is like unto the beast; who is able to
war with him. etc.

IT is marvelous that he says men worshipped the devil, whom every where
all do abhor and detest. But he understands that the worship and
obedience, which was yielded to Antichrist of the men that were seduced,
perteyned to the spreading abroad of the devils kingdom, seeing they hoonoure
Satan in his vicar or legate. Like as they do honor the king which reverence
those magistrates, which he has appointed under him. And that he expresses
when as immediately he adds (and they worshipped the beast, saying, who is
like to the beast? whose power is so great yt he can forgive sins, and open
the kingedome of heaven to whom he will. Who is able to war against him?
which draws down Emperors, and Kings as often as he lust, on^e of there
statelye seat, which thundreth out the sentences of cursing^, against his
enemies, and through the fullness of his power he can thrust down his
adversaries even into hell.

Verse. 5. And there was given him a mouth that spoke great things and
blasphemies. etc.

IF any shall marvel how the majesty of God can suffer so great
blasphemies, which the devil and Antichrist show out against the same: Saint
Ihon makes answer showing that this is by divine permission, that Antichrist
should exault him self above all heygh, whereby he might seduce the
reprobate, upon whom by the just judgment of God the efficacy, and strength
of error is sent, that they may believe lies which despised the truethe. 2.
Thessalo. 2. By this place we gather that the wicked can not brust forth into
blasphemies against God, at there pleasure, except God suffer, that they may
abuse there tongues, to there own destruction Moreover we may here note that
Antichrist ratleth one nothing, but great things, and blasphemies. For what
soever they boast as magnificall, concerning the dignity of the Pope, his
authority, keys, swords, and other prerogatives of his, is mere
blasphemy, by which he chalengeth to him self the place, and rowme of Christ
over the Church yea all the whole Popish doctrine, of the Sacrifice of the
Mass, of Purgatory, of Satisfactions, works of superurogation, and other
such like monstres, conteyneth infinite blasphemies.

And power was given unto him to do, two and ^ortie months. etc. This clause
does show that Antichrist could not obtain rule in the world but by the
secreat, and just judgment of God. But this power is shut within her limits,
that he can not reign so long as he would, nor exercise his ungodliness, but
his tyranny is limited by 42. months. Concerning this number of months
what I think is to be understood, I have expounded in the 11. chap. Verse. 2.
Here it shall suffice to note that this short space of half a week is put to
the comfort of the godly, that they should not fear. That the tyranny of
Antichrist should be eternal.

Verse. 6. And he opened his mouth unto blasphemy against God to blaspheme his
name his tabernacle, and them that dwell in Heaven. etc.

WHen the power of blaspheminge was once granted, he opened his mouth to
manifold blasphemies, for he spoke coneumeliouslye of God him self of his
name, and of his tabernacle, and of those which dwell in heaven, so he
counts it not enough to reproach the majesty of God only, but also his name
that is the worshipe and religion which he has prescribed to sanctify his
name, he co^de^neth as false, and heretical, and koyneth a new out to his own
brain. And also he blasphemeth the tabernacle of god, that is his Church, in
which God dwells by his spirit, when he calls it nothing else, but a
conspiracy of heretics and Schismatiques, We may two ways take this of
those which dwell in heaven, either for ye true members of the Church, which
he with great reproach of them calls Lutherans, and Zwinglians. etc. Or else
for the saints now triumphing in heaven whom he diverse ways sclaundereth
either when he braggeth that they are the patrones of his wickedness, or else
condemns their doctrine of error, or else when he does erecte temples unto
the^, Images, holy days, and other divine honors, making Idols of the holy
worshippers of God: that I may not speak with what stinking lies he extolleth
there lives, in the giving of martiloge, and in such kind of writings,
which are all mere blasphemy against the Saints, which dwell in Heaven.
And what reproaches he casts forth against God him self we have touched
before in the first verse.

Verse. 7. And it was given unto him to make war with the saints and to
overcome them, and power was given him over every kindred and tongue and
nation. etc.

HE signifies that Antichrist could do nothing, but in as much as ability
was permitted to him by God. In that therefore that he shows his cruelty upon
the holy martyrs of Christ, he does it not at his own pleasure, or at the
will of the devil, for then would he utterly extinguishe and des^oye all the
true worshippers of God: but by the will of god, for a punnishment of the
reprobate, and a trial of his children, for whom it is very profitable to be
proved with sundry temptations. There is given power to Antichrist to make
war against the saints, and to affect them them with sundry torments
until he may have the do^eiull victory of many thousand of the^ being slaien.
And this t^^anny does not rage in one region only, but every where through the
whole earth, this is a catholic crueltye. And that which we know partly by
histories, how many milians of marti^es were cruel murdered by the Emperores
and Roman Byshopes, we are partly taught by daily experience.

Verse. 8. Therefore all that dwell upon the earth shall worship him, whose names
are not written in the book of life of the lamb which was killed from the
beginning of the world. etc.

Like as he sore told in ye verse going before that Antichrist should show
his cruelty upon the bodies of the saints, so in this verse he shows
against the souls of whom his false illusions shall prevail. That is to say
against the reprobate only, which are not predestinate to eternal life in
Christ, whom he calls the lamb which was slaien from the beginning of y^
world, because the strength and effect of this sacrifice, can before he had
taken flesh profited the patriarchs from the beginning of the world, like
as it shall be profitable to the elect even to the end of the world. The
reprobate therefore being seduced partly by his sub^^lties, and partly
stricken with the cruelty used against those that resist, will acknowledge his
rule and au^thority, and will worship him instede of a most filthy Idol. For
his deceiptes and illusions shall not prevail in any, but in those which
perish.

Verse. 9. If any man have an ear let him hear. etc.

HE utters a matter worthy of great consideration as often as he moves
attentio^ with so earnest endeavor. We ought therefore with diligence to
imprint thoroughly in our minds the doctrine which follows to the hearing
whereof the holy ghost does as it were by name call every one of us.

Verse. 10. He that leads into captivity shall go into captivity, he that
kills with the sword must be killed with the sword, here is the patience and
the faith of the saints. etc.

THe law of repaying is decreed of the mighty God, for all tirantes, and to
those which oppress the Church of God with cruelty. Eternal captivity
abides for those which have led the the saints captives. They which have
slaien the martyrs with the sword, shall be killed with eternal death, which is
the sword of Gods furye and wrath. And also god will have certain signs of
his justice to remain apparent in the world, that all men may know that they
shall not escape vengeance, which according to the manner of beasts do
cruelly rage in madness against innocents. According to that of the poet: few
mighty cruel men descend to there grave without slaughter and blood few
tyrants by dry death. For if we should reckon up of the Emperors, those
which were the chief aucthors of persecutions, we shall find that they were
destroyed of God by diverse and sundry slaughters. Nero, Domitian, Decus,
Valerianus Licinius, Iulianus with many others, were slaien with bloody and
cruel death. Therefore the murtheringe of the saints is not so permitted to
Antichrist, that the Lord would leave the same always unrevenged. Here
therefore the saints have need of faith and patience, which follows next,
for except power were granted to Antichrist to e^ercise his tyranny, what
trial of faith should there be? what proof of patience? here therefore the
says and patience of the Saints is to be looked for.

Verse. 11. And I beheld an other beast coming out of the earth. etc.

NOw follows the description of the other beast which confirms the former
beast, yt we may know what instrument ^ Antichrist uses to the establisshing
of his kingdom. For as the Dragon with seven heads has for his vicare a
beast with seven heads: so the beast with seven heads has this beast with
two horns. He does not express of what form or shape this beast was,
although it be certain that he was a monster, because he was borne out of the
earth, that is of a most base and obscure beginning to the settinge forth of
the kingdom of Antichrist.

Which had two horns like a Lamb. etc. He has nothing like to a Lamb
besides his two horns, in the rest of his body deformed, uttering the nature
of a wild beast. But some do gather by these horns, that the pope is shadowed
by this beast, which chalingeth to him self the power of the kingdom, and of
the priesthood, which as it is probable, so I do not see how all things can
fitly agree to this exposition, which afterward are often repeated of both the
beasts. In my judgment therefore others do rightlyer interpret him to
signify the popish clergy, which endeavor with all there strength, to
maintain the dignity of there Pope, these will have somewhat like to Christ,
either when they boast them selves to be his servant or else when they
chalendge to them selves both the seculer and priestlye authority. I speak
of the chief Prelates, the Cardinales, the Archbishopes, and byshopes etc.
which usurp both a kingly and pontifical dignity.

But he spoke like the Dragon. etc. Howsoever by the number of his horns he
semethe to have some outward show, or likeness of Christ, yet he bewrays
himself by his voice that he is a preacher of the dragon and not of Christ.
For this beast, which afterward is called the false prophet, whose doctrine if
we shall examine according to the most certain rule of Gods word, it
shall be found to be Deuilishe, and quite contrary to Gods truethe. That I
may omit other profes, which are almost infinite, least I should be over
tedious, that one testimony of S. Paul in the first Epistle to Timothy and
fourth chapt. calling the forbidding of marriage and meats the doctrine of
devils, does sufficiently prove that this false prophet, which teaches ye
same things which the Pope prescribes, does speak the self same, which the
great Dragon inspireth into Antichrist.

Verse. 12. And he did all that the first beast could do before him. etc.

THe power of Antichrist is extended to his chief munsiers therefore he
exercises his power by them, this is yt which he says, that this beast with
the two horns did all that the first beast could do in his presence.

And he causes the earth and them that dwell therein to worship the first
beast whose deadly wound was healed. etc. The popish clergy labor with tothe
and nail, that all may every where acknowledge the authority of the Bishop
of Rome, and that all may require at his hands, Indulgences, dispensations,
Empires and kingdoms, and many yield to him homage, which thing whiles they
labor so sendiously to bring to pas, they call back again, the aunciente
tyranny of the Ethnikes, which being strike^ with a deadly wound, now at
length by there ayed has been perfectly healed.

Verse. 13. And does great wounders so that he makes fire come down from
heaven on the earth, in the sight of men. etc.

Saint Paul foretold that the coming of Antichrist should be in lying
signs. Because also Christ him self prophesied that there should come false
prophets, which with workinge monstrouse miracles should deceive many, in so
much that even the very elect if it were possible should also being seduced
be drawn into there destruction. And hear the false prophet, as it were an
apishe imitator of Elias, causethe fire to descend from heaven unto the earth,
in the sight of men, all which are either feigned to be done, or else by the
crafty conueyaunce and iugling castes of Satan, bewitching the eyes of men,
they are but boasted of, of which sort of Miracles the legens of the popish
saints are full. Yea those wonderful things, which they work by there
counsels and authority in the commune wealth, may worthelye be counted for
great signs and wonders, as when they translate kingdoms, from the lawful
heirs unto others, some Emperors they depose, others they place in there
roumes, and other such like, which are wonderful miracles to men. But we are
admonished so often in the scriptures of signs, miracles, and wonders, which
should be wrought by false prophets that we should not suffer our selves to be
led back from the truth of Gods word by any works, although they be never
so wonderful, against the truth of which word we ought not to give credit
to Angels coming down from heaven, to the Balath. Chapt. ^ Contrariwise it
has always been the manner of the false prophets, to call and provoke men
from the word of God to miracles, and here upon the papists instantlye
require of us to work miracles, as though the doctrine, which we profess,
were not sufficientlye confirmed with infinite miracles of Christ and his
Apostles.

Verse. 14. And deceives the^ that dwell on ye earth, by means of those
signs, which he has power to do in y^ sight of the beast. etc.

HE declares in this verse to what end he wrought great signs before men
verily that he might seduce the most of the^ into error. Such miracles
therefore with the workers of the same are to be accursed of the faithful by
which they are called away from the simplicity of Gods word to the devises
and inventions of men. But it is worthy to be noted, that he says power was
given him, that he might work signs in the sight of the former beast. For
god as S. Paul witnesses will give unto them the efficacy and strength of
error, yt they may credit lies, which would not believe the truth 2. These. ^.

Saying to them that dwell on the earth that they should make the image of the
beast, which had the wond of a sword and did line. And this is ye error into
which they seduced wretched men, that they should acknowledge the pope for God,
or rather for an Idolle, and that they should set up his Image for them selves
to worship as if it were some God, but some understand by the Image of the
beast, that in the papacy is restored, a certain Image of the Roman Empire
which was fallen to which opinion I would willingly subscribe, if the vision
did not express that both the beast, and his Image were extant at one time.
Add moreover that by the counsel and suggestion of this beast, an image of
the first beast ought to be made of the inhabitants of the earth. Lastly
that this two horned mo^ster, studieth by all means to aduau^ce the dignity
of the first beast, but the pope sets forth not the old Empire of the
Romans to be worshipped, but him self. I expound this Image therefore to be
the authority of the pope, which all are commanded to receive at the hands
of the popish clergy, being brought unto them by his legates a latere, and to
acknowledge it in the courts of Christianity as they call them, in which the
popes law is exercised, and the pope himself is chief judge which power
remaining in the court or in the Legate a Latere, may of good right be called
the Image of the pope. And that he repeateth so often that the deadly wou^d of
his head was healed, it is that we may know that it is notwithstanding the same
beast, although he somewhat differ in outward show, which made so many
slaughters of the martyrs whose cruelty although for a time being restrained
seemed as it were dead, at length revived to the exercising of the like or
rather greater tyranny.

Verse. 15. And he had power given him, to give a spirit unto the Image of the
beast, so that the Image of the beast should speak and should cause that as
many as would not worship the beast should be killed. etc.

HE always repeateth that it was given him, that we may understand that even
the very counsels and actions of ye wicked are ordered by the will of god, and
that the reprobate can do nothing at all, but that which god does permit.
Moreover least we should Imagen that this image here was dead, he adds that a
spirit was inspired into it of the beast being the priest thereof. So that the
Image should speak, that is the beast by his Legates, and other judges of the
papal court, which give sentence according to the popes law, so that now we
have an Image not dumb and dead, but which is living and speaks, we may
note, how the tyranny of the pope by little and little takes increase for in the
beginning, he only allureth and seduceth by miracles, then he persuades the
seduced to set up an Image of the beast in every city, into which being set
up he inspireth life and gives power to speak, and lastly he commands it
to be worshipped under pain of death. For we know that it was counted worthy
death, if any did contemn the power of the pope.

Verse. 16. And he made all both small and great, rich and pooer, fre and bound
to receive a marcke in there right hand or in there for cheades.

BEing not content to have set forth the pain of death to all that should
refuse to worship the Idol of the beast, that is to acknowledge the
authority of the pope, he also brings all of what state or condition soever
into bondage unto him compellinge every one, even as his boundslaues to
receive his marcke either in the right hand or in the forehead. By the right
hand by which the actions and deeds of this life are guided and wrought, he
signifies, that in all doings, whatsoever men of what state and condition so
ever princes or private persons do take in hand, always to the sea of Rome
her prerogative is to be reserved, that nothing may by any means be decreed
against that. And the marcke is imprinted in their forehead that always and
every where they may testify that they are slaves of that Apostolical or
rather Apostaticall sea.

Verse. 17. And that no man might buy or sell, save he that had the march or
the name of the beast, either the number of his name.

LEast any might escape by some subtlety he appoints this subjection that
none could buy, or sell that is exercise any action necessary, to the
sustentation of this life, but he which would confess him self to be
subject to this power. And to conclude, a man must be banished out of the
world, except he would take upon him this yoke of slavery and bondage. And he
puts three things, his mark, his name, and the number of his name which
perteyne all to one end, and they signify that by some outward sign or
ceremony, this servitude is to be professed to all men, that he may
acknowledge him self to be a member of the latin Church whosoever leads
his life within his Dominion.

Verse. 18. Here is wisdom: let him that has wit count the number of the
beast: for it is the number of a man, and his number is six hundredth,
threscore, and six. etc.

Because this mystery was very darcke, Saint Ihon forewarneth that here
lies wisdom hid, but yet because it is the number of man, that is, which
may be counted by the wisdom of man and is not infinite, he provoke wise
men which are endued with understanding to number the same: for the number is
six hundred, sixty and six. I will omit the most part of the expositions,
which are brought of this place, and I will bring forth that only, which
likes me best, which Ireneus affirms pleased many in his age, not long after
this revelation was received. Which is, that (...) is the name of the beast,
the number of which name, of ye computation of the numerall letters amounts
to six hundred sixty and six. Which if it seemed to be true in the time of
Ireneus, much more now unto us, seying the bishop of Rome in his common
prayers, in his laws, in his writings, in his faith is and will be counted a
latin. Moreover he ought to be a latin whosoever he be that will not be
called a Grecian, that is a Schismatike. So that rightlye in the verse going
before the number of his name is also to be taken for the marcke. Other do draw
ye same number out of ( Ecclesia Italica) the Church of Italy, which I do not
reiecte, when as whether thou sekest the Church, or the head of the same, thou
may find either of them in the mystery of this number.

The fourtenth Chapter.
YT is taught in this Chapter by what means the Church shall stand against the
tyranny of Antichrist, afterward the fall and ruin of ungodliness which
should be by the preachinge of the gospel, is sore told. The faithful are
admonished to take heed and keep them selves from the corruptions and defilings
of Antichrist, because the last judgment of God shall shortly after follow.

Verse. 1. And I looked and behold a lamb. etc.

WHen as he had foretold in the former Chapter that all tribes, tongues,
people, and nations should acknowledge the aucthority of ye most foul beast,
when as he had pronounced that the saints should be overcome of ye most
cruel monster, and also when he had fore showed yt all as many as would
exercise buying, and selling, and the traffic of this life, should profess
most filthy slavery and bondage, we might very well have doubted, whether the
whole Church of Christ, were utterly subdued or not, after yt the cruel beast
had apprehended and obtained dominion, except in this vision, as well the
preservation of the Church, as the destruction of that tyranny, had
consequently been declared. Like as therefore in the 12. chap. He saw Michaell
fighting with the dragon, so likewise now he sees a lamb placed against the
monstrouse beast. But it seems to be without reason, that he opposes and
sets a most meke lamb against a most cruel and wild beast. But we must
remember, that Christ is showed not such as he is to his enemies, but such as
he utters himself to his own. For to his enemies he is that Lion of the
tribe of Judah, but to the godly he is the lamb slaien from the beginning of
the world as louinge to his own, as he is terrible to his enemies.

stood upon Mount Sion. etc.

MOunt Sion is an ancient figure of the Church which should never perish,
of which there remain so excellent, and magnificall promises, that the Lord
will never forsake it. For out of that place, the doctrine of the Gospel
flows over the whole world, according to the prophecies of the old
Prophets, and according to the commandments of Christ him self which he
gave to his Apostles. Act. 1. Ye shall be witnesses unto me in Jerusalem, and in
all Judea, and Samaria, and unto the ends of the earth. That therefore, which
mount Syon was to the Jews, the same is the whole world, to us, if we have
respect to place, wheresoever the godly professors of the Gospel are found.
Which the prophet Isay witnesses Chapter 2. Saying: and the mountain of the
house of the Lord, shall be exalted above the top of all mountains and all
people shall be gathered unto it. Foundly therefore do they, which boast of some
particular city or place, to which ye Church of God may be bound and tied, as
the papists do of Rome, unless they would vaunte as they are very
impudente, that mount Sion is translated to that city, which is builded upon
seven hills. But it is manifest by the scriptures that the seat of God is
spread out of Sion over the whole earth. Therefore Christ is said to stand upon
the mount Syon, when he performs that which he promised other where: behold I
am with ye, even to the end of the world: and if we ask where he answers in
the 17. Chapter of saint Luke: Wheresoever the dead carkas shall be, thither
will the Eagles be gathered. This place does teach even by this one reason,
that the Church shall be perpetual, because it is the seats of the lamb,
whom the mount Sion shall never fail, in which he may stand with his chaste
worshippers.

And with him a hundredth and four and forty thousand. etc. The whole
fellowship of Gods faithful elect, gathered out of every one of the 12. tribes
of Israel, as we read in the seventh Chapter, is joined to Christ there head.
For wickedness never bears such sway in the world, but that God has his
sufficient number although much fewer then the reprobate, which he
preserves pure from Idolatry, filthiness, and defilinges, likewise as in the
time of Elias he kept to him self seven thousands which were clean and
unspotted from the filthiness of Baall.

Having his fathers name written in there foreheades. etc. That is, whose
election is not only sealed inwardly in there hearts by the holy ghost but
also, with outward and open profession testified before men. For they witness
by the whole conversation of there life whose servants they are, so that it
is ready and easy for every one, to read the name of god imprinted in there
foreheades.

Verse. 2. And I herd a voice from heaven. etc.

IT is not an idle nor dumb multitude which accompany Christ, but which is
always bent with most earnest study and endeavor in celebrating and
magnifying ye glory of god. S. Ihon therefore hears a loud voice from
heaven: but it may be meruailed wherefore it is said from heaven, seeing that
he had seen the lamb a little before standing on mount Sion. He signifies
therefore not an earthely hill, but that heavenly hill which is aunswereable,
to the heavenly Jerusalem, for the conversation of the Church being a
stranger in earth is in heaven.

As the sound of many waters and as the sound of a great thunder, and I herd
the voice of harpes harping with there harpes. etc. By a three fold similitude
he sets forth ye magnificence of the voice, which he herd. First that it
was like to that bellowing noise, which many waters tossed with contrary
winds, and russhing against rocks, and the sea banckes, do make. This is a
great confuse and troublesome sound, such at the first hearing, the voice of
them that sing forth the praises of God in the Church seems to be. Secondly
that voice was like to the crackes of the terrible thunder. For it strikes the
minds of sinners and specially of those, which are privy of there own
unthankfulness, when they hear the glory of god sounded forth, of his
faithful worshippers. Lastly when as the minds of men are subdued and brought
under to the obedience of god, and filled with the pleasant sweetenes of his
amiable grace, they hear with great delight a most pleasant harmony, as it
were of harpers singinge with there harpes. This is the true music, whose use
is in the Church rather then that chaunting, which creketh only in the voice,
and delights the outward ears, when as nevertheless the mind is void of
all sense or feling of godliness.

Verse. 3. And they song as it were a new song. etc.

SO great is the joyful willingness of the godly in setting forth Gods
glory, that when as nothing is more aunciente in the Church then the
celebration of divine praises, yet they seem always to them selves to sing a
new song. For the remembrance of Gods benefits toward them never waxes
old, neither does the praise of God ever fail in the Church, which always
indeuoureth with vnweried study to magnify his glory.

Before the throne, and before the four beasts, and the elders. etc. That is,
this exercise of singinge, does always florishe in the Church, before God,
the Angels, and the whole world, which is both approved to God and testified
to all his creatures.

And no man could learn that song, but the hundredth forty and four thousand,
which were bought from the earth. etc. None of the reprobate, nor yet of the
hypocrites, which feign even the most holiness, could learn this song, but
the elect only, to whom the holy ghost is wont to speak and teach the same
when as redemption is sealed in there hearts, yt they may with joyful and
sincere affection of heart, sing a psalm of thanks and praise unto him, whom
they acknowledge to be Abba and father. Where are therefore the songs and
prayers not understood, which please God eue^ for the work wrought as the
papists do mainteyn? For such songs every hypocrite can learn and sing, but
such are not allowed of God.

Verse. 4. These are they which are not defiled with women, for they are
virgins. etc.

THe conversation of life is agreeable to there profession. For they should not
be meet to celebrate ye praises of god, unless they could bring the^ forth of a
pure and undefiled heart. But under one kind, he co^prehendeth all other
defilings of a wicked life. They are free from whoredom, and other greater and
more veynouse vices. Although according to the manner of the scripture by
whoredom we may understand Idolatry, and other vices also which make a
diuorcemente between, Christ the only spouse of the Church, and men. For
this is most preciouse virginity before God, when the godly keep them selves
clean from adulterouse supersticions, and other defilinges of the world, like
as god commends his seven thousand, which were not defiled with any
filthiness of Baal. And Paul married the Corinthians, as a chaste virgin to
Christ which would not suffer her self to be drawn or led back from
Christ by wicked and counterfeyte devises of men, as it were with harlot like
enticementes. But in that the papists by this place would confirm the single
life of the popish clergy, it is without all reason. For ye holy ghost does
not speak of every conjunction with women, but of that only wherewith men
are polluted, but the Apostle witnesses in the. 13. chap. to the Hebrews that
ye marriage bed is undefiled. Neither does it make any thing for their purpose
yt they are called virgins. For this does perteyne to the whole company of the
elect, and not to the ministers of the word only, much less to the popish
priests, of which as there were many yt lived a single life, so there were
very few of the^ virgins, yea scarcely there is one among a 1000. of the^, but
yt he was defiled either with fornication, or preposterous lust, or at the least
wicked burning, so yt if when we give the^ single life, we may altogether deny
them virginity.

These follow the lamb whethersoeuer he goes. etc. The true members of the
Church are never separated from Christ there head, and the true worshippers of
God do not depart the breadthe of a nail from the side of Christ, he is the
sheperd, they are the sheep, therefore they follow the lamb wheresoever he
shall lead them, if we he careful therefore to find out the Church, let
us diligently seek Christ, not at Rome or Jerusalem, but in the Church
spread over the whole earth.

These are bought from men being the first fruits unto god and to the lamb.
etc. If thou demand wherefore these have so familier access to Christ, the
reason is reuered, because they are not of that lost lump of mankind, but
being redenied from men, and from the most miserable and filthy bondage of the
devil, they are restored into the liberty of the sons of God. And then he
shows the end of there redemption, when he says yt they are the first
fruits to God, and to the lamb, we know yt the first fruits were consecrated
to God, that it was not lawful for profane men to touch them, the faithful
therefore are redeemed from the earth and from men, that they may serve God in
holiness and innocence, to the praise of his glory. We are admonished by this
place how holily, and religiously innocence is to be embraced of all the godly,
when as they be certain, first fruits to God and Christ, not consecrate to
our own use, neither to the use of the world, or servitude of satan, but to
the glory of God. Moreover what horrible sacrilege it is to take from God and
Christ there first fruits, and to sacrifice them to the devil the flesh and
the world.

Verse. 5. And in there mouths was found no guile, for they are with out spot
before the throne of God. etc.

HE proceeds in declaringe the purity of those which are joined as companions
to the lamb. For nothing that is vnpure or corrupt can cleue to him. But it
may seem contrary to al reason, that he seems to make them free from all spot
of sin and iniquity, which is ye privilege of Christ alone, neither does it
agree to any other of the Sons of Adam. The comune sort refer it to the
infants that were cruelly slaien by Herod, which they call innocents. But that
is but a fond dream, saying this number comprehends all the elect, which
are not blameless before God in their own righteousness, but in as much as
that as lively members they stick to Christ there head.

Verse. 6. Then I saw an other Angel fly in the midst of heaven having an
everlasting Gospel to preach unto them that dwell on the earth, and to every
nation, and kindred, toungue and people. etc.

Hitherto he has expounded the figure of the church preserved out of the
midst of the waves and stars of Antichristian persecution. Now he tourneth
him to set forth the ruin and destruction of Antichrist. He sees an Angel
therefore: flyinge through the midst of heaven openly and publicly bringing
an everlasting gospel, which is to be preached to the world. By which figure
is signified that the light of the truth of the gospel, which seemed long time
obscured through the persecutions and darckenes of Antichrist, by the singular
benefit of god, should be restored again to ye world, which except we see to
be fulfilled in this our age, we are very stones, and not men. For now, the
Angel which is the minister of god flies, not in secreat places and darcke
corners, but through the midst of heaven, and he spreads that everlasting
gospel (which nevertheless the enemies cry out to be new, and latelye
sprung up) over the whole world, in spite of Satan, Antichrist and his
adherentes, that it may now be truly said, which S. Paul taught to be
agreeable to his time, there sound is gone forth into all the earth, and there
words into the ends of the world.

Verse. 7. Saying with a loud voice, fear God and give glory to him. etc.

THe Angel sounds forth with a clear and loud voice. That not Antichrist
or his tyranny, but that god above is to be feared. And that honor is to be
given not to Idols see up by the subtlety of the devil, but to god only.
For many under the tyranny of Antichrist depart away from the true worship
of God, unto deuilishe superstitions, these the voice of the gospel does
admonish to yield and offer to god alone due fear and obedience.

For the hour of his Judgment is come: and worship him that made heaven
and earth, the sea and all the founteynes of waters. etc. Because the
darckenesse is driven away, and the light restored and all ungodliness is
condemned, and the time will shortelye come, in which God will as^ite all
mankind before the tribunal seat of Christ, that every one may receive
according to that they have done in there bodies. Therefore it is now no time,
or place to dissemble, but the very aproching nere of Gods judgment does
admonish us that all glory and honor is due to him alone, which created all
things by his will and has appointed, and ordained his creatures for our use,
not only the sea and the earth, in which his wonderful power is showed, but
also the founteynes of sweet waters in which his singular goodness does shine.
We are taught here, which is the voice of the true and everlasting Gospel,
that we may distinguishe the same from feyned, and counterfayt gospels, verily
even that which teaches that god alone is to be feared, to him all glory is
to be given, him I say is to be worshipped which is the only creator of
all things.

Verse. 8. And there followed an other Angel saying it is fallen it is fallen:
Babylon that great City. etc.

WHen the Gospel is preached through the whole world, and the Church of
Christ established in the faith of the same, then follows the fall and
overthrow of the kingdom of Babylon. For the Babilonicall empire can not
stand, when Christ once standethe up the defendour of his Church, which will
bring his Israelites out of most miserable bondage into fredome, and will call
them out of banishemente into there country the heavenly Jerusalem. By the
fall therefore of Babylon, we understand by the consent almost of all as well
the old as new writers, the ruin and decay of the Romayne tyranny. For
that which Babylon in the East was to the Jews, the same is Rome, which is,
Babylon, the West to the Christians. And as God compassed about and measured
the cruelty of that old Babylon within certain limits, so also the Lord
has before appointed the end of the Roman tyranny, although the papists
boast that it shall be eternal. And the holy ghost in these words alludeth to
those things which are found in Isay, and Jeremy concerning the destruction
of Babylon. The dubling of these words, it is fallen, it is fallen, shows ye
certeyntie of her fall, for although she boast never so much yt she is builded
upon a rock, yet without all doubt she shall fall, and although it be counted a
great and famous city, yet nevertheless it shall be brought into a deserte
wilderness.

For she gave to all Nations to drink the wine of the wrath of her
Fornication. etc. The cause is added, because her wicked abominations are come
to the full, because with her wicked and blasphemouse doctrine she has
seduced all nations to idolatrye, and he calls it the wine of wrath, either
because it provoke the wrath of God, or else because it drives into fury and
madness the wicked being made drunken there with, so that they dote in folly
upon idols that is most filthy strumpets, even as though they were stricken
with madness. For god by his just judgment has sent upon them the efficacy
and strength of errore. And we know how gredely the world has anassed up and
stuffed it self with the doctrine of Antichrist, which is nothing else but
ye furiouse wine of spiritual fornication, which is the worshippinge of idols.

Verse. 9. And the third Angel followed them saying with a loud voice. etc.

AT length when wickedness is made manifest, and Antichrist reveled, the
faithful are to be feared from his wicked opinions, that they may not suffer
them selves to be drawn into bondage of him whose horrible fall and ruin, the
holy ghost foretold should shortly after follow. Therefore the Angel cries
with a loud voice, because many men geuinge them selves to the delights and
pleasures of Babylon, are so deaf to hear the voice of the Gospel that they
are scarsely raised up in the end with loud cryinge to repent and turn
from the filthynes of Antichrist. The Angel therefore which betokens the
faithful preachers of ye Gospel, denounces horrible and eternal
punnishments to all those which by any manner of means would profess
servitude and bondage to Antichrist.
