If any man worship the beast or his Image, and receive his mark on his fore
head or on his hand. etc. Least any by hypocrisy might fly and eschew the
judgment of God, as though he worshipped not Antichrist from the heart, but
from the teeth forward and in outward ceremony he numbereth all the kinds
of that deuilish worship which is bestowed upon the beast: Therefore whether any
man do acknowledge antichrist himself or his authority, or else profess him
self by some outward badge or sign to be subject unto him, he affirmethe
that the same person shall be cursed and condemned to the eternal torments of
hell.

Verse. 10. The same shall drink of the wine of the wrath of God, yea the pure
wine which is powered into the cup of his wrath. etc.

IT is to be noted with what vehement figures he expresses the horrible
vengeance of God. For first he callethe it the wine of Gods wrath, which if
it, seem to little, he adds, that it is pure, because it is not mitigated with
any clemency or gentleness, lastly he saiethe that it is powered into the
cup of Gods wrath, so that by all means, he heapeth up and increases the
quality and quantity of Gods vengeance, against Idolaters and the boundslaues
of Antichrist.

And he shall be punished in fire and brymestone before the holy Angels and
before the lamb. etc. The effect of Gods wrath is expressed, that it
tormenteth them most grieuouselye whom it shall burn for ever with fire and
brimestone before the holy Angels and before the lamb, that they may be
punished in the presence or beholding of them whose fellowship, and whole some
admonitions they despised whiles they lived. Which part of torments is not
the lightest, that they are set as a gasing stock for whom they mocked and
derided whiles they flowed in there wanton pleasures and delights.

Verse. 11. And the smoke of their torments shall ascend up evermore. etc.

HE goes foreward in amplifying the unhappy estate of the reprobate for least
they should flatter them selves that their torments should come to an end by
any length of time, he shows that the smoke which rises up of there burning
souls, and bodies, shall ascend for ever, whereby all hope of deliverance is
taken quite away.

And they shall have no rest day and night which worship the beast and his
Image, and whosoever receives the printe of his name. etc. The calamities of
many, some little consolation being intermedled, do grant as it were a
breathing time, but the miseries of these shall neither by day, nor by night
feel any release or ease at all. So heavy is the wrath of god against those,
which either make them selves subject to Antichrist, or else profess his
servitude by some external and outward sign. It is marvel that the false
Nichodemites, and other which remain among the papists, are not altogether
stricken with horror and fear, if at the least they weygh and consider, but
even with indifferent minds ye grieuousenes of this judgment.

Verse. 12. Here is the patience of the saints here are they which ke^e the
commandments of God and the faith of Jesus. etc.

THis seems over hard to the flesh that they which for a time through
fear of cruelty yielded them selves to Antitichrist, are to be committed to
everlasting torments. But the Angel answers, that here is a place for the
patience of the saints, which ought to be proved by afflictions as goulde
is tried in the fire. That here the true worshippers of God are distinguished
from hypocrites, for then is the obedience of the godly seen and perceived,
when as they can not neither by threateninges or promises be moved or drawn
away from the obedience of God. Moreover that here is place for faith, when
as the faithful being bent and fixed upon one God, do not only fly and eschew
all the delights and pleasures of ye world as it were enticing meremaydes, but
also will suffer stronglye, the most exquisite and grieuouse torments which
tyrants lay upon them, rather then that they will slide from the true and
sincere worship of God, to the profane superstitions of Idolatry.

Verse. 13. And I herd a voice from heaven saying unto me, write blessed are
the dead, which dye in the Lord, even so says the spirit, that they rest
from there labors, and there works follow them. etc.

Like as the Angel threatened horrible punishment to Antichrist and to those
that worship him, so. It behooves the minds of the faithefull to be lifted
up by some consolation, that they may with the more indifferent minds be able
to sustain and endure the persecutions moved against them by Antichrist. S.
Ihon therefore herd the voice of the holy ghost from heaven sounding alowde,
and promising eternal blessedness to all as many as shall suffer death for
the Lords cause. And the circumstaunces of this place are worth consideration,
This voice is herd from heaven, that the testimony might be more notable and
manifest and that we ought to give more diligent heed to the same, because it
brings a rare and vnwo^ted matter of comfort and consolation. Moreover he is
commanded to write as it were some certain oracle far excelling the rest,
for he was commanded in the beginning to write whatsoever he should hear or
see, which commandment being here repeated, declares that this is an
excellent voice, which never ought to slip out of our minds. And he is not
content to promise happiness to the souls departed, except also he confirm
the same with an oath, and vehemente affirmation, and he shows who it is
which promises this happiness unto them verily even the spirit of truth
which deceyueth no man, and lastly he adds the reasons or causes wherefore he
pronounces them to be blessed. First because they are drawn out and delivered
from the labors and miseries, to which this life is subject. And secondlye
that they receive the most ample reward, which is ordained and appointed by
the free mercy of God, for there good works. There is no cause therefore that
we should sorrow for there death, which as it brings an end of present
evils, so likewise it is the beginning of eternal felicity. And though he
chiefly speaks here of martires, which are slain for the testimony of
Christ, yet it is not to be doubted, but that those things are to be referred
to the end of all the godly, which the holy ghost here preaceth of ye happiness
after their death. Therefore away with ye popes sire of purgatory, in which
the souls do not rest from the^e labors, but are tormented with the pains
of hell, if we may believe the papists: as those, whom not there own works
do accompany, but the merits of others do a long time after them. Which is
plainly a doctrine of devils, which was devised to set up and maintain a
very bucherlie torment of conscience, and is not a doctrine of the holy ghost
set forth to the comfort and consolation of the saints.

Verse. 14. And I looked and behold a white cloud, and upon the cloud one
sitting like unto the son of man, having on his head a golden crown, and in
his hand a sharp sickle. etc.

AFter that he had described the state of the Church, of what sort it should
be, even unto the end of the world, now he foresheweth that the utter
destruction of the wicked shall come at length, by the last judgment of God.
And that is showed by two figures, the one of harvest the other of gathering
grapes. Either of them is repeated in ye same sense among the prophets, but
chiefly of Isay, in the 17.63. Saint Ihon therefore sees a white cloud and
a certain Angel sittinge upon the cloud in the shape and likeness of a man.
The cloud is a foreteller of the judgment because the Lord will come in ye
clouds of heaven. This Angel clothed with the shape of man represents
Christ, or at the least wise is a minister of his judgment. He has a golden
crown upon his head that we may understand that kingly authority is
committed to him of god. The sharp sickle which he carries in his hand,
expresses the severity and sharpenes of his judgment, which none of the
wicked can eschew, which all the attemptes of the reprobate ca^ no more resist,
then the ripe corn can the sickle of the reaper.

Verse. 15. And an other Angel came out of the temple crying with a loud
voice to him that sat on the cloud, thrust in thy sickle and reap* for the
time is come to reap, for the corn of the earth is ripe. etc.

THe former figure of the Angel sittinge upon the white cloud showed that
the judgment of Christ is prepared, but this figure of the other Angel
coming out of the temple teachethe that the time is at hand, in which God
will take vengeance upon the reprobate. He goes ^orthe of the temple, that
is, from the presence of God himself, opening his secreate counsel: for as
kings do dwell in palaces, so God is said metaphorically, to dwell in a
temple, he admonishes the Angel therefore which bare the sickle, which
waited daily for the will and pleasure of God, that now at length that day is
come, in which all wickedness being overthrown, the glory of God may
perfectly shine, and they may be punnished, which hitherto have disdained to
magnify and set forth the same glory. If any think it an absurdetye, that
Christ is admonished by the angel, he must know that these hid mysteries are
showed and revealed by fygures, so far as our understanding could
comprehend them, when as Christ also him self, in as much as he was man,
confesses that the day of judgment was hid from him. Here also not Christ
himself, but an Angel representinge the judgment of Christ is brought in.

Verse. 16. And he that sat on the cloud thrust in his sicle on the earth, and
the earth was reaped. etc.

THere is no delay, so soon as he understands that the ripe and full time
to exercise the severity of god is come, his sharp sickle being thrust into
the earth, he reapeth all the harueste of the earth, sooner then one word can
be spoken.

Verse. 17. Then another angel came out of the temple which is in heaven
having a sharp sicle. etc.

IT may be demanded what need there should be to use two figures, seeinge
that former of the corn reaped might suffice. We may answer to this that in
the former figure is e^pressed that general change of all as well of the
godly, as of the reprobate, which shall be in the last day, and that in the
latter figure the destruction only of the reprobate is described: for Christ
him self compares the end of the world to an harvest, the angels to
reapers, but because in the harvest there are not only tares, but also wheat,
which when it is purged from the tares, is to be laid up in the barn, and in
this place, the purpose of the holy ghost is chiefly to comprehend the ruin
of ungodliness, therefore omitting the harvest, by the figure of gatheringe the
grapes he propounds and sets forth for us to behold the horrible
destruction or end of ye wicked. Therefore there goes forth of the heavenly
temple, an other angel then ye former, which sitting upon the cloud did
exercise the general judgment of all men, and he also bearing a sharp
sickle, in which he is ready to streache forth the vengeance of god against
the reprobate when it seems good to yt lord him self. And he goes out of ye
temple which is in heaven, as he which has received from ye mouth of god him
self the commandment which he was prepared to execute.

Verse. 18. And an other Angel came out from the altar, which had power over
fire and cried with a loud voice to him that had the sharp sickle and ^aied
thrust in thy sharp sickle and gather ye clusters of the vineyarde of ye
earth, for her grapes are ripe.

WHiles that former Angel armed with the vengeance of god going forth of the
temple, only waited for the will and pleasure of the lord, what time he ought
to execute ye office committed unto him, behold there goes forth an other
Angel from the heavenly altar, bringinge the commandment of God, that the
time to gather grapes was come for now the clusters of the vine of the
ungodliness are ripe, which the lord has commanded straitway to be cut
down. Hither to these things are clear and manifest enough. But wherefore is
he said to go forth from the altar? verily in my Judgment he alludeth to the
form of the old temple in whose innermost rowme was the golden altar above,
which was the arcke of the covenant, above the arcke were the Cherubines
between which the Lord dwelled sacramently and under a figure. He signifies
therefore, yt from the secreat counsel of god, which at length shall be made
manifest, this commau^deme^t came forth concerning the taking away of the
reprobate, they shall take away said Christ out of the kingdom of God all
things yt offend, and them that work iniquity Mat. 13. But it is much more
darcke yt he says, that this Angel has power over fire. Some do therefore
interpret him to be Christ, which came to send fire into the earth. Others do
expound it a fiery affection wherewith ye Angels burn, to destroy the
ungodly. But seeing s. Paul, to ye. Ephesians. 1. chap. And likewise Collos. 1.
calls certain angels powers, I do simply understand yt here is meant ye angel
which by the dispensatio^ of god has rule over ye element of fire. Like as
also we here afterward in the 16. chap. The Angel of ye waters. For god has
disposed to Angels the preservation of the creatures of the world, which we
find often times witnessed in the scriptures here therefore the Angel which
has power over fire is sent, that it might be signified with what kind of
destruction the Lord has decreed to change the form of the world, whereof
no man is ignorant. But we may learn by this place, that the due and as it
were ripe time to take vengeance upon the reprobate, is not to be discerued,
at our will but by the most secreat judgment of God: because it becomes not
us to prefixe the time but patiently to wayt for the same.

Verse. 19. And the Angel thrust in his sharp sickle on the earth, and cut
down the grapes of the vineyarde of the earth, and cast them into the great
wine fat of the wrath of god.

NOw there follows the execution of Gods decree upon the reprobate, in which
this is to be observed, that first the branches or clusters are cut down,
that is, the ungodly are spoiled and bereft of all there ornaments and
strength, in which they were proud, and after being naked, as it were rotten
grapes they are cast in to the great wine fat of Gods wrath to be trodden down.

Verse. 20. And the wine fat was trodden without the city, and blood came out of
the wine fat, even unto the horse bridles, by the space of a thousand and six
hundredth furlonges. etc.

HOw sharp so ever the wrath of God be upon the wicked reprobate, the
punishments shall not come nighe the elect for without the holy city, and
heavenly Jerusalem, is the wine fat trodden, in which the wicked are tormented,
whose blood issues and flows out of the fat, even unto the horse bridles.
and that by a very great space of ground, Shewinge what a horrible and
wonderful slaughter the lord will make of yt wicked, when the due time of
punishment shall come. Concerning the number of the forlonges, they make two
hundred miles, which was almost the greatest length of the land of Canaan,
which represented the whole world, beside Jerusalem that is the Church.

The fyftenth Chapter.
WHen as he had foretold in the Chap. going ^t the that extreme punnishments
should be taken upon the wicked in the last judgment of God, we might have
doubted whether they should quietly triumph or not until that time and
should not in the mean time be chastised with any scorges of God. The holy
ghost therefore teaches in this chapter, and also in the chapter followinge,
that like as the last destruction remains for them in the last judgment of
god so also in the mean time the Lord would be revenged upon there
wickedness, with diverse and most greuouse punishements.

Verse. 1. And I saw an other sign in heaven great and meruailouse, seven
Angels having the seven last plagues, for in them is fulfilled the wrath of
God. etc.

Saying that nothing is more usual to the world then to ascribe the plagu^s
sent of God, to fortune or to some other second causes: S. John shows that a
certain great and wonderful sign was showed to him, with which it behooves
the minds of men to be earnestly stricken with the fear of Gods judgments:
that is seven Angels bringinge the wrath and vengeance of God from heaven
unto the earth. Therefore the diverse kinds of punnishmentes are sent down
from heaven upon the reprobate, and chiefly upon the body of Antichrist, not by
any blind adventure of fortune, but by the sure and determinate counsel of
God, and he says seven plagues, because ye ungodly, shall be stricken of God
for there sundry and very many heynouse offenses, not with one kind of
calamities, but with diverse, not with few, but with very many plagues, even as
the number seven signifies universality and fulness. Moreover he calls them
the last plagues, because in them the wrath of God is finished, that is does
power out it self wholly to the destruction of those which being
admonished, by no chastisementes would be brought to a better mind. But rather
look how much more they were chastised of God with punnishments, so much the
more they were hardened against all calamities.

Verse. 2. And I saw as it were a glasie sea mingled with fire and them that had
gotten the victory of the beast, and of his Image and of the number of (...)
name, stand at the glassie sea etc.

GOd does never prepare punishments against the reprobate, but yt first he
provides for his own, least they should be drawn into destruction together
with the wicked. Which thing is clearly described by this figure, for before
the seven Angels power out the viales full of gods wrath upon the earth, to
terrify the wicked, and the inhabitants of the great city, S. Ihon sees the
holy worshippers of God had kept them selves free from the most filthy
bondage of Antichrist, first placed in safety, least any little part of the
seven plagues might touch them. He sees therefore a glassie sea mingled with
fire, that is the greatness of perils and troubles to which the godly are
subject in this world, which is so great that it may be compared to a sea,
for the unmeasurable hugeness, and it is bitter with so hard and sharp
persecutions that it seems all to burn with fire, and yet it is as hard as
glass, so that the faithful may be tossed to and fro, but they can not be
drowned in it, for Ihon beholds those, which by the benefit of God have
overcome, even in the most difficulte and hard battle incountred with yt
beast, that is with Antichrist and all his impiety, standing joyfully at that
glassie sea, as it were dedeliuered from shipwrake or free from drowning
singing a song of victory to God there deliverer, with all sincere affection
of heart. We may here note, that we must strive and fight with Antichrist, if
we desire to be garnished with the rewards of conquerers. Moreover in that the
beast, his Image, his mark and the number of his name are so often repeated,
we ought to have no fellowship or agreement with Antichrist, or with any little
portion of his deuilishe superstition. But we must fight not only against the
beast him self, which is the Pope, but also against his Image, that is his
laws and decrees, by which his wicked authority and pride has been founded
and established, and against his marcke, yt is the ceremonies which he has
invented and found out, to lead souls captive into his filthy slavery and
boundage. And lastly we must fight against the number of his name that we may
hate with like hatred as himself, whatsoever may be called by his name.

Having the harpes of god. etc. The holy ghost does signify by this metaphor,
that matter of joy and gladness is daily ministered of god to the godly, which
never leaves of to heap his benefits upon them, that although they seem to be
ye most wretched and miserable of all others in the eyes of the world, yet they
feel and perceive them selves to be happy, so that being joyful and glad
they sing hymns, and Psalms to god, with the harp. We are taught here that
we are unmeet, or unapt to celebrate the glory of god, except we receive
our harpes, of him by the most sweet harmony of which being helped we may
record the heavenly and divine songs.

Verse. 3. And they song the song of Moses the servant of God.

Because they acknowledge it to be no less benefit, that they are delivered
from the daungerouse waves of the fiery sea, that is the world, then that in
time past god led the Israelites safe through the red sea: they sing to god
there deliverer that noble song, which Moses the principale servant of god
taught the people of Israel, as we read in the fiftenth Chap. of Exodus: let
us sing to the Lord for he has triumphed gloriously, and so as follows. Let
us learn here, not to esteem ye power and mercy of god in protectinge and
defendinge his saints from the wicked defilinges and other infinite dangers
of this world, to be less, then in those ancient and wonderful works by
which he delivered the old patriarchs from the evils which hanged over there
heads. Whose examples are therefore set forth, that we may hope that god
will be such to us in our afflictions, as we believe, he was to the old fathers,
and that we may offer up our selves and become such in piety and
thankfulness as we read those holy men showed them selves for the benefits
which they received.

And the song of the lamb. etc. Seeing the faithful have Christ both the
only aucthor and mediator of there redemption, they do not only sing the
song of Moses, but also together therewith they singe a most sweet and
pleasant song taught by the lamb him self. For that which Moses was to the
Israelites, that same and much more gloriouse is Christ to his Church.

Great and meruailouse are thy works, Lord God almighty. etc. This is that
magnificall song taught to the Church by the Lamb, that is drawn out of the
Doctrine of Christ our savior, which song does ascribe all praise,
honor, and glory, to one God almighty. Of whom therefore shall we believe
that the most part of the papisticall or popish hymns and songs were taught,
which are framed to celebrate the glory not of God the creator, but of the
creatures, of which ^orte are these, hayle queen of heaven, hayle, star of
the sea, hayle triumphing cross, hayle mother Anna, and many other of the
same stuff, which are also fraught full of most horrible blasphemies: The
lamb never taught these songs, but that monstrouse beast, which has nothing
like to the lamb, but his two horns. Here also we have a most clear and
lively image of the true worship of God in the Church, verelye where all
things do sound to the praises of God only: on the contrary part, that it
is the sinagoge of Satan, Wheresoever the glory is magnified of any other,
besides the glory of the true and one only god. Moreover in that the
faithful do acknowledge the works of God to be great and meruailouse, they
teach us how his benefits are to be esteemed. For the devil studieth by all
means to deminishe the dignity of them, therefore he persuades us by his
suggestions, that they are small and common works, which god exercises
daily, either in protecting ye godly, or restraining the wicked when as in ye
mean while, but that we are altogether blind even in the midst of y^ clear
light, and deprived of all right judgment, they are great and wonderful.
They are great because no man, or any other creature can do the like. They are
meruailouse because besides all hope and opinion of men they take there
effect, yea though Satan and all his guard of soldiers resist and wrestle
against the same. (Lord god almighty) god alone because he can do all things,
has wroughte and brought to pass very great and wonderful works, as often
therefore as the end and finishing of our matters seems hard, let us turn
our eyes to the sovereign rule and power of God, for all things obey his
will. And let us lean and permit that to his counsel, which seems hard, or
impossible unto us.

Just and true are thy ways, king of Saints. etc. The works of God are not
only great and wonderful, but also just and true are all things whatsoever he
does. For if he chastise the offenses of any with plagues he does it by Justice
and right being the Judge of the whole world neither does he at any time
punish the innocent for those which are guilty. If verily he show him self
favorable and gentle to his servants, he does it for his infinite mercies
sake, which he has promised he will power forth upon those, which worship him
with sincere and ernest affection and love of godliness. Neither will he keep
back any part of those things, which he has promised to his Church until
at length he shall adorn the same with eternal felicity. That they call God
king of the Saints, they show that they acknowledge the government of him
alone, to whose kingdom so long as they he subject they need not to be
afraid of any tyra^nie of Satan, or wicked me^. Lastly we are taught who are
worthy the honorable name of Saints, verily even they which acknowledge God
to be there king, and as it becomes subjects, do obey his wholesome laws and
most holy decrees.

Verse. 4. Who shall not fear thee o Lord, and glorify thy name. etc.

THey Judge it a matter of all other most absurd and without reason that the
wicked being void of all fear of God, do contemn and despise the glory of
his name. For when as his works are so great and wonderful, and of such power
that no strength can resist him, seeing his Judgments are Just, so that none
of the wicked can eschew ye punishments due for his sins, who shall not fear
him, except he be as a block endued with no sense at all? and seeing he is of
so great benignity and gentleness toward those that fear him, so that he
adorneth them daily with all kind of benefits, who will not study and endeavor
to celebrate the Glory of his name except he be uoide of all shadow of virtue
and humanity.

For thou only art holy. Here of they conclude that all fear and honor is
due to God alone, because he only is Holy. All other things are wicked and
Profane except those to which he does communicate his holiness. Do we not
here acknowledge one of the blasphemouse names of Antichrist that he suffers
himself to be called most holy, when as God only is holy. Neither is that
enough, except also he should challenge to himself this dignitye, that the
holiness of the whole Church should depend upon him, and that he can pour
a new holiness into those creatures which it pleases him, and to be short,
that he claims the Canonizinge of dead Saints as they term it to pertain
only to him. Whereto do these things tend? but that he might rob God of
this prerogative of holiness, and with great Sacrilege transfer it to himself.

And all nations shall come and worshipe before thee. etc. He signifies that
the wicked do strive and resist in vain, because will they, ^ill they, at
length they shall acknowledge his rule and government.

For thy judgments are made manifest. etc. Whiles the judgments of god are
secreat, it seems somewhat to be borne withal, if they fear not his
judgments, whose severity they are ignorant of, but when as the Judgments of
God are made open, and most clear and manifest examples are daily set before
there eyes, it argues more then a stony hardness of the reprobate, that they
are mollified with no scourges of God, and taught by no experimentes, that they
may learn to fear God, and that they may yield due glory to his most holy
name.

Verse. 5. And after that I looked, and behold the temple of the tabernacle of
witness was open in heaven. etc.

AFter that he had set the Church of Christ free from those plagues, which
were prepared to punish the wicked he retourneth now to the former narration,
shewinge after what manner the Angels proceaded, which had the seven last
plagues. The temple of the tabernacle of witness (says he) was open in
heaven, by which figure we are taught that the horrible plagues should rise up
in the world not rashly, or by chance, for these Judgments come forth of,
the innermost secreate of Gods will. For he alludethe to the form of the old
tabernacle out of the innermost rowme whereof, answers were given to those that
asked.

Verse. 6. And the seven Angels came out of the temple, which had the seven
plagues clothed in pure and bright linen and having there breasts girded with
golden girdles. etc.

THey proceade from the will of God even all the ministers of his Justice and
severity, clothed in linen garments, pure and brighte, that they might
signify the sincerity and equity of his Judgment. For the wrath of God
does never rage against the innocente, but it is inflamed against the wicked
contemners of all ungodliness. Moreover they are girded with golden girdels,
that they may show how ready they are with all diligence to execute the
ministry committed unto them. Such diligence which is figured by the girdle
is in so great price and estimation with God, that it garnisheth and adorneth
those blessed Spirits more then gold, or preciouse stones. Princes and
Magistrates must imitate and follow this diligence, to whom god has delivered
the sword into there hands, that they may be ready to exercise vengeance
upon the wicked transgressors of gods law, not to let there sword gather
rust in the scaberd, and the godly in the mean time be oppressed by the
number and injuries of the wicked.

Verse. 7. And one of the four beasts gave unto the seven angels seven golden
vials, full of the wrath of God, which lives for evermore.

WE have expounded the beasts before by conferring them with the vision of
Ezekiel, to be Cherubicall Angels, which govern the creatures of the world.
The sense therefore is, that the creatures of God created to the use and
service of men, do minister scourges and punishments to be taken upon the
reprobate against whom all even the most contemptible creatures of the world
are armed. These vessels conteyne a cert^n measure of Gods Judgments, which
seem good to his counsel to be powered forth in there several tournes. And
they are golden, that is preciouse, because they set forth ye glory of God in
his Justice. Lastly they are said to be full of the wrath of god which lives
for ever, whose wrath against the reprobate is vnappeaceable and eternal, not
ye fury of some mortal creature, which though it be not apeased whiles he
lives, yet by his death it is finished and has an end. Far other is the
fatherly correction of god, by which he chastises his children for a time
against whom his wrath does not long time, or much wax hot, but by and by,
so that they repent, he retourneth in to favor with them, and becomes
merciful and graciouse unto them.

Verse. 8. And the temple was full of the smoke of the glory of God, and of his
power and no man was able to enter into the temple till the seven plagues of
the 7. Angels were fulfilled. etc.

HEre is described how great is the majesty, and power of God when he has
decreed to show forth the same, and that by no means access is open unto
him, so long as his fury waxes wrath against the wicked. Not that he rages
like an angry man, which being incensed against the evil, does without reason
or difference strike the good also coming next to hand, but because, when he
takes upon him the person of a Just Judge no sinful flesh can stand before
him, except with the voice of clemency and mercy he calls us unto him being
very fearful, and trembling.

The syxtenth Chapter.
HE shows in this Chap. with what plagues and scourges the Lord would strike
the kingdom of antichrist before the last overthrow and utter destruction of
the same, least they should always please the^ selves securely in their
delights and pleasures, and deride and scorn the calamities of the Godly.

Verse. 1. And I heard a great voice out of the temple, saying to the seven
Angels, go your ways, power out the seven vials of the wrath of God upon the
earth. etc.

THe seven Angels stood gyrded about holdinge the vials full of Gods wrath
which were committed unto them, yet they dare not power them out, until that
being admonished by the heavenly oracle, they knew that the ripe time for that
busynes was at hand. Therefore the voice of Almighty God is heard thu^dringe
out^ of the temple of his holiness, which commands the Angels with speed
to power forth the vialls full of Gods wrath into ye earth. Let us learn here
to wait for the voice of God in all things before we take any thing in
hand. We do pray continually, thy will be done in earth as it is in heaven.
Behold here an example of aungelicall obedience, to the rule whereof we ought
to frame our obedience. The Angels are first called forth of ye temple, they
appear straightway, carefully waitinge what the Lord would command them:
there is given into every of their hands vials, that is power to exercise the
judgments of God against the Antichristian wickedness, which thing although
they desire spedely to dispatche, yet they tarry the time prefixed and
determined by God. Moreover we may here note the force of that voice, (pour
forth) that they are commanded to send them down not by drops as it were dew
or rain, but to power forth and emptye there whole vials at once, whereupon we
understand that rare and unwonted plagues were to be cast upon the reprobate.

Verse. 2. And the first angel went and powered out his vial upon the earth:
and there sell a noisome and grievous sore upon ye men which had y^ mark of ye
beast and upon the^ which worshipped his Image.

The seven plagues as we noted also before, signify in general all the
calamities, which God would send upon the kingedome of Antichrist, before
that Christ should flea the man of sin himself with the breath of his mouth.
And of those certain are usual scourges of God, with which he is accustomed
to afflict and punnish the world for sin, as pestilence, war famine,
contagiouse and sharp diseases, which are signified, by pouringe forth the
four first vials, And certain are ordained peculierly to beat down the
tyranny of Antichrist it self, which are described in the three other vials.
That which concerns the former, because the tyranny of Antichrist may
worthylye be compared to the bondage of Egipte, the holy ghost does denou^ce
the like punnishments by an allegory to the plagues of the Egiptia^s. For this
city is spiritually called Egypt, as we read before in the 11. chap. The first
Angel therefore powered forth his vial upon ye earth, and there followed a
noisome and grievous sore upon y^ men which professed y^ bon^age of ye beast,
and the^ which acknowledge his aucthority. And this plague represe^teth ye sixth
plague, wherwt god stroke y^ rebellious Egiptia^s by Moses as we read Exo. 9.
this plague signified, pestilence, sores, and specially ye french pockes with
which y^ popes cardinals, bishops and all y^ dregs of ye popish clergy are
chiefly afflicted, whose ungodliness god does daily reueng with sundry and
vnaccustomable kinds of diseases. And histories do testify how often ye
pestilence slew and devoured, at Rome in Italy, in spain, in france, and
sometime thorowout al Europe, as large as ye tira^ny of the pope exte^ded, so yt
we never read yt they were any where else so grievously afflicted with
pestile^ces, either before Christ, or after ye gospel revealed as in ye
midst of popery. But peradventure ye papists will object yt they are not only
plagued with pestilence, but ye the same does also take hold upon our countries
and cities: we confess ye same to come to pass through our sins and
iniquities: but here it is spoken of ye rare and unwonted greatness of ye
punishment which is plainly perceived to have been poured forth upon ye kingdom
of antichrist, when the lord does only afflict ours gently with fatherly
corrections.

Verse. 3. And the 2. Angel powered out his vial upon the sea and it b^came as
ye blood of a dead man, and every living thing died in the sea. etc.

THe Lord will beat down there pride not with and kind of punishment as we
said before, but with sundry plagues and often repeated. And this figure
resembles the first plague of yt Egiptians Exodus 7. When all the waters were
turned into blood. Here also the waters of ye sea are turned into corrupted
blood, he signifies (I think) yt with wars, seditions as well civil, as
foren, there should be made such a great slaughter of men, that the very sea
should draw into it a bloody color. And the amplification is hyperbolicall,
of which sort there are very many found in the scriptures, to express ye
grieuousnes of this punishment, wherewith god will afflicte ye reprobate. Whole
Europe almost is compassed about with sea, which when it is said to be turned
into blood, signifies yt all should redound, and as it were ouerflow with
wars, tumults, and bloody battles. Here also histories do witness, and
daily experience also does teach, what great slaughters the pride of the Roman
bysshopes has caused, whiles it set princes together by the ears with most
grieuouse battles to flea the^ selves on either part: whose force and
strengthes being weakened, he abuses to the confirmation of his tyranny. Who
can number, how many thousands of men he has slain? whiles he cast down
some Emperors from the Empire, and placed others in there rowmes, whiles he
absolved the common people from the faith given to there Princes, when he
against couenauntes invaded the Turckes, and Saracenes, whiles he makes
war for the cross, and the city of Jerusalem and whiles he sows discordes
and privy hatreds daily among Princes, and now before our eyes, what
tragedies has he raised up in Germany, France, Scotland, and Spain? and from
which our country of England is not altogether free. But howsoever he
applies his business, god in the mean time turns the calamity upon his own
head and makes the sea bloody with the slain carkases of the Papists. That
he says every living thing dyed in the Sea, it is a conueniente hyperbole
for the Allegory, and also together therewith he alludeth to the fishes of
the Egiptians that were slain, when the waters were turned into blood. But of
these things, which we have said it is not hard to understand what he
means.

Verse. 4. And the third Angel powered forth his vial upon the rivers and
fountaynes of waters and they turned to blood, etc.

THat nothing might remain pure and wholesome to the wicked, first the earth and
the sea, now the rivers and fountaynes, afterward the sun it self, are
stricken with sundry plagues. And this calamity does represente that first
plague of Egipte, by which the waters of the flood Nylus, and generally all
lakes and fountayns were turned into corrupt blood. But in that in the pouring
forth of two vials the waters are turned into blood, I think it is to be
referred to the more large settinge forth of the slaughter done upon the
wicked, which thing also the two Angels do afterward confess: that because
the thirste of blood is insatiable in the kingedome of Antichrist, therefore
by the law of equality, all things with them are turned into s^aughter, and
blood.

Verse. 5. And I herd the Angel of the waters say, etc.

I think the same concerning ye Angel of the waters which I saw before of
the Angel, which had power over fire. Verily that he is a certain power to
whom God has committed the government of the waters. For by this name,
(power) the Apostle Paul calls a certain order of the Angels, Ephesians. Chap.
1. Colloss. Chap. 1. And fitly is the Aungel of the waters brought in here,
acknowledging that this punishment has worthily happened unto them, that they
should drink blood insteade of water, which with so great heat of cruelty
thristed after blood. For although this Angel be set over the waters that he
might preserve and keep them from destruction, and corruption, notwithstanding
in that, being turned into blood they were corrupted, he confesses that it
came to pass, by the just judgment of God, for a punishment upon the wicked
for there monstrouse and horrible cruelty.

Lord thou art just, which art, and wast holy, because thou have judged these
things. etc. He magnifieth the most just Judgments of God, which fulfilleth
the office of a righteous and vncorrupt Judge. And such as he shows him self
in sending this plague, such has he been in all ages, even from the beginning
of the world. Which although according to the sense of the flesh may seem
sometime to be to little, yet notwithstanding at length when we shall be endued
with Aungelicall wisdom, we shall understand that all his Judgments do
consist in most beautiful equity.

Verse. 6. For they shed the blood of Saints and Prophets: and therefore have
thou given them blood to drink: for they are worthy. etc.

THe raging cruelty of Antichrist which he exercises daily upon the holy
martyrs of God, shall not escape unpunished, but he which is never satisfied
in drincking the blood of the righteouse, at length when the waters are
turned into blood shall drink his fill of blood. For the law of repaying is
most equal and right, that they which seek nothing, but the blood of the
Saints, and of the Prophets should them selves with bloody wars, and
cruel slaughters be satisfied even till they be weary.

Verse. 7. And I herd an other angel out of the alter saying. etc.

WHen as before he had placed the souls of those that were slain for Christ
under the altar Chapt. 6. Requiring vengeance upon there persecutours: I agree
with those which refer this voice, which came from the altar to the same
souls, now at length acknowledginge it to be true, which was said to them
before, that if they should rest a little while until the number of there
brethren which should likewise be slain for the testimony of the gospel,
were fulfilled, that by and by after god would grieuousely punish the wicked
reprobate.

Even so Lord God almighty, true and righteouse are thy Judgments, etc. First
this voice subscribeth to the Aungel^ of the waters, which had said that the
waters were worthily turned into blood, that they might be given for drink,
to blood thirsty men, afterward it does magnify the almighty power, truth
and righteousness of god. For God has declares his power, when as to beat down
ye proud, he has overthrown them with so great slaughters, he has co^me^ded
his truth seeing he has cast upon ye wicked ye punishments which he has
often threatened so sore. And he has showed his righteousness, when as he has
not only brought upon the^ the due pains for there heynouse offenses, but also
by the Just law of repaying like for like, has found out a convenient kind
of torment for there wickedness, that they which were so greatly delighted
with the deinties of cruel and bloody bankettes, should drink one of an
others blood, whiles to there own destruction, they rage daily with civil
wars, slaughters and tumultes. True therefore and just are his Judgments.

Verse. 8. And the fourth angel powered forth his vial on the sun, and it
was given unto him to torment men with heat of fire.

GOd will have nothing remain sound unto them, which by no benefits can be
drawn to worship him. We all know sufficiently how acceptable and amiable the
light of the sun is, how healthful the influe^ce of that star is, the
learned do acknowledge, how necessary the use of the same is to all men, the
learned together with the unlearned also do confess. But to the reprobate
ministers of Antichrist, which darckened the only sun of righteousness
with there own devises, and inuentio^s, and by there bloody decrees have
assayed to take him out of the world, God will make the natural, and
refreshing heat of the sun, pestiferouse and deadly, so that in burninge all
things, and also afflicting and tormenting men them selves with intolerable
heat, he brings in hunger and thirst, and most pestilent diseases which rise
and spring of the same. Moreover so large as the virtue of the sun does
extend, all things shall burn with immoderate heat, who can deny, but y^
they were afflicted with very great famine in the papisme? so that many also
perished for want of food. Moreover who knows not of the fevers, languishing
diseases, and pestilences springing of vnpure victuals, which sometime also
light upon the popes them selves, if he have read the history of the times
deduced from boniface the third, in whom the papacy begun, unto these our
times.

Verse. 9. And men boiled in great heat, and blasphemed the name of God.

HE signifies yt they parched not only with common heat of y^ sun, as they
be in hot countries, but scorched with far greuouser boiling heat of the
bright star: that they were almost turned into madness through ye torments.
But at length what proffitte took the wicked by these chasticeme^ts? they
blasphemed the name of god, ascribing these plagues not to there own
abominable wickedness, but to ye unrighteousness of the lord. To the Italians,
and also to the chief bysshopes, and popes the^ selves, how familier and
accustumable a thing it is to tear y^ sacred and holy name of god with
horrible blasphemies, yea even for ye lightest damages or hurtes, those know
which have seen and vewed there manners, and cities. With what fury and rage
think ye, would they bark against god as it were mad dogs? when these
grieuouse torments apprehended and took hold of the^. Moreover which is the
common blasphemy to all the papists, that they tear the holy gospel of
Christ, which god of his infinite clemency and mercy has vouchesafed to
open, and reveal unto us in these last days, with most filthy reproaches, and
attribute all the evils wherewith they are afficted, to the preaching and
spreading abroad of the same.

Which has power over these plagues. etc. He amplifieth there deuilish
wickedness, that directlye they touch him with there blasphemies, which has
power over these plagues either to increase or to deminish them, neither do
they fear, least being provoked to anger by there horrible blasphemies, he
should throw upon them more heavier and sorer torments. Here we may observe
and note the nature and property of the reprobate, which being subdued with
no chastismentes of god do yield or give place, but with how many more
scourges of God they are chasticed, so much ye more obstinatly and proudelye
they swell against God.

And they repented not to give him glory. etc. We are taught here what fruit
god looks for of our chastisement verily that we should repent for our sins,
and ascribe ye glory to god, which has worthily chastised us, confessinge
that we have deserved by our heynouse offenses, that he should punish us more
grieuousely, and may acknowledge that he tempereth this justice with cleme^cie
even then when he punishes. The wicked do not this, but they always complain
of the severity and sharpness of god, when as in very deed the thousand
part of there wickedness deserves not these temporal afflictions, but
eternal torments.

Verse. 10. And the fifte angel powered out his vial upon the throne of the
beast, and his kingdom waxed dark. etc.

ALthough god has hitherto with most grieuouse plagues taken vengeance upon
the ungodliness of the members of Antichrist, yet nevertheless the evils
scarce came near to the head him self. For in war famine and pestilence, ye
common people are rather afflicted thou the prelates and noble personages. Now
therefore the Lord does begin to punish the very head of the beast, and his
chief members, when as the first Angel powers forth the vial of gods
wrath, upon the throne of the beast, which I interpret to be done, when as
through the preachers of the gospel the controversy concerning the power of
Rome was first moved, which at length being discussed by the authority of
the scriptures, the Antichristian pride and arrogancy of the beast was made
manifest to the world. For then his kingedome waxed darcke. And that glory of
the popish kingdom, by which through mad pride he had exalted himself above
all Churches, yea above ye scriptures, is altogether darckened in the whole
world, so that every where, very many men do renounce the authority of
the Bishop of Rome, princes do expel and drive his authority out of there
Dominions, and to conclude the common people, yea even of the very papists,
do contemn his bulls, and pardons, and deride and mock his curses, violate
and break his laws and decrees without any conscience of them.

And they gnewe there tongues for sorrow. etc. The Romanistes take most heavily
this contempt of their dignity, but they find not how they may restore them
selves to their old glory and aucthority. They endeavor indeed with all
diligence and omit nothing, if by any means they might recover there lost
dignitye, but the matter is past recouerye, therefore being in despair for
the great anguishe of mind, like as it were mad men, they bite and gnaw there
own toungues. The holy ghost does signify by this metaphor, that nothing
could have happened unto them more greuouse, then that the throne and kingdom
of the beast should be darkened with the thick cloud of reproach and contempt.

Verse. 11. And blasphemed the god of heaven, for their pains and for there
sores, and repented not of their works. etc.

THey are says he oppressed on every side with so great sorrow, for the
disclosing of there frauds, errors, pride and shameful life, that being but
wicked inhabitants of the earth, they provoke the very God of heaven with
horrible blasphemies. For there sores. Rotten and festred sores cannot suffer
the least touching. But now when as they are not lightly touched only, but
lanched and seared with knives and hot irons, it is not to be meruailed at,
though the miserable men be driven into a furious madness. But yet in the mean
time they have no care of repentance, which is the only medicine and salve
for there pestred wounds. For although of what sort there works are they may be
of all men, yet never the latter they give themselves to there old accustomed
wicked and deuilishe vices, as covetousness cruelty and filthy lust. Moreover
this place does teach that true repentance is to abstain from wicked works.
For if we shall say a thousand times yt our wickedness does displease us,
except we bring forth fruits worthy of repentance, we are nothing else but
hipocrites. Here also we see and perceive the nature of the reprobate, which
look how much nearer they are to extreme and utter destruction, so much more
malipertly they despise the majesty of God.

Verse. 12. And the sixth Angel powered forth his vial upon the great river
Euphrates, and the waters thereof drie^ up that the way of the kings of the
east should be prepared. etc.

AFter that ye kingdom is obscured, so that there is nothing in the whole
world darkee then the papacy: the sixte Angel now powers forth the sixth
vial of Gods wrath upon the great river Euphrates. The city of Rome in this
prophecy is allegorically painted forth under the figure of Babylon, and the
river Euphrates was so great a defense to the old Babylon, that when Cyrus
would have taken that City, he could not by any other means, the^ by
deriuing the river Euphrates from his Channel, and tourning away the course and
stream of the waters, he made the floude it self passable: And by this means
he opened an entrance and passage to himself, into the most strong defenced
city, to the which History no doubt, the holy ghost here alludeth, when he
says that the waters of Euphrates were dried up, that a way should be
prepared to the kings of the East, to take and possese the city. He
signifies therefore that all the defenses and munitions of the Roman Empire
should by the Just judgment of God be destroyed, that the Romanistes being
spoiled and made naked of all there ayed, may be a pray to all there enemies
that shall invade them. Which thing whether it shall be by the Turcke, and other
tyrants of the East, or by the Princes of Europe, which have embraced the
Gospel, and shall occupy, and possess Babylon it self, I ca^ not for
certentie define any thing thereof, but the end shall once most plainly
show. Truly there is no man which sees not, that the West Babylon is
spoiled almost of all strength wherewith in time past she was furnished, (which
is that the waters of Euphrates are dried up) so that the assalte thereof is
now very easy and shall be to those to whom God shall sometime commit this
business.

Verse. 13. And I saw three unclean spirits like frogs, come out of the
mouth of the Dragon and out of the mouth of the beast. and out of the mouth of
the false Prophets. etc.

AFter that Satan perceived that great danger hanged over his kingdom, which
he governs by the hands of Antichrist the Roman bishop, that dilligent
watchful Dragon, stirs up the beast, that is the pope pricked with the
furies of his conscience, that by the consent and counsel of the false
prophet the two horned beast, that is, of the popish clergy of Cardinales,
and bysshopes, messingers, and Legates a Latere are sent forth to all Princes
o^ the earth, as many as acknowledge his authority, that they may stir
them up with there croking cries, like the furies of hell, and may arm them to
exercise cruelty against the godly professors of the Gospel, by the
inquisitours o^ heretical prauitie as they call them, and by other masters of
mischief. We are here admonished that there is one and the self same purpose
to the Dragon, the beast and the false prophet, that is, to the devil, the
pope, and the popish clergy, that when they fear that the ruin and
overthrow of his tyranny hangs over them, through the Gospel, they labor
and endeavor by all means to hinder and stop ye course thereof. For all
things are governed in the papacy, by the authority and inspiration of the
devil. Moreover he says that the Legates, or messingers of the pope, are
unclean spirits, like unto frogs or todes. Because that like as unclean
spirits drive those into madness in whom they dwell: so these inflame with
jury and mad rage, the princes and mighty men, to whom they are sent,
against all the godly, and against them selves, that to there own utter
destruction they may rage against Christ, and his sacred Gospel. And they are
said to be like frogs, either because they are delighted with mier and
mearish places, that is the filth puddles of errors, or else that without any
reason they always croke and cry out with making bubles like frogs, until
they shall compel kings to conspire against god, and against his sacred
truth.

Verse. 14. For they are the spirits of devils working miracles, to go out unto
the kings of the earth, and the whole world. etc.

WHen as before he had said that they were unclean spirits, now he repeateth
that they are the spirits of devils, that is even the very members and
Instruments of the devil, that all may know that the counsel wherewith they
inspire kings, is ungodly and diuilish. (Working miracles) bewitching the eyes
of men with illusions and feigned miracles, as though they were the ministers of
god, when as in very deed they are the slaves of Satan. For so they color
there lies to Princes, that they may turn there eyes from the light of the
gospel. For unless they were altogether blind, they would never apply there
ears to such brablers: that they should suffer them selves at the will and
beck of Antichrist to be mustred into that war which is taken in hand
against the almighty god him self.

To gather them to the battaill of that great day of God almighty. etc. In
which day a famous and such a slaughter as was never herd of before shall be
made upon all the proud contemners of god, which would suffer them selves to
be set in battle array against god, and against his Christ: in which day also
the perpetual praise of victory, and eternal triumph shall be obtained unto
Christ, When all the army of Antichrist being slain, overthrown, and
vanquished, the excellent glory of his virtue and power shall always have the
renown.

Verse. 15. Behold I come as a thief. etc.

I Confess that this verse is interlaced altogether without any hanging
together of the text, but not without reason. For seeing mention was made in
the end of the verse going next before, of that great and fearful day of
the Lord god almighty, which should catch and oppress the reprobate, like a
snare: this admon^tion is not out of season intermedled, that the godly may
learn always to watch, least the remembrance of that day should at any time
slip out of there minds. Behold I come as a thief, it is ye voice of Christ
Math. 24. Luke 12. Threatening that his second coming shall be sudden and
unlooked for to the world, as the flood of waters in the days of Noah, and the
fire in the days of Lot.

Blessed is he that watches, and keeps his garments lest he walk naked and
men see his filthiness. etc When as the coming of the lord is so uncertain,
it behooves us always to watch, neither at any time to sleep in the bed of
security. That therefore which they that watch do, for they do not put of
there garments, as they do which go to bed: that same is to be followed
of us in these Spiritual watches that we may always keep, and hold fast
the garment of faith and and innocence least if the light of that great day
springing up suddenly, should drive away all the darckenesse of dissimulation,
we be found to walk naked, and so the de^ormitie of our nakedness be
visible, or seen both to GOD and men. This garmente Christ does freely give
unto us, in that we will receive and gyrde the same diligently about us.

Verse. 16. And he gathered them into a place called in the Hebrewe tongue
Armagedd^n. etc.

THe order of his narration being a little interrupted, to bring in and place
between a most proffitable admonition, he returns again to his purpose
namelye that the Devil, and Antichrist by those Legates sent forth gathered
together Kings and there arms into a place appointed for there own killinge
and slaughter, to which the name Armageddon in the Hebrewe tongue is given, for
that which came to pass there which is worthy to be remembered. Concerning
the signification whereof, it is not agreed of among the learned, for some do
expound it Charmageddon, that is an army appointed to destruction, but others
do more rightly (in my Judgment) read this word in Hebrewe Guarmagedgnon,
that is the subtlety of destruction, so that the sense is, that by the deceypt
or fraud of the Devils, the Princes are brought into that place, where they
should perish by a slaughter in battaill, like as it is expounded more at
large in the last verse of the 19. chap. And we know that it was usual among
the Hebrews of the like things ye happened to give names to places: as
Kibroth, Hataauah, the graves of concupiscence, Numb. 11. And Hamongog, that is
the multitude Gog. Ezekiel. 39.

Verse. 17. And the seuenthe Angel powers ^orth his vial into the air. etc.

THis last plague seems the most grieuouse of all, because the other tauched
a part only, but this strikes the whole body of Antichrist with extreme
destruction. For now the lord God himself furnished with his own virtue and
power, will set upon the beast and his city Babylon, for now Antichrist shall
not have so much as the air, which he may breath, but being armed for his
destruction.

And there came a great voice out of the temple of heaven from the throne,
saying it is done. etc.

THis sentence proceeded or came forth from the majesty of God it self, and
from his certain determinate counsel, which is so suerly ratified and
confirmed, that it can by no meaanes be called back again. This voice
signifies that the last ruin of Antichrist does hang over his head which
he can by no means avoid or eschew.

Verse. 18. And there followed voices thundringes and lighteninges, and there
was a great earthquake, such as was not since men were upon the earth, so
mighty an earthquake I mean. etc.

THis is, that all things shall be tossed up and down with horrible terrors
that they whose iron breasts could not be pierced through with any strookes
of the plagues that went before, that they might repent: shall now be stricken
with so great horrore, that with fearefulnes of mind they shall down as
dead. Moreover those turmoles of the air, and chiefly the earthquake so
wonderful, do fore show the most greuouse and great chaunges in the world,
of which as we see the beginninges, so verily the end will be tragical and
horrible.

Verse. 19. And the great city was divided into three parts, and the cities
of the gentiles fell, etc.

NOW follows, the effect of this earthquake the greatest of all others, that
great city, which is the sea of Antichrist, the whole multitude of those which
were subjects to the pride of Rome, clone into three parts through the
violence of this earthquake, which many do thus interpret, and in my
judgment rightely. They which in time paste with one consent^ have worshipped
the beast, are now divided into three sects. For some of them do from there
very heart abhor and detest his tyranny, others do remain in the same
slauerye still, and the third kind of men do stick to neither part. But
has fallen either into Epicurisme, or Atheism. They expound the Cities of
the Gentiles, to be all the foreign and false religions, as of the Turckes, and
Jews and Barbarouse people, all which Religions it is certain shall be
destroyed at the coming of Christ or else a little before, but it becomes us
with sobriety to conjecture of those things which are not yet come to pass.

And great Babylon came in remembrance before God to give unto her the cup
of the wine of the fearcenesse of his wrath. etc. Not that God had at any
time forgot her, which has also sent upon her those former plagues. But he
signifies that his whole wrath was now to be powered forth at once upon her,
that he might utterly subuerte and overthrow her, as it shall be taught more
plainly in the Chapter 18. We have spoken before of the cup of the wine of
Gods wrath Chap. 14. But that here also is added an other word signifying
wrath to the greater Emphasis, for he says not only wrath, but also the
anger or fercenesse of his wrath.

Verse. 20. Every isle fled away and the mountains were not found. etc.

SO great shall the earthquake be that it does swalow up and devour the
Mountains and Isles. Some do refer this to the end of the world, but I
think it signifies that all place of refuge is taken away, for men are wont
in the greatest calamities, to fly for aid or safegarde to the mounteynes and
yles.

Verse. 21. And there fell a great haylle as it had been talentes* out of heaven
upon the men, and men blasphemed God, because of the plague of the hayle, for
the plague thereof was exceading great. etc.

LIke as God oppressed the men of Hierecho with hayle from heaven, so likewise
will he beat down and grind in pieces his adversaries the Antichristians,
with great stones as it were talentes, from heaven. All these are a Periphrasis
and as it were a description of the horrible end, which remains for the
reprobate, which we are taught can by no plagues be reformed, or brought to
repentance, but always they blaspheme God, so that they show them selves
worthy that God should make them perpetual monumentes of his wrath, and should
adiudge them to eternal torments.

The seuententh Chapter.
Hitherto he has with sundry colors painted out Antichrist him self now
also under the figure of the great whore, he describes his Church, or the
aldulterouse religion, afterward he expounds the mystery as well of the
whore as of the beast yt bears her: and lastly he foretells the
destruction of them both.

Verse. 1. Then there came one of the seven Angels which had the seven vials,
and talked with me, saying unto me.

THe self same Angels which are the Ministers of Gods wrath and severity
upon the wicked, do serve the godly to these comfort, and consolation, and to
the buyldinge up of the Church. Which thing truly is neither unprofitable
nor unpleasant to think yt we have those appointed of god to defend our
health and welfare, which as often as it seems good to god, can easily
overthrow and subvert, all the engines and subtilties of the adversaries. We
may note also how familiarly the Angels speak to the Apostle: whom for the
benefit of Christ they acknowledge to be there brother and fellow servant.

Come I will show thee the damnation of the great whore that sits upon many
waters. etc. When diverse times before he had made mention of the great city,
now the holy ghost that he might make manifest of what city he had understood
or meant, does describe it under the image or figure of the great whore. For the
great whore as the Angel afterward does expound it, signifies a great
city, like as many waters, whereupon she sits, do signify many people,
over which she rules and worthily is the Church or Romish religion, whose
whole aucthority depends upon that city of seven hills, compared to a
famous and noble harlot, which enticed the minds of me^ to her filthy love
with whorishe deceipts, and false colors as it were with harlotlyke
enticementes. For it is usual in the scriptures, to compare all false and
idolatrouse worshipping, to most filthy adultries. But the sinagoge of Rome,
which above all other herisies has invented false and idolatrouse
worshippinge of God, may as it were by her own proper right challenge to her
self the name of a great whore. Which although she does please and flatter
her self and her lovers, as though she were a bewtifull wife, yet
nevertheless by the just judgment of God, she is condemned to eternal
shame, and dishonor as a most filthy harlot.

Verse. 2. With whom have committed fornication the kings of ye earth.

THis was not the least part of the whorishe art, that she enticed and alured
kings and mighty men, with fained flatteringes, and practices of bawdry, into
fornication, for by this means she did hope that she should have the commune
people there subjects, even vowed to her love. Therefore she flattereth princes
and grants them license of all wickedness, in pardoninge all things as
murders, adultries, and incestes, so that they stand steadfast in the obedience
of the sea of Rome.

And the inhabitants of the earth are droncke with the wine of her
fornication etc. She has played the harlot not with kings only, but
generally with all the inhabitants of the earth, as a most impudente whore,
and with the furiouse wine of her fornication has made them droncken in such
abominable manner, that they are even like swine inflamed to fill and satisfy
there lust with her. And this is that zeal of the papists wherewith they are
in mad dotage upon masses, to Munckerie, Pilgrimages, Pardons, so that they
cared not to bestow all there substance upon the same baggage, because reason
being overcome with lust, they are made droncken with the wine of her
fornication.

Verse. 3. So he carried me away into the wilderness. in the spirit. etc.

SEeinge the time of manifestinge this whore in the world was not yet come,
although even then the mystery of iniquity did work, this harlotte is placed
in the deserte, which after certain hundred years should by the Just
Judgment of God be brought forth into the world, to bewitche the wicked
inhabitants of the earth: therefore Ihon is lead into the wilderness by the
Angel to behold this whore.

And I saw a woman sit upon a scarlat colored beast. etc.

WHen Ihon was come in to the wilderness, the Image of the woman sittinge
upon a scarlat colored beast, was showed and set before him, by the
description it appears that it is the very same beast which is lively
described in the thirtenth Chap. For the Church or religion of Rome is stayed
upon the authority of the pope and his clergy, which bear her up even as
beasts carry a burden, and with praises extol her beauty above the heavens
The color also of the beast is painted out to be like scarlet, which color we
know does please the court of Rome above all colors, for with this color
the pope him self, with this the Cardinales and there horses, with this the
prelates and Bysshopes being aparailed and decked, do walk in there
stateliness. Which thing, I suppose, is not done rashly or at adventure, but
that they might be aunswerable to this figure. And this red color does
signify there bloody desire in persecuting the true members of Christ and the
Church, even unto death.

Full of names of blasphemy. etc. If thou should weigh and examine the
names and callinges of all degrees, or orders in popery, thou should find
nothing but horrible blasphemies, as the holiness, the highness, and
fatherhoode of the pope, and prelates, and infinite blasphemies of the same
sort, with which base and unlearned verlets, are extolled above Christ, and
the Angels.

Which had seven heads and ten horns. etc. These are his badges or arms
whereby he is known, for they show that he is the self same beast, which he
saw before in the 13. Chapter: Whose mystical interpretacion also he
afterward received.

Verse. 4. And the woman which I saw was araide in purple and crimsin, and
girded with gold, preciouse stones, and pearls. etc.

THis verse conteyneth 2. things, the apparel and decking of this whore and
her wicked fornication. As concerning her apparaill she shines all over with
purple, crimsin, gold, pearls and preciouse stones that she may seem
beautiful to her lovers. Far other is the apparail of the true Church, of
which we read before in the twelfe Chapter, which is garnished altogether
with heavenly ornaments, but this stinckinge harlotte with the glitteringe
show of earthlye things hawkethe for the praise, and commendation of beauty,
for we see how that the Church of Rome, and popish religion, in altars copes,
vestume^ts, miters, crosses, chalisses, books, censers, patines, in gilding
and decking images does show nothing else, but a certain pomp of great riches,
of purple, crimsin, silk, silver, gold, preciouse stones and pearls, of which
things, Christian religion has no need of at all, but a popish religion
cannot stand without these things: for take from the pope, from the bysshopes,
temples, and priests, those player like apparials of purple, crimsin, gold, and
preciouse stones which are so beautiful to behold, with which ye eyes of the
blockish and rude multitud are daseled, and thou shalt find nothing in the
Church of Rome that any man will marvel a^ or esteem. For as common
harlates, when there preciouse apparaill is pulled of are, often times seen to
be deformed, so also the popish religion if thou take from it those tragical
attires, shall seem altogether naked and deformed, even to the very Papists
them selves. Which thing truly is an euidente proof, that there is no
spiritual beauty at all in her, when as she is wholly given to bodily
ornaments, sought out every where.

She had a golden cup in her hand full of abominations and filthiness of her
fornication. etc. I agree with those which by the golden cup do understand
the outward profession of Christian religion, and a certain show of the
truethe, whiles that she boasts that she does believe the word of God, and
use the sacraments, all which, notwithstanding, she has defiled with so
vnpure doctrines of devils, yt under an outward visor of truth she
comprehends nothing, but detestable abominations and the uncleanness of her
fornication. The cup therefore which she holds forth with her hand is of
gold, but the wine which is contained in it, is most deadly poison. But in
that she reaches forth with her hand, and offers the cup of these filthy
abominations to all men, her impudency is noted that she is not ashamed to
obtrude and thrust such stinking lies and filthy monstrouse errors: yea to be
credited even of wise men, he does also together there with show, that none
other are drawn into so great destruction of filthiness, and abominations,
but those whom she makes so mad with this bewitching cup, that they have lost
all spark of true judgment. The Emphasis also of these words is to be
noted, (...), that is abominatio^s, and the filthiness of her fornication,
because above all other nations, this sinagoge has abounded even wonderfully,
in unclean lusts, whoredoms and adulteries as well spiritual, as carnal.

Verse. 5. And in her forehead was a name written. etc.

THat her filthiness and impude^ce, might be hid from no man except he
burn in so great love toward her that he be altogether blind: she wereth a
name written openly in-that her whorish forehead, which fully and lively
expresses her qualities. For there is no man which has but even a spark, or
crome of true understanding, but that even in the very face, and so in the
forehead of this purple whore, he may read her name. For God has set this
mark of infamye upon her, that she might easily be known of the elect, least
they should be enticed and drawn into her filthy embracinges. Of which it
follows that the eyes of the papists are utterly blinded, which can not
behold this name princed and graven upon the forehead of the whore in such
sort that by no cunning she can hide the same, whereby at lenght they might
repent and turn from the dishonest company of her.

A mystery. etc. Although it be written in the forehead, yet it can not be
known of all without exception, but of those only to whom it is given to
understand mysteries. For this name is mystical, because that under a figure
it counteyneth* a true and natural description of her.

Great Babylon. etc. This is her name, which very fitly expresses her
manners. Not that this is the proper name of the city, as the papists are wont
now of late to expound it, with a feyned lie of a certain child borne at
Babylon, whom they would have men believe to be Antichrist, but as he said
before, this name is mystical and figurative, the interpretation whereof he
will afterward join, which should be altogether superfluouse, if Babylon
should signify literally that city of the Chaldeans. But because that city
in time past being most mighty and most proud, first was a rebel against
God, when as that tower was builded after which followed the confusion of
tongues, afterward it was the first city, which exercised tyranny upon
men, which being begun by Nymrod, continued even unto Nabuchadnezar, which
lead the people of the Jews capture, and held the^ in miserable bondage,
therefore the tyranny, Idolatry, pride and ungodliness of the city of Rome,
is signified under the figure of Babylon.

The mother of whoredoms, and abominations of the earth. etc. The east Babylon
was a sincke of all abomination and ungodliness, and not that alone, but also a
mistres of wickedness, yea a mother and nourse of all evil: all which are most
fitlye referred to the Sinagoge of Rome, which although she boaste her self
to be the Catholic and Apostolical Church the mother of all the faithful,
yet by her true and right name she is called great Babylon, the mother of all
Whoredoms and abominations of the earth: For what mischief, what ungodliness,
what uncleanness, and lewd lust, was not cherished by the support and defense of
that city? and where are there worse examples of all kind of deuilishe
wickedness, then at Rome? which are so great pestilences and corruptions, as
the very Popes, Cardinals and prelates themselves? of whom, besides there
blasphemouse errors, and profane contemptes of God there life also abounded
and ouerflowed with so great mischief that often times they exceded, Nero,
Domitian, Elagabulus, in pride, in murders, in poisoninges, treasons,
whoredoms, adultries, incestes, and preposterous lusts. Let their lives be
examined as they are set forth in histories, written even by the papists them
selves and let judgment be given by conferringe together.

Verse. 6. And I saw the woman droncken with the blood of saints and with the
blood of the martirs of Jesus. etc.

Hitherto her pride, excess and filthy abomination are described unto these
now comes so great cruelty, that Saint John affirms that he saw the whore
dronken with the blood of the saints, and martirs of Jesus Christ, which
she sucked and drunk, very gredilye, as most delicate wine, when it was shed
by the most cruel beast. This is a horrible and a barbarouse cruelty, that a
woman otherwise wanton and lasciuiouse should gorge in and devour blood
insteade of drink. And moreover that even unto drunckenes she should pour in
the blood of the godly into her belly the goulfe of all intemperaunce, what
should I here rehearse the murders, burnings, and torments, of the holy
martyrs of God, which the Roman beast like a butcher flewe, that the
continual thirsty harlot might not want drink even to make her droncken.
What a miserable slaughter of the servants of Christ has our country of
England seen in the five years persecution of Queen Mary? and what other
thing at all does the most cruel whore thirste for? whiles she raises up
civil tumultes, in France, Flaunders, Scotland, and Britanie, but the blood of
Gods saints? whiles the inquisitours in Spain, and Italy do draw great
companies of martires daily, even as sheep to the slaughter, they do there
diligence that the intemperaunce of there mistress the great whore, should not
fail.

And when I saw her I wondered with great meruaill. etc. When as S. Ihon had
seen before so great monsters armed against the Church of God, he less
wondered at them, because there terrible form and shape it self
sufficientelye bewrayed of what sort they were. But here when he had seen the
woman, shining in so bewtiefull and gorgiouse apparail, and with such whorishe
tricks enticinge the minds of men unto her, and the same also droncken with
the blood of the Saints, he wondereth vehementlye what she should be,
concerning whom as yet he had heard nothing.

Verse. 7. And the Angel said unto me wherefore meruailest thou* I will show
thee, the mystery of the woman and of the beast that bears her, which has
seven heads and ten horns. etc.

WHen as the Angel perceived yt Ihon meruailed so greatly at the beholding of
the whore, the mystery of whom he knew not, he speaks unto him familierly,
asking him why he wondered so much at her? for I said he will open, and
declare unto the all this whole mystery of what sort it is, as well of that
woman, which rides upon the scarlet colored beast, as of the Beast him
self, which bears her, which if thou have well remembered is the same,
which thou saw before furnished with seven heads and ten horns. We are
here much bound to the mercy of God, that he does vouchsafe to open this
mystery unto us, yt we should beware and take heed of the bewitchinges of this
most filthy harlot.

Verse. 8. The beast which thou have seen, was and is not, and shall ascend
out of the bottomless pit and shall go into destruction. etc.

THat beast by marks that are evident enough, does signifye the Empire of
Rome, which was most ample and large under Julius, Augustus, Tyberius, and
Claudius, but it had failed much of that ancient majesty, in Nero, Galba,
Otho, Vitellius, and Domitian, so that now it deserved not to be called a
monarchy, but was to be raised up again from hell by the popes and popish
clergy, which usurp and challenge to them selves the Empire over the whole
world, but his tyranny shall not endure for ever, because at length he shall be
apprehended by Christ and thrown headlong in to the lake that burns with
fire and brymstone, where he shall be tormented with perpetual flames, as we are
afterward taught in the 19. Chapter.

And they that dwell on the earth shall wonder, whose names are not written in
the book of life from the foundation of the world, when they behold the
beast that was, and is not, and yet is. etc. Although the falshoodes of
Antichrist shall be great, yet they shall not be able to seduce the elect into
destruction, but to deceive those only which were not predestinate to eternal
life, from the foundation of the world, but the reprobate when as they shall
see a new monarchy of the bishop of Rome raised by (which is the beast that
was under the first Emperors (but he is not) at that time when Ihon write
under Domitia^, (although he was after a certain manner) they will receive him
reverently, and as it were a new God they will worship the son of
