perdition, which extolleth him self above all that is called God, or that is
worshipped. For God by his Just Judgment shall send upon them the efficacy
of error, that they may believe lies which refused to give credit to the
truth. But here for the better understanding we must note, that the beast,
that is the monarchy of Rome, is said to have been, when as it flourished most
of all which was Nero, it is said not to be, when as the strengthes and
might thereof were weakened, so that at length they were brought almost to
nothing, which was the state of the Empire when Domitian reigned, when John
wrote these things, from which time it was never restored to her ancient
dignity, but failed and decreased by little and little, until it was altogether
decayed which we know came to pas many hundred years ago, this clause (and
yet is) shows that the empire was not then utterly abolished, although even
then the power and dignitye thereof began to be deminished. Last of all, that
ascending of the beast out of the bottomeles pit, is the monarchye of the
Pope, which always increased by the decay of the Emperors until at length
when they were quite cast down, he drew unto him self the aucthority of both
the swords.

Verse. 9. Here is the mind that has wisdom. etc.

THe Angel makes his preface, to stir up attention, that this is the most
wise interpretation of this mystery, that the faithful might diligently weigh
the same, least they should be catched unawares, by the frauds and deceipts of
this beast.

The seven heads are seven mountains whereon the woman sits. etc.

WHen as afterward in the eyghtenth verse the Angel by the woman
interprets the City, it is manifest, that this which he says of the
woman sittinge upon seven hills is to be understood of a City builded upon
so many hills. Now what City is there in the whole world, that is builded
upon seven hills, besides Rome? which Poets Historians, and Describers of
places, do all with one consent affirm to be builded upon seven Mountains,
the names whereof be these, Capitolinus, Paletinus, Anentinus, Celius,
Exquilinus, Viminalis, and Nuirinalis. Moreover this is no darcke Description
of the City of Rome, when as the Poet Virgill, also did Describe it with the
same Periphrase in his Georgikes, where he says, the city which within one
wall does compass seven hills. And it is very euidente that by the city of
Rome he signifiethe, the Church or popish religion, for all the excellency
thereof, as they them selves witness depends on the authority of the city
of Rome, which is the sea of the pope.

They are also seven Kings. etc. By the number of the heads he shows, that
not one note or mark only to decerne her may be taken, but diverse, for the
seven heads do signifye seven kings. And verily the city of Rome, in the
beginning had kings in number seven, but the verse following shows that, that
which he says here is not to be understood of them, and others some do
expound it to be the seven electors of the Empire, which seems to me not to
agree to yt matter. Others also number the Emperors from Nero, which were
these, Balba, Otho, Vitellius, Vespasian, Titus, Domitian, and Nerua, which was
the last of the Roman Emperors, seeing Traianus was a spaniard borne. But
whiles I weigh and consider all things, nothing seems more probable to me,
then that the seven heads should signify so many degrees, or orders of the
monarchy of Rome succeding one an other, for there have been so many heads
of that Empire, the first of kings, the second of consuls, the third of
dece^uiri, the fourth of dictators, the fifte of triumuiri, the sixth of
Emperors, and the seventh of popes. (Five are fallen, one is and the other is
not yet come) of those heads, or kingly powers, five are fallen that is are
abolished. That is, kings, consuls, dece^uiri, triumuiri, and dictators. The
sixte, that is that Emperors, do now bear the rule, the seventh that is the
Pope, which has not as yet invaded the tyranny. And when he commethe he must
tarry a little while, this is added to the consolation of the godly that they
might know yt the Roman Antichrist, should not always exercise his cruel
tyranny in the Church, but for a short time only, as it is showed before,
in the 11.12. and 13. Chapter.

Verse. 10. And the beast that was, and is not, is even the eyghte and is one of
the seven. etc.

Verily that is the new monarchy of Rome, which shall ascend out of the
bottomless pit, that is the whole body of Antichrist which shall make up the
eight kingdoms, that is, shall exercise a spiritual tyranny unlike to the
rest, and yet nevertheless he is of the number of the seven heads, because he
will also arrogate to him self civil gouernemente, and after the manner of
kings, of dictatours, and Emperors, he will govern with the glory of
outward pomp. We see here that the beast usurps to him self two powers,
and both of them the beyghest, when the selfsame is numbered for both the
seventh and eyghte of the kings.

And shall go into destruction. etc. When as he so often makes mention of his
destruction, he admonishethe us, that he is the same son of perdition, of
whom S. Paul speaks in the second epistle to the Thessalonians Chapter 2.
Which although being puffed up with a deuilish pride, he boastethe, that his
kingdom shall be eternal, yet shortly he shall go into destruction.

Verse. 11. And the ten horns which thou saw are ten kings, which have
received no kingdom as per, but shall receive power as kings at one hour
with the beast. etc.

THe ten horns like as also in Daniell, do signifye ten kings, that is all
the proconsuls and presidentes of the provinces, which in the Empire of Rome
governs ye common wealth, yet they were not endued with kingly power, because
they served under the emperor, and at his pleasure, were either set up in
authority or deposed. This is it that he says, that they have not yet
received a kingedome, but so soon as the beast should ascend out of the
bottomless pit, together with him they should receive power as kings. For
the monarchy of the pope, increased by the damages of the rule of the
Emperors, and when as the provinces departed from the Empire, creating and
setting up to them selves new kings, the bysshoprike of the Pope sprung up,
which received them into his Dominion and made them tributaries unto him.
Moreover it is to be noted that he says not simply they shall obtain a
kingdom, but they shall receive power as kings. For as long as they were
subject to the aucthoritye of the byshope of Rome, they were not kings
indeed, but only exercised as it were kingly power under him, because they
always depended upon his pleasure, whom also as often as it pleased him he
would thruste out of the kingdom, and place other in there roumes, at his
own will.

Verse. 12. These have one mind and shall give there power and strength unto
the beast. etc.

THese kings with one consent and agreement of mind, even as servants rather
the^ kings, shall resign all there strength and power to the beast, that is
they shall war under the Pope pay tribute unto him, execute his
commandments, as vassals shall acknowledge him for there Lord in all things.
Who knows not that this was the state of the kings of all Europe not many
years agon?.

Verse. 13. These shall fight with the lamb and the lamb shall over come them,
for he is lord of lords, and king of kings. etc.

THese shall after so slavish a manner serve the Pope, that he shall bring them
forth into battaill against Christ, that they may study by all means to
restrain the light of the Gospel brusting forth, but yet being overcome of
the Lamb, they shall be brought under. Which although in the humble shape of a
servant he be despised of the world, yet in the end of the war he will
plainly show that he is Lord of Lords and king of kings, whom no strength
of man can resist.

And they that are on his side, are called, and chosen and faithful. etc.
Those whom they condemn for heritiques, Schismatiques, and wicked men, are
called of God, because they were elected of him and they stand constantlye in
his faith, these shall war under the banner of there captain, against
tyrants, and in spiritual battaill shall overcome them. But of this famous
battaill and victory of Christ, we shall hear shortly after in the 19.
Chapter. In which after that the beast has powered forth all his poison he
shall be at length apprehended and thrown headlonge into the lake which burns
with brymstone.

Verse. 14. And he said unto me, the waters which thou saw where the whore
sits, are people, and folk, and nations, and tongues. etc.

THe Angel said in the beginnge of this Chapter, that the whore sac upon
many waters, now he expounds them to signify diverse people, great
multitudes, sundry nations and tongues, for this whore shall have a large
dominion almost over all Europe. And this is that universal consent of
nations, people and tongues, of which the papists brag so much. I confess
that many nations conspire together into the love and delights of this whore.
But shall it therefore he thought to be a Catholic Church?

Verse. 15. And the ten horns which thou saw upon the beast are they which
shall hate the whore, and shall make her desolate and naked. etc.

THose ten kings which were sometime subject to the beast at length being
instructed and taught by the gospel shall shake of her most filthy yoke. And
they which before committed fornication with the Church of Rome and her
abominable religion, after that the light of the gospel is spronge up, they
shall clearly see and perceive her deformity, they will hate her with deadly
hatred. So that the which before was environed and guarded with so great a
band of her lovers, shall be forsaken of all and shall remain desolate and
solitary, then which nothing can happen more grievous or sorrowful to a
harlot. For kings shall both withdraw themselves, and also the people of
there dominions, from her most abominable company. And also they shall spoil
her of her riches, substance, ornaments, farer buildinges, large possessions,
and all the rest of her goods, and shall drive her naked forth of the doors.

And shall eat her flesh and burn her with fire. etc. That is, they shall be
enflamed with so great hatred and lothinge of her filthynes, that they would
even rent and tear her with there teethe, and will curse her to extreme
destruction. And at the length they will wast and destroy with fire and sword,
the city of Rome it self which is the sincke of all mischiefs.

Verse. 17. For God has put it in there hearts to fulfill his will, and to do
with one consent for to give there kingedome unto the beast, until the words
of God be fulfilled. etc.

THat we may know that this whole matter is governed by God, he shows that
it was done by the counsel of God, that those kings for a time should
apply themselves to the beast. and should permit there kingedome to his will
and pleasure. For as by the just judgment of God, Antichrist came into the
world to seduce into destruction, the reprobate contemners of Christ and his
gospel, so all the increase of his tyranny shall depend upon Gods will.
Otherwise it seems incredible that kings should after so slauishe a manner
submit there necks to the Popes yoke, but that God had blinded there minds
for there heynouse offenses. But he teaches that this subjection shall not be
perpetual, but that it shall endure to that time only which is appointed by
the decree and purpose of God.

Verse. 18. And the woman which thou saw is the great city which reigns
over the kings of the earth. etc.

Saying that all writers of the ancient primitive Church as many as have
weighed this sentence could understand no other but the city of Rome, I greatly
merueile with what face the papists dare refuse this exposition. Yea verily
when as no man can bring any other interpretation which has at the least
any likely hode of truth what should we stick any longer in it. To whom I
pray ye, is this unknown, that the city of Rome even then when John writ,
had the dominion over the princes of the world? he could not therefore more
clearly even by name have said, Rome, then this periphrasis doethe signify.

The eyghtenth Chapt.
THE Angel promised to Ihon, that he would show not only the mystery, but
also the damnation of the great whore, which he does execute diligently in
this chapter, describinge the unrecoverable ruin of Babylon.

Verse. 1. And after these things I saw an other Angel come down from
Heaven* having great power. etc.

THis Angel does signify the preachinge of the Gospel, which God in these
last times has seat down from heaven, to reprehende the impudency of the
great whore, and to preach her most certain overthrow, which should never
be repaired again. This Angel is endued with great power, which brings the
unchangeable decree of GOD, concerning the subversion of Babylon. And we see
with what great zeal, freedom, and authority, all the abominations of the
Romish Church are reprehended by the faithful ministers of the gospel.

And the earth was lightened with his glory. etc. Whereas before was most
thick darckenesse, which covered ye whole kingdom of Antichrist, there the
gloriouse light of the gospel has shined, which has driven away all the mist
of errors and ignorance from the eyes of the elect.

Verse. 2. And he cried out mightelye with a loud voice saying, it is fallen:
it is fallen. Babylon the great city, and is become the habitation of Devils,
and the hold of all foul spirits, and a cage of every unclean and hateful
bird. etc.

THere is very great vehemency of every word, that he preached not but
cried out, and that strongely, with as great streyninge of voice as he could.
For it behooves the minds of men to be wakened, to the diligent considering of
gods Judgments. Such in time past seemed the stablenesse of Babylon to be,
when as it was on every side holden up with ye strength of kings and mighty
men, that men thought it should never be subject to any fall or ruin. The
angel therefore cries with a loud voice, that she is fallen, she is fallen,
even Babylon. although she were never so great and trustinge to her own
fortresses. The Church of Rome therefore may never look for any repayringe
of her ruins, for she is fallen, she is fallen even the West Babylon, and
shall never be restored again, for those things shall be performed upon the
Sinagoge of Rome, which were Prophesied of old Babylon, by Esaias the thirtenth
Chapter, and Jeremy 51. Because if there shall remain any broken pieces of the
buyldinges among the heaps of sherdes and rubbishe, they shall not be left
for any hope of restoring, but to the greater horror: for in those desert and
solitary houses, shall Zijm, and Ohijm dwell, that is spirits and Goblins:
Ostriches shall there make there nestes, and the Satyrs shall dance there,
Owls shall cry, the Serpents shall hiss, Dragons shall wallow and tumble
there, and horrible indeed shall be the face of all things in that place. Which
the Angel has expressed in the very same sense, and almost in the same
words, when as he sayethe that Babylon shall be an habitation of Devils, a hold
of all foul Spirits, and a cage of every unclean and hateful bird. When
the Gospel therefore is preached concerning the overthrow of Babilo^,
whatsoever remains in it, after the servants of god are called out, we ought
not to count the^ for any other, which rejoice to dwell in such desolate places
then for devils, foul spirits and all unclean birds. Moreover we may
plainly see before our eyes an Image of Babylon destroyed, in temples,
monasteries overthrown. Who would ever have believed, yt so great buildinges,
so beautiful palaces, so great riches and treasures should be laid wast, and
brought into so great desert? but ye voice of the Angel foretold this, it is
no doubt therefore, but yt the same end remains for all ye relics and all
re^nants of babylon.

Verse. 3. For all nations have droncke of the wine of the wrath of her
fornication, and the Kings of the earth have committed fornication with her,
and the marchantes of the earth are waxed rich of the abundaunce of her
pleasures. etc.

IF any peradventure might think yt Babylon deserved not grieuouse
punishments, that she should be stricken with destruction which should never
be restored, he rendereth a reason of the most just judgment, because with her
poisoned art. and bewitchinge cup she has seduced the people of all nations to
idolatry, and also she has procured all the kings of the earth to fornication
and has enticed them into spiritual whoredom being smothely handled by her
worishe tricks, and to conclud she is so given to her prodigal pleasures and
intemperaunce, that all the merchantes of the earth are made rich by her
excessive pleasure. Who is so blind that he sees not all these vices to over
flow in the Church of Rome? where is there such excess, where is there such
insatiable covetousness* where are there so great deceiptes and iudglinge
castes? and to be short where is there more filthier and more abominable
defiling of divine religion, then in poperye? Worthelye therefore she falls
into that destruction, appointed her of God?

Verse. 4. And I herd an other voice from heaven saying, come away from her my
people, that ye be not partaker of her sins, and that ye receive not of her
plagues. etc.

IT may be demanded, what there should need any other voice, when as that
Angel that a little before descended from heaven might have pronounced the same
things. Yea verelye the exhortation followinge is of so great weeght, and
worthy so diligent attention, that it behooves to be published with a new
voice sent from heaven, and we must observe, as well in this book, as in other
prophecies as in Esaye the 40. Chapter that as often a voice is said to be
heard without any aucthore seen, a matter of great weighte, and which is
to be recoined with deep consideration, is signified such as this most
weightye admonitions, that the faithful should depart from the fellowship
of the malignant Church, least if they be made partakers of her sins, they
should also be wrapped in her torments, and verily this heavenly voice
requires three things of the true worshippers of God, of which the first
is, that they should depart sacre away from her fellowship, the second
that they should take due vengeance upon her, the third that they should
rejoice with the whole affection of heart, and magnifye the name of God for her
unrecoverable fall. But as concerning that which perteyneth to the first
admonition, the holy ghost alludeth to the exhortation of the Prophet Jeremy
in the Chapter. 51. Verse. 45. Which with the same words, speaks to the
people of God, that they would depart out of the midst of east Babylon, if
they would provide for there life and safety. But here the heavenly voice
commands not only to fly the place, but especially to take heed of her
sins: least if they should favor and flatter them selves in her wickedness,
it might come to pass, that they should be also punished with her torments.

Verse. 5. For her sins are come up to heaven, and God has remembered her
iniquities. etc.

HE shows that the time is not now to be differed, because without delay
God will take most grieuouse punishementes upon her. For her sins are gone up
even unto heaven, as the enormities of the Sodomites, and her unrighteousness,
has put God in remembrance of his righteousness, that he can no longer suffer
so great and cruel injuries unrevenged. We are here admonished, that grieuouse
tra^sgressio^s, and great sins, do require a swifte vengeance from heaven.
Moreover how dangerouse a thing it is to have fellowship with the wicked,
whose heynouse sins draw the vengeance of God upon there heads. Let us
therefore as the prophet Jeremy warns us, fly far without the circuit
of Gods wrath, which hangs over the whole region of Babylon.

Verse. 6, Reward her even as she has rewarded you, and give her duble
according to her works: and in the cup that she has filled to you, fille her
the duble. etc.

THe next thing which god requires of his servants, is, that after the
abomination of the whore is disclosed, that they would show themselves
ministers of the most Just vengeance of God, in tormenting her in miserable
manner, reward her, says he, even as she has rewarded you. And the Psalm.
137 pronounces them blessed, which shall render to Babylon the same things
which she cruelly committed against the people of God. We must not therefore
spare her, but rather her vengeance is to be dubled, according to y^ measure
of her sins, and the cruelty, which she exercised upon the holy martyrs of
God, she is to be punished with duble torments. Princes therefore and
Magistrates shall see, which through two much gentleness do not punish her
wickedness, what they will answer to god, when they shall be accused of the
neclecte of this commandment.

Verse. 7. In as much as she glorified her self, and lived in pleasure, so
much give ye to her torment and sorrow.

HE teachethe that it is most equal and right, that by how much greater
pride, and presumption she has extolled her self, with so much greater infamy
she should be reproched, and look how much more the abominable whore has
applied her self to riote and intemperaunce, by so much more grieuouse
torments and punishments, her wantonness should be restrained. Therefore here
is no place of mercy, but her sins are to be weighed in the equal balance of
Justice, with her torments, and look whatsoever she has deserved, she ought
to suffer, without any favor showed at all. For it becomes not us to be
liberal of that which is none of our own. God the eternal Judge, has given
this sentence upon her, whose sharpenes no mortal creature can mittigate or
aswage. Let us therefore hate Babylon as we ought, with the greatest hatred,
and with vehement and earnest prayers let us desire her extreme destruction,
which so long as she remains safe the Church of Christ whose felicity we
ought by all means to procure, can never flourish.

For she sayethe in her heart, I sit being a Queen, and am no widow and
shall see no mourninge. etc. He paynteth out her arrogauncie, pride, and
security, that she said with her self, I sit being a Queen, that is, I
rule over all men as the Lady of the world, and I am no wedowe, which am
guarded and compassed about with so great a multitude of lovers, I am touched
with no fear of desolatio^, which am the spouse of Christ, the Catholic and
Apostolic Church, against which the gates of hell shall not prevail and
therefore I shall never be partaker of mourning and sorrow. After this manner
glories the malipart whore, but all these things shall vanish into smoke,
when God shall require at her hands the blood of his holy martires.

Verse. 8. Therefore shall her plagues come at one day, death and sorrow, and
famine, and she shall be burnte with fire. etc.

HE alludeth to the prophecy of Esaias concerning the old babylon in the 47.
Chapt. signifying that God will suddenly beat down her pride, bridle her
riote, and shake of her security. Because she shall be oppressed with diverse
calamities, and those coming upon her at once as with death, famine, and
sorrow, and at length even as it were appointed to extreme and utter
destruction, she shall burn with fire.

For strong is the Lord God which will condemn her. etc. If any man at the
beholding of her present estate should think that it could not come to pass
that so great strength, riches and dignity, could vanish away to naught: he
sets the strength of God against them all which seeing he has condemned her
to such destruction, he will throw down all her loftiness, break all her
strength, and tread all riches under foot, that the sentence which he has
pronounced against her may take place.

Verse. 9. And the kings of the earth shall bewail her, and lament for her,
which have committed fornication and lived in pleasure with her, when they
shall see the smooke of her burning. etc.

THat the horrible fall of Babylon, might be set as it were before our eyes,
there are brought in kings, marchantes, and mariners bewayling her, and as
many as under her defen^e have lived a voluptuouse and careless life. In the
first place kings and noble men, which under her protection gave them selves
to wanton pleasures and delights, do take it grieuousely that they are called
by the voice of the Gospel, to embrace righteousness and temperance, when
they shall see the smoke of her burninge, they weep, and after a womanlye manner
b^wayle her fall.

Verse, 10. And shall stand a far of for fear of her torment, saying alas,
alas, the great city Babylon the mighty city, for in one hour is thy
Judgment come. etc.

ALthough they loved her, and wished that she might remain safe for ever yet
through the fear of her torments they shall stand a far of and shall
acknowledge the Just Judgment of God upon her, saying, alas that notable city
Babylon, that most mighty city, how soon have thou fallen from so highest
degree of happiness? this verily is even the Judgment of God because thou
wast sufficientlye furnished against all the force and strength of man. We are
taught here that very tyrants and hypocrites do acknowledge the hand of God
in subuerting Babylon, and yet are not converted to God, but being in despayer,
do bewail the ruin of that city which they confess to be overthrown by the
Just Judgment of God for her wickedness.

Verse. 11. And the merchauntes of the earth shall weep and wayle over her, for
no man byeth there ware any more. etc.

AFter the bitter complaints of the Kings, and Princes, now follow the
doleful songs of the marchantes, which bewail Babylon not so much for any
love they have toward her, as for the loss of there own gain. Because no
man here after will bye there most precious wares, after the destruction of
this rich City. And by these merchants are understood not only the petie
merchants which were wont to sell such kind of pedlinge marchaundize to the
Prelates, to maintain the riote and in temperaunce of the Church of Rome: but
also the great Bysshopes, Prelates, and priests the^ selves, which had all
the ceremonies of there Church set to sail, whereupon they heaven up to them
selves infinite riches. But after yt vnproffitablenesse of there wares was made
manifest by the preaching of the Gospel there fayres and markets wax cold
and at length they shall find no man, which wlli bestow upon such baggage
and triflinge toys, so much as a dodkine, or a rotten nut. Not without just
cause therefore they weep and lament, because the hope of such sweet gain is
now all taken from them.

Verse. 12. The ware of gold, and silver, and of precious stone, and of pearls,
and of fine linen, and of purple, and of silk, and of scarlet and of all
manner of thine wode, and of vessels of yuerye, and all vessels of most
precious wode, and of brass and of iron, and of marble. etc.

IT is marvel that they should complain that these wares should be no more
saleable, seeing they were never had in greater price, then after the fall of
Babylon. But the meaning is, that all these things are esteemed no more as they
were the merchandise of the church of Rome, that is in masses, in images, in
the theatricall or player like shows of there temples, and in other
papisticall ceremonies, for otherwise, gold, precious stones and purple are
esteemed in there old price. But chalices, crosses images, miters of goulde,
silver, and pearls, are not embraced with there wonted reverence. Copes,
vestiments, and other tragical garments wrought of fine linen, silk, purple,
and scarlet are despised, neither do they dasill the eyes of men as in time
past. The other ornaments, and instruments of temples monasteries, and idols
of yuerye, ceder, cypress, of brass, iron and marble, are trodden down,
despised and broke in pieces.

Verse. 13. And of sinauion, and odours, and ointments, and frankincense and
wine and oil, and fine flower, and wheat, and beasts, and sheep, and horses,
and chariots, and bodies and souls of men.

NO man does now desire the perfume, of Frankensence, cinomon, and other
spices, with which they did perfume the temples and idols. No man requires the
oynetments and oil to baptize, to confirm, to ordeyne, and to bury men. No
man requesteth of them wine to wash altares, to howsell lay people, and to
heal the chincough and other infirmities of the throat. All men despise there
God made of fine flower, no man prepares wheat, oxen, or sheep to feed there
slothful belies; yea verily to be breife they might sterue, except they
should provide for themselves. The horses the chariots, and the slaves,
serving either to the necessary use or intemperance of the prelates, they the^
selves seeing they are spoiled of all there goods will not buy, neither will
other men buy the^ to give unto the^ after the manner of flatterers. Lastly, no
man will buy of them, by indulgences, masses, merits, and works of
superarogatio^, the souls of men which are the best cheap marchaundize among
the^, which nevertheless Christ purchased with his blood. Here of are those
tears, hereof come mourninges and bewaylings of the papists, hereof springs
that fretting and fuming against the doctrine of the gospel, which if it would
bring the^ the like gain they would not be altogether so sorry to change it
for popish religion. More over that he numbreth the souls of men also among
the wares, we easily understand of what Church he speaks. For never any
other heresy has set the souls of men to sale, besides popery. And also all
other merchandise which have place in popish religion, do sufficiently show
the condition of the same.

Verse. 14. And the apples which thy soul lusted after, are departed from thee,
and all things which were fat and excellent, are departed from thee, and thou
shall find them no more. etc.

NOw he tourneth his tale to babylon her self, for more veheme^cie sake, as if
he should say, not only those preciouse wares shall cease to be in price among
men, but also the sweet apples which thou have lusted after with thy whole
heart are departed from thee, and all things which were fat, and excellent are
departed from thee, and thou shall never find them any more. Nothing could
happen more grieuouse or sorrowful to a harlotte that is drowned in riote and
excess, then that all her dilicate delights and pleasures, in which she so
greatly sported her self are shaken of from her. This is therefore the
greatest torment to the Babilonicall whore, that she which a little before
flowed in such abundance of all things which she abused to intemperance, that
in riote she could compare with Cleopatra Queen of Egypt, now being naked and
deserte should be oppressed with the scarcity of all things that are good.

Verse. 15.16. The marcha^ts of these things which were wared rich shall stand
a far of from her, for fear of her torment weping and wayling, and say alas,
alas, ye great city, that was clothed in fine linne^, and purple. etc.

WHo will blame there sorrow, which by her fall also are deprived of so fat
gain? for they which by her abundaunce are made rich, by her fall also are
brought to need and powertie. Therefore they cry, they yell, they howell,
yet nevertheless they depart far from her burninge, least they should be
made partakers of her torments. But they shall not escape the hand of God
which at length will catch them. Here is described the nature of the papists,
which although they dearly love there mother the Church, for gain, and
pleasures sake, yet they fly from her torment as much as they ca^, denying her
forswearinge, and cursinge her from the mouth forward, yet they are sorrowful
within, bewaylinge her fall, and saying, alas, alas, that great City, which
was beautiefullye clothed in fine linen, and purple, and skarlat, gold,
preciouse, stones. and pearls, how soon so great riches are brought into
desolation. If any man hear the Monks, the Priests, or other Papists of the
same rabblement, bewayling the ruins of there monastries, or temples: they do
almost with the same voices testify there sorrow. They reckon up with great
bitterness of sorrow the riches, the ornaments and there beauty, and
chiefly they do not forget there own commodity, which they miserablye
complain to be taken from them, now that these things are destroyed. But they
are wretched men, which no man does pity because when Babylon stood in her
iolity, they filled the whole world with pride, covetousness, lechery,
cruelty, and Idolatry. Worthily therefore they suffer the punishments of so
great enormities, if they walk destitute and and needy of all things, and
also if they them selves feel the torments which they prepared for others.

Verse. 17.18. For in one hour so great riches are come to desolation, and
every shipmaister: and all the people that occupy ships: and shipmen and
whosoever trauaill on the sea, shall stand a far of and cry when they see
the smooke of her burning: saying: what city was like unto this great City.
etc.

THe destruction of Babylon is not known upon the earth only, but it is so
great that it is beholden also from the sea. The governors of ships
therefore and all the multitude of people that occupy ships, which were
wont to carry one^ wares by whole nauies, when they shall behold a far of
our of the sea, the smoke of her burninge: they shall acknowledge that her
utter destruction is come, and therefore they shall cry out for sorrow,
bewayling her fall and saying, what city was like to this great City, or
deserved to be compared with it? O miserable destruction of so great and so
rich a City.

Verse. 19. And they shall cast dust on there heads, and cry wepinge and
wayling and say, alas, alas, the great City, wherein were made rich all that
had ships on the sea, by her costlinesse, for in one hour she is made
desolate. etc.

THis was a sign of the greatest mourning among the Hebrews, when they cast
dust and ashes upon there heads. The holy ghost would express under this
figure, the sorrow of those, which in the fall of Babylon complain that there
gain is also fallen away. Therefore here are brought in shipmen cryinge,
wepinge, and mourninge, for the hope of gain which is taken away: after that
Babylon, by whose costlinesse were all made rich, as many as did carye wares
with ships, is brought into dust and ashes. And the complaints of all those
that mourn are to this end, that the horrible destruction of the fall of
Babylon might be set before our eyes.

Verse. 20. O heaven rejoice of her, and ye holy Apostles, and Prophets: for
God has given your Judgment on her. etc.

WE said before that the holy ghost required 3. things of the faithful in
the fall of Babylon, whereof this is the last, yt they should rejoice, for her
destruction, and give thanks to god, that he is revenged upon her ungodliness,
and chiefly upon her cruelty against the saints, he exhorts therefore the
heaven it self, that is all those, which are in heaven for ye greater
vehemency of speech, and the holy Apostles of Christ and the prophets, that
is the preachers of his holy Gospel, that they should rejoice, be glad, and
triumph, for ye vengeance, which is taken upon babylon. Because that
altogether for a time God seems to forget his servants, whiles the whore
being made drunken with the blood of the godly, did sit like a Queen in her
seat, and should make the holy martyrs of God subject to all kinds of
torments: now at length god has taken vengeance on her wickedness, for the
revenge of the saints. Worthily therefore ought the saints to rejoice, as
many as do either abhor her cruelty, or that do acknowledge and reverence
the Justice of God, in her just torments. For we ought not to be moved with
any pity of there calamity, whom we confess to be condemned by the
sentence of the most righteous God.

Verse. 21. Then a mighty angel, took up a stone like a great milston, and
cast it into the sea, saying, with such violence shall the great city Babylon
be cast, and shall be found no more. etc.

IN the fifty and one Chapter of Jeremy the Prophet does seal up the
prophecy concerning the destruction of old Babylon with the like sign. He
commanded Sheraiah a certain godly Prince which should go to Babylon, that he
should bind a stone to the book of that prophecy, and should cast it into
the midst of Euphrates saying, after this manner shall Babylon he drowned and
shall not rise from the evil that I will bring upon her. To which place
without doubt the holy ghost alludeth in this vision, sauinge that in all the
circumstaunces there is a greater Emphasis. For here not a man, but a mighty
Angel, whose force does far exceade the strength of man, took up a stone,
not a little one, but a very great one like as it were a millstone, and cast it
not into a river, but into the sea, speaking these words before, with such
violence shall the great city Babylon be cast down and shall be found no
more. And this is put for the everlasting comfort of the godly, that they
might quietly triumph of her destruction because all hope of restoringe
Papisterie is utterly taken away.

Verse. 22. And the voice of harpers and musicians and of ^ypers and trumpetters
shall be heard no more in thee, and no crafts man of whatsoever craft he be,
shall be found any more in thee. and the sound of a mylston shall be heard no more
in thee. etc.

THat he may teach that a perpetual desolation should be brought upon
Babylon, he reckeneth up all those things which are wont to serve for an
ornament and use to wealthy, and rich cities. Never, says he, shall the
voice of singers be heard, or of them which handle Instruments of music, so
that whatsoever things serve for there pleasure are taken away. Neither shall
there ever be found in her, the artificer of any art: By this means
whatsoever perteyne to the use of a civil honest life, are taken away: Lastly
the sound of a millstone shall be heard no more in her, so all the aids of
necessary sustenaunce are wanting, what remaynethe therefore, but horrible
solitariness.

Verse. 23.24. And the light of a candle shall shine no more in thee, and the
voice of the bridegroom and of the the bride shall be heard no more. etc.

NO man shall dwell there which may light a candle by night, neither shall
the voice of the bridegroom and of the bride be heard, there shall be no family
which shall ever go thither to dwell, there shall never be any marriages
celebrated there, that for the hope of posterity the city might look for
some renewing, but sorrow, solitude, silence, horror and confusion, shall for
ever occupy and posses her.

Because thy merchants were the great men of the earth and with thy
inchantements were deceived all nations. And in her was found the blood of the
Prophets and of the saints and of all that were slain upon the earth. etc.
The reasons are rendered wherefore God punished her so sharply. The first cause
therefore is assigned to be covetousness joined with pride, because her
merchants seeking dishonest gain, have heaped together infinite riches with
which being puffed up they would be counted for kings, and Princes in the
world. Who knows not how great were the riches of Cardinals, Bysshopes,
Abbotes, and of other prelates? and how great dignity have they challenged to
them selves? the second reason is given that with the witcheries and
inchauntementes or perverse doctrine, they seduced all nations into error. And
who is ignorant? with what lies they bewitched the minds of men, that they
might make all obediente, and addicte unto them. Lastly to whom is it not
manifest, how great a slaughter the synagog of Rome has made of the
prophets, and saints? so that it does worthily agree unto her which Christ
said upon Jerusalem, that all the righteouse blood which was shed, from the
blood of Just habell, eue^ to the end of the world, ought to be required at
her hands.

The nynetenth Chapter.
LIke as in the Former chapter there are brought in Kings, merchants and the
company of shipmen, miserably bewaylings the fall of Babylon: so in this
Chapter is described the joy, and exultation of all the heavenly orders, that
now when the whore is abolished, Christ shall now shortelye be joined to his
spouse. Lastly is prophesied, the last battle of Antichrist against Christ and
his Gospel, after which at length follows his eternal damnation.

Verse. 1. And after these things I heard a great voice of a great multitude in
heaven saying, halleluyah, salvation, and glory and honor and power, be to
the lord our God. etc.

THe holy ghost a little before exhorted the heaven and all that dwell therein
that they should rejoice with gladness for the fall of Babylon. Now therefore
John hears a great voice in heaven, of those which reioysed were glad and
song eternal praises to God, for the sharpness of his Judgment, which he
has showed forth against the whore. Whiles the Papists therefore mourn, weep
and houle for ye ruin of there most dear mother the sinagoge of Rome, there
is one voice of the whole church of Christ, wherewith they being wholly filled
with heavenly joy rejoice for them selves, and give thanckes to God for the
destruction of the abominable whore. And this verielye is there triumphing
song, Halleluiah, salvation, glory, honor, and power be to the Lord our God,
the Hebrew word Halleluiah is a voice that does exhort stirring up to
praise God, afterward they express by what means god is praised, verily, if
to him alone all our salvation be attributed, if all honor* glory, and power,
of beginning, continuing and perfitting of this most magnificall work, be
ascribed to God alone.

Verse. 2. For true and righteouse are his Judgment. etc.

LEast they should seem rashly and without cause of great joy to rejoice, as
common the peopel are often wont to do they expound what abundant matter of
gladness is offered unto them, that God has executed the office of a true and
just Judge, in reue^ging the wickedness of the great whore. He often times
threatened her, the deserved destruction, which she deserved because he
differred the same, she accused God and his prophets of lying, but when a
while after it had fallen upon her head, she perceived and felt that god is
true, which admonished her that she should repent. But when she despised the
admonitions of God, and would make no end of committing whoredom, ravening,
and killing, at the length, she knew by proof the Just Judgment of God, which
can not always suffer, so cruel and monstrouse sins unrevenged.

For he has condemned the great Whore which did corrupt the earth with her
fornication and has avenged the blood of his servants shed by her hand.
etc. Because he has pronounced the sentence of eternal damnation, against ye
most impudent and shamlesse harlotte ye Church of Rome, which with fornication,
as well spiritual as corporal has corrupted ye whole earth, so yt their has
scarce remained any corner pure from her dealinges Which cruelly slew the
servants of God the martirs of Christ daily with her and sw^orde, and
exquisite torments, even as it were sheep appoincted to the slaughter: whose
most innocent blood he has now by good right revenged, whereas he has
condemned her to eternal torments.

Verse. 3. And again they said Halleluiah. etc.

THose heavenly spirits do not once only but with often repeated voices singe
praises to God, and they stir up and provoke all others also to yeald the
same obedience to the Lord. We see therefore that they celebrate the name of
God without any irkesomnes or werines at all, which burn with a sincere love
toward him and that the blessed orders of heavenly spirits do satisfy
themselves with no praises or thanckes giving, yt they may show themselves not to
be unthankful, for the benefit received of the delivery of the Church from the
defilings, and cruelty of the great whore. We be here admonished of our
duetye, that we are bound with unwearied study and endeavor to magnifye the
infinite goodness of god, both for all other his benefits bestowed upon us, and
also chiefly for the light of the Gospel spronge up unto us, whereby the
clouds of Poperye being daily more and more driven a way, the western
Babylon is brought very nere to utter ruin.

And the smoke of her torments rose up for evermore. etc. Even here the
heavenly spirits gathered to themselves sound matter to joy quietly that they
see the smoke of Babylon being set on fire, ascend up for ever, when God has
delivered her up to be tormented with the everlasting torments of hell fire.
We may learn here that the hope of the papists concerning the restoring of
the dignity of there Church is but vain, whose Just condemnation when we
know by the word of God, we are taught by the same word, that her
burninge shall be for ever.

Verse. 4. And the four and twenty elders, and the four beasts fell down and
worshipped God that sat on the throne saying Amen Halleluiah. etc.

WE have often noted before, with how great reverence y^ honorable senate of
the 24. elders, with the four Cherubicall beasts, do come to celebrate the
glory of God. For they fall upon there faces, whereby they acknowledge them
selves to be unworthy, which should magnify, and set forth the honor of god,
they cast down there crowns, and bowing down worship god, which sits
upon the seat of majesty and glory for ever. Which thing as we see, they do
in this place. After therefore yt they have testified there humility with such
submission as was meet, they answer to the most holy song of the angels,
which they song in the name of ye whole Church, Amen, Halleluiah. By which
truly they do signify, yt they desire nothing more in there minds with
ardent prayers, then that god alone may have his sound and perfect glory, and
yt all may acknowledge, what a be^efite god bestowed upon his church, when he
took vengeance upon the great whore. And therefore these do also exhort all
the faithful to ascribe praise, glory, honor and power to God alone. This
voice Halleluiah so often repeated, does teach that the desire to praise God
is easily slacken of among us, except one of us often stir up an other to
this office.

Verse. 5. Then a voice came out of the throne saying praise our god all ye his
servants, and ye that fear him both small and great.

THis voice proceaded either from the 4. beasts which bear up the throne of
God, or else from those infinite millions of Angels, which compass the throne
about admonishinge, that god is to be extolled with due praises, of all his
servants which fear him unfeignedly whether they be small, or great. As many
therefore as will be counted for the servants of god, ought not to be
slothful in this office, but to labor with endeavor, that his glory may be
celebrated through ye whole earth. For this voice does speak as well to the
great, as the small, yt is of what state or condition soever they shall be, least
any might suppose yt he should be free from this office. Afterward it also
teaches, who are in very deed the servants of God, when as instede of an
exposition he added, this, they yt fear and reverence his co^maundeme^ts from
there heart. All do in words acknowledge god to be there father and lord, but as
the Lord does expostulate, with the Jews in the first Chapter of mathewe. If I
be father where is mine honor if I be a Lord where is my fear? so this voice
by the fear of God definith his servant.

Ver. 6. And I heard like a voice of a great multitude, and as the voice of
many waters, and as the voice of strong thundringes, saying halleluiah, for
our lord god almighty has received. etc.

THis voice which he has described so diligently seems, that it was ye voices
of all ye heavenly companies, joined in one with this acclamation concluding ye
song and saying, halluiah for our lord god almighty has reigned the whole
church being taught of our savior Christ does desire ye the kingdom of God
may come, when as all his enemies being vanquished ye dominion of God alone
may excel in the sight of all creaturrs. The heavenly voice does testify, ye
kingdom has now come, when as the Church of Antichrist being abolished and
destroyed, God alone does rainge in the congregation of the faithful, because
now the subversion and ouerthrone of all the enemies of God and his church is
at hand, when as a little after the beast being overcome in battle is
apprehended, and the devil him self at length together with the beast and
the false prophet is thrown hedlonge into the burninge lake of fire.

Verse. 7. Let us be glad and rejoice and give glory to him. etc.

TO our selves say they let us rejoice for so happy a victory, and let us in
the mean time with delectation use our own joy, but let us not forget to
yield due honor to God if we ask what new cause of joy there is 2. the
answer.

For the marriage of the lamb is come, and his wife has made her self
ready. etc. For now the time is at hand, that Christ may bring the
Church which he espoused in time past to be his wife, home to his house, and
the Church even now about to come into the most acceptable imbracinges of
her dear spouse, does adorn and deck her self, that she may receeue him
when he comes according to his dignitye we are admonished here, that what
space of time soever shall be remain to the Church, from the destru^tion of
the Synagoge of Antichriste, even to the end of the world that the same is
granted unto her, that she being bewtifullye adorned with faith, godliness,
and innocence of life, may come forth into his presence, which thing I would
to God we all diligently considered, yt the most filthy garments of the flesh
being cast a way, we may garnish our souls with ye new ornaments o^
righteousness and holiness, yt we may be prepared to go forth to mete Christ in
what hour soever he shall come.

Verse. 8. And unto her was granted that she should be araied with pure fine
linen and shininge, for the fine linen is the righteousness of the saints. etc,

THat the Church should not come forth naked, or covered with torn garments,
seeing of her self, she has no clenelines or shining bewty, he shows that
marriage garments are otherwise prepared for her. For by the gift of God she is
decked with fine linen pure shininge, which are ye righteousness of the saints
that is those good works which are the testimonies of a lively faith. For after
that all the spots of the Church are washed a way in the blood of the lamb,
she is clothed with new righteousness also, that she studieth to please God by
good works, and through Christ, her obedience is acceptable to God although
it be imperfect.

Verse. 9. Then he said unto me write, blessed are they which are called unto
the lambs supper, and he said unto me these words of God are true. etc.

WE have said often, that as often as John is commanded to commit any thing
to writing, after that first commandment, which he received in the
beginning that he should write whatsoever things he saw, that it is a matter
of great weight which ought diligently to be weighed and considered of us.
When the heavenly voice therefore pronounces them blessed, which are called to
the supper of the lamb he signifies that they are happy, which by the
preachinge of the gospel are called to the partakinge of the heavenly life,
so that they themselves do acknowledge there own happiness. Which how great it
is it shall the^ perfectly appear, when the day shall come, which is appointed
for ye celebrating of the marriage of the lamb, and in y^ he repeateth that
these words of God are true, he does therefore yt with a^most weighty
affirmatio^ he might seal this doctrine concerning the felicity of those
which are made partakers of the calling of the gospel and verily we have to
much experience how necessary this sealing is, when we see such profane
co^tempte of the Gospel every where to abound.

Verse. 10. And I fell before his feet to worship him, but he said unto me see
thou do it not I am thy fellow servant and one of thy brethren, which have the
testimony of Jesus, worship God, for the testimony of Jesus is the spirit of
the Prophecy. etc.

S. Ihon does not dissemble his own fall, seeing yt a profitable doctrine to
the Church should follow thereof. For there was so great dignity of person in
the Angel, that Ihon was ready prepared to give to him divine honor. But the
Angel suffered not the glory, which is due unto God to be transferred into
him self, for he confesses that he is not his Lord, but his fellow servant,
and one of his brethren, which bear testimony of Christ. That god alone
therefore is to be worshipped and not he, and therefore he declares, that he
is one of those whom god does use, to reuele his mysteries to the prophets,
which they should expound to other men, for the testimony of Jesus is the
spirit of prophecy in both. For to this end or mark are all prophecies
referred, and that only is the true spirit of prophecy, which leads unto
Christ. Of what sort therefore is the spirit of the popish doctrine, which
always leads us away from Christ unto creatures, when as the Angel being a
most excellent creature, so earnestly refused the honor offered unto him.
Shall we therefore worship Images, Crosses, and relics, seeing it is such
abominable wickedness to worship the Angels them selves.

Verse. 11. And I saw heaven open, and behold a white horse and he that sat
upon him was called faithful and true, and he judges, and fights
righteously. etc.

NOw remains the last battaylle to be fought against the wicked, in which
the strength and furniture of all the enemies being overthrown and slain
Christ alone has the victory, and extreme torments are laid upon the
reprobate. Ihon therefore sees the heaven open, from whence we look for our
Lord Jesus Christ, which with the breath of his mouth shall destroy
Antichrist, and by the brightenesse of his coming shall abolishe him. And the
white horse goes out of heaven, which represents the ministry of the
Gospel pure and sincere from all the dregs, and spotes of perverse doctrine,
whose office is to carry Christ, to this last battle which he will fight
against Antichrist. For by the preachinge of the gospel Antichrist is
overcome. Others by the white horse understand the white cloud, in which
Christ will come to judgment, but I think this vision is to be expounded not
of ye judgment, which is described in the next Chap. following, but of the
victory of Christ against all his ennemies, which goes immediatlye before
the last Judgment. He that sits upon this horse is called faithefull, and
true, for the help which he promises, he will bring unto his, he brings
in due time, and he Judges and fights in righteousness, by cause he has
not without Just causes taken the war in hand, as the Princes of the
World, for light or no causes do oftentimes take great battles in hand:
But here he does nothing rashely, nothing headlonge, but all things with
Judgment and according to the rule of equitye. Therefore being provoked
with innummerable injuries by Antichrist, he proceadeth forth into battaille
to vanquish and overcome him.

Verse. 12. And his eyes were as a flame of fire. etc.

THe sharpness of his eyes is more percinge, then any fire, and makes
passage to it self even unto the innermoste, and depest thoughts of the
heart. No Hypocrisye therefore, no subtilties can deceive the quick
sharpness of his sight. If Antichrist feign a thousand times that he
promoteth the glory of God, and acknowledge Christ for his King: Yet he shall
never fly the judgment of Christ, which will draw all his dissimulation in
to light.

And on his head were many crowns. etc. Antichrist of Rome against who^ he
proceadeth furnished unto battaill with great sacraledge usurped to him self
many crowns as though he had all the rule alone in heaven, earth and hell. But
Christ by good right of inheritance, has his head crowned with many crowns,
as he to whom the father has granted the rule of all thing, as he himself
witnesses saying, all power is given to me both in heaven and earth Matthew. 28.
He shall require vengeance of Antichrist because he so traitorously usurps
the ensigns of his power, when as nevertheless he is endewed with no divine
virtue or strength.

And he had a name written that no man knew but him self. etc. When as he is
partaker of the same essence, majesty, and glory, with the father, and the
holy ghost, which dignity no creature can by understanding thoroughly
comprehend, he is said to have a name, whose force he alone, which is the
wisdom of the father does understand. Except peradventure he allude to that
saying of Christ in the 11. Chapter of Math. When he says, that no man
knows the son, but the Father, neither that any man knows the father but
the son, and they to whom the son will reveal him, yet the former
exposition likes me best.

Verse. 13. And he was clothed in a garment dipte in blood. etc.

THey are deceived as I Judge which by the garment dipte in blood, understand
the manhood of Christ, in which by his blood, he has purchased the mercy and
favor of God toward us. For here Christ is described as a warrior, and
Judge, which has put on such armor as should make him terrible to his
enemies. And it is a manifest alluding to the vision of Esaias Chapter 63.
Which brings in the Lord, all bloody and red by the slaughter of the
Edomites. Christ therefore wears a garment dipped in blood, that he might
thoroughly fear his adversaries when as they are admonished by this sign what
slaughters he made in time past upon the enemies of his Church, that they may
know that the like or greater hangs over there necks.

And his name is called the word of God. etc. Before he said that his name
was known to him self alone, now he shows that he is called the word of
God. Therefore we may understand the former name, of his incomprehensible
essence, but this name of his office, in as much as he does vouchsafe to reveal
him self unto us in the person of the mediator. He is therefore that word of
God begotten of the father before all worlds, which in the time determinate by
the heavenly counsel, was made man, and wroughte the wonderful work of man's
redemption in our flesh.

Verse. 14. And the warriers which were in heaven followed him upon white
horses, clothed with fine linen white and pure.

ALthough alone he treads the wine fat of Gods wrath, as we are taught in
the next verse following, and alone is of might to subdue his enemies, yet he
joins to him self companions of war, even all the heavenly Armies, that
is the faithful ministers of his Church, and professors of his Gospel,
which he leads forth, not so much to bear part of the labor, as that he
takes them to the participation of the victory. Which we may easily perceive
by there deckinge, for after the manner of those that triu^phe, they sit upon
white horses, and are clothed in fine linen white and pure, which as we heard
before are the righteousness of the Saints, and when they are endued with
these ornaments, that is, with faith, and innocence, they dare go forth into
battle, as it were sufficiently armed against death and wounds.

Verse. 15. And out of his mouth went a sharp sword. etc.

THis sword as we also heard before in the first Chapt. signifies the word
of God, whose truth and certentie proceadeth out of his mouth: he teachethe
therefore with what weapon Christ will fight against Antichrist, verily even
with a spiritual sword, by the preaching of his word: this place makes that
I can not fitly interpret this battaill of the last Judgment. And S. Paul to
the Thessalo. Seems to foretell two degrees of his victory, the one whereby
he is slain with the breath of Christ's mouth, the other when which the
brightness of his coming he shall be utterly abolished.

That with it he should smite the heathen: for he shall rule them with a rod of
Iron: for he it is that treads the wine press, of the fercenesse and wrath
of almighty God. etc. According to the prophecy of David reciting the
ordinance of god Psalm 2. That he should smite the rebelliouse heathen; with a
sword and should break the raging people in peaces with an Iron rod, as it
were the potters vessels. And Christ him self also is the ruin of yt
reprobate, which treads the wine press of the wrath of almighty God, that
is he shall condemn all the reprobate, being overcome by his power, to the
eternal torments of hell. The emphasis of every word is here to be noted,
which is put to terrify the wicked. And he alludeth to the prophecy of Esaias
in the 63. Chap. concerning the slaughter of the Edomites, as we said before,
in which Chapter of Esaye, there are almost the same words concerning the
treading of the wine press.

Verse. 16. And he has upon his garments and upon his thighe a name written,
the king of kings and Lord of Lords. etc.

THat all may acknowledge his invincible power, he has a name openly written
in his garments and upon his thighe, which declares his majesty and
Dominion, verily that he is king of all kings, and lord of all lords.
Whosoever therefore challenge to them selves a kingdom or Lordship in the whole
world, are his subjects, but if that of there own accord, and willinglye
they do not acknowledge his rule over them, will they, nill they, they shall be
drawn to his obedience. In vain therefore is Antichrist proud with the
insolent titles of kingedome and Lordship, because he must be made subject to
the yoke of this chief and highest king of kings. For he sits at the
right hand of God until all his enemies be made his foot stole, Psalm. 110.

Verse. 17. And I saw an Angel stand in the sun who cried with a loud
voice, saying to all the fowls that flyed by the midst of heaven come and
gather your selves together unto the supper of the great God. etc.

IT is wont to be unlucky among men to singe the triumph before the victory,
and the enemies as yet not being vanquished to think of the spoils and the
pray is ridiculous. But the matter is far otherwise in those battles which
Christ sighteth. For he being always sure of a happy end, may boldly triumph
over his enemies. Like as this Angel which exercises the office of a heralde
taking his place in the sun, as it were in the middle market place of the
world, or theater proclaims with a loud voice yt victory of Christ obtained
against antichrist and that there shall be made such a slaughter of his
adversaries, that with great diligence, he bids all the fowls as many as
fly through the midst of heaven, to the supper of the great God, which he
has prepared for them with so innumerable dead carkases of his enemies which
are overthrown.

Verse. 18. That ye may eat the flesh of kings, and the flesh of the high
captains, and the flesh of the mighty men, and the flesh of horses and the^
that sit on them, and the flesh of all free men, and bond men, and of small
and great. etc.

THat the fowls might know with how deintye ^here they should be welcomed
in the supper of the great God, the angel nu^breth up, that they shall be
filled with the flesh of noble men, of kings, of dukes, of strong captains,
of horsemen and of horses, and moreover with the carkases of all both free and
bond both small and great. By which similitude he would signify how horrible a
slaughter should be brought upon antichrist, yt the men of no state or
condition, which came to ayed him, should ^ly from his torment whether they
were princes; or whether the common people, whether they were small or great.
For yt there shall none remain of ye whole army of antichrist, or yt should be
raunsomed with money, but yt all should be slaie^ and not on left, we are here also
admonished in yt he calls Christ ye great God, against y^ blasphemouse cauils
of Arrians, like as paul also in the second chap. to tytus, speakinge of his
second coming. For in either place yt holy ghost understands christ to be
most great and equal, with the father whom he sets forth and honoreth by ye
name of ye great God.

Verse. 19. And I saw the beast and the kings of the earth and there warriors
gathered together to make battle against him that sat on the horse and against
his soldiers. etc.

NOw begins the most grieuouse battle, for now Antichrist, with his wicked
confederate Princes, and with there whole army sets him self against Christ
ye victoriouse Captain. We read before in the sixtenth Chapter that by the
common counsel of the Devil the pope and his clergy, Legates were sent
forth, which like frogs boasting nothing, but bubles and a vain croking, yt
by there babbling they would stir up Princes that they might set them selves
in armor against Christ. Now therefore in this last battle they fight
under Antichrist, whiles they study by all means to establish his tyranny,
which God will have abolished, and with great labor they desire to overthrow
ye kingdom of Christ which is spread abroad by the Gospel. They fight
therefore with all there force against Christ and his army, that is against the
preachers and professors of his truth, as we daily see before our eyes.

Verse. 10. And the beast was taken, and with him that false Prophet^ that
wrought miracles before him, with which he deceived them that received the
beasts mark, and them that worshipped his. Image, these both were cast quick
into a lake of fire, burninge with brymstone. etc.

THe two verses which remain of this Chapter do teach, what end there shall be
of this last battaill, and first what remains for the captains the^ selves.
They are taken says he (all there army being overthrown) even the beast
and the false Prophet, that is the Roman Antichrist and his false
Prophetical clergy, which with feyned signs and miracles seduced the
nations into error, that they might bring into there minds to profess
bondage to the beast, and to worship his Image. These two therefore after there
infinite abominations, at length being taken, are cast headlonge a live into a
lake that burns for ever with brymstone: that is, they are condemned to the
most grieuouse damnation of all, verily to be tormented with so much more
grieuouse torments, as they have excelled, other men in more haynouse sins.
This shall be the end of the tyranny of Antichrist.

Verse. 21. And the remnant were slain with the sword of him that sat upon the
horse, which sword proceaded out of his mouth and all the fowls were filled
with there flesh. etc.

ALthough a most sharp sentence be uttered upon the heads of this wicked
conspiracy against Christ, yet the members there of shall not escape for as
many either kings, or magistrates, as have made them selves ministers of the
fury of Antichrist, with all the rest of the men of what state or condition so
ever, which had rather yt Antichrist should reign then Christ: All they are
slain with eternal death by the sword of Gods word, which they would not
obey that they might live. And that they should not please them selves in there
multitude all the fowls of the air shall fill them selves even to satisfey
with there slain karkasses. This end, this Judgment tariethe for all the
Profane contemners of the Gospel, which the most merciful God turn from
us through his son Christ Jesus. Amen.

The twentye Chapter.
THe joining of this Chapter with the former vision shall seem somewhat more
obscure, except we repeat the matter further of and from the beginning. In
the beginning therefore of this vision is that Dragon ye great Devil brought
in, as the principal enemy of the Church, under whom afterward do war
Antichrist and his clergy, with the Princes and people, which obey them, the
damnation of all which was set for the next before in the end of the 19. Chap.
now therefore in good order follows the comdemnation of Satan himself, which
shall be in the last day of judgment. But because ye wickedness of ye devil
against Christ and his Church, extends more largely the^ which may be
contained in the tyranny of the pope or of the Church of Rome: he composeth a
short history of all his subtle practice and treachery, from the time that
Christ suffered unto the end of the world. Which is diligently to be marked,
least we fall into the dotage of the Chiliastes, if we think these thousand
years of which S. Ihon speaks to be begun and counted from the time that
Antichrist was overcome.

Verse. 1. And I saw an Angel come down from heaven having the key of the
bottomless pit and a great chain in his hand. etc.

THere remain as yet the torments which are to be laid on Satan which is
the head, and Prince of all the persecutions moved against the Church. First
therefore is described his wickedness, that we may know that he has deserved
the most sharp sentence of eternal damnation. For before the incarnation of
Christ, he seduced the whole world except a very few of the nation of the
Jews, into Idolatry and most abominable life. But at length an Angel came
down from heaven, which represents Christ, or at the least his minister,
which had the key to shut the bottomless pit, which was the prison in which
Satan should be shut up, and in his hand a great chain, with which the
devil should be bound, so long as he should be kept in prison so we see that
Satan is not only shut up in prison, but also bound with a chain that he
might not hurt. For so great a just and desire to hurt is even bred in him,
that unless he be cast into bounds, and prison he will always raise up some
tormoyles and troubles. But there is no cause why the elect should be afeard
of his tyranny, because Christ as often as he will thrusts him down into the
bottomless pit, and holds him bound both hand and foot with a great chain,
until he shall think good to send him forth to seduce the reprobate. For as
he does shut him up in the bottomless pit, whiles he provides for the salvation
of his own, so also he suffers him losed from his bounds to range, that he
may work at his pleasure in the wicked children of wrath and perdition, that
at length with just punishment they may be tormented with him for ever.

Verse. 2. And he took the Dragon that old Serpent which is the devil and
Sathanas, and he bound him a thousand years. etc.

WHen as the Devil had walked at liberty through all nations almost from the
beginning of the world, and had filled the whole world with all kind of
wickedness and heynouse sins, at length in the coming of Christ, which had
chosen to him self a Church and much people among the gentiles, his
licenciousnesse is bridled, and although he striued very much to get forth,
yea verily he endeavored if he could by any means overcome Christ him self, by
the Pharisees and high priests: yet he was caught although he be a great and
terrible Dragon, though he be a most ancient and subtle serpent, which before
had seduced all me^, howsoever he became a sclanderouse reprocher of Christ and
his doctrine, and a most bitter enemy, he was caught I say and bound with that
great chain of sincere doctrine, that he can not range abroad at liberty as
he was wont. That S. John sets him forth with sundry titles, he did it
not only for this, that we may know whom he understands by the great
Dragon, but also he marketh him with these names, that we may learn to know
his manners and subtle nature, and learn to eschew and take heed of them. As
we have expounded before in 12. Chapter. And also in this place he recites hi^
diverse names, that we might understand, that although he be an artificer of a
thousand subtilties, and like proteus could transform him self in a hundred
shapes, yet he could not avoid this purpose of Christ, but that he should be
taken and cast into bounds. But the time which here is compassed in the space
of a thousand years, in which the Devil should be kept bound in prison, does
signify a long time, and uncertain to men. In which space of time the pure
doctrine of the Gospel should florishe in the world, and many men out of all
nations should be taken into the eternal inheritance of Christ and we see
that almost by the space of a thousand years after Christ some light of
sincere, doctrine remained in the world, at the least many did consent upon
the points of Christian religion which were chief and most necessary to
salvation: until at length the doctrine of Antichrist being brought in, of
merits, of satisfactions, of the sacrifice of the mass and other monsters,
the only foundation of faith and free Justification of faith was taken away.
In that whole space of time therefore, the power of satan was bound, so long
as by faith in the merits of Christ alone, the way was open for men to heaven.
And we must note that satan is said to be bound, and shut in prison, so long
as he does not seduce the greatest multitude to eternal destruction. For he
wrought in ye reprobate, all the time of those thousand years in which he was
bound, but because he could not wast the whole world together or the greatest
multitude thereof he is said to be shut up in the bottomless pit and bound
with a great chain.

Verse. 3. And he cast him into the bottomless pit, and he shut him up, and
sealed the door upon him. etc.

THe Angel cast Satan being taken and bound into the deep bottomless pit,
and after when the door of the prison was shut and locked, he printed the seal
of God upon the same, that no man should be so bold as to open or unlock it.
The similitude is taken of the costume of Princes, which shut those into the
innermost dungeonse of the prisons, whom they will keep in the strayghtest
ward, and then they seal the door with there own seal. In that Satan
needs so great enclosures that his wickedness might be restrained, we must
acknowledge, the desire and study wherewith he burns to do hurt, and the
nature of those men, which in continual desire of hurting resemble there
father the devil. And moreover that the rage of the devil should be
restrained with many fetters it was acceptable to the faithful, which desired
to have the kingedome of Christ spread furthest abroad.

That he should deceive the people no more till the thousand years were
fulfilled. etc. Nothing is more grieuouse to Satan, then if he can not work
his malice and fury, that he might draw the greatest company of men to
eternal torments, or at the least if he cannot bring some hurt or
discomoditie to the Church. The whole legion of devils besoughte Christ, that
he would not command them to descend into the deep, but at the least that
he would suffer them to rage upon the swine: Luke 8. Whereupon we understand
that satan is then cast into the bottomless pit, when the power of hurtinge
is taken from him. What a great torment therefore was it to Satan when he was
constrained to remain bound, for so long a time in the bottomless pit. But
it seems against reason, that ye devil was bound for a thousand years,
s^einge there were never more greuouse persecution moved against the Church,
then in the ages next after Christ, but we must note, that Satan was not
let to rage in cruelty upon the bodies but that he should not seduce the
nations as he was wont in time paste, to Idolatrye, and all kind of wickedness
which is to be refered to the great multitud of the elect, which were called
in the time of those thousand years under the Gospel, and have stood
constant in the faith of Christ in all adversities.

For after that he must be losed for a little season. etc. When as now the
pestilence of the Mahumet, and the Pope waxed strong and increased. He must be
losed for a little time, that he may seduce the nations into Idolatrye, as he
seduced the whole world before the birth of Christ. For after a thousand
years whiles the turks in the East, and the papists in the west possessed
all with there dotages, we may rightelye conjecture that Satan was losed out
of prison. But this evil shall not endure long, for the end of the world is
at hand, and the truth of the gospel being restored again to the world,
has disclosed the falshods of both the enemies.

Verse. 4. And I saw seats, and them that sat on the^, and judgment was given
unto the^, and I saw the souls of them y^ were beheadded for the writings of
Jesus, and for ye word of God and which did not worship the beast, neither his
image neither had taken his mark upon their foreheads or on their h^nds, and
they lived and reigned with Christ a thousand years. etc.

IT is described in this Verse how blessed the estate of the faithful was for
the thousand years space, in which Satan is shut up in prison. Verelye
that all difficulties being overcome, yea even the fear of death also they
did happily depart unto heaven. For when as all wicked and carnal affections
are mortified, they are regenerate into a new life, so that they would not
refuse to be smitten with are, rather then they would deny the testimony of
Jesus or the the word of God, or would submit them selves by any means to
the tyranny of Antichrist. Therefore being delivered from the calamities of
this miserable life by the first death which is of the body, and being taken
up into heavenly joys, they live still and reign with Christ through the
whole thousand years, that is, so long as Satan shall remain in bonds,
not that after the thousand years they shall dye or shall cease to ra^gne
with Christ, but that he might express to how great a benefit it was to
the godly, that the devil was kept in prison for so long a space of time,
when as in the mean while a great multitude of the elect, not seduced by his
illusions, do pass this mortal life in hope, and being unclothed of there
bodies do pass the rest of the time in blessed happiness. In that he saw
thrones set for them being received to judgment, he does sufficientlye
declare, that the happiness which the blessed spirit of the dead inioye shall
endure even to the end of the world that then even as members joined to there
head, they may exercise the judgment of the world with Christ as Paul
witnisseth, that we shall judge the world and the Angels first Corinthians.
6.

Verse. 5. But the other of the dead men did not live against until the
thousand years were finished, this is the first resurrection. etc.

Like as he set forth in the verse goinge next before the state and condition
of the godly for the thousand years space. So in this verse he describes
the state of the wicked namelye yt they were dead in whom Christ lived not,
neither should they be raised up from the death of ye body into blessed life,
but should remain dead those whole thousand years, as well in body as in
soul: not yt there soul shall perish with ethre body, but that having died the
first death which is of the body, they should also be punnished with the
second death which is eternal damnation of the soul. For this is the
first resurrection, whereby the souls being raised up from sin, which
bringethe forth death, we rise into a new life, which being begun in
this world, after ye dissoluing of this body receives great increase, and at
length in the second resurrection after the restoring of the body shall be
fully perfected.

Verse. 6. Blessed and holy is he that has part in the first resurrection: for
on such the second death shall have no power: but they shall be the priests of
God, and of Christ, and shall reign with him a thousand year. etc.

HE magnifieth the happiness and holiness of those whose part is in the
first resurrection, which is the regeneration of the soul from sin, because
on those the second death which is eternal torment of body and soul, has
no power and as Christ said before, he that shall overcome shall not be hurt
of the second death, but they shall be priests to god and Christ, which being
sanctified shall never cease to offer up the sacrifice of thanckes giving, and
they shall reign with Christ a thousand years, whiles the wicked shall not
rise from that death of the soul until they shall be judged to eternal
torments, We are taught here that they, which by the spirit of Christ are
regenerate into a new life, are delivered from the fear of eternal
damnation, neither can they ever fall from the grace of god into destruction,
but he which has begun the work of regeneration, the same shall make
perfect the same to eternal felicity.
