Verse. 7. And when the thousand years are expired Satan shall be losed out of
his prison. etc.

WHen the time appointed of god shall come, in which the world for
vnthanckefullnesse and contempt of the gospel, deserved to fall into the old
errors, the power of seducing which before was taken away from Satan, is
permitted again unto him that he may draw almost the whole world with his
wonted deceyptes and illusions into false and adulterate religion. Truly this
is a horrible example of gods seuerite and sharpness, and this also Saint
Paul foretold should be, that GOD would send the strength and efficacy of
error upon those which despised the light of the Gospel. There is no cause
therefore why we should marvel if two most absurd and gross errors, the
one of Mahumete the other of the Pope took so great increase in the world,
seeing when the devil is losed all kind of evil must needs flow and
abound.

Verse. 8. And shall go out to deceive the people which are in the four
quarters of the earth. etc.

Saint Ihon says that Satan is sent forth by the certain and
determinate counsel of God, not that he might seduce and deceive some one
nation, but all nations which are in the 4. quarters of the earth, that he
might compel them to fall away from the faith of Christ which they professed
in mouth only, to Turkishe and Popish superstitions, so that very few
should remain through the whole world, which should embrace the true
Gospel of Christ and retain the purity of doctrine.

Gog and Magog, to gather them together to battaylle, whose number is as the
sand of the Sea. etc. There is no doubt, but that by these he means, the
privy, and open enemies of Christian religion, that is all his adversaries of
what sort so ever, for Gog, signifies covered, Magog uncovered. For the Pope
couerethe his wickedness under pretense of the name of Christ, when as he is
his sworn enemy, but Mahumete blasphemethe the name of Christ openly,
although under these names, all other Heresies, which are in the world are
comprehended. And there remains a notable clear Prophecy concerning these
enemies of the Church and there subversion, Ezekiel. 38.39. For there the Lord
commands the prophet that he should prophecy against Gog, and the land of
Magog, the Prince and head of mischief, and tuball. And we learn by the psalm
120. yt mischief signifies Arabia and tuball is said to have dwelt in
Italye. Magog gave the Original to the Scythians, these were all the
posterity^ of Iapheth. And we see that the chief enemies of the Church took
there beginnge of these regions. Mahumet of Arabia, the Pope of Italy, and
Othomannus the turk of Scythia. The devil must coth all these being seduced
into errors, into battle to be fought against Christ and his Church. And he
prepares to him self an army of those, whose number is infinite, even as the
sand of the sea. So great is the multitude of the wicked, which war under
Satan. Now let the papists go and boast of there multitude, yea we will
reckon the Turks, and all Mahumetistes with them, by whose access they shall
get nothing else but that all of them being compact together into one
company, they may be the army of the devil.

Verse. 9. And they went up into the plain of the earth and compassed the
tents of the saints about, and the beloved city but fire came down from
God out of heaven and devoured them. etc.

HE expresses in this verse how great the multitude of them was, in that there
army, covered the whole upper face of the earth, and they compassed the tents
of the saints about, that is the Church, and they beseiged the beloved city
the heavenly Jerusalem with a most straight sege. Here we are taught into how
narrow a room the Church should be brought, when as the army of the devil,
covered almost the whole earth, and compassed in on every side the tents of
the saints which possess only a small space of ground, with the
furniture of Satan. For we see that from the East the turk hangs over
Christendom, in the west the tyranny of the Roman Antichrist does raunge,
so that on either side they have beseiged the beloved city. But let us be of
good comfort that are beseiged, for God which loves our city will not
suffer it to be delivered up into the power of the enemies. Although gog and
magog assault the camp of the Saints with all there engines: yet the Lord
of hosts stands on our side, and compasses us on every side with so
deep a trenche that they can never spoil or drive us out of our camp. But
at length a horrible, sudden and unlooked for, destruction, as it were fire
from heaven upon Sodoma and Gomorra, shall apprehende them and consume them to
ashes: This shall be the end of Gog and Magog, which that the Lord would
vouchsafe to bring spedely, we ought vehemently to desire of him with ardent
prayers.

Verse. 10. And the devil that received them was cast into a lake of fire and
brimstone, where the beast and the false prophet shall be tormented day and
night for evermore, etc.

NOW at length comes the last damnation of the devil. For after that he
has persecuted the Church by all ways and means he could, as it is declared
in the 12 chapter, raisinge up against her the Roman Antichrist and his
clergy, settinge a whorishe Church against her, and at length also stirringe
the hatred of the Mahumetistes against her, last of all he is apprehended and
together with the beast and the false prophet shall be condemned to eternal
torments. This shall be his reward for so great labors, which although
Satan know well enoughe, yet he releaseth no part of his madness, wherewith
he rages against the godly, but how much nerer he is to extreme tormente, so
much more he waxes mad against the Church. But Christ when the faithful
are taken unto him, shall condemn him, as the head and aucthore of all
wickedness which flows in the world, together with his Angels, to be
tormented with the everlasting torments of hell. Then at the last, the
Church, when all enemies are overcome, even the devil, death and sin,
shall quietlye triumph for ever under Christ her King. In the mean time
whiles she as a pilgrim in earth, being sustained with the hope and
expectation of this happiness, with a quiet mind she suffers all adversities,
and despisinge the world she daily aspireth unto heaven.

Verse. 11. And I saw a great white throne, and one that sat on it, from whose
face fled away both the earth and the heaven and there place was no more
found. etc.

NOW he concludes this vision with a description of the last judgment for
though he were constreyned, often before to touch the same, yet he reserved
and kept the full form of it into this last place. He seethe therefore a
throne of wonderful greatensse, by the whiteness of the same testifyinge the
synceritie of the Judge, and the Iudgem^nte. For there shall be no corruptinge of
Judgment in that tribunal seat, no accepting of persons, bribes shall there
nothing preuarie, love or hatred shall do nothing, but he shall moderate all
things by Justice. Verelye the Judge that is our Lord Jesus Christ is of so
great Majesty, that the heaven and earth fly from his presence for by his
coming he shall change the whol^ face or shape of the world. To this we
may refer the darckeninge of the Sun and Moon, the shakinge of the powers
of heaven, the horrible roringe of the Sea, and the trembling of all creatures.
So great is the horror of that Judgment, that men being discoraged they
shall be tormented with fears of him before he shall come. What shall be the
terror therefore, when the Judge shall sit upon the tribunal seat. But that
he denies that the place of heaven and earth shall be found, he does not
understand that the creature shall be utterly abolished, but that this old
form shall be put of, that it may have a new, and a far more perfect put
upon it, as we read Psalm 102. and 2. Pet. 3.

Verse. 12. And I saw the dead both small and great stand before god and the
books were opened, and an other book was open which is the book of life, and
the dead were judged of those things which were written in the books
according to there deeds. etc.

FIrst of all is expressed the severity of the Judgment, that none either
great or small can fly or eschew it, for we must all appear before the
tribunal fear of Christ. Afterward the books shall be opened, which are the
consciences of every one. The^ shall hypocrisy nothing prevail, or feigned
holiness, when as the conscience being opened, every one shall receive sentence
by it, such as by his own Judgment he has deserved. For that which the
Poet says is always most true: this is the first reuengemente; that no
guyltie person is absolved, although he be his own Judge, howsoever unlawful
favor may deceive the Judgment of the praetor. But in the mean time what
salvation shall there be for the elect? For they also are gyltie to them
selves of many sins and sometime also of great and heynouse offenses. But
John answers this doubt; shewinge that an other book was brought forth
and opened, which is called the book of life, whereby it was manifest whom
God had before ordained to life, by his unchangeable decree. Here upon
dependethe the salvation of the elect, which they obtained by faith in the
worthiness and merits of Christ in whom there election is founded, and being
formed into new creatures by the grace of the holy ghost, they make the same
manifest in the world by good works, to the glory of his name. Therefore of
the works which every one has done in the flesh, Judgment shall be given
upon him, his own conscience being witness. But unfitly shall any man move the
question in this place, what kind of Judgment infantes shall have, which
have done neither good or evil. For these things perteyne to the instructing
of those which are grown to ryper age, and are to be understood of there
Judgment, for in those which have done noe works, only election or
reprobation shall have place.

Verse. 13. And the sea gave up her dead, and death and hell gave up there dead,
which were in them, etc.

Because by sundry kinds of death men are taken out of this life, as some
being drowned in the sea, some consumed with fire, some cut in pieces, it
seems incredible to flesh, that all shall rise again after the same manner.
Therefore Ihon reherseth as it was showed to him in vision, that the sea, death
and hell gave up those to Judgment, which were found dead in them. Whereby he
signifies that no man of what death soever he has died, shall perish, but
all and every one, by the voice of Christ our savior after the last trumpe
and the voice of the Archaungell, shall be raised up to Judgment with their
bodies. It is certain therefore that neither the bodies of the godly are
corrupted into nothing, neither that the karkasses of the wicked shall escape
torments.

And they were Judged every man according to his works. etc. Because nothing
is more easy to hypocrites, then to feign holiness in words, he repeatethe
again that every man shall be Judged by his works, his own conscience, which
is like to a thousand witnesses, alowinge the sentence as Just.

Verse. 14. And death and hell were cast into the lake of fire, this is the
second death. etc.

IN the words of death and hell, is the figure Metonomia signifying those
which were guyltie of the Judgment of death and hell. For the reprobate,
which by the testimony of there own conscience, are damned for there sins,
without all delay are cast into that fiery lake, that is into eternal
torments. And he affirms this to be the second death, when as the soul
having put on the body, shall be tormented in eternal torments of hell with the
devil and his Aungells. Let us do our endeavor therefore, that we may be
made partakers of the first resurrection, least we be thrown headlong into the
second death.

Verse. 15. And whosoever was not found written in the book of of life was
cast into the lake of fire. etc.

Now he expounds more plainly what he understands, by death and hell,
which he said should be cast into the lake, that is even all the reprobate,
which are not predestinate in Christ to eternal life. All these by the most
Just Judgment of God, although secret to us, are cast into the lake which
burns with fire and brymstone. For the elect only are free from this
damnation. We se here that sanctification follows election, the reprobate
remain in there corruption. For all are Judged according to there works, and
yet the elect only are saved, and all the reprobate are condemned to eternal
torment. As many therefore as have the spirit of election given us, let us
study to make the same firm and sure to our selves by good works, which god
has prepared that we should walk in them, to the praise and glory of his
name, to whom be given all honor and power for ever.

The twentye and one Chap.
NOW Follows the last vision of this revelation which is contained in the two
chapters which remain, in which is described the restoring of all things with
the happy estate and condition of the Church after ye resurrection.

Verse. 1. And I saw a new heaven and a new earth. etc.

HE propheciethe that the happy renewinge of the whole world shall be, when
Christ the redeamer of the elect shall once appear. And he alludeth to those
things which Esaye prophecieth Chap 65.66. Concerning the restoration of
the new heaven and the new earth. For as by the fall of man the whole world
fell in to ruin and destruction, so also with the restoring of mankind, the
other creature shall be repaired. Wherefore the^ do we so much esteem this world
which waxes old, and almost rotten for age, and not rather with daily prayers
earnestly groan for yt new heaven and new earth, in which righteousness does
dwell. For the first heaven and the first earth were passed away. etc. All
things are so subject to vanity and corruption, in this heaven and this
earth, in which we now live, that they must of necessity be abolished, yt
there may be place for the new heaven, and the new earth. Not yt the creature
shall be brought to nothing, but because yt glorious restoring into the liberty
of the sons of God, for which the creature mourns with us. Romans 8. shall be
as it were a new creation of heaven and earth.

And there was no more sea. etc. Nothing yt is terrible, or deformed such as
the sea seems to us, shall be seen in that blessed renouatio^ of the world.
Nothing which shall sever the elect dwelling as it were in one city, nothing
shall be to them any stop of passage, or any danger in there way. But it is
impertinent to inquire here, what shall be done with the elemente of water, when
it is not ye purpose of the holy ghost to describe the substance or matter
whereon the world renewed shall consiste but the qualities.

Verse. 2. And I Ihon saw the holy City new Jerusalem come down from God
out of heaven. etc.

NOt only the reparatio^ of the whole world shall be happy, but principally ye
state and condition of the Church shall be the most blessed of all, as for whose
cause the rest of the world shall be made partaker of the blessedness. And her
state is compared to the most holy city new Jerusalem, garnished with a new and
wonderful buylding, whose buylder is God him self, whose foundations are laid
from heaven, which does so much exceade ye glory and beauty of that old
Jerusalem, as it has more noble beginnings. For yt Jerusalem was set in an
vneue^ place, of ye earth and not well watered with springes, first builded of
certain profane Iebusites, so often vanquished and at length rased up from the
foundatio^s and made even with the ground. But this most holy city has god
for her buylder, and she came down from heaven, bringing all ye bewty of
heaven with her. Let us rejoice that we are citizens of ye city, which s. Ihon
so constantly affirms, that he saw, that we may understand that it is now
buylte already least after the manner of the common sort, which thinks the
end of all things to come to be doubtful and uncertain, because we see it
not, we should less believe that it is prepared.

Prepared as a bride trimed for her husband. He exposideth in what the
blessedness of ye saints does chiefly consist, namely yt they may be
perfectly joined to god, that the bride may come into the imbracinges of ye
bridegrom, yt the members may be joined to the head, yt his servants may be
received into the joy of there Lord. But the Church has not this decking of a
bride wherewith she comes so beautiful into the presence of god, of her self,
but she boroweth all her righteousness, wisdom and holiness of Christ* we which
ornaments being garnished, she excels all queen's in glory and beauty. And
until yt most renowned day of yt marriage shall come a great part of her does
wander as a stranger here in earth, which notwithstanding does possess these
dowries in the mean time by faith, but at length she shall perfectly obtain
the^ for ever.

Verse. 3. And I herd a great voice out of heaven, saying. etc.

AS often as it is said in yt scriptures yt a voice is heard without an aucthor,
it is met as we have noted often before, yt it proceaded immediately from the
majesty of god it self, and is to be received of us with great attention. And in
this place, the great voice, that is, a loud sounding voice, sent from heaven
ought to stricke all our senses, and frame them to a diligent marking.

Behold the tabernacle of God is with men. etc. Although the old tabernacle
was but a shadow, yet it was said to be the greatest glory of Israel, and it
was reputed of all the godly insteede of an incomparable treasure. Which not
withstanding was scarcely his footestole as Jeremy calls it lament 2. But
Christ has given much more excellent signs of his presence in the Church,
even as he promised that he would be with us even to the end of the world, but
then shall be indeed the fruit of joining together when God, will pitche his
eternal tabernacle with men.

And he will dwell with them, and they shall be his people. etc. Although the
tabernacle and arcke of the couenaunte were among the Israelites yet god
dwelled not always with them, for as much as he was provoked to anger with
their heynouse sins, as the Psalmist does singe, he often forsook the
habitatio^ which he had chosen among men. But when these times shall come there
shall be no sins, nor any other thing that shall separate us from the eternal
fellowship and cohabitation of God, for we shall be his peculier people, whom he
will always acknowledge for his, and we likewise, shall cleave wholly unto him.

And God him self shall be with them, and be there God. etc. There is a great
Emphasis almost of every word, God him self says he shall be with men, and
shall be there most loving God. The things therefore which it is mere, for God
to bestow upon those whom he holds most dear the same ought the faithful
to look for at his hands. Now great and how magnificall the things are
which God will grant to those men, whom he shall vouchsafe his presence,
and whose god he shall not be ashamed to be counted, can not be comprehended in
the thought of man, nor can not be expressed with the tongue or speech of
any man.

Verse. 4. And God shall wipe away all tears from the eyes. etc.

THe fear of evils aproching which does trouble men that are subject to
death, even in there greatest gladness, shall be furthest from the most happy
condition of the blessed ones. For no sorrow, no grief shall come upon there
happiness, by which they should less have the truitio^ of sownd and perfect
joy for ever. For god shall wipe away all tears from there eyes. For he shall
fill them being delivered out of the greatest miseries and calamities, with an
inspeakable joy of comfort and consolation. And there shall be no more death.
What soever evil sin brought in with it, all that same, when sin is abolished
shall be taken away. Therefore when as death is the reward of sin, it shall
have no place in those which by Christ have over come sin. For Christ
triumphed over death not for him self but for his chosen, they therefore
which shall be partakers of the resurrection from death by Christ, death shall
no more reign over them. Therefore they shall inioye immortal glory, and
felicity, whosoever they be which are called to the partakinge of his kingdom.

Neither sorrow. etc. The benefit of drawinge ou^e the life into eternity
should not be so great, if it should be often affected with mourning and the
bitterness of sorrow, as this our frail life is. Therefore the heavenly
voice does express by name, that all sorrow and mourning are utterly banished
from that life, least there should be any thing at all, which might spot or
darcken the glory of eternal felicity.

Neither crying. etc. The bitterness of sorrow does often times wring out of
us, beside tears, complaining voices also, and lamentable wepinges. Like as it
is given of nature, to all living creatures at the least, which utter any
voice, yt when they are grievously hurt, or do feel peine: by and by they send
forth miserable howlings, by which with out doubt they lame^tably crave ye help
of god after their manner, for their sorows. But the^ when all cause which may
bring sorrow and grief shall be altogether taken away, there shall no where be
heard weping, cries, and lamentable, howlinges, but of all creatures, that is
of as many as shall be received into the gloriouse liberty of the soones of God
there shall be one only voice of ioyfulnes praising god for his infinite
benefits, and rejoicing one with an other for the^ selves.

Neither shall there be any more pain. We attain nothing in this life that is
preciouse, without labor and grief and this is a part of the punishment, in
the sweat of thy brows thou shalt eat thy bread: but in that life there
shall be in a readiness, whatsoever things they be that may adorn our
felicity. Yea verelye the infinite liberality of God shall minister
perpetually all things in flowing abundaunce to us resting in quiet. But it
seems absurd, seeing God be fore man fell, would have him exercised in
dressinge the garden that he should not wax slothful by idleness, that
now when men are restored into a more higher degree of happiness, all labor
and care of work is taken from them. But it is easy to answer, that all
labor which shall bring ircksomnesse, weariness or grief, shall be utterly
abolished. But yet the blessed shall not live in idleness or sleep. But to
demand what shall remain for them which they may do when they have put on
there bodies, is superfluouse, seeinge it is not defined in the scriptures.

For the first things are passed. etc. The reason why none of those evils
which he has reckened up shall remain, is, because the first things, that is
all those old things are abolished, and in the world renewed none of these
shall be found. For like as with sin and for sin, all those plagues entered
into the world, to revenge the ungodliness of men, so when the corruptible
figure of this world shall pas away, they also shall be destroyed, and shall
not find any place in the blessedness to come.

Verse. 6. And he that sat upon the throne said, behold I make all things
new, etc.

THat there might be a full certentie of all these things to the faithful
God him self is brought in sittinge upon the throne of his majesty,
publishing a decree, concerning the renewinge of the world. Behold says he I
make all things new. That there should be no fear of those old evils, which
now cover the whole earth, he promisethe not only that those old things
to are passed away, but that he will create all things now.

And he said unto me write, for these words are faithful and true. etc.
Because this consolation which the remembrance of the happiness to come does
bring forth, is especially necessary to the Church being miserablye afflicted
with sharp calamities, God does not only establishe this decree concerning
the restoring of the world, but commands the same also to be committed to
writing, that by readinge and hearing the same the afflicted consciences of
the Godly might draw out comfort, and for the greatenesse of the rewards
might strongely bear all labors, for there is nothing more certain then this
decree concerning the eternal blessedness and triumph of the godly, of
which all those shall be partakers after the resurrection, which now do fight
valiantly under the banner of Christ.

Verse. 6. And he said unto me it is done, I am Alpha and Omega the beginning
and the end. etc.

IT does even in this place sufficiently appear, how sure and perfect Christ
would have this consolation be to his, that by so many constante affirmations,
he establishes this his fixed and immovable decree. It is done says he, as
if he should say, there is now no place left for doubting, for this felicity
is as suer, which ye now possess by hope, as if ye held it in your hands.
For the unchangeable and vnreuocable sentence of God, which can never be
broken, is passed upon it. It is also to be referred to this that he says,
that he is Alpha and Omega, the beginning and the end, that is, the eternal
God, whose stable and through all ages immovable will has decreed this,
which can neither deceive nor be deceived, whose word, though heaven and earth
should pass, does never fail, but indureth for ever. Here therefore the
faithefull, may atteyne most plenteouse matter of consolation as often as the
devil labors by his engines to overthrow there faieth, that lokinge to the
reward laid up for them in heaven, they may valiantly contemn all the vain
pompes, of the world. And may rather bear all labors, Crosses, reproaches,
with a quiet mind, for which so undoubted glory, blessedness and
everlasting felicity is laid up in heaven.

I will give to him that is a thurst of the well of the water of life freely.
etc. Because it is necessary ye ye minds of the godly should after a
wonderful manner be affected with the desire of this reward, neither can they
read or hear these things, but that by and by they thirst after most
earnestly, the most pleasant springes of eternal life. Behold Christ him
self meets them in the way that seek him, which liberallye profferrethe
drink to every one that thirsts out of the most clear founteyne of
eternal life. What wants therefore to the felicity of the saints? Of
which they shall freely be made obteyners if they be touched with a desire of
the same, here is no reason, or respect of merits, for eternal life is the
gift of God, not a reward due for works, but proceading of the infinite
liberality of him, which gives it. In the mean time here is the
slouthfullnesse and sluggishnesse of those condemned, which being wrapped in
the filthiness of this world, and more then droncken with worldly pleasures,
do never thirst after eternal life, but carelessly set at naught whatsoever
they hear out of the scriptures of paradise, of the new Jerusalem, of the
founteyn of the water of life, and such like rewards. These because they do
not thirst for the water of life, shall drink of the pure unmixed wine of
Gods wrath, and as the bound slaves of the world and the Devil, they shall be
subject to eternal torments.

Verse. 7. He that overcomes shall inherit all things, and I will be his God
and he shall be my son. etc.

THat we might not think that these ample rewards of happiness are set
forth to the idle and sluggish, he shows that we must fight and that
manfully, so that we may become conquerers, and then the inheritance of all
things, shall be ours by the testament of Christ, which he has sealed with his
blood. And if we be esteemed to be the soons of Abraham by faith, we shall be
appointed heirs of the new world with him, but that which extolleth all
things, we shall take possessetion of the inheritance of the sons of God.
For we ought not to look for a less ample and rich inheritance, then it
pleases God to assign to those, whom he has adopted in his only begotten
for we shall be the heirs of God and fellow heirs of Christ.

Verse. 8. But the fearful and unbelieving, and the abominable, and murderers,
and whoremongers, and sorcerers and idolators, and all liers, shall have there
part in the lake which burns with fire and brimstone, which is the second
death. etc.

THat the wicked should not always securely please them selves in their
filthiness and conte^ne all friendly admonitions he denounces horrible and
eternal pains unto them who shall not only have this intolerable
punnishements to be shut out from this happiness, but shall moreover be cast
into the most grievous torments of hell. But he reckenenth up only certain
kinds of wicked me^, yet he co^prehendeth under these all kinds of iniquity,
he calls those fearful which fear me^ more the^ god, which are ashamed of
ye name of Christ through ye fear of those evils which men can lay upon the^,
which if they be ye greuosest they bring but the death of the body only, in
the mean time, they are not afraid to betray his cause, which can throw both
body and soul into hell fire. He calls those unbelieving which will not
embrace the doctrine of the gospel, neither will they sustain to lose things
present for things to come, they count it for a fable whatsoever is spoken of
eternal life or of Christ ye aucthor thereof. Those may be called cursed or
abominable, which having shaken of all ye yoke of ye fearee of god, do ru^ne
headelonge into all wickedness, as though they did all things in despite of
God. They also which defile themselves with Murders. Adultries,
inchauntementes, and other wickedness, and do not in due time repent of there
sins, are thrust down into the same dungeon of torments. And idolaters also
which worship the corruptible creature insteede of the incorruptible creator,
shall suffer the due punnishementes for their heynouse sins, unless they
spedely repent. Lastly all kind of liars but chiefly h^pocrites, which with
the fained visor of holiness think they can deceive both god and men, shall
have there portion in the lake which burns with fire and brimstone which is
the second death, which eternal torments of body and soul do accompanye.

Verse. 9. And there came unto me one of the seven Angels. etc.

Hitherto he has generally described the condition of the blessed after the
resurrection now he shows perticulerlye by what visions he was taught these
things.

Which had the seven vials full of the seven last plagues, and he talked with
me saying. etc It is not absurd that the same Angel is both a minister of
Gods wrath upon the reprobate and also appointed a mesenger of consolation to
the godly. One of these seven Angels also showed the damnation of the great
whore Babylon in the 17. chap. one also of the number does bring the
description of the chaste spouse of Christ new Jerusalem, but whether it be the
same that the former was it nothing perteyneth to us to know.

Come I will show thee the bride the lambs wife. God in time past betrouthed
the Church to his son Christ and now she being garnished with all her or
nature she prepares her self to the celebration of the marriage, that Christ
may lead her being his wife into his fathers house, that is into the
heavenly glory that she may enjoy all the goods of her husband which as yet
being but a spouse she possesses only by faith,

Verse. 10. And he carried me away in the spirit to a great and an high
mounteyne. etc.

THey must be carried in mind far from the center and lowest face of the
earth into an exceeding high mounteyne, which shall be beholders of this most
sweet vision, together there with John shows that he was taken up into an
high place and set a lofte, that from thence as it were from a beholding
place, he might in contemplation see the whole figure of new Jerusalem her
situation and placinge.

And he showed me the great city holy Jerusalem. etc. Although Babylon were
the greatest of all cities in earth that is the Church of Antichrist, and was
proud in her own greatness: but Jerusalem was small and despised, as being a
stranger in this world, yet after the renewing of the world, when all her
members are gathered together in one, she is an ample and a magnificall city
to behold. This is the first praise of the City taken of the greatness,
that with her largenes she sufficethe to conteyne all her Citizens, with a
commodiouse habitation for every one. Secondelye he calls it holy, not
only in respect of the profane Whore, and vnpu^e City Babylon, but also in
respect of her self whiles she was a Pilgrim in earth. For then she shall be
altogether beautiful without any spot or uncleanness from which perfection she
is now far and much distance. She is called Jerusalem, for the noble
promises sake, which remain as concerning her perpetual induringe, the
accomplishement of which perteyneth to these times.

Descending out of heaven from God. etc. God himself the maker of all things
is the buylder of this city, which he has framed, and made not of some
elimentall, or matter which is under the moon, but has adorned her with
heavenly and external glory. This seat is prepared a rest of all laborers to
to the faithful, and after long and hard pilgrimages, a firm and stable
byding place is appointed.

Verse. 11. Having the glory of God. etc.

BY the shining and or nature it self this City does testify her buylder
for the wonderful glory of God shinethe in it. So in one word he uttered
her glory, which by it self to our tongues is unspeakable. But because our
understanding can not conteyne heavenly things any otherwise then by the
similitude of those things, which are set before our senses: he compares her
glory to those things, which are most preciouse and beautiful among men, as
to gold, preciouse stones and pearls.

And her shininge was like to a stone most preciouse, even a Jasper clear as
Cristall. etc. First we must note, that nothing can be found in this world
of such beauty and shining, that deserves but even to shadow the glory of
this city. Wherefore he does not simply compare her shininge to a Jasper
stone or a Cristall, but he feyneth a certyne stone containing the greatenesse
and the most beautiful variety, of the Jasper and most clear through
shininge of the Cristall, and that preciouse stone also which should be of
great price, when among men the Jasper, and Cristall are of small valewe. The
first sight therefore of this city, if we behold it is all at once, is most
acceptable with wonderful shininge. In which that greenesse of the Emeraulde,
distinguished with the most beautiful variety of colors, wherewithe, the
Jasper excellethe the Emerauld, does promise, a City always florishinge and
flowinge in the happy abundaunce of all things. But the clear and through
brighte shininge of the Cristall, takethe away all corners, of obscurity and
darckenesse, finallye all things, even at the first syghte appear beautiful
and preciouse.

Verse. 12. And had a great wall on high. etc.

Walls are not only fortresses, but also ornaments to the famosest Cities.
Well therefore is this City furnished, and beautifullye also adorned being
environed with a great and exceadinge high wall, which can both defend the
Citizens and easily keep of the enemies.

And had twelve gates, and at the gates twelve Angels, and the names written,
which are the names of the twelve Tribes of the children of Israel. etc. This
is praised in the Sytuation of Cities, if they be of hard entrance to the
eunemies, and easy passage in for the Citizens. Therefore as the wall
restrayneth the enemies from entringe in, so the twelve gates do receive the
Citizens and friends coming on every side. And that all fear should be
absente, least any injury might bruste open the gates, there are placed so
many Angels, every one the keeper of a Seueralle gate, which as they know,
all the Citizens, so they can espy and take all traiterouse adversaries, and
will let them from entering. Upon every gate also are graven the names of the
twelve tribes, as it were the ensigns, whereby is signified that all the
number of the elect being graffed into the body of Israel has the fredome of
this city, and ought not to be shut out from the free passage into the same

Verse. 13. On the east part there were three gates, and on the north side three
gates, on the south side three gates, and on the west side three gaets.

Like as Christ shall send forth his Angels which shall gather the elect from
all the quarters of the world. Math. 24. So the gates of this heavenly city
are open to receive her inhabitants coming from all parts. Therefore the
banishments which are furthest of are not to be feared, which the citisins of
the heavenly Jerusalem are often compelled to suffer in this earth. From all
quarters of the world, the way is open to those which return to there
country, from which they now wander as strangers. Neither skilleth not in
what corner of the world any of the godly do dwell, for he may prepare his
journey from every region of the world to this city and be admitted into it.

Verse. 14. And the wall of the city had twelve foundations and in them the
names of the lambs twelve Apostles. etc.

THe wall which compasses the whole circuit of the city, and fortifieth the
city on every side from the adversaries, that is that sacred bond of unity,
wherewith the whole Church is bound together, and is defended from the
pernicious danger, of errors and ignorance: it is builded upon, the
foundation of the prophets and Apostles Jesus Christ being the head corner
stone. For under the names of the Apostels, are comprehended also the names of
Prophets in as much as the doctrine of the prophets and of the apostels is the
self same, but the apostolical doctrine is much more evident and clear.
Therefore if we embrace the unity of the Church, it must be builded on these
foundacions, if we seek a defense or fortress against heresies, let this be
a brazen wall never to depart so much as an here bredeth from the foundacions
of the Apostels.

Verse. 15. And he that talked with me had a golden read to measure the city
with all, and the gates thereof and the wall thereof. etc.

WE saw other where that is to say in the eleventh Chapter, to what use the
Lord is said to measure any cities, those verily which he will build up and
not destroy. The Angel therefore with a goulden reed measured this City,
that he might signify that the Lord will build up the same for ever and we
must note, that in the eleventh Chapter Saint John is commanded to measure
the temple, and those that worship in it, because then the Lord used the
labor of men to build up his Church, but this heavenly city is builded only
of heavenly workmanship. The instrument which the Angel uses is a goulden
read whereby the excellency of the work and of the divine workemanshippe is
shadowed. And he repeateth all the several parts, as the city, the gates,
the wall, that nothing to her eternal continuance might seem to be neclected
or omitted.

Verse. 16. And the city lay four square, and the length is as large as the
breadeth of it, and he measured the city with the read, twelve thousand
furlonges: and ye length, the breadth and the heyght of it are equale. etc.

NOW follows the form and measure of the city, and the form thereof is most
fyrme and stable that is to say four square and cubycall, of which form some
of the old philosophers did think the earth to be, for the vnmoueablenes of
the same. Moreover we lea^ne by this form to Imagen nothing earthlye of this
city, for the heyghte of no city is so large as the length and breadth thereof.
The measure if we count the greatness, which is of twelve thousand furlonges,
that is 1500 miles commends the largenes and capacitye of the city, which is
great enough to the commodiouse dwellinge of all the citizens. If we consider
the proportion of the number, it clearly conteyneth that most bewtifull
concord in proportion which we noted very often to be expressed in the number
of twelve.

Verse. 17. And he measured the walls there of an hundredth forty and four
cubits, by the measure of man, that is of the angel, etc.

THe measure also of the heighte of the wall is to be noted, both in the
quantity of the largeness, and also of the number. For the great height
thereof declares, yt the defense thereof is safe enough against all the engines
of the adversaries. And the number 144. rises of twelve multiplied in it
self, of which what is to be gathered, we have expounded otherwhere, but in
this measure, least we should according to the small proportion of our
bodies, measure the cubits, Ihon shows that they were not the cubits of
men, but of the Angel, which appeared in shape of man, but he exceaded in
wonderful greatness and far above the stature of man.

Verse. 18. And the buylding of the wall of it was o^ Jasper. etc.

OF the twelve foundatio^s rises the buyldinge of the wall, which is to be
compared to the most beautiful shining and variety of the Jasper. For as the
Jasper co^teyneth in it self, the diverse colors of all preciouse stones, so
of those twelve most preciouse stones, which signify the doctrine of all the
Apostles is this wall builded, and seems to be compacte of a most beautiful
composition.

And the city was pure gold like unto clear glass. etc. The buyldinge of
the whole City is aunswerable to the beauty of the wall, which is all
shininge and glitteringe of most pure gold, and that which is more beautiful
shining through as most clear glass. No earthelye glory may be compared to
this. Let us therefore, neclectinge the color of this gross metal, which
among us is most preciouse fervently desire this beautiful riches for the
heavenly gold is through shininge.

Verse. 19. And the foundations of the wall of the city were garnished, with
all manner of preciouse stones, the first foundation was Jasper, the second of
Sapphire, the third of a Chalcedome, the fourth of an Emerale. etc.

WE know that the twelve preciouse stones in ye breast place of Aaron signified
so many tribes, but here we are before admonished, that the 12. foundations
have the names of the 12. Apostles written in them, which are ye 12.
Patriarchs of the Church, collected as well of the Jews as of the gentiles. In
these are ye sundry and preciouse gifts of God, but yet all applied to the
buylding up of one temple. If there be any thing therefore in preciouse
stones, that is shining and preciouse, if there be any beauty and virtue, they
shall all be found abundantly in these foundations. Men do greatly esteem small
pieces and sparcke of preciouse stones, therefore what glory of riches is
there where the greatest foundations of the walls, consist of whole preciouse
stones? But to reason more subtly concerning the colors and properties of
every of the preciouse stones, seems to me more curiouse then necessary. I
had rather therefore, briefly and with sobriety dispute of them all, then
subtly and curiousely.

Verse. 21. The twelve gates were twelve pearls, and every gate is of one
pearl, and the streate of ye city is pure gold as shining glass.

THe wonderful beauty of the gates is described which co^siste every of a
whole pearl how small a portion of these gates was that pearl of Cleopatra,
which was so much magnified among writers, if it should be compared to this
greatness. All these things perteyne to the describing of the magnificence
and beauty of this city, under the figure whereof is shadowed the most sweet
and blessed dwelling of the faithful with God, which shall be after the
resurrection. And the streat of the city is pure gold like shininge glass.
We may conjecture even by this, how great the beauty, and magnificence, how
great the riches, and how preciouse the furniture is of the other parts of
the city, that the very streat also of this city, is paued with that
heavenly and shining gold. He that shall conceive these riches in his mind,
shall easily contemn that small pomp of gold, preciouse stones and pearls,
which even the most mighty Emperors could ever show. Neither can poverty be
burdenouse to him, which is persuaded that so great tresures of riches are
laid up for him in heaven.

Verse. 22. And I saw no temple in it, for the Lord God almighty and the lamb
are the temple of it. etc.

THe temple of Salomo^, was the chief ornament of the old Jerusalem, but of
this heavenly Jerusalem, the temple is no part, but the whole City is the
temple of god and Christ. Yea verilye, God, and Christ are said to be the
temple thereof, whose presence is spread over the whole body of ye Church For
the holy religion and worship of God, is not shut into one corner or streat,
but over the whole city, which is the seat of God, and of our savior Christ.
Whom verily without the outward sacraments of his presence, cleauinge unto
him in very deed, we shall know not in a glass or a darcke speakinge but
manifestly, and perfectlye. And this place fights against those profane
dogs, which deny the divinity of our savior Christ. For he to whom
equal glory of the temple perteyneth, with God, can be none other but
eternal God, but Christ, with god almighty is the temple of the blessed
city, and to be worshipped with equal honor with the father, therefore he
is god almighty. Which thing also he performs eue^ now to his Church, being
a stranger as yet in earth, to which he has promised his presence eue^ until
the and of the world. For god dwells not in a temple made with hands, of
which sort was that temple of Salomo^, but spreads forth him self by the
presence of this goodness every where through ye whole Church. Although now
we see him imperfectly, yet when these times shall come, all signs being taken
away, and also all stoppes whatsoever, we shall see him as he is, and we shall
know him even as we are known of him.

Verse. 23. And this city has no need of the sun, neither of thy moon to
lighten it: for the glory of God did light it: and the lamb is the light of
it. etc.

WHat need should there be of the Sun, or the moon* where every one of the
Just shall shine as the sun, where (as I say) the glory of God, and the
brightenesse of Christ, shall show it self openly. Verelye the sun and the
stars, as it were through certain riftes of heaven, do exhibit unto us
scarcely the least sparks of Gods glory to be seen. And when as we shall be
partakers of Gods glory, the shining of the sun and the moon shall seem
darcke. And the holy ghost alludeth to those things which the prophet Esaias
in the 60. Chap. prophecieth concerning the renewing of the Church.

Verse. 24. And the people which are saved shall walk in the light of it. etc.

THe earthly Jerusalem did abhor and deteste all the gentiles as profane,
but the heavenly Jerusalem does acknowledge them for the Citizens being
purged and sanctified in Christ, and not vnwillinglye does admit them into
the partaking of her happiness.

And the kings of the earth shall bring there glory unto it. etc. Not only
the common people of the gentiles shabe received, but also kings them selves
shall lay down their glory in it, and shall live in equal condition with
the rest, not that they shall lose any part of there glory, for they shall be
all kings, which shall be partakers of the heavenly kingdom, but because, if
there be any glory in kings, the same shall be common to all the godly. Kings
and Magistrates therefore are not shut out of the heavenly city as the
Anabaptists do dream.

Verse. 25. And the gates of it shall not be shut by day: for there shall be no
night. etc.

THey live safe and without care in that city, for they fear no hurt of the
adversaries, which never shut the gates: and verily the cities in earth
except they be beseiged shut not the gates by day time, but in the night they
are locked for sudden assaults or invasions. But where there is no night but
continual day, there the gates are always open. For the Citizens being
furnished with the safegarde of the most mighty god fear not any beseiginge
or sod^yne assault.

Verse. 26. And the glory and honor of ye Gentiles shall be brought unto it.

THat we might want nothing which we desire, which seems pleasant or
gloriouse unto us in this life, he shows that all the glory of ye gentiles
shall be heaped up into this City. Not that any thing can be added to set forth
the glory of god which by it self is heighest and greatest, but because we
shall be heirs of the world and of all good things.

Verse. 27. And there shall enter into it none unclean thing, neither
whatsoever works abomination or lies: but they which are written in the
Lambs book of life. etc.

Although the gates are always open, yet there shall be no passage in for the
reprobate, because they defile all things with there profane touching, and
they which commit detestable abominatio^s, and rejoice in lies and
hypocrisy, but for the elect servants of god only, and they which are
sanctified in the blood of Christ, we may note here that sanctification can
not be separated from the eternal predestination of god. For they are not
written in the book of life, which always geuinge over them selves to lies
and wickedness, do never think of newness of life.

The twentye and two Chap.
THE perpetual stablenes of the eternal felicite of the blessed is described
in the beginning of this Chap. by the perpetual founteyn of the water of life
and by the tree of life bearing fruit every month. Then after followethe the
conclusion of this prophecy, to which authority is procured, both of the
person of him, which uttered it, as also of the person of him which received it.

Verse. 1. And he showed me a pure river of water of life, clear as Cristall
proceading out of the throne of God and of the lamb. etc.

THe state and co^ditio^ of man might have seemed blessed enough, when straight
after ye creation he was placed in ye garden of Ede^, which was most ple^tifull
in all delights of pleasure. But his banishment was more bitter the^ any death.
For to have been happy is most wretched. But after we shall be received into this
heavenly paradise, we shall never be cast down from ye top, or heighe of
blessedness, for neither sin, banishmente neither death, shall be to be
feared. Therefore saint Ihon says, that the Angel which uttered these
mysteries, showed him a most pure river of water of life clear as cristall
proceading out of the throne of God and the la^be that earthly paradise had a
river of most wholesome water, which should water the garden on every side, and
make it most fruitful of all things, which are required to a happy life
Gene. 2. Yet much more delectable and wholesome was that fountain of most pure
water which Ezechiell saw flowing out of the temple, in the Chapter 47. By
which the renewing of the Church is described But this river flowing out not
of the earth, nor out of the temple of Jerusalem, but out of the throne of God
almighty and of his Christ, does minister the joys of eternal life most
abundantly to the Citizens of the new Jerusalem. They therefore need never
fear death, which drink daily of the river of the water of life. Neither can
sorrow or any grief happen to those, which draw water out of the most pure
founteynes of this river, which are more clearer then any crystal. For the
pureness, and clearenesse of this water is opposed to those troublesome rivers
and muddie waters, of which wretched men do quench there thirst, and
afterward are subjected to sundry calamities and diseases. For nothing that
is pure or sincere is bred in the earth. Would God therefore we would contemn
the muddie and unpleasant waters of this world, whereby with greater and
feruenter desire, we may pantinglye breathe after the heavenly waters, even
like the heart, which David speaks of, boylinge with the heat of the sun,
with runninge and poison. Moreover when as this water is said to flow out of
the throne of god and Christ, we are admonished that eternal life does flow
unto us from god alone, being reconciled unto us by Christ. Moreover the
madness of the Arrians is abundantlye confuted, which envy Christ equal
dignity with the father, when as here there is said to be the self same
throne of god the father and of his son Christ, wherefore there is the same
glory, majesty and power, for the throne is a sign of the glory and
majesty of God.

Verse. 2. In the midst of the streate of it and of either side of the river
was the tree of life which bare twelve manner of fruits and gave fruit every
month. etc.

IN the earthly paradise, there was one only tree of life in ye midst of the
garden which was a sacrament and pledge of blessed and eternal life, if they
should stand in the obedience of God and when man was cast out of the garden,
together he was deprived of ye sign of eternal life. Genesis 3. But after he
shall be received into yt heavenly blessedness, he shall eat of ye fruit of the
tree of life for ever. For to all the citizens of new Jerusalem, access shall be
open to ye tree of life, which shall spring forth most happily, not in one
corner only of the city, but in ye midst of the streat and of either side of
the river. And least we should fear the course of winter and summer, such as
is with us, every month shall be autumn, and shall yield and minister the
abundaunce of most sweet fruits. Also if variety have any pleasure in it, it
shall be so great, that no lothinge or weariness of the meat, can never come
upon them for every month shall abound with new delights of diverse and
sundry fruits.

And the leaves of the wood served to heal the gentiles. etc. There is no doubt
but that this tree does represent Christ, by whose virtue all ye wou^des and
diseases of ye gentiles are healed. But it is worthy y^ considering, how great
force there is in ye fruit it self to life everlasting, when as ye leaves of
the tree would suffice to heal so manifold and those so deadly diseases, of
ye gentiles. But wherefore are ye leaves attributed to ye healing of ye gentiles
rather then the Jews, when as all have perished alike, and have need of
medicine? It is certain that the first place is always given to the Jews,
for the covenant GOD made with Abraham, whom nevertheless the Gentiles
follow in there order. For Christ is the common salvation to all men,
although in the first place to the Jews and then to the gentiles. And it
shall not unaptly agree, if we say that the leaves of the tree are taken for
the hope of eternal life, which we conceive by the preachinge of the Gospel.
For as leaves and flowers which never fall nor fade, do promise timely
fruits, so by the faith of the Gospel, we have the most certain hope of
eternal life, whose most abundant fruit we shall receive, when as that
redeamer of ours shall appear. And Saint Ihon alludethe to the prophecy of
Ezechiel Chapter 47. As we said before. Who is able to comprehend in his
mind, but even the thousand part of this happiness of the blessed Citizens?
If there be any delights of the city, they inhabit a city most abundant of
all pleasures, if there be any pleasure of the country, in the midst of the
city, the streams of the founteynes, and most acceptable shadows of the
woods delight the mind. That whatsoever the Poets have feigned of the Gardens
of the Hesperides, or of the Elisean, yea if it were true, yet it deserves not
to be called a shadow of this felicity. Therefore that must needs be an Iron
breast, which is moved with no desire of the same.

Verse. 3. And there shall be no more curse. etc.

THe most miserable curse of the whole world, followed shortly after the
most blessed state and condition of man in the earthly paradise so that the
highest felicity, was changed so cleanly into extreme calamity: but in the
heavenly paradise, me^ need not any more to fear any curse, which should
trouble the state of the blessedness. The godly therefore shall have perfect
and perpetual joy. Moreover it is manifest, what horrible cursinges the law
thundreth out against the transgressors thereof yet that blessed seed of
Abraham, in which all the nations of the earth are blessed, has taken away all
these curses. For seeing that curse is the sentence of Gods vengeance upon
sinners, now that sin is taken away and abolished by Christ, all Gods curse
is also taken away, and with the curse all kind of evil which afflicte
miserable men with sundry torments. Rightly therefore it is said Chapter. 21.
and 4, Verse: that tears, death, sorrow, labor, and crying are banished from
the city new Jerusalem. This place ought also to in flame in us the desire
of forsaking this world, which for sin is subject to so many curses of God,
and that we may wish to be gathered to that number of the blessed ones, which
without any curse inioye perpetuuall felicity.

But the seat of God, and of the lamb shall be in it. etc. The reason why no
cursednesse can pearce to that city, is, because the throne of God and of our
Lord Jesus Christ, shall defend and keep the same free from all curse. For when
as the curse, as we have noted before, is the execution of gods wrath, God
shows him self pacified to these, in the midst of whom he does vouchesafe
to place the throne of his magnificence. And that lamb which was slain from
the beginning of the world which has the throne of majesty common with God
the father, is he, which became the mediator, to draw men out of the dungeon
of malediction, and to bring them being purged with his blood, into the
presence of God.

And his servants shall serve him. etc. Here is an other reason joined, why
there shall be no more curse. That is to say, because the servants of God, after
this shall not be disobedient to the commandments of there Lord, but shall
yield perfect obedience unto him. There shall be no punishment therefore, where
there shall be no transgression of the law. But that servitude shall not hinder,
but that we may also reign with Christ our head, for it shall be no
constrained subjection, such as is seen in tyranny, but a voluntary
submission, such as is of sons to there Father, under whom they shall live,
nevertheless well and blessedly. And also to offer to God his due obedience,
is a more gloriouse Empire the^ all the Kingdoms of the world: according to
that saying to serve god is to reign. In vain therefore proud men and those
that are puffed up in arrogancy, endeavor to make all things subject to them
selves, when in the mean time they are found rebels to God, which sets
himself against the proud, and vouchsafes his grace only to the humble.

Verse. 4. And they shall see his face. etc.

THe countenance of God is most acceptable to all those, which love him with
sincere affection of godliness, and David places the fullness of pleasures in
it Psalm. 16. because when god is merciful nothing can be wanting to the full
heap of felicity. And S. Paul reasons magnifically of the beholding of his
gloriouse countenance 1. Corint. 13. And to conclude there are six hundredth
testimonies of the holy scripture, by which all things happy and pleasant are
promised, in the favorable countenance of god. Whom we shall behold, not as
we do now as it were in a glass or a darcke speakinge, but face to face, with
great delectation.

And his name shall be in there foreheades. etc. They have now also the name of
God written in there foreheades, whom the Lord does acknowledge for his own,
and will have them to be known among men for his servants, but it does not
yet appear of what sort we shall be. But after that Christ shall appear we
shall be like unto him, because we shall see him as he is 1. Ihon. 3. And then
it shall plainly appear what reward is laid up for the faithful servants
of God.

Verse. 5. And there shall be no night, and they need no candle, neither light of
the sun: for the lord God gives them light.

IN the presence of God, with whom there is no shadowing of clearenesse, there
shall be no changeable course of day, and night. The sun of righteousness
and glory never goethe down to this city, as the Angel showed before also,
Chap. 21. Verse. 23. and 25.

And they shall reign for ever more. etc. Now he plainly expresses that the
servitude of the sons of God, is not repugnant to the Kingdom, which is
promised them. Together in one word he comprehends all there happiness,
that they shall reign for ever more. In this place the ignorance of the
Chi^iastes is thoroughly confuted, because the elect shall reign not for a
thousand years, but for ever, and it does sufficiently declare that those
thousand years in the 20. Cha^ter are otherwise to be expounded, then of the
state of the blessed after this life.

Verse. 6. And he said unto me these sayings are faithful and true. etc.

NOw follows the conclusion of this prophecy, in which authority and
reverence, is gotten to this doctrine, by many means: for first the Angel
which uttered the mysteries, makes his preface, that these sayings are true
and worthy to be believed, which thing when he has done once or twice before,
now he does it chiefly to increase the hope of heavenly rewards in us. For
we know how hardly the mind of man does suffer it self to be pluct from the
beholdinge of things present, whether they be prosperouse, or adverse, that
they might conceive and nourish new hope of eternal life. Therefore the
Angel repeateth, that these promises are proceaded from him which can not
deceive, as he cannot be deceived, wherefore without great injury of him we
can not doubt, concerning the faithfulness and truth of these things.

And the lord God of the holy prophets, sent his Angel to show unto his
servants, the things which must shortly be fulfilled. etc. That same God,
which spoke up the mouth of all the Ancient prophets of whom the authority
is most holy in the Church, is the aucthour of this prophecy. We must not
therefore with less reverence embrace the same, then the oracles of the most
holy prophets, whose end has proved their faithfulness. And least we
should esteem any thing more basely in the manner of the revealing, God has
sent his Angel, which should show to his servants, the things which
should shortly come to pas. Concerning which chause, because there is enoughe
said, in the Chapter 1. Verse 1. I pass over many things.

Verse. 7. Behold I come shortly: happy is he that keeps the saying of this
prophecy. etc.

FOr the greater credit, Christ him self is brought in speaking, and
promising the certeyntie and spedinesse of his coming, in which the effect of
Gods promises, shall take place in all the godly. But in the mean time he
lays up the doctrine of this prophecy with them as a passing great treasure,
whose words if they will diligently imprinte in mind, and keep the^ so
imprinted, he pronounces that they shall be blessed. Neither shall the perils
hanging over the Church oppress them unawares or unprepared* neither shall
there faith be overwhelmed with any storms of temptations, neither shall there
simplicity be deceived with the pestiferouse illusions of Antichrist, and
even in the midst of death they shall nourishe the most assured hope of
eternal life, the fruit whereof at length in the coming of Christ, shall
manifestlye declare forth it self, to establishe perpetual felicity unto them.

Verse. 8. And I am John which saw these things and herd them, etc.

NOw of his own person, he procures aucthoritye, and credit to this
prophecy. For least it might seem to have proceaded from some frantic
false prophet, or diuilishe inspired person: S. John testifies, that it was
him self which has seen these things which which were delivered unto him
after the manner of a vision and has heard these things which the holy ghost
commanded to be written. And we know sufficiently by the history, how
famous, the name of Saint John, and how holy his aucthoritye was among
these Churches, to whose custody this book was committed. But that some do
conjecture, that this John was surnamed mark which ministered to the Apostels
Paul and Barnabas: It seems not to me agreeable, both for other reasons, and
also even of that, that so often he names him self John without the addition
of the surname Mark, which thing it is very like that he would not have
omitted, seeinge this only might make for difference: And it was the purpose
of John to bring forth the aucthoritye of his name. But that other John seemed
to have been more known by the name of Mark then of John, whom Paul calls
the kinsman of Barnabas, Coll. 4. of whom also he makes mention 2. Tim. And
also in the Epistle to Philemon, whom they think to be the very same which
wrote the Gospel which is entitled the gospel after S. Mark.

And when I had heard and seen I fell down, to worshipe before the feet of
the Angel, which showed me those things. etc. Saint John does not hyde or
dissemble his own fault, that he has suffered himself now twice for the
excellency of the person of the Angel, to be drawn away to give the
honor that is due to God alone to a creature. Whereupon may be gathered the
weakness and frailty of man, so ready to Idolatry, when so great an Apostle
dasshed his foot twice against the same stone. Moreover we may note what kind
of honor he gave to the Angel, when he fell upon his face, for that fond
distinction (which the papists make) of (...), and (...). For he would not
worship the Angel for God, whom he knew suerlye enoughe to be an Angel
and not GOD, but he thought religeously to exhibit some reverence and
honor, as to a heavenly creature. Which nevertheless the Angel by no
means does allow.

Verse. 9. But he said unto me, see thou do it not, for I am thy fellow
servant, and the fellow servant of thy brethren the prophets, and of them
which keep the sayings of this book: worship God. etc.

THis forbiddinge is grounded upon two reasons, first that it is not equal
for a servant to be extolled with ambiciouse honor of his fellow
servants. For he confesses him self to be the fellow servant, not of
John only, but also of all his brethren the prophets, that is of all the
Preachers of the Gospel, and not of these only, but of those also, which keep
the sayings of this book, that is, of all the faithefull. The second reason,
that is an vnworthtie act, that the creature should attempt to draw to him
self the honor of adoration, which is proper to God alone. And there is no
doubt, but that all the Saints departed this life, are of the same mind,
that they refuse the importunate honors, which folishe men offer unto them,
and desire to have God worshipped alone with all kind of worship. The
Papists therefore do very great injury to the Saints, whiles they obtrude
such things upon the^, not only, such which can be colored by the fond
devise of (...), but which co^teyne manifest Idolatry. Whiles they do not
only set up Images unto them, and worship the same, but also erect temples,
and they apoint festival days, for them, then which things what can be more
wicked.

Verse. 10. And he said unto me, seal not the sayings of the prophecy of this
book, for the tune is at hand. etc.

BEcause so many secreat and holy mysteries of god are revealed in this book.
Saint John might have doubted, whether he should publishe them or not but
that he had been flatlye forbidden, by the heavenly oracle, to seal up ye
sayings of the book of this prophecye, as it it were certain unspeakable
words, Although an other reason also is added that is to say that ye time was
at hand, in which this prophecy should take effect. For even then did the
misterye of iniquity work, and prepared the way for Antichrist 2 Thessalonians. 2.
Chapter. Therefore even then was the use of this Revelation in the Church.
Daniell and other prophets were commanded to seal up many things, the
execution whereof should be deferred alonge time after. But S. John is
forbidden to seal up the sayings of this prophecy, because the time of there
fulfillinge was at hand. And this place does abundantlye confute the follye
of those, which think that nothing is contained in this book, but doubtful
and dark speakinges, out of which we can draw nothing that is certain or
determinate. For the sayings of this prophecy are not sealed, but that the
godly and diligent reader may understand very many things very profitable to
be known. For the holy ghost commits nothing to writing in vain, so that
we come soberly and reuerentlye, as it is meet to so great misteryes, to
expound the same.

Verse. 11.12. He that is unjust let him be unjust still, and he that is filthy
let him be filthy still: and he that is righteous let him be righteous still,
and he that is holy let him be holy still. etc. And behold I come shortly and
my reward is with me to give every man according as his work shall be. etc.

LEast the minds of the godly should be broken with yrckesomenes, by
continuance of so great evils, Christ again stirs up the hope of his
coming not long to be differred, that by the vprightenesse of his
Judgment, he may restore into order althinges which are now confused and
out of order, that is that he may apoincte, rewards for the godly and
punnishementes for the wicked, for we see that the greater part of men do boast
them selves in wrong dealinges, and being given to the enticements of filthy
pleasures, boast yt all things are lawful for them to do, so long as God
does not thunder from heaven against there ungodliness. And hypocrites think
that they can pleasantly mock both God and men. In these so great corruptions
and offenses, it is hard for the godly to retain and keep there godliness,
least that either they should be hurt by example, or should be overcome with
injuries, or should be offended at the prosperity of the wicked. Therefore
Christ confirms the godly and holy ones, that they should not by any
means depart from there holiness and innoce^cye of manners for neither shall
the wicked bear there stunes without punnishmente, neither shall the godly
want there reward, seeinge he will shortly come, and will give to every one
such reward as his works require, but as concerning the merits of good
works, there is no need to show here what is to be thought, saying it is
expounded often other where. For rewards are given by the mercy of God, and
not as due for good works, seeinge we are debitours to fulfill the whole law
if we will require reward for the deserts of our works.

Verse. 13. I am Alpha and Omega, ye beginning and the end the first and the
last.

THat we may believe that nothing is surer then this doctrine concerning ye
rewards of the good, and punnishments of the reprobate, ye unchangeable decre
of god is interposed, yt is to say, that this is ye sentence of him, which is
alpha and Omega the beginning and the end, that is ye eternal Iehoua, of
whom all things have there being, and to whom all things are referred which
alone is without beginning and without end of him self. He has given eternity
to other things being his creatures to which he would.

Verse. 14. Blessed are they that do his commandments, that there right may
be in the tree of life, and may enter in through the gates into the City.

IT is a blessed servitude to obey his commandments, which does adorn with
so great rewards those that harken unto him, and has determined so horrible
punishments against the rebelliouse and stubborn. For as many as obey his
commandments, shall be satisfied with the fruit of the tree of life, from
eating whereof our first parents were deprived for there disobedience. And so
free access shall be open through the gates into the city, to the Citizens of
the new and heavenly Jerusalem which the rebelliouse Ada^ was banished with
all posterity.

Verse. 15. For without shall be dogs, and enchaunters, and whoremongers, and
murderers, and Idolatours, and whatsoever loves or makes lies. etc.

THese verily which being deceived with the enticements of this world, had
rather be inhabitants of the cursed earth, carelessly contemning the precepts
of God, they have no right in the holy city, into which nothing that is
profane or vnpure shall enter. Not dogs which in madness rage against
those which cast holy things before them. Not wicked inchau^ters, which abuse
the sacred name of God, to Deuilish impiety. Not fornicatours, nor
adulterours, which have defiled the^ selves with filthy iustes, like swine.
Not murderers, which like wild beasts do thirst after the blood of men. Not
Idolatours, which frame to the^ selves new Gods, with most great and horrible
injury of the only true God. Not false hypocrites, not lying heretics, the
Aucthors of false opinions, neither they which willingly apply there ears to
such delusions, shall have place in the holy city, in which dwells
holiness, cleanes, charity and truethe. And least we should Imagen a mean or
some certain third place or state between, the chiefest felicity and extreme
misery, he places all the wicked with out the city, whom before in the 21.
Chapter he cast into the lake of fire and brimstome. Away therefore with those
fables of the papists, concerning those places which they call ye limbus of
Fathers and of children not baptized with other monstruouse lies of the same
sort, which idle belies and well fed, panches have dreamed. For they which
are without the citi are most miserable, not only because they want those
good things which the Citizens of it do inioye in her, but also because they
shall be tormented with the eternal torments of hell.

Verse. 16. I Jesus have sent mine Angel to testifye unto you these things
in the Churches. etc.

Now Jesus Christ does plainly and without any allegorical darckenes
confess yt he is the aucthour of this prophecy, which sending his Angel,
has opened it to John after the manner of a revelation, to the great profit
and commodity of the whole Church. Admonishing also in the end. Those seven
Churches of Asia, with which this treasure should be reposed, like as he did in
the beginning, how great honor he has bestowed upon them, that he would
appointe them kepers and witnesses of this revelation. And how necessary this
admonition was, we may well perceive by this that the devil has made all the
assaults he could against the authority of this prophecy, that ye
subtilties of Antichrist might the better be cloked which in this revelation
are clearly discovered. Whereupon this book was very necligently kept in the
old time notwithstanding the Christ commanded it should be pre^erwith great
diligence.

I am the rote and generation of David and the brighte morning star. etc.
That those things might be ratifyed with the godly, which he has spoken
concerning the blessedness to come: Christ professes him self to be the
rote and generation of David, to whom that eternal and most blessed Kingdom
is appointed, by the prophecies of all the prophets. That he is that brighte
and morning star, which promisseth that the day of most clear light
shall shortly come, when as all darckenesse being driven away, the faithful
shall inioye perpetual light.

Verse. 27. And the spirit and the bride say come. etc.

SO soon as Christ gives the hope of his coming, by and by that spirit,
which helps our infirmities, and makes intercession for the Saints with
groninges that are unspeakable, with ye whole Church, which is the spouse of
Christ, as it were goinge forth to meet him and embrace him, she brusteth
forth into this voice of prayer. Come, and do not defer thy coming.

And let him that hears, say come: and let him that is a thirst come: and
let whosoever will, take of the water of life freely. etc. Those that are the
prayers of the whole Church, the same ought to be the prayers of every
several person, therefore the holy ghost does exhort every one that
hears this prophecy, to love the coming of Christ, and to pray diligently
for it, and Christ that he may comfort his servants, even in the middle
course of this life, gives freely by faith the waters of eternal life to all
that thirste. But he seems to attribute eternal life to our will. He that
will (says he) let him take. It is true, but yet that any may will, it
behoue^h him to be prevented by the grace of God. Although we ought not to
understand, the will for some light motion of the will, but rather for that
ardent desire, which he has expressed before by thirste: such a will except
it be framed of God is in no man, by nature. For it is neither of him that
wills, nor of him that runs but of God that shows mercy. Romans 9.

Verse. 18. For I protest to every man that hears the words of the
Prophecy of this book, if any man shall add unto these things, God shall
add unto him the plagues that are written in this book. etc.

Verse. 19. And if any man shall minishe, of the words of the book of this
prophecy, God shall take away his part out of ye book of life, and out of
the holy city, and from those things which are written in this book. etc.

THe holy ghost for knowinge the controversies which the devil would raise
up concerning the authority of this prophecy, moves and inforceth S. John
to seal the same with a most weighty protestation. And yet nevertheless
Satan has left nothing undone against it, but all in vain. Therefore that
the authority thereof might be established equal with the other oracles of
God, to which it is lawful to add nothing, neither to take any thing from
them, he threateneth horrible punishments to those, which shall be so bold as
to attempt any such thing against this prophecy. That he says his part
shall be taken out of the book of life, he means not that he had a portion
in it before, but he follows the Antichesis, seeing before he had spoken of
adding.

Verse. 20. He that testifies these things says suerly I come quickly.
Amen, even so come Lord Jesus. etc.

THat it might not seem to be the protestation of a man only, when as men
often times in vain cast for the horrible thunder boltes of threatninges,
Christ him self for confirmation sake does subscribe, and promises that he
will come shortly, that by effect he may ratify the^e decrees. Saint Ihon
makes answer in the name of the whole fellowship of the faithful. Saying
Amen, come Lord Jesus make an end of all calamities of the Church, that the
glory may shine over all things, and the faithefull may obtain the promised
inheritance.

Verse. 21. The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with you all. Amen.

HE concludes the Epistle which was sent in common, to the seven Churches
commendinge there health and salvation to the grace, of our Lord Jesus Christ.

The end of the Commentaries of William Fulke Doctor of Divinity, upon the
sacred revelation of Saint John.


Imprinted at London, in Paul's Churchyard: by Thomas Purfoote, at the sign of
the Lucrece. Anno. 1573.
